 सः ह That गार्ग्यः Gargya उवाच said अयं this शब्दः sound यः which एव indeed पश्चात् behind यन्तं a going man अनूदेति follows, issues एतम् upon it एत verily अहम् I उपासे meditate upon, adore ब्रह्मइति (as) Brahman. सः ह That अजातशत्रुः Ajatshatru उवाच said मा not मा not संवादिष्ठाः talk, speak एतस्मिन् about him वै verily. अहम् I उपासे meditate एतम् इति upon it असुः इति (as) life. सः He यः who उपास्ते meditates upon, adores एतम् it एवम् thus, as such अस्मिन् in this लोके world (reaches) एव ह indeed सर्वम् full आयुः इति term of life प्राणः life न not जहाति leaves, depart from एनम् him पुरा before the complete कालात् time, true.

 Gārgya said—"This sound which follows a going man, I adore as Brahman." Ajatshatru said—"Please do not speak to me about him as Brahman. Verily I adore him as life." He who adores him with this attribute reaches, in this world, full age as acquired through his past work, and even though troubled by disease, life does not leave¹ him before the completion of the full age measured by his past work.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. He does not die a premature death.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** स होवाच गार्ग्यो य एवायं दिक्षु पुरुष एतमेवाहं ब्रह्मोपास इति स होवाचाजातशत्रुर्मा मैतस्मिन्संवदिष्ठा द्वितीयोऽनपग**



**इति वा अहमेतमुपास इति स य एतमेवमुपास्ते द्वितीयवान्ह भवति नास्माद्गणश्छिद्यते॥११॥**

 सः ह That गार्ग्यः Gargya उवाच said: अयं this पुरुषः being यः who (is) एव indeed दिक्षु in the directions एतम् upon it एव verily अहम् I उपासे meditate ब्रह्म इति (as) Brahman. सः ह That अजातशत्रुः Ajatshatru उवाच said मा not मा not संवदिष्ठाः talk, speak एतस्मिन् about him. वै Verily अहम् I उपासे इति meditate upon adore एतम् him द्वितीयः (as) second अनपगः इति non–separating, being attended. सः He यः who उपास्ते meditates upon, adore एतम् if (that being) एवम् as such भवति ह becomes द्वितीयवान् attended with a second. अस्मात् From him गणः the party, followers न not छिद्यते departs, is separated.

 Gārgya said—"This Being^(1) who is identified with the directions and is in the ear and the heart I adore as Brahman." Ajatshatru said—"Please do not speak to me about him as Brahman. I adore him as second and as non–separating. He who adores that Being with these attributes is always attended by friends and is never deserted by his followers.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. The presiding deities of the directions are the Ashwins, the twin gods who are never separated from each other.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** स होवाच गार्ग्यो य एवायं छायामयः पुरुष एतमेवाहं ब्रह्मोपास इति स होवाचाजातशत्रुर्मा मैतस्मिन्संवदिष्ठा मृत्युरिति**



**वाऽहमेतमुपास इति स य एतमेवमुपास्ते सर्व^(ꣳ) हैवास्मिल्ँ लोक आयुरेति नैनं पुरा कालान्मृत्युरागच्छति॥१२॥**

 सः ह That गार्ग्यः Gargya उवाच said अयं this पुरुषः being यः who एव indeed छायामयः (is) in the shadow, in the external darkness अहम् I उपासे meditate एतम् upon him एव indeed ब्रह्म इति (as) Brahman. सः ह That अजातशत्रुः Ajatshatru उवाच said मा not मा not संवदिष्ठाः talk, speak एतस्मिन् about him, वै Verily अहम् I उपासे इति meditate upon, adore एतम् him मृत्युः इति (as) death. सः He यः who उपास्ते meditates upon, adores एतम् him एवम् as such अस्मिन् ह in this लोके world (reaches) सर्वम् एव full आयुः इति age. मृत्युः Death न not आगच्छति approaches, overtakes एनम् him पुरा कालात् before the full age.

 Gārgya said—"This Being who is identified with the external darkness and is in the heart, I adore him as Brahman." Ajatshatru said—"Please do not speak to me about him as Brahman. Verily I adore him as death." He who adores him with this attribute reaches full age in this world and death does not approach him till the end of that term.

 **स होवाच गार्ग्यो य एवायमात्मनि पुरुष एतमेवाहं ब्रह्मोपास इति स होवाचाजातशत्रुर्मा मैतस्मिन्संवदिष्ठा आत्मन्वीति वा अहमेतमुपास इति स य एतमेवमुपास्त आत्मन्वी ह भवत्यात्मन्विनी हास्य प्रजा भवति स ह तूष्णीमास गार्ग्यः॥१३॥**



 सः ह That गार्ग्यः Gargya उवाच said अयम् this पुरुषः being यः who (is) एव indeed आत्मनि in the self (Hiranyagarbha) अहम् I उपासे meditate upon, adore एतम् him एव verily ब्रह्म इति (as) Brahman. सः ह That अजातशत्रुः Ajatshatru उवाच said मा not मा not संवादिष्ठाः talk, speak एतस्मिन् about him. वै Verily अहम् I उपासे इति meditate एतम् upon him आत्मन्वी इति (as) Self–possessed. सः He यः who उपास्ते meditates, एतम् upon him (that being) एवम् as such भवति ह becomes. आत्मन्वी Self–possessed. अस्य This प्रजा progeny भवति becomes आत्मन्वी Self–possessed. सः ह that गार्ग्यः Gargya आस became तुष्णीम् silent.

 Gārgya said—"This being who is identified with Hiranyagarbha and the intellect, I adore as Brahman." Ajatshatru said—" Please do not speak to me about him as Brahman. I adore him as self–possessed. He who adores him with this attribute becomes self–possessed. The result of his meditation reaches him and is extended to his progeny also. When his knowledge of Brahman was exhausted, Gārgya became silent with his head bent down."

 ** स होवाचाजातशत्रुरेतावन्नू^()३ इत्येतावद्धीति नैतावता विदितं भवतीति स होवाच गार्ग्य उप त्वा यानीति॥१४॥**

 सः ह That अजातशत्रुः Ajatshatru उवाच said एतावत् नु त इति (Is) this all ? (The other said) एतावत् ह इति this (is) all.



एतावता By this much भवति (Brahman ) is न not विदितम् इति known. सः ह That गार्ग्य Gargya उवाच said उप + यानि (I) approach इतित्वा you (as a student).

 Ajatshatru said—'Is this all the knowledge of Brahman you have ?' The other replied: 'This is all.' Ajatshatru said—'Brahman is not known by this much¹ knowledge.' Gārgya said—'Let me approach you as a student for the knowledge still to be attained.'

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. For this is the knowledge of conditioned Brahman. The knowledge of unconditioned Brahman realised by Ajatshatru still remains to be known. The knowledge of the conditioned Brahman leads to the knowledge of the supreme Brahman.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** स होवाचाजातशत्रुः प्रतिलोमं चैतद्यद्ब्राह्मणः क्षत्त्रियमुपेयाद्ब्रह्म मे वक्ष्यतीति व्येव त्वा ज्ञपयिष्यामीति तं पाणावादायोत्तस्थौ तौ ह पुरुष^(ꣳ) सुप्तमाजग्मतुस्तमेतैर्नामभिरामन्त्रयाञ्चक्रे बृहन्पाण्डरवासः सोम राजन्निति स नोत्तस्थौ तं पाणिनाऽऽपेषं बोधयाञ्चकार स होत्तस्थौ॥१५॥**

 सः ह That अजातशत्रुः Ajatshatru उवाच said एतद् it (is) प्रतिलोमं च contrary to usage, against custom यत् ब्राह्मण a Brahman उपेयात् should approach क्षत्रियं a Kshatriya (their king) वक्ष्यति (he) will tell (teach) मे me ब्रह्म इति about Brahman. एव However वि ज्ञपयिष्यामि (I) will instruct



will enlighten त्वा इति you. उत्तस्थौ (He) rose आदाय taking तम् him (Gargya) पाणौ by the hands. तौ They both आजग्मतुः ह came सुप्तम् to a sleeping पुरुषम्ः man. एतैः By these नामभिः names आमन्त्रयाञ्चक्रे (Ajatshatru) addressed तम् him बृहत् Great पाण्डरवासः White–robed राजन् Radiant सोम इति Soma. सः He उत्तस्थौ got up न not वोधयाञ्चकार (the king) roused तम् him आपेषम् by pushing (him) पाणिना by the hands. सः He उत्तस्थौ ह got up, awoke.

 Ajatshatru said—"It is against custom¹ that a Brāhman should approach a Kshatriya, thinking, 'He will teach me about Brahman.' I will, however, enlighten you about true Brahman." Seeing Gārgya abashed, the king took him up by the hand to set him at ease, and rose. They both (Gārgya and Ajatshatru) came to a sleeping man at a certain place. Ajatshatru addressed him by these names—"Great, Whiterobed, Radiant, Soma ?" Even though thus addressed the sleeping man did not get up. The king pushed him by his hands and roused him. Then he awoke.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. It is prohibited in the scriptures that lay down rules of conduct.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** स होवाचाजातशत्रुर्यत्रैष एतत्सुप्तोऽभूद्य एष विज्ञानमयः पुरुषः क्वैष तदाऽभूत्कुत एतदागादिति तदु ह न मेने गार्ग्यः॥१६॥**



 सः ह That अजातशत्रुः Ajatshatru उवाच said यत्र when एतत् that एषः this पुरुषः \*self यः who एषः this (is) विज्ञानमयः full of consciousness, identified with the intellect अभूत् was सुप्तः asleep क्व where अभूत् was, went एषः this तत् that कुतः whence आगात् (it) come एतत् इति it. गार्ग्यः Gargya मेने ह was aware of, knew न not तत् उ that.

 Ajatshatru said—"When this self¹ was identified with the intellect and got asleep,² where did it go in sleep ? Whence it came after sleep ?" Gārgya was not aware of that.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Self is not a modification of, but full of, the consciousness. Consciousness is that which is perceived in the intellect, which is perceived through it and which perceives through it.

 2. The self in profound sleep, does not perceive anything whatsoever like pleasure and so forth which are caused by the past work. In the waking state too it is not effected in reality by them. Therefore it is proved that self is nonattached.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **स होवाचाजातशत्रुर्यत्रैष एतत्सुप्तोऽभूद्य एष विज्ञानमयः पुरुषस्तदेषां प्राणानां विज्ञानेन विज्ञानमादाय य एषोऽन्तर्हृदय आकाशस्तस्मिञ्छेते तानि यदा गृह्णात्यथ हैतत्पुरुषः स्वपिति नाम तद्गृहीत एव प्राणो भवति गृहीता वाग्गृहीतं चक्षुर्गृहीत^(ꣳ) श्रोत्रं गृहीतं मनः॥१७॥**

——————————————————————————————

 \*The self dwells in the intellect as a man lives in a city (Puri). So it is called Purusha.

——————————————————————————————



 सः ह That अजातशत्रुः Ajatshatru उवाच said यत्र when एतत् that एषः this पुरुषः being यः who (is) विज्ञानमयः full of consciousness, associated with mind तत् it आदाय taking away, absorbing विज्ञानम् consciousness, functions, capacity to perceive एषाम् of these प्राणानाम् organs विज्ञानेन by its consciousness, instrument of knowledge, mind शेते lies अस्मिन् in that आकाशे sky, Supreme Self यः which एषः this (is) अन्तः inside हृदये the heart यदा when एतत् this पुरुषः being, Self, गृह्णाति takes, absorbs तानि them अथ ह then नाम (it is) called स्वपिति Swapiti (asleep). तत् Then एव indeed प्राणः the smell भवति is गृहीतः withdrawn, absorbed वाक् the organ of speech गृहीतं (is) absorbed, withdrawn, चक्षुः the eye गृहीता (is) absorbed, withdrawn, श्रोत्रम् the ear गृहीतम् (is) absorbed, withdrawn, मनः the mind गृहीतम् (is) absorbed, withdrawn.

 In order to convey his intended meaning Ajatashatru said—"When the self is identified with intellect and gets asleep, it takes away by the mind at the time the capacity of the organs to perceive and lies in the supreme self that dweils in the heart. When the self takes away the functions of the organs, it is called asleep.¹ During sleep the smell is withdrawn, the organ of speech is withdrawn, the eye is withdrawn, the ear is withdrawn, and the mind is also withdrawn.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. In deep sleep the self gives up its differentiated forms and remains in its undifferentiated form. It then rests in its own absolute nature.\]

——————————————————————————————



 **स यत्रैतत्स्वप्न्यया चरति ते हास्य लोकास्तदुतेव महाराजो भवत्युतेव महाब्राह्मण उतेवोच्चावचं निगच्छति स यथा महाराजो जानपदान्गृहीत्वा स्वे जनपदे यथाकामं परिवर्तेतैवमेवैष एतत्प्राणान्गृहीत्वा स्वे शरीरे यथाकामं परिवर्तते॥१८॥**

 यत्र When सः it (individual Self) एतत् this चरति moves, remains स्वप्न्यया in dream ते ह these, the following अस्य (are) its लोकाः worlds, achievements, results of past work it उत then इव as it were, apparently भवति becomes महाराजः Suzerain, Emperor, महाब्राह्मणः a noble Brahman उत indeed इव as it were, apparently यथा as सः that महाराजः Suzerain, Emperor, परिवर्तेत goes about, moves about यथाकामम् as he pleases, freely स्वे in his own जनपदे territory गृहीत्वा taking withdrawing जानपदान् (his) citizens एवम् thus एव indeed एषः it (the Self) एतत् this, (here) thus गृहीत्वा taking, withdrawing प्राणान् the organs परिवर्तेत goes about, moves about यथाकामम् as it pleases, freely स्वे in its own शरीरे body.

 When the self thus moves in dream which is a kind of perception, the following are the results of its past work. Apparently¹, not actually, it then becomes a suzerain, or a noble Brahman, or obtains high or low positions such as that of a god or an animal. As a suzerain takes his citizens, retinue and others who minister to his comforts and goes about freely in his own territory, so does the individual self withdraws the organs from the



places they occupy in the waking state and goes² about freely in its own body and not outside.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Self's becomings are apparent, because they are contradicted by waking state. The self has an unattached nature and is not connected in dream with grief, delusion, etc. The dream world is nothing but a reflection of this world perceived in the waking state. The dream experiences are therefore false. Likewise the waking experiences are also false and are super–impositions of ignorance.

 2. The self in dream experiences impressions that correspond to things perceived previously. Therefore in dream, worlds that never exist are falsely superimposed as being a part of the self. It is to be known from this that the worlds experienced in the waking state also are such. Hence it goes without saying that the. self is pure and is never connected with action, its factors and its results in dream.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **अथ यदा सुषुप्तो भवति यदा न कस्यचन वेद हिता नाम नाड्यो द्वासप्ततिः सहस्राणि हृदयात्पुरीततमभिप्रतिष्ठन्ते ताभिः प्रत्यवसृप्य पुरीतति शेते स यथा कुमारो वा महाराजो वा महाब्राह्मणो वाऽतिघ्नीमानन्दस्य गत्वा शयीतैवमेवैष एतच्छेते॥१॥**

 अथ Again यदा when भवति (the Self) becomes सुषुप्तः perfectly asleep, यदा when, वेद knows न not कस्यचन anything प्रत्यवसृप्य coming back, returning ताभिः alone there द्वासप्तति– seventy–two सहस्राणि thousand नाड्यः nerves नाम called हिता Hita अभिप्रतिष्ठन्ते (which) extend branch off पुरीततम् to the pericardium (the whole body) हृदयात् from the heart शेते



(and) remains पुरीतति in the body यथा as कुमारः वा a baby वा or महाराजः a Suzerain वा or महाब्राह्मणः a noble Brahmin गत्वा going, enjoying अतिघ्रीम् an acme, a degree अनादस्य of bliss शयीत lies, lives एवम् so एषः this एव indeed एतत् this (here) thus शेते remains.

 Again when the individual self becomes perfectly asleep¹ it has no particular² consciousness. From that state it returns to the waking along the seventy–two thousand nerves called Hita, which branch off from the heart³ and cover the whole body like the veins of an Aswattha leaf. In waking it remains in the body uniformly pervading it as a fire does a heated lump of iron. As a baby, or a suzerain whose subjects are entirely obedient, or a noble Brahman who is exceedingly mature in erudition and modesty and enjoys a degree of bliss, that blots out all misery entirely, so does the self remain in its own nature beyond all attributes during the profound sleep.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Even when it dreams, it remains pure as in the deep sleep.

 2. In profound sleep the self remains in its natural state of perfect purity. Then it gives up like water the impurity due to contact with other things.

 3. It is a lotus–shaped lump of flesh and the seat of the intellect, which is the internal organ and director of all external organs. The intellect which abides in the heart in

——————————————————————————————



the waking state extends along those nerves interwoven like a fish–net. The individual self pervades the intellect with a reflection of its own manifested consciousness. And when the intellect contracts, the self also contracts. That is the sleep state of the individual self. And when it perceives the expansion of the intellect, it is waking experience. The self follows the nature of the intellect, just as a reflection of the moon follows the nature of water.\]

 ** स यथोर्णनाभिस्तन्तुनोच्चरेद्यथाऽग्नेः क्षुद्रा विस्फुलिङ्गा व्युच्चरन्त्येवमेवास्मादात्मनः सर्वे प्राणाः सर्वे लोकाः सर्वे देवाः सर्वाणि भूतानि व्युच्चरन्ति तस्योपनिषत्सत्यस्य सत्यमिति प्राणा वै सत्यं तेषामेष सत्यम्॥२०॥ इति प्रथमं ब्राह्मणम्॥१॥**

 यथा As सः that ऊर्णनाभिः spider उच्चरेत् moves, comes out तन्तुना along the thread यथा as अग्नेः from a fire क्षुद्राः little, tiny विष्फुलिङ्गाः specks, sparks व्युच्चरन्ति fly, come forth एव just एवम् so अस्मात् from this आत्मनः self व्युच्चरन्ति emanate, proceeds सर्वे all प्राणाः organs, सर्वे all लोकाः worlds सर्वे all देवाः Gods, सर्वाणि (and) all भूतानि beings. तस्य Its उपनिषद् secret name (is) सत्यम् इति Truth सत्यस्य of truth.वै Verily प्राणाः the vital powers (are) सत्यम् truth. एषः It (is) सत्यम् the truth तेषाम् of them.

 As in this world a spider comes out along the thread it produces and as from one homogeneous fire, little specks^(1) come forth in different ways or numbers, just so from this self before it wakes up,



proceeds² all organs, all worlds (such as earth), all gods (such as fire who presides over all organs and worlds) and all living beings from Hiranyagarbha down to a clump of grass. The secret name of the self is Truth of truth. The vital power is truth and the self is the Truth of the vital power.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. This does not mean a change or a modification of the supreme self. The identity of the individual and the supreme self is taught in all the Upanishads. Then with the help of examples and arguments this truth which is the highest of all is established. The Vedantic teachers narrate the following parable to bring out the great truth: A certain prince was given up by his parents in childhood. The child was picked up and brought up by a fowler. Being ignorant of his royal lineage, the child thought himself to be a fowler and pursued the fowler's profession, not that of a prince as he would if he knew himself to be such. When however a very kind man who knew his princely descent and capacity told him who he was and that by some chance he came to live in a fowler's family, he gave up the false notion and took up the duties of a prince and followed the ways of his forefathers. Similarly this individual self which is of the same nature as the supreme self being separated from it like a spark of fire, has penetrated this wilderness of the body, organs, etc. Although it is in reality transcendent, it puts on the relative attributes of the latter and thinks itself to be the aggregate of body and organs, to be lean or stout, happy or miserable, on account of its forgetfulness of its real nature. But when the teacher enlightens him about his real

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

transcendent nature, then it discards the pursuit of three–fold desire and realises that it is the Brahman.

 2.Taittiriya Āranyaka (3.12.7.) says that the wise one projects all forms and then names them and goes on uttering those names.\]

——————————————————————————————

CHAPTER TWO: SECTION TWO

 ** यो ह वै शिशु^(ꣳ) साधान^(ꣳ) सप्रत्याधान^(ꣳ) सस्थूण^(ꣳ) सदामं वेद सप्त ह द्विषतो भ्रातृव्यानवरुणद्धि। अयं वाव शिशुर्योऽयं मध्यमः प्राणस्तस्येदमेवाऽऽधानमिदं प्रत्याधानं प्राणः स्थूणाऽन्नं दाम॥१॥**

 वै ह Verily यः who वेद knows शिशुम् the babe, the calf स+आधानम् with abode स+प्रत्याधानम् with special resort स+स्थूणाम् with post स+दामम् with rope, with tether ह indeed अवरुणद्धि keeps off, kills सप्त seven द्विषतः envious, भातृव्यान् relatives, kinsman अयम् This प्राणः vital power यः who (is) मध्यम् in the body वाव indeed (is) अयम् this शिशुः babe, calf. तस्य Its अवधानम् abode एव indeed इदम् (is) this (body). प्रत्याधानम् Special resort (is) इदम् this (head), प्राणः strength, power (born of food and drink ) स्थूणा post अन्नम् food दाम tether, rope.

 Verily he who knows the babe with its abode, special resort, host, and rope keeps off his seven relatives^(1) who envy him. Indeed the vital power



which in its five–fold form as the subtle body is like a babe and this body which is an effect is its abode; the head is its special resort; the power that comes out of food and drink is its post and food² is its rope.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Of the two kinds of relatives the envious and the friendly, the former is meant here. The seven sense organs such as the two eyes, two ears, two nostrils and the mouth which are channels of perception are situated in the head. The attachments to sense–objects which they cause are called relatives. Because they turn the vision of the person outward to the sense–objects and thus hinder him from perceiving the inner–self, they are called envious relatives.

 2. The food that is eaten is converted into three forms. The grossest form is execrated from the body and absorbed into the earth. The intermediate form which is chyle passes through the stages of blood, etc. and sustains the gross body composed of seven ingredients such as, skin, blood, flesh, fat, marrow, bone and semen. The body is the product of food. In the absence of food it decays and dies. The finest form of food called nectar and highly powerful goes past the navel to the heart and penetrates the seventy–two thousand nerves that radiate from there, generates power which is here designated as 'post', and thereby helps the subtle body which is the aggregate of the inner organs and is here called the 'babe' to live in the body. Therefore food is the connecting link between the vital force and the body like a calf's tether with a loop at either end.\]

——————————————————————————————



** तमेताः सप्ताक्षितय उपतिष्ठन्ते तद्या इमा अक्षन्लोहिन्यो राजयस्ताभिरेन^(ꣳ) रुद्रोऽन्वायत्तोऽथ या अक्षन्नापस्ताभिः पर्जन्यो या कनीनका तयाऽऽदित्यो यत्कृष्णं तेनाग्निर्यच्छुकं तेनेन्द्रोऽधरयैनं वर्तन्या पृथिव्यन्वायत्ता द्यौरुत्तरया नास्यान्नं क्षीयते य एवं वेद॥२॥**

 एताः These सप्त seven अक्षितयः imperishable gods, mantras instrument to prayer उपतिष्ठन्ते worship, pray तम् it (vital power). इमाः These लोहिन्यः pink, red राजयः lines याः which (are) तत् in that अक्षन् eye, ताभिः through them रुद्रः Rudra अन्वायत्तः attends, clings to एनम् it. अथ And आपः the water याः which (is) अक्षन् in the eye ताभिः through them पर्जन्यः Parjanya या which (is) कनीनका pupil (of the eye) तथा through that आदित्यः Sun यत् which (is) कृष्णम् dark (iris) तेन by that अग्निः fire यत् which (is) शुक्लं in white (eye ball) तेन through that इन्द्रः Indra अधरया through the lower वर्तन्या eye–lid पृथ्वी the earth अन्वायत्ता attends on, prays to एनम् it एवम् as such अस्य his अन्नम् food न not क्षीयन्ते be short, decrease.

 These seven imperishable gods (i.e. mantras instrumental to prayer) worship the vital power that is tied to the body by food and resides in the eye. The familiar red lines in the eye as aids the god Rudra prays to it. Through the aid of the water that is in the eye and comes out when there is contact with smoke, etc. the god Parjanya prays to it. Through the pupil which has the power of



sight the god,sun prays to it.Through the dark iris the god fire prays to it. Through the white eye–ball the god Indra prays to it. Through the lower eyelids, the god earth prays to it. And through the upper eyelid the god heaven prays to it. He who knows that these seven gods which are the food of the vital power constantly pray to it never gets short of food as a result of that knowledge.

 ** तदेष श्लोको भवति। अर्वाग्बिलश्चमस ऊर्ध्वबुध्नस्तस्मिन्यशो निहितं विश्वरूपम्। तस्याऽऽसत ऋषयः सप्त तीरे वागष्टमी ब्रह्मणा संविदानेति। अर्वाग्बिलश्चमस ऊर्ध्वबुध्न इतीदं तच्छिर एष ह्यर्वाग्बिलश्चमस ऊर्ध्वबुध्नस्तस्मिन्यशो निहितं विश्वरूपमिति प्राणा वै यशो विश्वरूपं प्राणानेतदाह तस्याऽऽसत ऋषयः सप्त तीर इति प्राणा वा ऋषयः प्राणानेतदाह वागष्टमी ब्रह्मणा संविदानेति वाग्ध्यष्टमी ब्रह्मणा संवित्ते॥३॥**

 तत् On this (subject) भवति (there) is एषः this श्लोकः mantra, verse चमसः (there is) a bowl, cup अर्वाग्बिलः having the mouth below. ऊर्ध्वबुध्नः bottom above तस्मिन् in that विश्वरूपम् manifold यशः Glory, knowledge निहितम् has been placed सप्तः Seven ऋषयः sages आसते sit तस्य on its तीरे lip, side वाक् the organ of speech सं विदाना communicating with, uttering ब्रह्मणा the Vedas अष्टमी इति (is) the eighth. चमसः The bowl, cup अर्वाग्बिलः having the mouth below, having the



bottom above, तत् that इदम् this (is) शिरः the head f because एषः it (is) चमसः the bowl, cup अर्वाग्बिलः having the mouth below ऊर्ध्वबुध्नः having the bottom above. तस्मिन् In that विश्वरूपम् manifold यशः Glory, knowledge निहितम् इति has been put वै Verily प्राणाः organs विश्वरूपम् manifold यशः Glory, knowledge एतत् this आह says, refers प्राणान् to organs. तस्य On its तीरे side, lip सप्तः Seven ऋषयः Sages आसते इति sit. वै Verily प्राणाः organs (are) ऋषयः the sages एतत् this आह says, refers प्राणान् organs. वाक् The organ of speech सं विदाना communicating with, uttering ब्रह्मणा the Vedas हि because वाक् organ of speech अष्टमी (is) the eighth संवित्ते (and) communicates with, utters T the Vedas.

 On this subject there is in the Atharva–Veda samhita (10.8.9) this mantra: There is a cup which has its mouth below and bottom above. Manifold knowledge has been placed in it. Seven sages (organs) sit by its side and the organ of speech which utters the Vedas is the eighth sage. 'The cup that has its mouth below and bottom above' is this head (of ours) which is shaped like a cup and has its opening below and bulges at the top. 'Manifold knowledge have been placed in it.' This refers to seven organs which are indeed the instruments, of perceiving sound, etc. 'Seven sages sit by its side' means that the seven organs are verily the sages. 'The organ of speech which utters, the Vedas' means that the organ of speech is the eighth¹ sage and utters the Vedas.



——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. The tongue being both the organ of taste as well as the organ of speech count as two. In this passage it is described as the organ of speech and in the next as the organ of taste, the seventh sage.—Anandagiri.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **इमामेव गोतमभरद्वाजावयमेव गोतमोऽयं भरद्वाज इमावेव विश्वामित्रजमदग्नी अयमेव विश्वामित्रोऽयं जमदग्निरिमावेव वसिष्ठकश्यपावयमेव वसिष्ठोऽयं कश्यपो वागेवात्रिर्वाचा ह्यन्नमद्यतेऽत्तिर्ह वै नामैतद्यदत्रिरिति सर्वस्यात्ता भवति सर्वमस्यान्नं भवति य एवं वेद॥४॥ इति द्वितीयं ब्राह्मणम्॥२॥**

 इमौ These two (ears) एव indeed गोतम–भरद्वाजौ (are) Gotama and Bharadwaja. अयम् This one (is) एव indeed गोतमः Gotam अयम् this (is) भरद्वाजः Bharadwaja. इमौ These two (eyes) एव indeed विश्वामित्रः जमदग्निः (are ) Viswamitra and Jamadagni. अयम् This one (is) एव indeed विश्वामित्रः Viswamitra. अयम् This (is) जमदग्निः Jamadagni. इमौ These two (nostrils) एव indeed वशिष्ठ–कश्यपौ Vashistha and Kashyapa. अयम् this one (is) एव indeed वशिष्ठः Vashistha अयम् this (is) Kashyapa. वाक् The tongue (is) एव indeed अत्रिः Atri; हि because वाचा through the tongue अन्नम् the food अद्यते is eaten. वै indeed एतत् this, familiar नाम name अत्तिः ह Atti (is) यत् which (is) अत्रिः इति Atri. यः Who वेद knows (it) एवम् as such (described above) भवति becomes अत्ता the eater सर्वस्य of all (food). सर्वम् All, every thing भवति becomes अस्य his अन्नम् food.

 These two ears are Gotama and Bharadwāja: The right one is Gotama and the left one is



Bharadwāja (or inversely). These two eyes are Viswāmitra and Jamadagni. The right one is Viswāmitra and the left one is Jamadagni (or inversely). These two nostrils are Vasistha and Kashyapa. This right one is Vasistha and this left one is Kashyapa (or inversely). The tongue is called Atri; because it eats food. Atri is only the familiar. name 'Atti' on account of being the eater. He who knows the true nature of vital power as described above becomes the eater¹ of all kinds of food belonging to the vital power and every thing becomes² his food.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES— 1. In the next world he becomes only the eater of all food and is never looked upon as food.

 2. He becomes the vital power in the body and becomes. only the eater of food and never is treated as food.\]

——————————————————————————————

CHAPTER TWO: SECTION THREE

 **द्वे वाव ब्राह्मणों रूपे मूर्तं चैवामूर्तं च मर्त्यं चामृतं च स्थितं च यच्च सच्च त्यच्च॥१॥**

वाव Indeed, emphatically ब्राह्मणः of Brahman (Supreme–Self) द्वे two रूपे aspects, forms, (are there) एव indeed मूर्तं च gross, च and अमूर्तम् subtle मर्त्यं च mortal च and अमृतम् immortal, स्थितम् limited च and यत् unlimited, pervasive सत्



च defined, made conceivable च and तत् undefined, inconcievable.

 \[Brahman has two aspects, the conditioned and the unconditioned. Conditioned Brahman is connected with body and organs and consists of actions and their factors and results, and admits of all kinds of association. But unconditioned Brahman is above duality and devoid of all limiting adjuncts and beyond the reach of even speech and mind. By the superimposition of these forms supreme Brahman becomes defined or made conceivable.\]

 Brahman indeed has only two aspects, gross and subtle, subject to destruction and immortal, limited and pervasive, conceivable and inconceivable.¹

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Which is undefined, i.e. only referred to distantly as something we know not what.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **तदेतन्मूर्तं यदन्यद्वायोश्चान्तरिक्षाच्चैतन्मर्त्यमेतत्स्थितमेतत्सत्तस्यैतस्य मृर्तस्यैतस्य मर्त्यस्यैतस्य स्थितस्यैतस्य सत एष रसो य एष तपति सतो ह्येष रसः॥२॥**

 एतत् This मूर्तं च gross, compact, solid (form) तत् (is) that यत् which अन्यत् (is) other, different वायोः च than air च and अन्तरिक्षात् than the ether. एतत् This (triad of elements) मर्त्यम् (is) mortal, subject to destruction, एतत् this (is) स्थितम्



limited, एतत् this (is) सत् defined, made conceivable. एषः This रसः essence तस्य of that एतस्य this मूर्तस्य gross एतस्य of this मर्तस्य mortal, perishable. एतस्य of this स्थितस्य limited एतस्य of this स्थितस्य defined यः which एषः this (sun) तपति shines: हि because एषः this (is) रसः the essence सतः of the defined (three elements).

 \[The gross and the subtle have each four features. The four phases of the gross form is shown first.\]

 The gross form is that which is different from air and the ether, i.e., earth, water and fire. This triad of elements is perishable. It is limited. It is defined. The shining sun which represents the cosmic body is the essence of the gross form which is perishable, limite¹ and defined; because it is the quintessence of the three elements.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Because it is related with some other object. As a jar when joined to a post or wall is checked by it, so is the limited form by other objects.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** अथामूर्तं वायुश्चान्तरिक्षं चैतदमृतमेतद्यदेतत्त्यं तस्यैतस्यामूर्तस्यैतस्यामृतस्यैतस्य यत एतस्य त्यस्यैष रसो य एष एतस्मिन्मण्डले पुरुषस्त्यस्य ह्येष रस इत्यधिदैवतम्॥३॥**

 अथ Now अमूर्तम् the subtle (form) वायुः च air च and अन्तरिक्षम् the ether एतत् this (is) अमृतम् immortal, not subject to destruction. एतत् This (is) यत् unlimited, pervasive.



एतत् It (is) त्यत् undefined एषः This (is) रसः essence तस्य of that एतस्य this अमृतस्य subtle, एतस्य of that अमृतस्य immortal एतस्य of that यतः unlimited, एतस्य of that त्यस्य undefined, that can only be indirectly described एषः this पुरुषः (is) being यः who (is) एतस्मिन् in this मण्डले Sun, हि because एषः this (is) रसः the essence तस्य of it. इति अधिदैवतम् (This is) with regard to the Gods.

 Now the subtle form is being set forth. It is the air and the ether. The subtle form is immortal. It is pervasive. It is something that can only be indirectly described because it cannot be distinguished from others. The essence of the subtle, immortal, pervasive and undefined (that is, of the two subtle elements each having four attributes) is the being¹ that is in the sun; because that being is the essence of the undefined. This is with regard to the gods.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Being means here the cosmic subtle body of Hiranyagarbha. The seven beings such as the five senseorgans, the organ of speech and mind are made one in the subtle body. Shatapath Brahmana (6.1.1.3) says: They made these seven beings into one in the subtle body.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** अथाध्यात्ममिदमेव मूर्तं यदन्यत्प्राणाच्च यश्चायमन्तरात्मन्नाकाश एतन्मर्त्यमेतत्स्थितमेतत्सत्तस्यैतस्य मूर्तस्यैतस्य मर्तस्यैतस्य स्थितस्यैतस्य सत एष रसो यच्चक्षुः सतो ह्येष रसः॥४॥**



 अथ Now अध्यात्मम् with regard to the body. मूर्तम् The gross (form ) इदम् एव (is) but this यत् which (is) अन्यः other प्राणात् च than the (corporeal) air यः which (is) अयम् this आकाशः ether अन्तरात्मन् in the body एतत् This ( is ) मर्त्यम् mortal एतत् it (is) स्थितम् limited. एतत् It (is) सत् defined. एषः This (is) रसः essence तस्य of that एतत्य this मूर्तत्य Gross एतत्य of this मर्तस्य mortal एतस्य of this स्थितस्य limited एतस्य of this सतः defined यत् which (is) चक्षुः the eye; हि because एषः this (is) रसः the essence सतः of the defined.

 Now the division of the gross and subtle with regard to the body is described. The gross form is, indeed, the three constituent elements of the body, other than the corporeal air and the ether. The subtle body is mortal. It is limited. It is defined. The eye¹ is the essence of the gross, mortal, limited and defined; for it is the essence of the defined (that is, the three gross materials that build up the body).

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Because the eye lends importance to the three elements in the whole body, just as the sun does with regard to the gods. The three elements are also prior to the other two in point of time. In the Shatapath Brahmana (4.2.1.28) it is rightly said that the eyes are formed first in the embryo.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **अथामूर्तं प्राणश्च यश्चायमन्तरात्मन्नाकाश एतदमृतमेतद्यदेतत्त्यं तस्यैतस्यामूर्तस्यैतस्यामृतस्यैतस्य यत एतस्य त्यस्यैष रसो योऽयं दक्षिणेऽक्षन्पुरुषस्त्यस्य ह्येष रसः॥५॥**



 अथ Now अमूर्तम् the fine, the subtle (form). अयम् It (the fine form) प्राणः च is the (corporeal) air च and आकाशः the. ether यः who (is) अन्तः–आत्मन् in the body. एतत् It (the fine) अमृतम् (is) immortal. एतत् It (is) यत् unlimited. एतत् It (is) त्यत् undefined. एषः This रसः essence तस्य of that एतत्य of that अमूर्तस्य subtle (form). एतस्य Of that अमृतस्य immortal एतस्य of that यतः unlimited एतस्य (and) of that त्यस्य undefined (being) यः who अयम् this पुरुषः being (is) दक्षिणे in the right अक्षन् eye हि for एषः this (is) रसः essences त्यस्य of the undefined.

 Now the fine form is being described. The fine form is the corporeal air and the ether that is in the body. The fine form is immortal. The fine form is unlimited. The fine form is undefined. The fine form is the essence of that Being which is subtle, immortal, unlimited and undefined. It is specified in the scriptures that the fine form is especially manifest in right eye. It is the essence of the undefined and cannot be definitely perceived.

 **तस्य हैतस्य पुरुषस्य रूपम्। यथा महारजनं वासो यथा पाण्ड्वाविकं यथेन्द्रगोपो यथाऽग्न्यर्चिर्यथा पुण्डरीकं यथा सकृद्विद्युत्त^(ꣳ) सकृद्विद्युत्तेव ह वा अस्य श्रीर्भवति य एवं वेदाथात आदेशो नेति नेति न ह्येतस्मादिति नेत्यन्यत्परमस्त्यन्थ नामधेय^(ꣳ) सत्यस्य सत्यमिति प्राणा वै सत्यं तेषामेष सत्यम्॥६॥ इति तृतीयं ब्राह्मणम्॥६॥**



 रूपम् The form तस्य of that एतस्य this पुरुषस्य ह being (is described). यथा As वासः a cloth महारजनम् Saffron–coloured dyed with turmeric, यथा as पाण्ड्वाविकम् Grey sheep's wool, यथा as इन्द्रगोपः deep red insect calls Indra Gopa, यथा as अग्नि–अर्चिः a tongue of fire, यथा as पुण्डरीकम् a white-lotus, यथा as सकृत् one, single विद्युतम् flash of lightening. यः Who वेद knows एवम् as described above वै ह verily अस्य his श्रीः splendour, fame भवति gets, becomes, इव like सकृत् once विद्युत्ता flash of lightening. अथ Now अतः therefore आदेशः the description (of Brahman) न इति not this: हि because अस्ति there is न no अन्यत् other परम् better, more appropriate (description) एतस्मात् इति than this, न इति not this. अथ Now नामधेयम् its names. सत्यम् The truth सत्यस्य of truth वै verily प्राणः the vital powers (is) सत्यम् truth एषः it (self) सत्यम् (is) the truth तेषाम् of them.

 Now the form of that being who is identified with the subtle body¹ is described. As a cloth is dyed with turmeric, so is the mind tinged with impressions^(2) in the presence of sense–objects. As a sheep's wool is grey, so are some forms of impressions. As the scarlet insect called Indragopa, is deep red, so are some impressions of the mind. As a tongue of fire is bright, so are some people's impressions at times. Like a white lotus too are impressions of some. As a single flash of lightning illumines everything, so the impressions of Hiranyagarbha which suddenly manifests itself as he



emanates from the undifferentiated. He who knows the particular form of impressions belonging to Hiranyagarbha gets fame suddenly, like a single flash of lightning. Now therefore follows the description of Brahman. 'Not this, Not this^(3') is the best description of Brahman; because there is no description which is more appropriate than this. Now Its secret name is 'the Truth of truth.' The vital power is truth and the Self is 'the Truth of:  
truth.'

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. The subtle body consists of impressions and is produced by the union of the intellect and the impressions of the gross and subtle objects. It is variegated like pictures on a canvas or a wall. It is comparable to an illusion, or a magic or a mirage and is puzzling to all. But it ceases to exist in the state of profound sleep.

 2. The colouring of impressions varies sometimes according to the objects presented to the mind and sometimes according to the tendencies of the mind itself. It is impossible to ascertain the beginning, or middle or end, or number or place, or time or cause of these impressions; for they are innumerable and infinite are their causes.

 3. These two negative particles are used not only to eliminate the two limiting adjuncts, the gross and the subtle forms, but also to eliminate all possible specifications and predications that may occur to us about Brahman who is free from all differentiations of limiting adjuncts. The supreme self has no distinguishing marks such as name or form or action or heterogeneity, or species or qualities.\]

——————————————————————————————



 **मैत्रेयीति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्य उद्यास्यन्वा अरेऽहमस्मात्स्थानादस्मि हन्त तेऽनया कात्यायन्याऽन्तं करवाणीति॥१॥**

 याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said मैत्रेयि इति Maitreyi वै verily अरे my dear अहम् I अस्मि intend, wish उद्यास्यन् to renounce अस्मात् from this स्थानात् place, life of householder हन्त well करवाणि इति wish to make अन्तम् an end ते between you अनया with this कात्यायन्या इति (and) Katyayani.

 \[The following story is introduced with a view to enjoin renunciation of the world as the means to self–knowledge.\]

 The sage Yajnavalkya said to his wife Maitreyi: 'My dear, I intend to renounce this householder's life in order to take up the life of renunciation. Permit me, therefore, to divide my property between you and Katyayani, and make an end of my relationship with you both.'

 ** सा होवाच मैत्रेयी। यन्नु म इयं भगोः सर्वा पृथिवी वित्तेन पूर्णा स्यात्कथं तेनामृता स्यामिति नेति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यो यथैवोपकरणवतां जीवितं तथैव ते जीवित‍^(ꣳ) स्यादमृतत्वस्य तु नाऽऽशाऽस्ति वित्तेनेति॥२॥**

 सा That मैत्रेयी Maitreyi उवाच ह said, asked, भगोः revered sir यत् if नु indeed इदम् this सर्वा whole पृथ्वी earth पूर्णा full



वित्तेन by wealth स्यात् be मे mine तेन through that कथम् how स्याम् (I) shall be अमृता इति immortal ? याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said, replied न इति no. ते You जीवितम् life स्यात् will be एव just तथा so यथा as एव indeed जीवितम् the life उपकरणवताम् of those having plenty. तु But अस्ति (there) is न no, आशा hope अमृतत्वस्य of immortality वित्तेन इति by wealth, by rites performed with wealth.

 Thus addressed Maitreyi asked—'shall the rites such as the Agnihotra performed with the entire wealth of the earth make me immortal ?' Yajnavalkya replied in the negative and added: 'Your life will be like the life of people having plenty, but even in thought there is no hope of immortality by rites performed with wealth¹.'

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Vyasdev says in the Mahabharat (12.247.1, 2, 7): Men are bound by rites and freed by knowledge. Rites performed according to scriptures results in progress leading up to the world of Hiranyagarbha. But if the rites are not performed in accordance with scriptures they make way for degradation to the level of stationary objects. Supreme self alone is the goal of the Upanishads, while relative existence consisting of ends and means of rites lies within the realm of ignorance. That is why Yajnavalkya who was a performer of rites in his householder's life renounced the world. Because knowledge of Brahman obliterates all ignorance together with its effects and makes one absolutely free.\]

——————————————————————————————



 ** सा होवाच मैत्रेयी येनाहं नामृता स्यां किमहं तेन कुर्यां यदेव भगवान्वेद तदेव मे ब्रूहीति॥३॥**

 सा That मैत्रेयि Maitreyi ह then उवाच said, replied किम् what अहम् I कुर्याम् shall do तेन with that येन by which अहम् I न not स्याम् shall be अमृता immortal ? भगवान् revered sir ब्रूहि tell मे me तत् of that एव alone यत् which एव indeed वेद इति (you) knows.

 Thus addressed Maitreyi replied—' What shall I do with that wealth by which I shall not be immortal ? Tell me; revered sir, of that alone which you know to be the only means of immortality.'

 **स होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः प्रिया बतारे नः सती प्रियं भाषस एह्यास्स्व व्याख्यास्यामि ते व्याचक्षाणस्य तु मे निदिध्यासस्वेति॥४॥**

 सः That याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya उवाच said बत अरे my dear सती (you) have been नः my प्रिया beloved, dear (now) भाषसे (you) say प्रियम् (what is) dear (to my heart). एहि come आसस्व Take (your) seat, seated व्याख्यास्यामि (I) will explain, will describe ते to you तु but मे mine व्याचक्षाणस्य (while) explaining, describing. निदिध्यासस्व उति meditate on, reffect.

 When rites performed with wealth were given up as a means of immortality.

 Yajnavalkya was highly pleased with Maitreyi and said to her: You have been dear to me even



before and now you say what is very dear to my heart. Therefore come and be seated near me. I will describe to you the knowledge of self which confers immortality. But while I describe it, reflect steadfastly on it.'

 ** स होवाच न वा अरे पत्युः कामाय पतिः प्रियो भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय पतिः प्रियो भवति। न वा अरे जायायै कामाय जाया प्रिया भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय जाया प्रिया भवति। न वा अरे पुत्राणां कामाय पुत्राः प्रिया भवन्त्यात्मनस्तु कामाय पुत्राः प्रिया भवन्ति। न वा अरे वित्तस्य कामाय वित्तं प्रियं भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय वित्तं प्रियं भवति। न वा अरे ब्रह्मणः कामाय ब्रह्म प्रियं भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय ब्रह्म प्रियं भवति। न वा अरे क्षत्रस्य कामाय क्षत्रं प्रियं भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय क्षत्रं प्रियं भवति। न वा अरे लोकानां कामाय लोकाः प्रिया भवन्त्यात्मनस्तु कामाय लोकाः प्रिया भवन्ति। न वा अरे देवानां कामाय देवाः प्रिया भवन्त्यात्मनस्तु कामाय देवाः प्रिया भवन्ति। न वा अरे भूतानां कामाय भूतानि प्रियाणि भवन्त्यात्मनस्तु कामाय भूतानि प्रियाणि भवन्ति। न वा अरे सर्वस्य कामाय सर्वं प्रियं भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय सर्वं प्रियं भवति। आत्मा वा अरे द्रष्टव्यः श्रोतव्यो मन्तव्यो निदिध्यासितव्यो मैत्रेय्यात्मनो वा अरे दर्शनेन श्रवणेन मत्या विज्ञानेनेद^(ꣳ) सर्वं विदितम्॥५॥**



सः He (Yajnavalkya) उवाच ह said वै verily अरे my dear न not कामाय for the sake पत्युः of husband पतिः the husband भवति is प्रियः dear तु but कामाय for the necessity आत्मनः of the self पतिः the husband भवति is प्रियः dear वै Verily घरे my dear न not कामाय for the sake जायायै of the wife जाया the wife भवति is प्रिया dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self जाया the wife भवति is प्रिया dear वै Verily अरे my dear न not कामाय for the sake पुत्रानाम् of the sons पुत्राः the sons भवन्ति are प्रिया dear तु but कामाय for the necessity श्रात्मनः of the self पुत्राः the sons भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear वै Verily अरे my dear न not कामाय for the necessity वित्तस्य of wealth वित्तम् the wealth भवति is प्रियम् dear तु but कामाय for the sake of आत्मनः of the self वित्तम् the wealth भवति is प्रियम् dear loved वै Verily अरे my dear न not कामाय for the necessity ब्राह्मणः of Brahmin ब्रह्म Brahmin, भवति is प्रियम् dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self ब्रह्म Brahmin भवति is प्रियम् dear. वै Verily अरे my dear न not कामाय for the necessity क्षत्रस्य of the Kshatriya क्षत्रम् the Kshatriya भवति is प्रियम् dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self क्षत्रम् the Kshatriya भवति is प्रियम् dear वै Verily अरे my dear न not कामाय for the sake of लोकानाम् the worlds लोकाः the worlds, भवन्ति are प्रियः dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self लोकाः the worlds, भवन्ति are प्रियम् dear वै Verily अरे my dear न not कामाय for the sake देवानाम् of the gods, देवाः the gods भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self, देवाः the gods, भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear. वै Verily अरे my dear न not कामाय for the sake भूतानाम् of beings भूतानि



the beings भवन्ति are प्रियाणि dear तु but कामाय for the necessity आत्मनः of the self भूतानि the beings भवन्ति are प्रियाणि dear. वै Verily अरे my dear न not कामाय for the sake सर्वस्य of all सर्वः all भवति is प्रियः dear, loved तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self सर्वम् all भवति is प्रियः dear. वै Verily आत्मा the self द्रष्टव्यः should be seen, should be made the object of realization, श्रोतव्यः should be heard of मन्तव्यः reflected on, निदिध्यासितव्यो meditated upon, अरे my dear मैत्रेयि Maitreyi वै verily अरे my dear दर्शनेन by the vision, by the realization आत्मनः of the self विज्ञानेन through hearing मत्या through reflection (and) विज्ञानेन through meditation सर्वम् all, इदम् this विदितम् (is) known.

 \[In the passage (1.4.8) it has been said that the self is dearer than a son, etc. The following text serves as a detailed commentary on that. It shows that in truth our love for the self is primary whereas our love for other objects is secondary. Because everything else contributes to the love of the self.\]

 Yajnavalkya said to Maitreyi: Verily the husband is dear to the wife not for the necessity of the husband, but for the sake of the self he is dear to her. Verily the wife is dear to the husband not for the necessity of the wife, but for the sake of the self she is dear to him. Verily the sons are dear to the parents not for the necessity of the sons, but for the sake of the self they are dear. Verily the



wealth is dear not for the necessity of the wealth, but for the sake of the self that wealth is dear. Verily the Brāhmin is dear not for the necessity of the Brahmin but for the sake of the self he is dear. Verily the Kshatriya is dear not for the necessity of the Kshatriya, but for the sake of the self that he is dear. The worlds are dear to men not for the necessity of the worlds, but for the sake of the self they are dear. The gods are dear not for the necessity of the gods, but for the sake of the self they are dear. Beings¹ are dear not for the necessity of beings, but for the sake of the self they are dear. All^(2) is dear not for the necessity of all, but for the sake of the self all is dear. The self, my dear Maitreyi, should be made the object of realisation. For that purpose the self should first be heard of from a teacher and from the scriptures, then reflected on through reasoning and then steadfastly meditated upon. By the realisation of the self, my dear, through hearing, reflection and meditation, all³ this is known.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. The priority of enumeration is in the order of closeness of objects to us as sources of joy. Because it is all the more desirable first to create a distaste for the objects that are very close to us.

 2. It includes everything that has been and has not been mentioned.

——————————————————————————————





——————————————————————————————

3\. Various orders of life, castes and so on are false notions superimposed on the self by ignorance like the false perception of a snake on a rope. These notions are destroyed by self–knowledge.

——————————————————————————————

** ब्रह्म तं परादात् योऽन्यत्रात्मनो ब्रह्म वेद क्षत्रं तं परादात् योऽन्यत्रात्मनः क्षत्रं वेद लोकास्तं परादुर्योऽन्यत्रात्मनो लोकान् वेद देवास्तं परादुः योऽन्यत्रात्मनो देवान् वेद भूतानि तं परादुः योऽन्यत्रात्मनो भूतानि वेद सर्वं तं परादात् योऽन्यत्रात्मनः सर्वं वेद इदं ब्रह्म इदं क्षत्रमिमे लोका इमे देवा इमानि भूतानि इद‍^(ꣳ) सर्वं यदयमात्मा॥६॥**

 ब्रह्म The Brahman परादात् ousts, rejects तम् him यः who वेद knows considers ब्रह्म the Brahman अन्यत्र other than, different from आत्मनः the self. क्षत्रम् The Kshatriya परादात् ousts, rejects तम् him यः who वेद knows, considers क्षत्रम् the Kshatriya अन्यत्र different from आत्मनः the self. लोकाः The worlds परादुः oust, reject, तम् him यः who वेद knows लोकान् the worlds, अन्यत्र other than आत्मनः the self. देवाः The Gods परादुः rejects तम् him यः who वेद considers देवान् the Gods अन्यत्र different from आत्मनः the self. भूतानि The beings परादुः oust तम् him यः who वेद knows भूतानि the beings अन्यत्र different from आत्मनः the self. सर्वम् All परादात् ousts तं him यः who वेद knows सर्वम् all अन्यत्र different from आत्मनः all. इदम् This ब्रह्म Brahman, इदम् this क्षत्रम् Kshatriya, इमे these लोकाः worlds, इमे these देवाः Gods इमानि these भूतानि beings इदम् this सर्वम् all (are) यत् that अयम् this आत्मा self.



 The Brāhmin rejects him who considers the Brahmin to be different from the self. The Kshatriya abandons him who knows the Kshatriya to be other than the self. The worlds oust him who considers the worlds to be different from the self. The gods abandon him who knows that gods are not the self. The beings reject him who considers the beings to be different from the self. All oust him who considers all to be other than the self. This Brāhmin, this Kshatriya, these worlds, these gods, these beings and this all are nothing but the self.

** स यथा दुन्दुभेर्हन्यमानस्य न बाह्यान् शब्दान् शक्नुयात् ग्रहणाय दुन्दुभेस्तु ग्रहणेन दुन्दुभ्याघातस्य वा शब्दो गृहीतः॥७॥**

 सः That (the example is). यथा As (one) न not शक्नुयात् is able गृहणाय for the seizure बाह्यान् of external शब्दान् notes. दुन्दुभेः of a drum हन्यमानस्य being beaten तु but शब्दः the sound गृहीतः (is) seized, ग्रहणेन by the seizure, दुन्दुभेः of the drum वा or दुन्दुभि–आघातस्य of the beater of the drum.

 As one cannot seize the external (particular) notes of a drum (or the like) when beaten (with a stick etc.), but the sound is seized by the seizure of the drum or its beater.



** स यथा शङ्खस्य ध्मायमानस्य न बाह्यान् शब्दान् शक्नुयात् ग्रहणाय शङ्खस्य तु ग्रहणेन शङ्खध्मस्य वा शब्दो गृहीतः॥८॥**

 सः That यथा as (one) न not शक्नुयात् is able गृहणाय for seizure वाह्यान् of external शब्दान् sounds, शङ्खस्य of the conch ध्मायमानस्य being blown, तु but शब्दः the sound गृहीतः (is) seized ग्रहणेन by the seizure शङ्खस्य of the conch वा or शङ्खध्मस्य blower of the conch.

 As one cannot seize the external (particular) notes of a conch when blown, but the sound is seized by the seizure of the conch or its blower.

** स यथा वीणायै वाद्यमानायै न बाह्यान् शब्दान् शक्नुयात् ग्रहणाय वीणायै तु ग्रहणेन वीणावादस्य वा शब्दो गृहीतः॥९॥**

 सः That यथा as (one) न not शक्नुयात् is able गृहणाय for the seizure बाह्यान् of external, शब्दान् notes वीणायै (वीणायाः) of the Vina, वाद्यमानायै being played, तु but शब्दः the sound (is) seized ग्रहणेन by the seizure, वीणाये of the fute वा or वीणावादस्य the Vina player.

 As one cannot seize the external (particular) notes of a Vina when played, but the sound is seized by the seizure of the Vina or its player.

 \[As the sound of the drum, conch or Vina has no separate existence apart from the drum, conch or Vina, similarly nothing particular is perceived



in the waking and dream states apart from self or Brahman. Therefore those things are to be looked upon as non–existent and the self to be perceived in and through them. Many examples are cited here to indicate that genus, sentient and insentient, are various but they are all included in the supreme genus—the self or Brahman.\]

** स यथा आर्द्रैधाग्नेरभ्याहितात् पृथग्धूमा विनिश्चरन्ति एवं वा अरेऽस्य महतो भूतस्य निःश्वसितमेतत् यत् ऋग्वेदो यजुर्वेदः सामवेदोऽथर्वाङ्गिरस इतिहासः पुराणं विद्या उपनिषदः श्लोकाः सूत्राण्यनुव्याख्यानानि व्याख्यानान्यस्यैवैतानि सर्वाणि निःश्वसितानि॥१०॥**

 सः That (the example is): यथा As धूमाः Smokes. पृथक् Separately विनिश्वरन्ति issue, proceed, अभ्याहितात् from a lighted आद्रैधाग्नेः (आद्र+एध+अग्नेः) fire kindled with damp fuel, एवम् even so वै verily अरे my dear अस्य of this महतः great, infinite. भूतस्य Reality एतत् this निःश्वासितम् (is) breathed out यत् which (is) ऋग्वेदः the Rig–Veda यजुर्वेदः Yajur–Veda सामवेदः Sama–Veda अथर्वाङ्गिरसः Atharvangirasa इतिहासः History पुराणम् mythology विद्या arts उपनिषदः Upanishad श्लोकाः Verses, Mantras, सूत्राणि aphorisms अनुव्याख्यानानि elucidations व्याख्यानानि (and) explanations, eulogistic passages. एतानि They निःश्वासितानि (are) breathed out एव indeed अस्य of this (supreme Self).



 As various clouds of smoke, sparks, etc. proceed from a lighted fire¹ kindled with damp fuel, even so, my dear Maitreyi, the Rig–Veda, Yajur–Veda, Sama–Veda, Atharvangirasa, history², mythology³, arts⁴ (treating of music, dancing, etc.), Upanishads, mantras occurring in the Brahmanas, Vedic aphorisms⁵, elucidations of aphorisms, and explanations of the mantras are breathed⁶ out of this great Reality, the Brahman (Self). They are indeed like the breath of this supreme Self.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. As before the separation of the sparks, smokes, embers and flames, all these are nothing but fire, so it is reasonable to infer that this universe differentiated into names and forms is before its origin nothing but Brahman. Name and form are to Brahman as foam is to water.

 2. Such as the dialogue between the nymph Urvashi and Pururavas occurring in the Shatapath Brahman (11.4.4.1).

 3. Such as "this universe was in the beginning unmanifested" in Taittereya Upanishad (2.7).

 4. This also Veda says, Shatapath Brahmana (13.4.3.10–14.)

 5. Passages of the Vedas which treat the truth in a nut–shell. For example—'The Self alone is to be meditated upon.'

 6. As breath come out of a man without any thought or effort on his part, so do all these issue easily out of Brahman.\]

——————————————————————————————

** स यथा सर्वासामपा^(ꣳ) समुद्र एकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वेषा^(ꣳ) स्पर्शानां त्त्वक् एकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वेषां गन्धानां नासिके एकायनमेव‍^(ꣳ)**



**सर्वेषा^(ꣳ) रसानां जिह्वा एकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वेषा^(ꣳ) रूपाणां चक्षुरेकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वेषा^(ꣳ) शब्दाना^(ꣳ) श्रोत्रमेकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वेषा^(ꣳ) सङ्कल्पानां मन एकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वासां विद्याना^(ꣳ) हृदयमेकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वेषां कर्मणा^(ꣳ) हस्तावेकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वेषामानन्दानामुपस्थ एकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वेषां विसर्गाणां पायुरेकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वेषामध्वनां पादावेकायनमेव^(ꣳ) सर्वेषां वेदानां वागेकायनम्॥११॥**

 सः That (the example is): यथा As समुद्रः the sea (is) एकायनम् (एक+अयनम् ) the one goal, the only meeting place, the sole place of unification सर्वाणाम् of all. अपाम् Water; एवम् as त्वक् the skin, touch in general perceived by the skin. एकायनम् (is) meeting place, centre सर्वेषाम् of all. स्पर्शानाम् touch; एवम् as नासिके the nostrils, odour in general एकायनम् the meeting place सर्वेषाम् of all गन्धानाम् odours; एवम् as जिह्वा the tongue, taste in general एकायनम् (are) the goal सर्वेषाम् of all रूपानाम् colours; एवम् as श्रोत्रम् the ears, sound in general एकायनम् (is) the goal, centre सर्वेषाम् of all शब्दानाम् sounds; एवम् as मनः the mind एकायनम् (is) the goal, meeting place सर्वेषाम् of all सङ्कल्पानाम् deliberations; एवम् as हृदयम् the heart (intellect) एकायनम् (is) the goal, centre सर्वेषाम् of all विद्यानाम् knowledge; एवम् as हस्तौ the hand एकायनम् (is) the goal सर्वेषाम् of all कर्मणाम् work; एवम् as उपस्थं the organ of generation एकायनम् (is) the goal सर्वेषाम् of all आनन्दानाम् sense pleasure, enjoyments; एवं as पायुः the anus (is) एकायनम् the goal सर्वेषाम् of all विसर्गाणाम् excretions; एवम् as पादौ the legs एकायनम् (is) the centre:



सर्वेषाम् of all अध्वनां walking; एवम् as वाक् the organ of speech एकायनम् (is) the meeting place सर्वेषाम् of all वेदानाम् the Vedas.

 As the sea is the meeting place of all sorts of water (such as that of the rivers, tanks and lakes); as the skin is the one goal of all kinds of touch (such as soft or hard, rough or smooth); as the nostrils (odour in general) are the centre of all odours (which are modes of earth); as the tongue (taste in general perceived by the tongue) is theplace of unification of all savours (which are modes of water); as the eye (colour in general perceived by the eyes) is the meeting place of all colours (which are modes of light); as the ear (sound in general perceived by the ear) is the one goal of all sounds; as the mind is the source of all deliberations; as the intellect is the centre of all kinds of knowledge; as the hands are the one goal of all sorts of work; as the generative organ is the centre of all sense–pleasures; as the anus is the meeting. place of excretions; as the legs are the one goal of all kinds of walking; as the organ of speech is the place of unification of all Vedas.

 \[The examples are illustrative of dissolution. The Universe is nothing but Brahman not only at the time of its origin and continuance but also at the time of dissolution. Just as bubbles, foam, etc..



have no existence separate from water, so name, form and action have no reality apart from Brahman. The organs are but modes of the objects perceived by them. Therefore they also fall within the same category as the objects.\]

 **स यथा सैन्धवखिल्य उदके प्रास्त उदकमेवानुविलीयेत न हास्य उद्ग्रहणायेव स्यात् यतो यतस्त्वाददीत लवणमेव एवं वा अर इदं महद्भूतमनन्तमपारं विज्ञानधन एव एतेभ्यो भूतेभ्यः समुत्थाय तान्येवानु विनश्यन्ति न प्रेत्य सञ्ज्ञास्तीति अरे ब्रवीमीति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः॥१२॥**

 सः That (the example is): यथा as सैन्धवखिल्यः \* a lump of salt प्रास्तः thrown, dropped उदके into water अनुविलीयत dissolves एव indeed उदकम् with water न no स्यात् (one) is able एव at all उत्ग्रहणाय for the picking up अस्य ह of it तु but यतः यतः whence so ever, from which so ever part. आददीत (one) takes लवणम् (it tastes) salt एव only एवम् even so वै verily अरे my dear इदम् this महत् great भूतम् reality, truth अनन्तम् (is) endless अपारम् infinite एव indeed विज्ञानघनः solid mass of intelligence. समुत्थाय coming out एतेभ्यः from these भूतेभ्यः elements. विनश्यति is destroyed एव indeed अनु with तानि them प्रेत्य (individuality ) having ceased. सञ्ज्ञा (particular) consciousness न not अभि इति exists

——————————————————————————————

 \* The derivative meaning of the word 'Sindhu' is water, because it flows. That which is a modification or product of water is 'Saindhava' i.e. salt, as salt is the product of Sea–water which is saline.

——————————————————————————————



अरे my dear इति this ब्रवीमि (I) say याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya उवाच said, propounded ह so.

 As a lump of salt thrown into water becomes dissolved into water and none, not even an expert can at all pick it up, but from whichsoever part one takes the water and tastes it, it tastes saltish, but there is no longer any lump; even so, my dear Maitreyi, this great, endless, infinite Reality is a solid mass of Intelligence¹. With the aid of these elements the Self comes² out separately as a lump salt. When this separateness is destroyed, the individualised existence of the self ceases along with them. After attaining oneness with the supreme self particular consciousness of the self. does not exist. This I say, my dear. So Yājnavalkya propounded the philosophy of self to his wife, Maitreyi.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. It excludes all foreign elements like a solid mass of gold or iron.

 2. As from water reflections of the sun and moon arise or as in the proximity of red cotton pads a transparent crystalturns red, so in the contact of body, organs and sense–objects the Self appears as an individualised entity. By the realisation of Brahman, these limiting adjuncts which are the cause of: its individualisation are dissolved like the foam and bubbles in water.\]

——————————————————————————————



** सा होवाच मैत्रेय्यत्रैव मा भगवानमूमुहन्न प्रेत्य सञ्ज्ञाऽस्तीति स होवाच न वा अरेऽहं मोहं ब्रवीम्यलं वा अर इदं विज्ञानाय॥१३॥**

 सा That मैत्रेयी Maitreyi उवाच ह said एव just अत्र here भगवान् revered Sir. अमूमुहत् (you) have confused मा me प्रेत्य having departed. अस्ति there is न not सञ्ज्ञा इति consciousness. सः ह He उवाच said, replied: वै verily अहम् I न not ब्रवीमि say मोहम् anything confusing अरे my dear वै verily इदम् this (is) अलम् quite enough विज्ञानाय for knowledge.

 Thus enlightened Maitreyi said: 'just here, venerable sir, you have confused me by saying that after attaining oneness the Self loses particular consciousness.'Yājnavalkya replied: 'O Maitreyi, verily I am not using any confusing language. This great Reality¹ is indeed quite enough for knowledge.'

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Explained in the last paragraph.\]

——————————————————————————————

** यत्र हि द्वैतमिव भवति तदितर इतरं जिघ्रति तदितर इतरं पश्यति तदितर इतर^(ꣳ) शृणोति तदितर इतरमभिवदति तदितर इतरं मनुते तदितर इतरं विजानाति यत्र वा अस्य सर्वमात्मैवाभूत्तत्केन कं जिघेत्तत्केन कं पश्येत्तत्केन क^(ꣳ) शृणुयात्तत्केन कमभिवदेत्तत्केन कं मन्वीत तत्केन कं विजानीयात्।**



** येनेद^(ꣳ) सर्वं विजानाति तं केन विजानीयाद्विज्ञातारमरे केन विजानीयादिति॥१४॥ इति चतुर्थं ब्राह्मणम्॥४॥**

 हि Because यत्र when भवति there is द्वैतम् duality इव as it were, apparently तत् then. इतरः one जिघ्रति smells इतरम् the other, something; तत् then इतरः one पश्यति sees इतरम् the other; तत् then इतरः one शृणोति hears इतरम् the other; तत् then इतरः one अभिवदति speaks इतरम् the other; तत् then इतरः one मनुते thinks इतरम् the other -; तत् then इतरः one विजानाति knows इतरम् the other. वै Verily यत्र when अस्य of him (the knower) सर्वम् all अभूत् has become एव only आत्मी the Self तत् then केन through what जिघ्रेत् (one) smells कम् what ? तत् then केन through what पश्येत् (one) sees कम् what ? तत् then शृणुयात् (one) hears कम् what केन through what, तत् then कम् what अभिवदेत् (one) speaks केन through what ? तत् then मन्वीत् (one) thinks कम् what केन through what ? तत् then विजानीत knows कम् what केन through what ? येन By whom इदम् this सर्वम् all विजानाति (one) knows केन through what विजानीयात् (one) should know तम् it. अरे My dear केन through what विजानीयात् इति (one) should know सिज्ञातारम् the knower.

 In the state of ignorance^(1) there is apparent duality in Brahman, then one smells the other, one sees the other, one hears the other, one speaks the other, one thinks something, one knows something. But to the knower of Brahman all name and form become merged in the Self. In the state of



self–knowledge what object one should smell and through what instrument ? What one should see and through what ? What one should hear and through² what ? What one should think and through what ? What one should think and through what ? What one should know and through what organ ? Through what instrument one should know That  
by which all this is known. Through what, O Maitreyi, one should know³ the knower

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. This is the state of ignorance.

 2. The words 'what' and 'through what' are used as a fling to suggest the sheer impossibility of the other factors of an action.

 3. As the fire cannot burn itself, so the Self does not know itself as an object.\].

——————————————————————————————

CHAPTER TWO: SECTION FIVE

** इयं पृथिवी सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्यै पृथिव्यै सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्यां पृथिव्यां तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चायमध्यात्म^(ꣳ) शारीरस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥१॥**

 इदम् This पृथ्वी earth (is) मधु (like) honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. सर्वाणि All भूतानि beings (are) मधु (like) honey (effect) असौ to this पृथ्वी earth. अयम् This तेजोमयः



bright, effulgent अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः who (is) अस्याम् in this पृथिव्याम् earth. अयम् This तेजोमयः shining, bright अमृतमयः immortal शरीरः corporeal पुरुषः being च and यः who (is) अध्यात्मम् in this body अयम् this (is) एव indeed सः that आत्मा Self च and यः who (is) अयम् this आत्मा Self this (knowledge of Brahman) अमृतम् (is the means of) immortality. इदम् This (underlying unity) ब्रह्म (is) Brahman. इदम् This सर्वम् (is) all.

 This earth is the honey to all beings from. Hiranyagarbha down to a clump of grass. Likewise all beings are the honey (effect) of this earth. Also the bright immortal being who is identified with this earth and the effulgent, immortal being¹ who is incorporated in this body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. These² fourfold division is nothing but the Self. This self–knowledge is the only means of immortality. The unity that underlies the phenomena is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman is the means of becoming all.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. The Self as identified with the subtle body.

 2. These four are the composite effect of all beings and all beings are the effects of these four. Brahman from which the universe has sprung up is alone real; and everything else is an effect, a modification, a mere name, an effort of speech merely.\]

——————————————————————————————



** इमा आपः सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वासामपा^(ꣳ) सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमास्वप्सु तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चायमध्यात्म^(ꣳ )रैतसस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥२॥**

 इमाः This आपः water (is) मधु honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. सर्वाणि All भूतानि beings (are) मधु honey आसाम् of this अपाम् water अयम् This तेजोमयः shining, bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः who (is) आसु in this अप्सु water, अयम् this तेजोमयः shining, effulgent अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being रैतसः identified with semen (seed) अध्यात्मम् in the body. सः That (is) अयम् this एव indeed यः who (is) अयम् this आत्मा Self इदम् this अमृतम् (is) immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This (is)सर्वम् all.

 Similarly this water is honey to all beings, and all beings are honey to this water. The effulgent immortal being who is identified with water^(1), and the bright immortal being who is identified with the seed in this body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but the Self. This self–knowledge is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman is the means of becoming all.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NoTES—1. In the body it exists especially in the seed.\]

——————————————————————————————



** अयमग्निः सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्याग्नेः सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्मिन्नग्नौ तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चायमध्यात्मं वाङ्मयस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद‍^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥३॥**

 अयम् This अग्निः fire मधु (is) honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. सर्वाणि All भूतानि beings मधु honey अस्य of this अग्नेः fire. अयम् This तेजोमयः shining, bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः च who (is) अस्मिन् in this अग्नौ fire एव indeed. सः That (is) अयम् this यः च who (is) अयम् this (self). इदम् This (is) अमृतम् immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This (is) सर्वम् all.

 This fire is honey to all beings and all beings are honey to this fire. The effulgent, immortal being who is identified with fire and the bright immortal being who is identified with the organ^(1) of speech in the body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. These fourfold division is nothing but the Self. This self-knowledge is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman is the means of becoming all,

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. In the body it exists especially in the organ of speech.\]

——————————————————————————————

** अयं वायुः सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्य वायोः सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्मिन्वायौ तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चायमध्यात्मं**



**प्राणस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥४॥**

 अयम् This वायुः air मधुः (is) honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings अस्य of this वायोः air सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings (are) मधु honey. अयम् This तेजोमयः shining, bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः Being यः च who (is) अस्मिन् in this वायौ air, अयम् this तेजोमयः shining, effulgent अमृतमयः immortali पुरुषः being यः च who (is) प्राणः the vital power अध्यात्मम् in the body. अयम् This एव indeed सः that यः which अयम् this आत्मा Self इदम् this (is) अमृतम् immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This (is) सर्वम् all.

 This air is honey to all beings, and all beings are honey to the air. The bright immortal being who is identified with the air¹, and the effulgent immortal being who is identified with the vital power in the body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but this Self. This self–knowledge is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman is the means of becoming all.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Air and other elements are called honey because they help the body to furnish materials.\]

——————————————————————————————

** अयमादित्यः सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्याऽऽदित्यस्य सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्मिन्नादित्ये तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चा-**



**यमध्यात्मं चाक्षुषस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥**५**॥**

 अयम् This आदित्यः Sun मधुः (is) honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings अस्य of this आदित्यस्य Sun सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings मधुः (are ) honey अयम् this being तेजोमयः shining, bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः च who (is) अस्मिन् in this अदित्ये Sun अयम् this तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being चाक्षुषः identified with the eye, ocular अध्यात्मम् in the body सः that अयम् this एव indeed यः च who (is) अयम् this आत्मा Self इदम् this (is) अमृतम् immortality इदम् this (is) ब्रह्म Brahman इदम् this (is) सर्वम् all.

 This sun is honey to all beings and all beings are honey to the sun. The bright immortal being who is identified with the sun and the bright immortal being who is identified with eye in the body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but this Self. This knowledge of Self is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman is the means of becoming all.

** इमा दिशः सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वासां दिशा^(ꣳ) सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमासु दिक्षु तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चायमध्यात्म^(ꣳ) श्रौत्रः प्रातिश्रुत्कस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥**६**॥**



 इमाः These दिशः directions, quarters, मधु (is) honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings, आसाम् of these दिशाम् directions सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings (are) मधु honey. अयम् This तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः च who (is) आसु in these दिक्षु directions. अयम् This तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः deathless पुरुषः being श्रोत्रः identified with the ear प्रातिश्रुत्कः identified with the time of hearing अध्यात्मम् in the body. सः That अयम् this एव indeed यः च who अयम् (is) this आत्मा Self इदम् this अमृतम् immortality इदम् this (is) ब्रह्म Brahman इदम् this (is) सर्वम् all.

 These directions¹ are honey to all beings and these beings are honey to these directions. The bright immortal being who is identified with these directions and the bright immortal being who is identified with the ear and the time of hearing in the body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but this self. This knowledge of Self is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman (of Self) is the means of becoming all.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Although the ear is the counterpart of the directions in the body, yet the being who is identified with time of hearing is mentioned on account of its being specially manifest at the time of hearing sounds.\]

——————————————————————————————



** अयं चन्द्रः सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्य चन्द्रस्य सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्मि^(ꣳ) चन्द्रे तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चायमध्यात्मं मानसस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेदँ सर्वम्॥७॥**

 अयम् This चन्द्रः moon मधु (is) honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूनानाम् beings. अस्य of this चन्द्रस्य moon सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings मधु (is) honey. अयम् This तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः च who (is) अस्मिन् in this चन्द्रे moon (and) अयम् this तेजोमयः bright, shining अमृतमयः deathless पुरुषः being यः च who (is) मानसः identified with the mind अध्यात्मम् in the body. सः That अयम् this एव indeed यः who (is) अयम् this आत्मा Self इदम् this (is) अमृतम् immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This (is) सर्वम् all.

 This moon is honey to all beings and all beings are honey to this moon. The bright im-mortal being who is identified with this moon and the bright immortal being who is identified with the mind in the body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but the self. This knowledge of self is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman (of Self) is the means of becoming all.

** इयं विद्युत्सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्यै विद्युतः सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्यां विद्युति तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चायमध्यात्मं**



**तैजसस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥**८**॥**

 इदम् This विद्युत् lightning मधु (is) honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. अस्यै of this विद्युत् lightning सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings (are) मधु honey. अयम् This तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः च who (is) अस्याम् in this विद्युति lightning (and) अयम् this तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः च who (is) तैजसः identified with light अध्यात्मम् in the body. अयम् This एव indeed सः (is) that यः which (is) अयम् this आत्मा Self. इदम् This (is) अमृतम् immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This (is) सर्वम् all.

 This lightning is honey to all beings and all beings are honey to this lightning. The bright immortal being who is identified with the lightning and the bright immortal being who is identified with light manifest in the organ of touch in this body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but this self. This knowledge of self is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman (of Self) is the means of becoming all.

** अय^(ꣳ) स्तनयित्नुः सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्य स्तनयित्नोः सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्मिन्स्तनयित्नौ तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः**



**पुरुषो यश्चायमध्यात्म^(ꣳ) शाब्दः सौवरस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥९॥**

 अयम् This स्तनयित्नुः cloud मधु (is) honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. अस्य of this स्तनयित्रोः cloud सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings (are) मधु honey. अयम् This तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः who (is) अस्मिन् in this स्तनयित्तौ cloud (and) अयम् this तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुष being यः च who is शाब्दः identified with sound सौवत् identified with voice अध्यात्मम् in the body. अयम् This (is) एव indeed सः that यः who (is) अयम् this आत्मा Self. इदम् This अमृतम् immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This (is) सर्वम् all.

 This cloud is honey to all beings and all beings are honey to this cloud. The bright immortal being who is identified with this cloud and the bright immortal being who is specially manifest in voice and identified with sound and voice in this body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but this self. This knowledge of self is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman (Self) is the means of becoming all.

** अयमाकाशः सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्याऽऽकाशस्य सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्मिन्नाकाशे तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चाय-**



**मध्यात्म^(ꣳ) हृद्याकाशस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥१०॥**

 अयम् This आकाशः sky, ether (is) मधु honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. अस्य of this आकाशस्य sky, ether सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings (are) मधु honey. अयम् This तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः who (is) अस्मिन् in this आकाशे ether, अयम् (and) this तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः who (is) आकाशः identified with ether हृदि in the heart अध्यात्मम् in the body. अयम् This (is) एव indeed सः that यः who (is) अयम् this आत्मा Self. इदम् This (is) अमृतम् immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This (is) सर्वम् all.

 This ether is the honey to all beings and all beings are honey to this ether. The bright immortal being who is identified with this ether, and the bright immortal being who is identified with the ether in the heart in the body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but this self. This knowledge of self is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman (Self) is the means of becoming all.

** अयं धर्मः सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्य धर्मस्य सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्मिन्धर्मे तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चायमध्यात्मं**



**धार्मस्तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥११॥**

 अयम् This धर्मः Dharma मधु (is) honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. अस्य of this धर्मस्य Dharma सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings (are) मधु honey. अयम् This तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः who (is) अस्मिन् in this धर्मे Dharma (and) अयम् this तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being धार्मः identified with Dharma अध्यात्मम् in the body. अयम् This (is) एव indeed सः that यः who (is) अयम् this आत्मा Self. इदम् This (is) अमृतम् immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This (is) सर्वभू all.

 This Dharma (justice)¹ is honey to all beings. and all beings are honey to this Dharma. The bright immortal being who is identified with this Dharma (justice) and the bright immortal being who is identified with Dharma in this body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but this self. This knowledge of self is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is. Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman (Self) is the means of becoming all.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Dharma is not directly perceived, only its effects—the earth, etc. are directly perceived. In the passage (1.4.14.) Dharma is explained as that which consists of the

——————————————————————————————



shrutis and smritis. It is the power which directs even the Kshatriyas, etc. and causes the manifold universe through the transformation of the elements. Dharma also is practised by people. These—truth and justice—have been stated as identical. But here both are separately mentioned, because they produce their effects in a distinct form—visible and invisible. Justice that is invisible, is called Apurva, or original, and produces invisible effects in a general and a particular form. In its general form, it controls the earth and elements, and in its particular form it fashions the aggregate of body and organs, in corporeal matters.\]

** इद^(ꣳ) सत्य^(ꣳ) सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्य सत्यस्य सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्मिन्सत्ये तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चायमध्यात्म^(ꣳ) सात्यस्तेजोमयोमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥१२॥**

 इदम् This सत्यम् truth मधु (is) honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. अस्य of this सत्यस्य truth सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings (is) मधु honey. अयम् This तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः who (is) अस्मिन् in this सत्ये truth अयम् (and) this तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being सात्यः identified with truth अध्यात्मम् in the body. अयम् This (is) एव indeed सः that यः who (is) अयम् this आत्मा Self. इदम् This अमृतम् (is) immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This सर्वम् (is) all.

 This truth^(1) is honey to all beings and all beings are honey to this truth. The bright immortal



being who is in the truth that is inherent in the elements and consists of present action and the bright immortal being identified with the truth that is inherent in the body and organs are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them.
