This fourfold division is nothing but this self. This knowledge of self is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman (Self) is the means of becoming all.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Dharma (justice) in its visible form as good conduct is called Truth. It also is twofold—general and particular. The general form is inherent in the elements and the particular form is inherent in the body and organs. Rightly Mahanarayan Upanishad (22.1) says: The wind blows through Truth.\]

——————————————————————————————

** इदं मानुष^(ꣲ) सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्य मानुषस्य सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्मिन्मानुषे तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥१३॥**

 इदम् This मानुषम् human (and other) species (is) मधुः honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. अस्य of this मानुषस्य man सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings मधु (are) honey. अयम् This तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः च who (is) अस्मिन् in this मानुषे man (and) अयम् this तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः च who (is) मानुषः identified with



human species (in the body). अयम् This (is) एव indeed सः that यः who अयम् this आत्मा Self. इदम् This (is) अमृनम् immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This (is) सर्वम् all.

 This human (and other) species are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to this human (and other) species. The bright immortal being who is in this human (and other) species and the bright immortal being who is identified with the human and other species in the body are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but this self. This knowledge of self is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman is the means of becoming all.

** अयमात्मा सर्वेषां भूतानां मध्वस्याऽऽत्मनः सर्वाणि भूतानि मधु यश्चायमस्मिन्नात्मनि तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषो यश्चायमात्मा तेजोमयोऽमृतमयः पुरुषोऽयमेव स योऽयमात्मेदममृतमिदं ब्रह्मेद‍^(ꣳ) सर्वम्॥१४॥**

 अयम् This आत्मा (cosmic) body (is) मधु honey सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. अस्य Of this आत्मनः body सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings (are) मधु honey. अयम् This तेजोमय bright अमृतमयः immortal पुरुषः being यः च who (is) अस्मिन् in this



आत्मनि (cosmic) body (and) अयम् this तेजोमयः bright अमृतमयः immortal being यः च who (is) अयम् this आत्मा (individual) Self. अयम् This (is) अमृतम् immortality. इदम् This (is) ब्रह्म Brahman. इदम् This (is) सर्वम् all.

 This cosmic¹ body is honey to all beings and all beings are honey to this cosmic body. The bright immortal being² who is identified with this cosmic body and the bright immortal being who is identified with this individual self are honey to all beings and all beings are honey to them. This fourfold division is nothing but this self.³ This knowledge of the self is the only means of immortality. This unity that underlies all is Brahman. This knowledge of Brahman (Self) is the means of becoming all.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. The cosmic body is the aggregate of bodies and organs. It is connected with the human and other species, and is devoid of all distinctions pertaining to the body and the elements. It consists of all elements and gods.

 2. It refers to the cosmic mind which is the essence of the subtle and has also no limitations.

 3. The entity that is meant here is the individual self whose purpose this aggregate of gross and subtle bodies subserve.\]

——————————————————————————————

** स वा अयमात्मा सर्वेषां भूतानामधिपतिः सर्वेषां भूताना^(ꣳ) राजा तद्यथा रथनाभौ च रथनेमौ चाराः सर्वे समर्पिता एवमे-**



**वास्मिन्नात्मनि सर्वाणि भूतानि सर्वे देवाः सर्वे लोकाः सर्वे प्राणाः सर्व एत आत्मानः समर्पिताः॥१५॥ **

 वै Verily सः that अयम् this आत्मा self अधिपतिः (is) the ruler सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings, राजा the king सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. तत् That यथो just as सर्वे all आाराः च spokes रथ–नाभौ च in the nave of a chariot wheel, रथ–नेमौ च and in the felloe of a chariot wheel, समर्पिताः are fixed एवम् So अस्मिन् in this एव very आत्मनि Self, सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings, सर्वे all देवाः gods, सर्वे all लोकाः worlds, सर्वे all प्राणाः organs. (and) सर्वे all एते these आत्मनः (individual) Selves, समर्पिताः (are) fixed.

 The Supreme Self is the absolute ruler (self) of all beings, the king¹ of all creatures. Just as all spokes are fixed in the nave and the falloe of a chariot–wheel, so are all beings from Hiranyagarbha down to a clump of grass all gods such as fire, all worlds such as this earth, all organs, and all these individual selves are fixed in this Supreme Self.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Not like a prince or a minister but a king.\]  
 \[Even before realisation one has always remained Brahman, but through ignorance, one considered himself different from It. One has always been all, but through ignorance one thought himself otherwise. Therefore banishing this ignorance through the knowledge of Brahman, the knower of Brahman, having all the while been Brahman, became Brahman and having all the time being all, became

——————————————————————————————



all. As the rising sun dispells the gloom of night, so the knowledge of Brahman removes ignorance.\]

** इदं वै तन्मधु दध्यङ्ङाथर्वणोऽश्विभ्यामुवाच। तदेतदृषिः पश्यन्नवोचत्। तद्वां नरा सनये द^(ꣳ)स उग्रमाविष्कृणोमि तन्यतुर्न वृष्टिम्। दध्यङ् ह यन्मध्वाथर्वणो वामश्वस्य शीर्ष्णा प्र यदीमुवाचेति॥१६॥**

 वै Verily इदम् this (is) तत् that मधु (विद्या) Secret meditation, Self–knowledge दध्यङ् Dadhyach, आथर्वणः versed in the Atharva–Veda उवाच taught, proclaimed, अश्विभ्याम् the two Ashwins, ऋषिः sage (Kakshivat) पश्यन् seeing, perceiving तत् that एतत् this अवोचत् said नराः O heroic Ashwins, तत् that उग्रम् fearful, terrible दंसः deed वाम् you both (did) सनये out of gain आविष्कृणोमि (I) will make manifest, will disclose न \* as, like तन्यतुः the lightening, the cloud वृष्टिम् (does) rain यत् that मधु (विद्या) secret meditation, Self–knowledge यत् ईम् + which दध्यङ् Dadhyach आथर्वणः versed in the Atharva–Veda प्र उवाच taught, proclaimed वाम् you both शीर्ष्णा through the head अश्वस्य of the horse.

 This is verily that secret meditation known as self–knowledge which Dadhyach¹ versed in the Atharva–Veda proclaimed to the two Ashwins. Seeing this, sage Kakshivat² said, 'O heroic

——————————————————————————————

 \* The particle 'na' after a word in the Vedas denotes comparison, not negation.

 + 'im' is an expletive.

——————————————————————————————



Ashwins, that fearful deed which you performed out of gain, I will disclose as a cloud indicates rain through rumbling noise. I will make manifest this secret meditation known as self–knowledge which Dadhyach, versed in the Atharva–Veda, proclaimed to you through a horse's head.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. The story of how Dadhyach taught self–knowledge to the two Ashwins is given in Shatapatha Brāhmana (14.1.1.22-24) as follows: It was a favourite subject to the Ashwins. Dadhyach came to them and wished to teach them this knowledge. Dadhyach said to them: Indra threatened me that he will cut off my head the moment I teach this knowledge to anybody. Therefore I am afraid of him. If he does not behead me then I will teach you this secret meditation. Ashwins said in reply: "We will save you from his threat." Dadhyach wanted to know how they will save him. Ashwins said: "When you will accept us as your disciples, we shall behead you, take your head to a safe place and preserve it there. Then we will bring a horse's head and fix it on you. You will teach us the knowledge through that head. When you teach us Indra will cut off that head of yours and then we shall bring back your original head and replace it on you." Brahman Dadhyach agreed to this device and accepted them as his disciples. When he did so, they beheaded him and preserved it in a safe place; then brought a horse's head and fixed it on him. Through that head Dadhyach taught them the knowledge. When he was teaching them, Indra cut off that head. Then the Ashwins brought his own head and replaced it on him.

——————————————————————————————



2\. Verses appearing in passages 16, 17 and 19. See Rig–Veda 1. CXVI. 12, 1. CXVII. 22 and VI. XLVII. 18 respectively.\]

** इदं वै तन्मधु दध्यङ्ङाथर्वणोऽश्विभ्यामुवाच। तदेतदृषिः पश्यन्नवोचत्। आथर्वणायाश्विना दधीचेऽश्व^(ꣳ) शिरः प्रत्यैरयतम्। स वां मधु प्रवोचदृतायत्वाष्ट्रं यद्दस्रावपि कक्ष्यं वामिति॥१७॥**

 वै Verily इदम् this (is) तत् that मधु (विद्या) secret meditation (which) दध्यङ् Dadhyach आथर्वणः versed in the Atharva–veda उवाच said to, taught अश्विभ्याम् the two Ashwins ऋषिः sage (Kakshivat ) पश्यन् seeing, perceiving तत् that एतत् this अवोचत् said अश्विना O heroic Ashwins. प्रत्यैरयतम् (You) set, fix अश्वम् a horse's शिरः head दधीचे on Dadhyach आथर्वणाय versed in the Atharva–Veda. दस्रौ O fearful ones वाम् to you ऋतायन् (सन्) to fulfil promise, to keep word प्रवोचत् (he) proclaimed, taught. वाम् You मधु (= मधु विद्या) the (ritualistic) meditation. त्वाष्ट्रम् Connected with the Sun यत् as अपि also कक्ष्यम् the spiritual meditation.

 This is verily that secret meditation which Dadhyach, versed in the Atharva–Veda, proclaimed to the two Ashwins. The sage Kakshivat who visualised this mantra said,— 'when the Brāhmana's head was severed, O heroic Ashwins, you cut off a horse's head and fixed it on the shoulders of Dadhyach who is versed in the Atharva–Veda. O fearful ones, in order to fulfil his promise the



Brahmana taught you the (ritualistic) meditation connected with the sun¹ as also the secret meditation on them relating to Supreme Self.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. When, the head of Vishnu was cut off, he became the sun. To replace the head of Vishnu the rite called pravargya was commenced. The meditation with regard to the severance and restoration of Vishnu's head, etc. which forms a part of the rite is the ritualistic meditation connected with the sun. The story as follows appears in Shatapath Brahman (14.1.1.6-10) as well as Taittiriya Aranyak (5.1.3-6); Once Vishnu became proud of his power and excellence over the other gods and stood resting his chin on the end of a bow. Then the other gods out of jealousy got some white ants to gnaw off the bow–string. This resulted in the severance of Vishnu's head.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **इदं वै तन्मधु दध्यङ्ङाथर्वणोऽश्विभ्यामुवाच। तदेतदृषिः पश्यन्नवोचत्। पुरश्चक्रे द्विपदः पुरश्चक्रे चतुष्पदः। पुरः स पक्षी भूत्वा पुरः पुरुष आविशदिति। स वा अयं पुरुषः सर्वासु पूर्षु पुरिशयो नैनेन किञ्चनानावृतं नैनेन किञ्चनासंवृतम्॥१८॥**

 वै Verily इदम् this तत् that मधु (विद्या) secret meditation दध्यङ् Dadhyach आथर्वणः versed in the Atharva Veda उवाच proclaimed, taught अश्विभ्याम् the Ashwins. ऋषिः Rishi पश्यन् seeing, perceiving तत् that एतत् this अवोचत् said: चक्रे (He) made, created पुरः bodies द्विपदः with two feet. चक्रे (He) made, fashioned पुरः bodies चतुष्पदः with four–feet सः that पुरुषः supreme being भूत्वा becoming पक्षी a bird (the



subtle body) आविशत् entered पुरः the bodies. वै Verily सः that अयम् this पुरुषः is (called) Purush पुरिशयः on account of dwelling सर्वासु in all पूर्षू bodies. न Not किञ्चन anything अनेन by him अनावृतम् (न+आवृतम् ) not covered, enveloped. न Not किञ्चन anything अनेन by him न not असंवृतम् pervaded.

 This is verily that secret meditation known as self–knowledge which Dadhyach versed in the Atharva–Veda proclaimed to the Ashwins. Seeing this the Rishi Kakshivat said—'The Supreme Being created human and bird bodies with two feet and animal bodies with four feet. That supreme Being first entered the created bodies as subtle bodies. As He dwells in all bodies He is called Purush. There is nothing that is not enveloped¹ by Him in its inside and outside. There is nothing that is not pervaded by Him.'

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. The Supreme Being as name and form (i.e. body and organ) is the inside and outside of everything.\]

——————————————————————————————

** इदं वै तन्मधु दध्यङ्ङाथर्वणोऽश्विभ्यामुवाच। तदेतदृषिः पश्यन्नवोचत्। रूप^(ꣳ) रूपं प्रतिरूपो बभूव तदस्य रूपं प्रतिचक्षणाय। इन्द्रो मायाभिः पुरुरूप ईयते युक्ता ह्यस्य हरयः शता दशेति। अयं वै हरयोऽयं वै दश च सहस्राणि बहूनि चानन्तानि च तदेतद्ब्रह्मापूर्वमनपरमनन्तरमबाह्यमयमात्मा ब्रह्म सर्वानुभूरित्यनुशासनम्॥१९॥ इति पञ्चमं ब्राह्मणम्॥५॥**



 वै Verily इदम् this (is) तत् that मधु (विद्या) secret. meditation दध्यङ् Dadhyach आथर्वणः versed in the Atharva–Veda proclaimed to, taught the Ashwins ऋषिः Sage (Kakshivat) पश्यन् seeing, perceiving तत् that एतत् this अवोचत् said. बभूव (He) was प्रतिरूपः transferred, assumed likeness रुपं रूपम् into each form. तत् That रूपम् form अस्य of him प्रतिचक्षणाय for making manifest (known) इन्द्रः the lord ईयते is perceived पुरु–रूपः manifold मायाभिः through maya, divese knowledge, false identification; हि because दशः ten हरयः organs शताः hundreds (of them ) युक्ताः (are) yoked, अस्य to him. वै Verily अयम् he हरयः (is) the organs. वै Verily अयम् He (is) दश ten सहस्राणि (and) thousands च and बहूनि many च and अनन्तानि infinite तन्त् that एतत् this ब्रह्म Brahman अपूर्वम् without prior (cause), अनपरम् without posterior (effect), अनन्तरम् without interior, अबाह्यम् without exterior. अयम् This आत्मा Self सर्वानुभूः the perceiver of all, ब्रह्म (is) Brahman इति अनुशासनम् This (is) the teaching, gist.

 This is that secret meditation which Dadhyach, versed in the Atharva–Veda, proclaimed to the two Ashwins. The sage Kakshivat who visualised this mantra said: 'The Supreme Being assumed the likeness of each form. He put on so many forms to make Himself manifest.^(1) On account of false identifications with name and form he is apparently perceived as manifold, not truly. Because to Him are yoked, like horses to a chariot, ten organs called



Hari², nay hundreds of them as there are infinite beings. He has become the organs. He has become ten and thousands, many and infinite organs. That Brahman is without cause, without effect, without interior, without exterior. This Supreme Self, who perceives everything, is Brahman. This is the gist of all Vedant Texts.'

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. It is, therefore, possible to know the transcendent nature of the Self through name and form.

 2. Sense–organs are called Hari because they draw us to sense–objects.\]

——————————————————————————————

CHAPTER TWO: SECTION SIX

** अथ व^(ꣳ)शः पौतिमाष्यो गौपवनाद्गौपवनः पौतिमाष्यात्पौतिमाष्यो गौपवनाद्गौपवनः कौशिकात्कौशिकः कौण्डिन्यात्कौण्डिन्यः शाण्डिल्याच्छाण्डिल्यः कौशिकाच्च गौतमाच्च गौतमः॥१॥**

 अथ Now वंशः\* the line of teachers and pupils. पौतिमाष्यः Pautimashya गौषवनात् from Gaupavana. गौपवनः Gaupavana

——————————————————————————————

 \*The line of teachers is called Vamsa in Sanskrit, because it resembles to a Vamsa (bamboo). Like bamboo this line of teachers, from the top down to the bottom, is divided into sections. The order of succession of teachers of the first four chapters of the last book of the Shatapatha Brahman (of which the first chapter of this Upanishad forms the third chapter of Kanwa recension) is here given. The names in the nominative case belong to the disciples and those in the ablative are of the teachers.

——————————————————————————————



पौतिमाष्यात् from (another) Pautimashya. पौतिमाष्यः (This) Pautimashya गौपवनात् from (another) Gaupavana. गौपवनः (This) Gaupavana कौशिकात् from Kaushik. कौशिकः Kaushika कौण्डिन्यात् from Kaundinya. कौण्डिन्यः Kaundinya शाण्डिल्यात् from Shandilya. शाण्डिल्यः Shandilya कौशिकात् from Kaushika च and गौतमात् from Gautam गौतमः Gautam.

 Now follows the geneology of teachers and pupils by whom the Madhu¹ kanda was handed down: Pautimashya received the Vidya (knowledge) from Gaupavana. Gaupavana from another Pautimashya. This Pautimashya from another Gaupavana. This Gaupavana from Kausika. Kausika from Kaundinya. Kaundinya from Shandilya. Shandilya from Kausika and Gautama. Gautama (from Agniveshya).

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. The first two chapters of this Upanishad is called Madhukānda which aim at expounding the knowledge of Brahman.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **आग्निवेश्यादाग्निवेश्यः शाण्डिल्याच्चानभिम्लाताच्चानभिम्लात आनभिम्लातादानभिम्लात आनभिम्लातादानभिम्लातो गौतमाद्गौतमः सैतवप्राचीनयोग्याभ्या^(ꣳ) सैतवप्राचीनयोग्यौ पाराशर्यात्पाराशर्यो भारद्वाजाद्भारद्वाजो भारद्वाजाच्च गौतमाच्च गौतमो भारद्वाजाद्भारद्वाजः पाराशर्यात्पाराशर्यो बैजवापायनाद्बैजवापायनः कौशिकायनेः कौशिकायनिः॥२॥**



 अग्निवेश्यात् (Gautam) from Agniveshya अग्निवेश्यः Agniveshya शाण्डिल्यात् च from Shandilya च and आनभिम्लातात् from Anabhimlata. आनभिम्लातः Anabhimlata आनभिम्लातात् from (another) Anabhimlata. आनभिम्लातः (This) Anabhimlata आनभिम्लातात् from a (third) Anabhimlata. आनभिम्लातः (This) Anabhimlata गौतमात् from Gautam. गौतमः Gautama सैतवप्राचीनयोग्याभ्याम् from Saitava and Prachinyogya. सैतवप्राचीनयोग्यौ Saitava and Prachinyogya पाराशर्यात् from Parasharya. पाराशर्यः Parasharya भारद्वाजात् from Bharadwaj. भारद्वाजः Bharadwaja भारद्वाजात् च from (another) Bharadwaj च and गौतमात् from Gautam, गौतमः Gautam भारद्वाजात् from (another) Bharadwaja भारद्वाजः Bharadwaja पारशर्यात् from (another) Parasharya पारशर्यः Parasharya बैजवापनायात् from Baijavapanaya बैजवापनायः Baijavapanaya, कौषिकायनेः from Kaushikayana कौशिकायनिः Kaushikayani.

 (Gautama) from Āgniveshya. Āgniveshya from Shandilya and Ānabhimlata. Ānabhimlāta from another Ānabhimlāta. This Ānabhimlāta from a third Ānabhimlāta. This Ānabhimlāta from Gautama. Gautama from Saitava and Prachinayogya. Saitava and Prāchinayogya from Pārāsharya. Pārāsharya from Bhāradwāja. Bhāradwāja from another Bhāradwāja and Gautama. Gautama from another Bhāradwāja. Bhāradwāja from another Pārāsharya. Pārāsharya from Baijavāpayana. Baijavāpanaya from Kausikayani. Kausikayani (from Ghrita kausika).



** घृतकौशिकाद्घृतकौशिकः पाराशर्यायणात्पाराशर्यायणः पाराशर्यात्पाराशर्यो जातूकर्ण्याज्जातूकर्ण्य आसुरायणाच्च यास्काच्चाऽऽसुरायणस्त्रैवणेस्त्रैवणिरौपजन्धनेरौपजन्धनिरासुरेरासुरिर्भारद्वाजाद्भारद्वाज आत्रेयादात्रेयो माण्टेर्माण्टिर्गौतमाद्गौतमो गौतमाद्गौतमो वात्स्याद्वात्स्यः शाण्डिल्याच्छाण्डिल्यः कैशोर्यात्काप्यात्कैशोर्यः काप्यः कुमारहारितात्कुमारहारितो गालवाद्गालवो विदर्भीकौण्डिन्याद्बिदर्भीकौण्डिन्यो वत्सनपातो बाभ्रवाद्वत्सनपाद्भाभ्रवः पथः सौभरात्पन्थाः सौभरोऽयास्यादाङ्गिरसादयास्य आङ्गिरस आभूतेस्त्वाष्ट्रादाभूतिस्त्वाष्ट्रो विश्वरूपात्त्वाष्ट्राद्विश्वरूपस्त्वाष्ट्रोऽश्विभ्यामश्विनौ दधीच आथर्वणाद्दध्यङ्ङाथर्वणोऽथर्वणो दैवादथर्वा दैवो मृत्योः प्राध्व^(ꣳ) सनान्मृत्युः प्राध्व^(ꣳ)सनः प्रध्व^(ꣳ)सनात्प्रध्व^(ꣳ)सन एकर्षेरेकर्षिर्विप्रचित्तेर्विप्रचित्तिर्व्यष्टेर्व्यष्टिः सनारोः सनारुः सनातनात्सनातनः सनगात्सनगः परमेष्ठिनः परमेष्ठी ब्रह्मणो ब्रह्म स्वयम्भु ब्रह्मणे नमः॥३॥ इति षष्ठं ब्राह्मणम्॥६॥ इति बृहदारण्यकोपनिषदि द्वितीयोऽध्यायः॥२॥**

 घृतकौशिकात् From Ghritakaushika, घृतकौशिकः Ghritakaushika पाराशर्यायणात् from Parasharyayana. पाराशर्यायणः Parasharyayana पाराशर्यात् from Parasharya. पाराशर्यः Parasharya जातुकर्णात् from Jatukarna. जातुकर्ण्यः Jatukarnya आसुरायणात् च from Asurayana च and यास्कात् from Yaska. असुरायणः Asurayana त्रैवणेः from Traivani. त्रैवणिः Traivani औपजन्धनेः from Aupajandhani औपजन्धनि Aupajandhani आसुरेः



from Asuri. आसुरिः Asuri भारद्वाजात् from Bharadwaja. भारद्वजः Bharadwaja आत्रेयात् from Atreya आत्रेयः Atreya माण्टेः from Manti. मण्टिः Manti गौतमात् from Gautam. गौतमः Gautam गौतमात् from (another) Gautam. गौतमः (This) Gautama वात्स्यात् from Vatsya. वात्स्यः Vatsya शण्डिल्यात् from Shandilya. शाण्डिल्यः Shandilya केशोर्यात् काप्यात् from Keshorya Kapya. केशोर्यः काण्यः Keshorya Kapya कुमारहरितात् from Kumarharita. कुमारहरितः Kumarharita गालवात् from Galaba. गालवः Galaba विदर्भीकौण्डिन्यात् from Vidarbhikaundinya. विदर्भीकौण्डिन्यः Vidarbhikaundinya वात्सनपातः वाभ्रबात् from Vatsanapat Babhrava. वत्सनपात् बाभ्रतः Vatsanapat Babhrava पथः सौभरात् from Pathin Saubhara पन्थाः सौभरः Pathin Saubhara. अयास्यात्–आङ्गिरस्यात् from Ayasya Angrirasa. अयासः आङ्गिरसः Ayashya Angrirasa आभूतेः त्वाष्ट्रात् from Abhuti Twastra. आभुतिः त्वाष्ट्रः Abhuti Twastra विश्वरूपात् त्वाष्ट्रात् from Vishwarupa Twastra. विश्वरूपः त्वाष्ट्रूः Vishwarupa Twastra अश्विभ्याम् from the two Aswins. अश्विनौ The Ashwins दधीचः अथर्वाणात् from Dadhicha Atharvana. दध्यच् आथर्वणः Dadhyach Atharvana आथवर्णः दैवात् Atharvana Daiva, अथर्वा दैवाः Atharvan Daiva. मृत्योः प्राध्वांसनात् from Mrityu Pradhwansana. मृत्युः प्राध्वंसनः Mrityu Pradhwansana, प्रध्वंसनात् from Pradhwansana. प्रध्वंसनः Pradhwansana, एकर्षेः from Ekarshi. एकर्षिः Ekarshi विप्रचित्तेः from Viprachitta. विप्रचित्तिः Viprichitti व्यष्ठेः from Vyashti. व्यष्टिः Vyashti सनारोः from Sanaru. सनारुः Sanaru सनातनात् from Sanātana सनातनः Sanatan सनगात् from Sanaga. सनगः Sanaga परमेष्ठिनः from Parmeshtin (Viraj). परमेष्ठी Parmeshthi (Viraj) ब्राह्मणः from Brahman. ब्रह्म Brahman (Hiranyagarbha) स्वयम्भुः (is)



self–born, eternal नमः Salutation ब्रह्मणे to Brahman (Hiranyagarbha).

 (Kaushikāyani) from Ghritakaushika. Ghritakaushika from Pārāsharyayana. Pārāsharyayana from Pārāsharya. Pārāsharya from Jatukarnya. Jatukarnya from Āsurayana Yāska. Āsurayana from Traivani. Traivani from Aupajandhani. Aupajandhani from Āsuri. Āsuri from Bhāradwāja. Bhāradwāja from Ātreya. Ātreya from Mānti. Mānti from Gautama. Gautama from another Gautama. This Gautama from Vatsya. Vatsya from Shāndilya. Shāndilya from Kaishorya Kāpya. Kaishorya Kāpya from Kumārahārita. Kumārahārita from Gālava. Gālava from Vidarbhikaundinya. Vidarbhikaundinya from Vatsanapat Bābhrava. Vatsanapat Bābhrava from Pathin Saubhara. Pathin Saubhara from Ayāsya Āngirasa. Ayāsya Āngirasa from Ābhuti Twashtra. Ābhuti Twashtra from Vishwarupa Twashtra. Vishwarupa Twashtra from the Ashwins. The Ashwin couple from Dadhyach Ātharvana. Dadhyach Ātharvana from Ātharvan Daiva. Ātharvana Daiva from Mrityu Prādhwamsana. Mrityu Prādhwamsana from Prādhwamsana. Prādhwamsana from Ekarshi. Ekarshi from Viprachitti. Viprachitti from Vyashti. Vyashti from Sanaru. Sanaru



from Sanātana. Sanātana from Sanaga. Sanaga from Viraj. Viraj from Hiranyagarbha.¹ Hiranyagarbha is self–born. Salutation to Hiranyagarbha.

 \[NOTES—1. In His mind were revealed the Vedas which are but another form of Hiranyagarbha.\]

——————————————————————————————

CHAPTER THREE: SECTION ONE

** ॐ जनको ह वैदेहो बहुदक्षिणेन यज्ञेनेजे तत्र ह कुरुपञ्चालानां ब्राह्मणा अभिसमेता बभूवुस्तस्य ह जनकस्य वैदेहस्य विजिज्ञासा बभूव कःस्विदेषां ब्राह्मणानामनूचानतम इति स ह गवा^(ꣳ )सहस्रमवरुरोध दश दश पादा एकैकस्याः शृङ्गयोराबद्धा वभूवुः॥१॥**

 ॐ Om जनकः ह Janaka वैदेहः King of Videha ईजे performed a sacrifice यज्ञेन by a sacrifice बहु–दक्षिणेन\* by plenty of presents, by many gifts तत्र There ब्राह्मणाः Brahmans कुरु–पाञ्चालानाम् of Kuru and Panchala बभूवुः were अभिसमेताः assembled, तस्य of that ह जनकस्य of Janaka विदेहस्य of the king of Videha बभूवुः was, arose विजिज्ञसा desire of knowledge कःस्विद् which एषां of these ब्राह्मणानाम् of the Brahmans अनूचानतमः इति most erudite, best–versed (in the Vedas). स ह He अवरुरोध had confined, pent in a fold

——————————————————————————————

\*It may also mean the sacrifice itself of that name referred to elsewhere in the Vedas. On account of the abundance of gifts, the borsesacrifice may be so called here.

——————————————————————————————



सहस्रं a thousand गवाम् of cows दशः ten दशः ten पादाः Padas (of gold) बभूवुः were श्राबद्धाः fixed, attached शृङ्गयोः on the horns एकएकस्याः of each (cow).

 \[The preceding Chapter was mainly of the nature of scriptural evidence, whereas this chapter is mainly argumentative. When both scriptural evidence and argument (reasoning) are combined to demonstrate the nature of the Self, they can show it as clearly as a fruit on the palm of one's hands.

 The following story is introduced either as an eulogy on knowledge or as prescribing the way to the acquisition of knowledge. Making of presents as well as association with adepts in the line and discussion with them are pointed out as the two customary ways of acquiring knowledge.\]

 Om. There was a king of Videha named Janak who performed a sacrifice in which abund-ance of gifts were made. Learned Brahmanas from Kuru and Panchāla, the famous seats of scholars, were assembled there either on invitation or as spectators. At the sight of that large gathering of Vedic scholars, a desire arose in the mind of the sacrificer, King Janak of Videha, to know who was the most erudite among them. Being desirous of knowing this, he as a means of ascertaining it,



had pent in a fold a thousand young cows on each horn of which were attached five Pādas¹ of gold.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. A Pāda is equal to a quarter of a pala or is about one–third of an ounce.\]

——————————————————————————————

** तान्होवाच ब्राह्मणा भगवन्तो यो वो ब्रह्मिष्ठः स एता गा उदजतामिति। ते ह ब्राह्मणा न दधृषुरथ ह याज्ञवल्क्यः स्वमेव ब्रह्मचारिणमुवाचैताः सोम्योदज सामश्रवा३ इति ता होदाचकार ते ह ब्राह्मणाश्चुकुधुः कथं नो ब्रह्मिष्ठो ब्रुवीतेत्यथ ह जनकस्य वैदेहस्य होताऽश्वलो बभूव स हैनं पप्रच्छ त्वं नु खलु नो याज्ञवल्क्य ब्रह्मिष्टोऽसी३ इति स होवाच नमो वयं ब्रह्मिष्ठाय कुर्मो गोकामा एव वय^(ꣳ) स्म इति त‍^(ꣳ) ह तत एव प्रष्टुं दध्रे होताऽश्वलः॥२॥**

 तान् to them उवाच ह (King Janaka) said इति thus भगवन्तः venerable ब्राह्माणाः Brahmans सः he यः who (is) ब्रह्मिष्टः the greatest Vedic scholar वः among you उदजताम् take home एताः these गाः cows. ते These ब्राह्मणाः Brahmans दधृषुः came forward, dared ह न not. अथ ह Then याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya उवाच said ब्रह्मचारिणम् to a pupil स्वम् of his इति thus सोम्य dear सामश्रवा Sāmashrava उदजा take home एताः these (cows). उदाचकार (He) drove, took away ताः them. ते ह Those ब्राह्मणाः Brahmans चुक्रुधुः were enraged. (he) calls, declares (himself) ब्रह्मिष्टः इति the greatest Vedic scholar नः among us. अथ Now बभूव there was होता a Hotri अश्वलः (named ) Ashwala जनकस्य of Janaka वैदेहस्य



King of Videha. सः He ह then पप्रछ asked एनं him याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya न असि \* are त्वं you खलु indeed. ब्रह्मिष्टः इति The greatest Vedic scholar नः among us ? सः ह He उवाच said इति thus वयं we, (here) I कुर्मः do नमः salutation ब्रह्मिष्ठाः greatest Vedic scholar वयम् we, I एव स्म only गोकामाः desirous of cows. ततः ह there upon आश्वलः Ashwal होता the Hotri दध्रे made up his mind, determined प्रष्टुम् to ask questions, to interrogate.

 Having thus pent the cows, King Janak addressed the assembly of Brahmanas saying: Venerable Ones, let him who is the greatest Vedic scholar among you take away these cows home. The Brāhmanas thus addressed did not come forward to declare himself as such. Silence prevailed for a time. Then Yajnavalkya asked his pupil Samashravas¹ to drive these cows towards his home. He did accordingly. This enraged the other Brāhmanas, who thought 'How does he dareto declare himself the greatest Vedic scholar among us who are each a great scholar ?' There was present a Hotri, named Ashwala, of the sacrificer Janaka, King of Videha. Ashwala now dared to challenge Yājnavalkya thus, 'Yājnavalkya, are you indeed the greatest Vedic scholar among us.' To this Yajnavalkya said in reply, 'I salute the greatest Vedic scholar. I am only desirous of the cows.'

——————————————————————————————

 Censure is signified by prolongation of this accent.

——————————————————————————————



Thereupon Ashwala the Hotri made up his mind to ask him questions.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Means one who learns to chant the saman.\]

——————————————————————————————

** याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यदिद^(ꣳ) सर्वं मृत्युनाऽऽप्त^(ꣳ) सर्वं मृत्युनाऽभिपन्नं केन यजमानो मृत्योराप्तिमतिमुच्यत इति होत्रर्त्विजाऽग्निना वाचा वाग्वै यज्ञस्य होता तद्येयं वाक्ंसोऽयमग्निः स होता स मुक्तिः साऽतिमुक्तिः॥३॥**

 उवाच ( Ashwal) said इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. यतः Since इदम् this सर्वम् all (accessories of this rite) आप्तम् (is) overtaken, seized, मृत्युना by death (ritualistic work) सर्वं all अभिपन्नम् swayed, devoured मृत्युना by death केन by what (meditation) यजमानः the sacrificer अतिमुच्यते goes beyond becomes independent आप्तिम् इति reach, rule मृत्योः of death ? वाचा by speech अग्निना by fire ऋत्विजा by the priest होत्रा by Hotri वै Verily वाक् the speech यज्ञस्य of this sacrifice होता the Hotri. तत् that यत् which इयं this वाक् speech (is) सः that अयम् this अग्निः fire. सः that (fire) होता the Hotri. सः that (Hotri) (is) मुक्तिः liberation. सा That (liberation) अतिमुक्तिः (is) emancipation.

 \[In the third section on the Udgitha of the First Chapter a general statement has been made that a sacrificer can transcend death by the sacrifice with five factors combined with meditations about it. There it has been briefly stated also that



identity with vital power seated in the mouth is the way of escape from death. The present section examines that and introduces particulars about that meditation.\]

 Ashwala said to Yājnavalkya, 'Since all the accessories of this sacrifice such as the priests and the fire etc. are seized and swayed by death (ritual–istic work¹) and attended with our natural attachment, what meditation can make the sacrifice independent of it ?' Yājnavalkya replied, 'By speech, by fire² which is the real priest called Hotri. The speech of the sacrificer is the Hotri. The speech of the sacrificer is the well–known fire with reference to the gods. That fire is the Hotri³. When Hotri is meditated upon as fire it is the means of liberation for the sacrificer. The liberation is itself emancipation; for the former is a means to the latter.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Sacrifice here means the sacrificer. As Shatapath Brahmana (14.2.2.24) says, "The sacrifice is the sacrificer."

 2. If the sacrificer meditates upon the two auxiliaries of the sacrifice, the speech and the Hotri, as fire, their divine form, he is liberated from death which consists in his limited  
natural attachment to the body and the elements.

 3. As Shatapath Brahmana (6.4 2.6) says: 'Fire is the Hotri'.\]

——————————————————————————————



** याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यदिद^(ꣳ) सर्वमहोरात्राभ्यामाप्त^(ꣳ) सर्वमहोरात्राभ्यामभिपन्नं केन यजमानोऽहोरात्रयोराप्तिमतिमुच्यत इत्यध्वर्युणर्त्विजा चक्षुषाऽऽदित्येन चक्षुर्वै यज्ञस्याध्वर्युस्तद्यदिदं चक्षुः सोऽसावादित्यः सोऽध्वर्युः स मुक्तिः साऽतिमुक्तिः॥४॥**

 उवाच ह (Ashwal) said इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya यत् since इदं this सर्वं all (accessories of the sacrifice) आप्तम् (is) overtaken, seized अहोरात्राभ्याम् by day and night सर्वम् all अभिपन्नम् (is) swayed, devoured अहोरात्राभ्याम् by day and night केन by what (meditation) यजमानः the sacrificer अतिमुच्यते is freed, goes beyond आप्तिम् इति reach, rule अहोरात्रयोः of day and night. (Yajnavalkya said ) चक्षुषा by the eye आदित्येन by the Sun ऋत्विजा by the priest अध्वर्युणा by Adhvaryu. वै Verily ऋतुः the eye यज्ञस्य of the sacrifice, of the sacrificer अध्वर्युः (is) Adharyu. तत् That यत् which (is) इदं this चक्षुः eye. सः That असौ this आदित्यः Sun. सः That (is) अध्वर्यः the Adharyu. सः That (is) मुक्तिः the liberation. सा That (is) अतिमुक्तिः emancipation.

 \[This passage indicates the way to deliverance from Time which causes changes in the accessories of the new–moon and full–moon sacrifice and other rites. Death which is another name for ritualistic work rests on this time which has two forms. The one form of time consists of day, night, etc.; and the other of lunar days, etc. The deliverance from the former form of time is first indicated.\]



 Ashwal said to Yājnavalkya, 'Since the accessories of the sacrifice seized and also devoured by day and night—one form of Time—What meditation can make the sacrificer free from them ?' Yājnavalkya replied: By the eye, by the sun which is the real priest called Adhwaryu.¹ The eye of the sacrificer is the Adhwaryu. Verily the eye of the sacrificer is to be meditated upon as the sun. The Adhwaryu is to be meditated upon as the sun. This meditation is the means of liberation² for the sacrificer. This liberation is emancipation.³

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. The Adhwaryu keeps ready the accessories of the rite and offers oblations while reciting from the Yajur Veda.

 2. Liberation consists in stripping the two accessories of the sacrifice—( the sacrificer's eye and Adhwaryu) of their natural limitations relating to the body and the elements, and meditating upon them as the sun.

 3. Because there is no day and night for one who is videntified with sun.\]

——————————————————————————————

** याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यदिद^(ꣳ) सर्वं पूर्वपक्षापरपक्षाभ्यामाप्त^(ꣳ) सर्वं पूर्वपक्षापरपक्षाभ्यामभिपन्नं केन यजमानः पूर्वपक्षापरपक्षयोराप्तिमतिमुच्यत इत्युद्गात्रर्त्विजा वायुना प्राणेन प्राणो वै यज्ञस्योद्गाता तद्योऽयं प्राणः स वायुः स उद्गाता स मुक्तिः साऽतिमुक्तिः॥५॥**



 उवाच ह (Ashwal) said इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya यत् since इदं this सर्वम् all (accessories of the sacrifice) आप्तम् (is) overtaken, seized पूर्वपक्ष-परपक्षाभ्याम् by the bright fortnight and dark fortnight केन by what (meditation) यजमानः the sacrificer अतिमुच्यते is freed, goes beyond आप्तिम् reach, rule पूर्वपक्षपरपक्षयोः इति of the bright fortnight and dark fortnight (Yajnavalkya replied) प्राणेन by the vital power वायुना by the air ऋत्विजा by the priest उद्गाता by Udgatri वै Verily प्राणः the vital power यज्ञस्य of the sacrifice, of the sacrificer उद्गाता (is) the Udgatri. तत् That यत् which अयं this प्राणः vital power सः thet (is) वायुः air cosmic vital power सः that (is) उद्गाता Udgata. सः That (is) मुक्तिः liberation. सा That (is) अतिमुक्तिः emancipation.

 Ashwal said to Yājnavalkya, 'Since the accessories of the sacrifice are seized and devoured by the bright and the dark fortnights, what meditation makes the sacrificer free from them?' Yājnavalkya replied, 'By the vital power—by air which is the real priest called Udgatri (the chanter of Samans). The vital power of the sacrificer is verily the Udgatri.¹ This vital power of the sacrificer is again air. This is the Udgatri. Meditation on this vital force and Udgatri as cosmic vital power (Sutratman) is liberation. This liberation is indeed emancipation.²

———————————————————————————————

  \[Note-1. It is known from the first chapter (1. 3. 24, and 1. 4. 13).

———————————————————————————————



———————————————————————————————

 2. This passage indicates the way to the emancipation from time represented by days and nights caused by the moon. Unlike solar days and nights, lunar days and nights are increased and decreased in the bright and dark fortnights. The changes of the moon are caused by air which is the conventional symbol of cosmic vital power (Sutratman). By meditating on the Udgatri and the vital power of the sacrificer in their divine form the moon which divides Time into bright and dark fortnights and finally being identified with the moon, one goes beyond the reach of bright and dark fortnights\]

——————————————————————————————

** याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यदिदमन्तरिक्षमनारम्बणमिव केनाऽऽक्रमेण यजमानः स्वर्गं लोकमाक्रमत इति ब्रह्मणर्त्विजा मनसा चन्द्रेण मनो वै यज्ञस्य ब्रह्मा तद्यदिदं मनः सोऽसौ चन्द्रः स ब्रह्मा स मुक्तिः साऽतिमुक्तिरित्यतिमोक्षा अथ सम्पदः॥६॥**

 उवाच ह (Ashwal) said इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya यत् since इदम् this अन्तरिक्षम् sky इव as it were अनारम्बनम् (न-अरम्बनम्) (is) without a stay (approach) केन by what आक्रमेण stay. (approach) यजमानः the sacrificer आक्रमते approaches, attains स्वर्गम् heaven लोकम् इति world. (Yajnavalkya said) मनसा by the mind, चन्द्रेन by the moon ऋत्विजा by the priest ब्रह्मणा called Brahmā. मनः The mind यज्ञस्य of the sacrifice, of the sacrificer वै verily ब्रह्मा Brahmā. तत् That यत् which (is) इदं this मनः mind सः that (is) असौ this चन्द्रः moon. सः This ब्रह्मा (is) the Brahmā. सः This मुक्तिः (is) deliverance. साः This अतिमुक्तिः (is) emancipation. इति Such, so far अतिमोक्षाः (the ways of) emancipation. अथ



 Now संवादः meditation on achievement, meditation based on resemblance (similarity).

 \[The passage answers the inquiry about the support by means of which the sacrificer is released from death.\]

 Ashwal asked again Yājnavalkya thus: 'Since the sky is, as it were¹. without approach, by what approach does the sacrificer attains the heaven (is released)?' Yājnavalkya replied that the sacrificer goes to heaven by the approach of the mind meditated upon as the moon, which is the real priest called Brahmā. Verily the mind of the sacrificer is Brahmā. This mind² is to be medítated upon as the moon. The moon again is the priest called Brahmā³. This moon meditated upon as the unlimited form of the mind is deliverance from death. This deliverance is emancipation. Such are the various ways of emancipation from death. Now follows the meditation⁴ by virtue of some point of similarity.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. This indicates that there is an approach to heaven but it is unknown.

2\. The mind in the body is the same as the moon among the gods, because moon-god is the presiding deity of the mind.

3\. The sacrificer sees the moon as the unlimited form of his mind and the priest instead of his limited form, as the

———————————————————————————————



———————————————————————————————

mind confined in his body, and the Brahmā among the elements. respectively.

4\. It is a meditation is based on some point of similarity on sacrificer with lower results like the Agnihotra, as sacrifices with higher results, with a view to attain these results, or it is a meditation on some part of the lower sacrifice as those very results. People may fail to attain certain results of a sacrifice through some unavoidable defect in spite of their best ardour. So a man should meditate on the particular results sought of the sacrifice such as Agnihotra, which he can manage to perform. For, it is beyond the means of most people to perform the awfully elaborate and expensive sacrifices such as the Rajasuya, Ashwamedha, Naramedha and Sarvamedha sacrifices. But they can obtain the results of these sacrifices only by means of the meditation based on resemblance.\]

—————————————————————————————

** याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच कतिभिरयमद्यर्ग्भिर्होताऽस्मिन्यज्ञे करिष्यतीति तिसृभिरिति कतमास्तास्तिस्र इति पुरोनुवाक्या च याज्या च शस्यैव तृतीया किं ताभिर्जयतीति यत्किञ्चेदं प्राणभृदिति॥७॥**

 उवाच ह (Ashwal) said इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya कतिभिः with how many ऋग्भिः classes of Rich करिष्यति will do (his) functions, will recite hymns अयम् this होता priest called Hotri अस्मिन् in this यज्ञे sacrifice अद्य इति today. Yajnavalkya replied तिसृभिः इति with three classes. (Ashwal said) कतमाः which (are) ताः those तिस्रः इति three पुरोनुवाक्या च the preliminary, chanted before the sacrifice याज्या



the sacrificial, chanted during sacrifice शस्यो the eulogistic, chanted in praise of sacrifice तृतिया एवा the third. ताभिः By them (three kinds of hymns) किम् what जयति इति (he) conquers, obtains किम् इदं च whatever यत् that (is) प्राणभृत् इति bears life living.

 Ashwal asked again Yājnavalkya, 'How many classes of Rich hymns will the priest called Hotri recite in the sacrifice today?' Yājnavalkya replied: The priest will do his function with three classes of Rich. Ashwal asked again, "Which are those three?” Yaājnavalkya replied: "Firstly by that class of hymns that are chanted before the actual sacrifice; Secondly by those that are used for the sacrifice and thirdly by those that are sung in praise of the sacrifice.” Ashwal asked: ‘What is conquered by those three kinds of hymns?' Yājnavalkya replied: 'Whatever bears life in the three worlds is won by him.'

 ** याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच कत्ययमद्याध्वर्युरस्मिन्यज्ञ आहुतीर्होष्यतीति तिस्र इति कतमास्तास्तिस्र इति या हुता उज्ज्वलन्ति या हुता अतिनेदन्ते या हुता अधिशेरते किं ताभिर्जयतीति या हुता उज्ज्वलन्ति देवलोकमेव ताभिर्जयति. दीप्यत इव हि देवलोको या हुता अतिनेदन्ते पितृलोकमेव ताभिर्जयत्यतीव हि पितृलोको या हुता अधिशेरते मनुष्यलोकमेव ताभिर्जयत्यध इव हि मनुष्यलोकः॥८॥**  




 उवाच ह (Ashwal) said, asked इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya कति how many आहुतिः (kinds of) oblations अयम् this अध्वर्युः the priest called Adhwaryu होष्यति will offer अस्मिन् in this यज्ञे sacrifice अद्य इति today? (Yajnavalkya replied). तिस्रः इति Three (kinds), कतमाः which (are) ताः (those) तिस्रः इति three (kinds)? याः (those) which उज्वलन्ति blaze up, flame up हुताः thrown, offered; याः (those) which हुताः thrown, offered अतिनेदन्तेः make a loud noise; याः (those) which हुताः thrown,offered अधिशेरते penetrate the earth, sink in, ताभिः By those (oblations) किम्म् what जयति इति (one) conquers. ताभिः By those ताः which हुताः (being) offered a उज्वलन्ति blaze up, flame up जयति (the sacrificer) conquers एव indeed देवलोकम् the world of the gods. हि For देवलोकः the world of the gods दीप्यते blazes, shines इव as it were. ताभिः By those याः which हुताः (being) offered अतिनेदन्ते make great noise जयति ( sacrificer) conquers एव indeed पितृलोकम् in world of the fathers ; हि for पितृलोकः the world of the fathers अति (is) excessively (noisy) इव as it ताभिः By those याः which हुता (being) offered अधिशेरते go down sink जयति (sacrificer) wins एव indeed मनुष्यलोकम् the world of men. हि For मनुष्यलोकः the world of men अधः (is) low, lower इव as it were.

 \[This passage introduces a meditation on some part of the lesser sacrifice as the very form of the result he seeks. It is a meditation on similarity.\].

 Ashwal asked again Yājnavalkya, 'How many kinds of oblations will the priest called Adhwaryu offer in this sacrifice today?' Yājnavalkya replied:



The priest will make three kinds of offerings. Ashwal asked: Which are those three kinds? The other replied: The first kind is of the oblations of wood and ghee that flame up when thrown into fire. The second kind is of the oblations of meat that make loud noise when offered. The third kind of oblations is of milk and soma juice that penetrate into the earth when thrown into fire. It is asked, 'What does the sacrificer attain by those oblations?' The reply: By the oblations of wood and ghee that blaze up on being offered, the sacrificer attains¹ the world of the gods; because this world is so shining that it looks ablaze, as it were. By the oblations of meet that make horrible noise when offered he attains the world of the Fathers; because this world seems to be excessively noisy². and by the offerings of milk and soma juice that go down to the earth he attains the world of men, because this world is lower than the higher worlds to be won.

—————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. The offerings as well as their results-the world of the gods-are both bright. On account of this resemblance, the sacrificer meditates that the bright offerings are the very form of the world of gods and that he is attaining the result by his sacrifices.

2\. The world of the Manes is attached to the city of Yama, the god of death. People being put to tortures by him.

—————————————————————————————



cry, 'Alas, we are finished. Relieve us, Oh, relieve us from these unbearable sufferings.'\]

—————————————————————————————

** याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच कतिभिरयमद्य ब्रह्मा यज्ञं दक्षिणतो देवताभिर्गोपायतीत्येकयेति कतमा सैकेति मन एवेत्यनन्तं वै मनोऽनन्ता विश्वे देवा अनन्तमेव स तेन लोकं जयति॥९॥**

 उवाच ह (Ashwal) asked इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya कतिभिः by how many देवताभिः gods अयम् this. ब्रह्मा Priest called Brahma गोपायति protects यज्ञं sacrifice दक्षिणतः from the right अद्य इति today. (Yajnavalkya replied) एकया इति by one. (Ashwal asked ) कतमा which (is) सा that एका इति one. (Yajnavalkya replied) मनः the mind एव इति only वै Verily मनः the mind अनन्तः (is) infinite; विश्वेदेवाः the Vishwadevas अनन्ताः (are) infinite. तेन By this (meditation) सः he जयतिः conquers अनन्तम् infinite लोकम् world एव indeed.

 Ashwal asked, 'Yajnavalkya, by how many gods¹ does the priest called Brahmā from his seat on the right protects the sacrifice today?' Yājnavalkya replied that the priest does his function by one god only. Ashwal asked 'What is that god?' To this the other replied: Mind is that god. It is well known that the mind is infinite on account of tits endless modifications and infinite are the Vishwadevas. This meditation enables one to conquer an infinite world.



———————————————————————————————

\[NOTES —1. The plural form is used for the sake of conformity with previous questions and also for puzzling the opponent.\]

—————————————————————————————

 ** याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच कत्ययमद्योद्गाताऽस्मिन्यज्ञे स्तोत्रियाः स्तोष्यतीति तिस्र इति कतमास्तास्तिस्र इति पुरोनुवाक्या च याज्या च शस्यैव तृतीया कतमास्ता या अध्यात्ममिति प्राण एव पुरोनुवाक्याऽपानो याज्या व्यानः शस्या किं ताभिर्जयतीति पृथिवीलोकमेव पुरोनुवाक्यया जयत्यन्तरिक्षलोकं याज्यया द्युलोकꣳ शस्यया ततो ह होताऽश्वल उपरराम॥१०॥ इति प्रथमं ब्राह्मणम्॥१॥**

 उवाच ह (Ashwal) said, asked इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya कति how many स्तोत्रियाः kinds of hymns, collection of Riks that can be chanted अयम् this उद्गाता priest called Udgatri स्तोष्यति will chant अस्मिन् in this यज्ञे sacrifice अद्य इति today. (Yajnavalkya replied) तिस्रः इति three kinds. कतमाः which (are) ताः those तिस्रः इति three kinds पुरोनुवाक्या च the preliminary, chanted before the rite याज्या च the sacrificial, chanted during the rite च and शश्या the eulogistic, chanted in praise of the rite तृतीया the third एव indeed कतमाः which (are) ताः these (three kinds) याः which अध्यात्मम् इति with regard to the body. प्राणः Prana एव indeed पुरोनुवाक्या (is) the preliminary (hymns), अपानः Apana याज्या (is) the sacrificial (hymn) व्यानः Vyana शस्या (is) the eulogistic (hymn). ताभि By those जयति (the sacrificer) attains किम् इति what? पुरोनुवाक्या by this preliminary (hymns) जयति (he) attains



पृथिवी-लोकम् the earth-world. अन्तरिक्ष-लोकम् The sky-world याज्यया by the sacrificial (hymns) द्युलोकम् the heaven-world शस्यया by the eulogistic (hymns) ततः ह thereupon होता Hotri अश्वलः Ashwala उपरराम kept silent.

 Ashwal asked: 'Yajnavalkya, how many kinds. of hymns (collection of Riks) will be chanted by the priest called Udgatri in this sacrifice today?' Yājnavalkya replied that the priest will chant three kinds of collections of Riks. The one questioned: Which are the three kinds?' The other replied: The first kind is that collection of Riks that are chanted before the sacrifice. The second is that collection that are chanted during the sacrifice and the third collection is of those Riks that are chanted in praise of sacrifice. The one questioned: "Which are the three collections of Riks that are with regard to the body?' The other replied: The Prāna is first kind of collections of Riks, the Apāna' is second collection of Riks and the Vyāna is third collection. Question: 'What does the sacrificer attain by them?' Reply: By the first collection of Riks the sacrificer attains the earth-world, by the second collection the sky-world and by the third the heaven-world. When his questions were thus answered Hotri named Ashwala understood the depth of his opponent's erudition and kept silent.



 ** अथ हैनं जारत्कारव आर्तभागः पप्रच्छ याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच कति ग्रहाः कत्यतिग्रहा इति। अष्टौ ग्रहा अष्टावतिग्रहाइति ये तेऽष्टौ ग्रहा अष्टावतिग्रहाः कतमे त इति॥१॥**

** **अथ Then (when Ashwal stopped) आर्तभागः Ārtabhāgā, a son of Ritabhāga जारत्कारवः a descendant of Jaratkaru पप्रच्छ ह asked questions एनम् to him (Yajnavalkya). उवाच ह (He) said, asked इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya कति how many ग्रहाः (are) Grahas,\* organs of perception कति how many अतिग्रहाः इति\* Atigrahas sense-objects. (Yajnavalkya replied) अष्टौ (There are) eight ग्रहाः Grahas, sense-organs, अष्टौ eight अतिग्रहाः इति Atigrahas organs of preception ये which ते (are) those अष्टौ eight ग्रहाः Grahas, अष्टौ eight अतिग्रहाः Atigrahas कतमे what ते इति (are) they?

 \[Deliverance from time and rites-the two forms of death has been explained in the previous section. The present section describes deliverance from other two forms of death-the organs and objects. Shatapath Brahmana (10.5.2.16) rightly says that though death is one, it has many forms, and again the same scripture (10.5.2.2) observes that hunger is death. The whole range of relative existence consisting of ends and means is ruled by

——————————————————————————————

\*Literally Graha means that which perceives and Atigraha means that which is greater than a graha or that which determines the nature of perception.

———————————————————————————————



the organs and objects that really mean death.Liberation from the relative existence—which is the ultimate goal of human life, means emancipation from the bondage of organs and objects—the formidable forms of death. When the bondages. are known, one in bondage can try to escape from them. Hence this section describes the fetters of organs and objects.\]

 When Ashwal stopped, Artabaga, a son of Ritabhaga, a descendant of Jaratkāru, put questions to Yājnavalkya.He asked Yājnavalkya,'How many sense-organs are there and how many sense-objects?' Yājnavalkya replied: There are eight sense-organs and eight sense-objects. Arthabhaga asked again, 'Which in particular are those eight sense-organs and eight sense-objects spoken of by you?'

 ** प्राणो वै ग्रहः सोऽपानेनातिग्राहेण गृहीतोऽपानेन हि गन्धाञ्जिघ्रति॥२॥**

 वै Verily प्राणः the Prāna, nose ग्रहः (is) the Graha. सः It गृहीतः (is) overtaken अतिग्रहेण by the Atigraha अपानेन by the Apāna, odour; हि because जिघ्रति (one) smells the odours अपानेन by the Apāna, air breathed in.

 The nose is verily a sense-organ. It is over-taken by its object—odour. Because everybody



smells through the nose odours presented by the air that is breathed in.

 **वाग्वै ग्रहः स नाम्नाऽतिग्राहेण गृहीतो वाचा हि नामान्यभिवदति॥३॥ **

 वै Verily वाक् the speech ग्रहः (is) a sense-organ. सः It गृहीतः (is) overtaken अतिग्राहेण by the sense-object नाम्ना by name; हि because अभिवदति (one) speaks; pronounces नामानि names, words by the speech.

 The speech is verily a sense-organ. It is over-taken by its object—the name. Because one pronounces names (the words ) by speech.

** जिह्वा वै ग्रहः स रसेनातिग्राहेण गृहीतो जिह्वया हि रसान्विजानाति॥४॥**

 वै Verily जिह्वा the tongue ग्रहः (is) a sense organ. सः It गृहीतः (is) overtaken अतिग्राहेणा by the sense-object रसेन by the taste; हि for जिह्वया by the tongue विजानाति (one) knows,perceives रसान् the tastes.

 The tongue is verily a sense-organ. It is over-taken by its object—the taste. Because one perceives tastes by the tongue.

 **चक्षुर्वै ग्रहः स रूपेणातिग्राहेण गृहीतश्चक्षुषा हि रूपाणि पश्यति॥५॥**  




 वै Verily चक्षुः the eye ग्रहः (is a sense organ सः It गृहीत; (is) overtaken by the sense-object रूपेण the form हि for चचुषा by the eye पश्यति (one) sees रूपाणि forms.

 The eye is verily a sense-organ. It is overtaken by its object-the form. Because one sees forms by the eye.

 **श्रोत्रं वै ग्रहः स शब्देनातिग्राहेण गृहीतः श्रोत्रेण हि शब्दाञ्शृणोति॥६॥**

 वै Verily श्रोत्रम् the ear ग्रहः (is) a sense-organ. सः It गृहीतः (is) overtaken अतिग्राहेण by the sense object शब्देन by the sound; हि for श्रृणोति (one) hears शब्दान् the sounds श्रोत्रेण by the ear.

 The ear is verily a sense-organ. It is overtaken by its object-the sound. Because one hears sounds by the ear.

 ** मनो वै ग्रहः स कामेनातिग्राहेण गृहीतो मनसा हि कामान्कामयते॥७॥**

 वै Verily मनः the mind ग्रहः (is) a sense-organ. सः It गृहीतः (is) overtaken अतिग्राहेण by the sense-organ कामेन by the desire; हि for कामयते (one) desires कामान् desires मनसा by the mind.

 The mind is verily a sense-organ. It is overtaken by its object-the desire. Because one desires by the mind.



** हस्तौ वै ग्रहः स कर्मणाऽतिग्राहेण गृहीतो हस्ताभ्याꣳ हि कर्म करोति॥८॥**

 वै Verily हस्तौ the hands, arms ग्रहः (are) a sense-organ. सः It, they गृहीतः (are) overtaken अतिग्राहेण \* by the sense-object कर्मणा by work; हि for करोति (one ) does कर्म work हस्ताभ्याम् by the hands (arms).

 The hands are verily a sense-organ. They are overtaken by their object-the work. Because one does work by the hands.

** त्वग्वै ग्रहः स स्पर्शेनातिग्राहेण गृहीतस्त्वचा हि स्पर्शान्वेदयत इत्येतेऽष्टौ ग्रहा अष्टावतिग्रहाः॥९॥**

 वै Verily त्वक् the skin ग्रहः (is) a sense organ. सः It गृहीतः is controlled अतिग्राहेण by the sense-object स्पर्शेन by the touch. हि For त्वचा by the skin वेदयते (one) perceives स्पर्शान् touches. एते these (from nose up to skin) अष्टौ the eight sense-organs; एते these अष्टौ eight प्रतिग्रहाः इति sense-objects.

 The skin is verily a sense-organ. It is overtaken by its object-the touch. Because one perceives touches by the skin. These from nose up to the skin are the eight sense-organs and these from odour to touch are the eight objects of perception.

—————————————————————————————

\*The long vowel in Atigrāha which occurs in this and some proceding passages is a Vedic license.

———————————————————————————————



** याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यदिदꣳ सर्वं मृत्योरन्नं कास्वित्सा देवता यस्या मृत्युरन्नमित्यग्निर्वै मृत्युः सोऽपामन्नमप पुनर्मृत्युं जयति॥१०॥**

 उवाच ह (Artabhaga ) spoke इति thus : याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnevalkya यत् since सर्वम् all इदम् this (manifested Universe) अन्नम् (is) the food मृत्योः of death का स्वित् which (is) सा that देवता God यस्याः whose अन्नम् food (is) मृत्युः इति death. वै Verily अग्निः the fire (is) मृत्युः death. सः It (is) अन्नम् the food अपाम् of water. अपजयति (He) conquers, overcomes पुनः further मृत्युम् death.

 At the conclusion of the topic on the organs and their objects, Artabhaga spoke again. He said, 'Yājnavalkya, since this manifested Universe is swallowed by death, which is that god. who is the destroyer of death¹?' Yājnavalkya replied, There is the death (destroyer) of death. For instance, fire being a destroyer is the death of all.' But as it is swallowed by water, it is the food: of water. Therefore one who knows this overcomes further death.

—————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. As Katha Upanishad ( 2. 25 ) says that death? is His sauce.\]

—————————————————————————————

 **याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यत्रायं पुरुषो म्रियत उदस्मात्प्राणाः क्रामन्त्याहो ३ नेति नेति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्योऽत्रैव समवनीयन्ते स उच्छ्वयत्याध्मायत्याध्मातो मृतः शेति॥११॥**



 उवाच ह (Artabhaga) spoke, asked इति thus : याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya यत्र where, when अयम् this पुरुषः man म्रियते dies अस्मात् from him आहो do प्राणाः the organs उत्क्रामन्ति go up. याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said न इति no न इति no. अत्र Here, in him एव only समवनीयन्ते (they) merge, become one. सः It (the body) उच्छ्वयति swells, आध्मायति is inflated; आध्मातः (being) inflated शेते lies मृतः dead, motionless.

 Artabhaga asked again, 'Yājnavalkya, when man, liberated from death in the form of organs and objects, knows Brahman and dies, do his organs and objects¹ go up from him (the dying Knower of Brahman) or not?' Yājnavalkya replied: They do not go up. They become one with him, their cause like waves in the ocean. It is the body that dies; for it swells, is inflated by the external air like a pair of bellows, and lies motionless in that condition.

—————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES 1. Which exist in him in the form of impressions and impell him to action.\]

—————————————————————————————

 **याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यत्रायं पुरुषो म्रियते किमेनं न जहातीति नामेत्यनन्तं वै नामानन्ता विश्वे देवा अनन्तमेव स तेन लोकं जयति॥१२॥**

 उवाच ह (Artabhaga) spoke, asked इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya यत्र where, when अयम् this पुरुषः man म्रियते dies



passes away किम् what न not जहाति leaves एनम् इति him (Yajnavalkya replied) नाम इति the name वै Verily नाम the name (is) अनन्तम् infinite, अनन्ताः infinite (are) विश्वेदेवाःthe Viswadevas. सः He जयति conquers तेन by that (knowledge) एव indeed अनन्तम् infinite लोकम् world.

 Artabhaga again asked, Yājnavalkya, when the liberated man passes away what is that which does not leave him?' Yājnavalkya replied that it is name that does not leave him; for the name is infinite¹. Infinite are the Vishwadevas for they possess infinity of the name. He who knows this conquers indeed an infinite world by the virtue of that knowledge.

—————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Infinity of the name is its eternity.\]

—————————————————————————————

 **याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यत्रास्य पुरुषस्य मृतस्याग्निं वागप्येति वातं प्राणश्चक्षुरादित्यं मनश्चन्द्रं दिशः श्रोत्रं पृथिवीꣳ शरीरमाकाशमात्मौषधीर्लोमानि वनस्पतीन्केशा अप्सु लोहितं च रेतश्च निधीयते क्वायं तदा पुरुषो भवतीत्याहर सोम्य हस्तमार्तभागाऽऽवामेवैतस्य वेदिष्यावो न नावेतत्सजन इति। तौ होत्क्रम्य मन्त्रयाञ्चक्राते तौ ह यदूचतुः कर्म हैव तदूचतुरथ यत्प्रशशꣳसतुः कर्म हैव तत्प्रशशꣳसतुः पुण्यो वै पुण्येन कर्मणा भवति पापः पापेनेति ततो ह जारत्कारव आर्तभाग उपरराम॥१३॥ इति द्वितीयं ब्राह्मणम्॥२॥**



 उवाच ह (Artabhaga) said, asked इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya यत्र when वाक् speech, the vocal organ अस्य of this मृतस्य dead पुरुषस्य person अप्येति enters, goes back अग्निम् into fire, प्राणः vital power, the nose वातम् into air, चक्षुः the eye आदित्यम् into the sun, मनः the mind चन्द्रम् into the moon, श्रोत्रम् the ear; दिशः into the quarters, directions, space, शरीरम् the body पृथिवीम् into the earth, आत्मा Self, the ether (in the heart) आकाशम्
into sky, into outside ether, लोमानि the hairs (on the body) औषधीः into herbs, into shrubs, केशाः the hairs (on the head) च and रेतः the semen निधीयते go back, are deposited अप्सु in the water क्व whree, on what तदा then अयम् this पुरुषः person भवति इति is, rests? सौम्य my friend, gentle one आर्तभाग Artabhaga आहर give (me) हस्तम् (your) hands. आवाम् We two एव only वेदिष्यावः shall know, shall discuss एतस्य of this सजने in crowd, in public नौ we two एतत् this इति न not (discuss). तौ ह They, both उत्क्रम्य going out, retiring मन्त्रयाञ्चक्राते discussed, talked out यत् which तौ ह they ऊचतुः said, decided तत् ह that ऊचतुः (they) said, decided कर्म (is) work एव indeed. अथ And यत् which प्रशशंसतु (they) praised तत् that प्रशशंसतु ह (they) praised कर्म (is) work एव indeed. वै Verily भवति (one) becomes, turns पुण्यः good (enjoined by the scriptures) पुण्येन by good कर्मणा work पापः bad पापेन इति by bad (forbidden by the scriptures). ततः ह There upon आर्त्तभागः Artabhaga जारत्कारवः a descendant of Jaratkaru उपरराम kept silent, stopped.

 \[Liberation from death in the form of organs and objects consists in the dissolution here itself



of the organs and objects like the extinction of a light. This passage ascertains what starts and stimulates this form of death.\]

 Artabhaga asked again, 'Yājnavalkya, when the speech¹ of a man, who is dead without the highest knowledge but with the idea of his personality, goes back into fire, the nose into air, the eye² into the sun, the mind into the moon, the ear into the directions, the body into the earth, the ether of the heart (which is the seat of Self) into the out-side ether, the hairs on the body into the herbs, the hairs on the head into the trees, as well as the blood and the semen are deposited³ in water, on what does he rest then?' Yājnavalkya said: 'Give me your hand, gentle Artabhaga. This question will be discussed between you and me. It cannot be done in public.' They both retired to a solitary place and discussed the question there. Listen what they decided at the end of the discussion. There they decided that work is the support on which the disembodied man rests. There they refuted all other causes but praised work that stimulates the repeated taking of the body and organs. Since work is the cause of embodiment one turns good by works enjoined by the scriptures and turns bad by works forbidden by the same. Thereupon, Artabhaga, a descendant of Jaratkaru stopped.



———————————————————————————————

\[NOTES-1. What are meant here by speech and others are their respective presiding deities. The organs themselves are not merged before the final liberation. When the presiding deities of the organs stop work, the organs become like a bill-hook or any other tool laid down. Then man who is the agent is rendered quite helpless owing to his disembodiment.

2\. In each case the verb 'goes back' is understood.

3\. It indicates that they are again withdrawn when a new body is taken.\]

—————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER THREE: SECTION THREE**

 **अथ हैनं भुज्युर्लाह्यायनिः पप्रच्छ याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच मद्रेषु चरकाः पर्यव्राजाम ते पतञ्जलस्य काप्यस्य गृहानैम तस्याऽऽसीद्दुहिता गन्धर्वगृहीता तमपृच्छाम कोऽसीति सोऽब्रवीत्सुधन्वाऽऽङ्गिरस इति तं यदा लोकानामन्तानपृच्छामाथैनमब्रूम क्व पारिक्षिता अभवन्निति क्व पारिक्षिता अभवन्स त्वा पृच्छामि याज्ञवल्क्य क्व पारिक्षिता अभवन्निति॥१॥**

 अथ Then भुज्युः Bhujyu लाह्यायनिः the grandson of Lahya पप्रच्छ asked (questions) एनं ह him (Yajnavalkya). उवाच ह (Bhujyu) said, asked इति thus : याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya मद्रेषु in the country called Madra पर्यत्रजाम (we) travelled चरकाः\*(as) students ऐम (we) came, arrived गृहान् to the

—————————————————————————————

\* Students, observers of the appropriate vow for study. Priests called Adhwaryu. For further light on the word see Sir R. G. Bhandarkar in ' Indian Antiquary'.

———————————————————————————————



houses ते of that पतञ्जलस्य of Patanjala काप्यस्य Kapya, a descendant of Kapi. तस्य His दुहिता daughter आसीत् was गन्धर्वगृहीता possessed by a Gandharva. अपृच्छाम (We) asked, interrogated तम् him (Gandharva) इति thus : कः who असि are (you) ? सः He (Gandharva) अब्रवीत् said, replied सुधन्वाआङ्गिरसः (I am) Sudhanwan, a descendant of Angirasa. यदा Then अपृच्छाम (we) asked तम् him (Gandharva), अन्तान् the extent, the limits लोकानाम् of the worlds, of the cosmic orb. अथ Then अब्रूम (we) said एनम् to him क्व where पारिक्षिताः the descendants of Parikshit अभवन् इति were याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya त्वा you पृच्छामि (I) ask क्व where अभवन् इति क्व where पारिक्षिताः the descendants of Parikshit.

 \[It has been stated before that the liberated man does not go anywhere after death. When he dies, he goes out like a light leaving only the name behind. The present section brings out the idea that liberation is not attainable by work of any kind. It is wrong to think that a high degree of excellence in work may lead to liberation. Work has no access to liberation at all. Work with its factors and results is solely confined to the relative world of name and form. Liberation is neither an effect, nor a created object. It is eternal, unmanifested, beyond name and form and absolutely devoid of all the characteristics of action. Production, attainment, modification and purification are the fourfold functions of work. Except these



it has no other function. But liberation is none of 'them. Liberation is the destruction of bondage to bodies and organs and elements and total exhaustion of work both bad and good. It is indeed the cessation of transmigration. Therefore it is very clearly shown in this section that results of work however good is within the range of relative world and does not lead to liberation.\]

 When the descendant of Jaratkaru had stopped, the grandson of Lahya named Bhujyu asked questions to Yājnavalkya. Bhujyu asked, "Yājnavalkya, while we travelled in the country called Madra observing appropriate vow for study we arrived at the house of Patanjala, a descendant of Kapi. His daughter was possessed by a Gandharva¹ (a celestial being). We asked the Gandharva who was he? He replied that he was a descendant of Angiras named Sudhanwan. Desirous of knowing the extent of the cosmic orb we asked him where the descendants of Parikshit were? He revealed to us all about the limits of the universe. Possessed of that knowledge from the Gandharva I ask you, 'Yājnavalkya, where were the descendants of Parikshit?'

—————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. Gandharva is a being other than human, or an extraordinary or celestial being, or the fire that is worshipped in the house, or the god who is a priest to the gods.

———————————————————————————————



———————————————————————————————

2\. A royal race of yore supposed to have been vanished from earth. The names of their descendants are given in Shatapath Brahmana(13.5.4.1-3).\]

—————————————————————————————

 ** स होवाचोवाच वै सोऽगच्छन्वै ते तद्यत्राश्वमेधयाजिनो गच्छन्तीति क्व न्वश्वमेधयाजिनो गच्छन्तीति द्वात्रिꣳशतं वै देवरथाह्न्यान्ययं लोकस्तꣳसमन्तं पृथिवी द्विस्तावत्पर्येति ताꣳसमन्तं पृथिवीं द्विस्तावत्समुद्रः पर्येति तद्यावतीः क्षुरस्य धारा यावद्वा मक्षिकायाः पत्रं तावानन्तरेणाऽऽकाशस्तानिन्द्रः सुपर्णो भूत्वा वायवे प्रायच्छत्तान्वायुरात्मनि धित्वा तत्रागमयद्यत्राश्वमेधयाजिनोऽभवन्नित्येवमिव वै स वायुमेव प्रशशꣳस तस्माद्वायुरेवव्यष्टिर्वायुः समष्टिरप पुनर्मुत्युं जयति य एवं वेद ततो ह भुज्युर्लाह्यायनिरुपरराम॥२॥ इति तृतीयं ब्राह्मणम्॥३॥**

** **स ह He (Yajnavalkya) उवाच said, replied. सः He (Gandharva) वै evidently उवाच said तत् that वै verily ते they (the descendants of Parikshit) अगच्छन् went, dwelt यत्र where अश्वमेधयाजिनः the performers of the horse sacrifice गच्छन्ति इति go. (Bhujyu asked ) क्वनु where अश्वमेध याजिनः the performers of the horse-sacrifice गच्छन्ति इति go वै Verily द्वात्रिंशतम् thirty two lines देवरथ-अह्न्यानि covered by the Sun's chariot in a day अयम् this लोकः (is) world. समन्तम् Around तम् it पर्येति surrounds द्विः twice तावत् as much, as large पृथिवी the earth. समन्तम् Around ताम् that पृथिवीम् earth पर्येति surrounds द्विः twice तावत् as much, as large समुद्रः the ocean. तत् Now यावती as धारा the edge तुरस्य of a razor



वा or यावत् as पलम् the fine wing मक्षिकायाः of a fly, of a mosquito तावान् so, that much आकाशः sky, opening अन्तरेण between, at the junction (of the two halves of the cosmic shell): इन्द्रः Indra, God, fire kindled in the horse-sacrifice प्रायच्छत् delivered, handed over तान् then (the descendants of Parikshit) वायवे to the air भूत्वा being सुपर्णः a falcon. वायुः The air धित्वा putting, holding तान् them आत्मानि within itself अगमयत् made (them) go, conveyed (them) go, conveyed तत्र there यत्र where अश्वमेध-याजिनः the performers of horse-sacrifice अभवन् इति were, dwelt एवम् इव Thus वै indeed सः he प्रशशंस praised वायुम् the air एव indeed. तस्मात् Therefore वायुः the air एव indeed (is) : the individuality, the cause of individual forms: arg: the air (is) व्यष्टिः the indiviuality, the cause of individual forms : वायुः the air समष्टिः aggregate, collectivity. य Who वेद knows एवम् thus अपजयति (he) conquers, overcomes पुनः मृत्युम् repeated death. ततः ह Therefore भूज्युः Bhujyu लह्यायनि the grand son of Lahya उपरराम kept silent, stopped

 Yājnavalkya replied to Bhujyu: I suppose the Gandharva told you that the descendants of Parikshit go where the performers of the horse sacrifice go. Bhujyu asked where the performers of the horse-sacrifice go. Yājnavalkya replied that the world¹ where they go is equal to thirty-two times the space journeyed by the sun's chariot in a day. The earth twice as large as this world surrounds it on every side. The ocean² twice as large as the earth surrounds the latter. Now, as



the edge of a razor, or the wing of a mosquito is fine, so small is the opening between the two halves of the cosmic shell. Through that opening³ fire kindled in the horse-sacrifice in the form of a falcon with wings, tails, etc., handed over the descendants of Parikshit to air. The air holding" them within itself conveyed them where the previous performers of the horse-sacrifice dwelt. did the Gandharvas praise the air by which the performers of the horse-sacrifice reached their goal. Therefore the air is the cause of individuality relating to the body, the elements and the gods. It is also the cause of their collectivity as the one cosmic vital power. He who has got this knowledge overcomes repeated death by becoming identified with air in its individual and collective aspects. Thereupon Bhujyu, the grandson of Lahya stopped.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. This world is surrounded by the mountain,Lokāloka which is the same as the world of Viraj, where people reap the fruits of their past works. This much is the Loka; beyond this is the Aloka.

2\. Ocean is named after rain-water by the authors of the Puranas.

3\. It is the exit through which the performers of the horse-sacrifice go out and spread.

4\. Making them a part of itself.\]

———————————————————————————————



**CHAPTER THREE: SECTION FOUR**

** अथ हैनमुषस्तश्चाक्रायणः पप्रच्छ याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यत्साक्षादपरोक्षाद्ब्रह्म य आत्मा सर्वान्तरस्तं मे व्याचक्ष्वेत्येष त आत्मा सर्वान्तरः कतमो याज्ञवल्क्य सर्वान्तरो यः प्राणेन प्राणिति स त आत्मा सर्वान्तरो योऽपानेनापानीति स त आत्मा सर्वान्तरो यो व्यानेन व्यानीति स त आत्मा सर्वान्तरो य उदानेनोदानिति स त आत्मा सर्वान्तर एष त आत्मा सर्वान्तरः॥१॥**

 अथ Then उषस्तः Ushasta चाक्रायणः the son of Chakra पप्रच्छ asked एनं ह him (Yajnavalkya). याज्ञवल्क्य इति (Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said (he) व्याचच्व explain, tell about मे to me तम् that ब्रह्म Brahman, (literally) vastest यत् that (is) साक्षात् immediate unobstructed अपरोक्षत् direct, used in a primary sense अत्मा the inmost self, यः that सर्वान्तरः इति (is) within all एषः This ते your अत्मा individual self सर्वान्तरः (is) within all. याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya कतमः which सर्वान्तरः (is) within all? सः That यः which प्राणिति breaths, does the function of Prāna प्राणेन through the Prāna ते your आत्मा innerself सर्वान्तरः (is) within all. सः That यः which अपानिति \* goes downwards अपानेन through the Apāna ते your आत्मा inner self सर्वान्तरः (is) within all. सः That यः which व्यानिति which pervades व्यानेन through the Vyāna ते your आत्मा Self सर्वान्तरः (is) within all. सः That यः which

—————————————————————————————

\*The long 'i' in the two verbs is a Vedic licence.

———————————————————————————————



उदानिति goes out उदानेन through the Udān ते your आत्मा inner self सर्वान्तरः (is) within all. एषः This ते your आत्मा Self सर्वान्तरः (is) within all,

 \[It has already been said that the perfection of merits is only concerned with the transmigratory existence and leads to the identity with Hiranyagarbha. Does the transmigrating entity exist? What it is like? This section explains the inner-most Self as a distinct entity. Transmigration stops when one knows that the Self is eternally free from all ideas of agency and enjoyment.\]

 When Bhujyu stopped, the son of Chakra named Ushasta asked questions to Yājnavalkya Ushasta asked: Yājnavalkya, tell¹ me about the Brahman that is never obstructed from the seer (subject) by anything—the Self that is always used. in a primary sense and never figuratively. Thus addressed Yājnavalkya replied that Brahman is the innermost Self that is within all. Ushasta asked: Which of these Selves² you mean as my Self that is within all. Thus spoken to, Yājnavalkya replied: That Self which does the function of the Prāna³ is the Self that is within all. That Self which goes downwards through the Apāna is the Self that is within all. That Self which through the Vyana pervades the body and organs. and make them function like a wooden puppet is



the Self that is within all. That which goes out through the Udāna is the Self that is within all. This is your Self that is within all.

—————————————————————————————

\[NOTES — 1. Explain to me as clearly as one shows a cow by catching hold of its horns.

2\. Firstly Self of the body and organs. Secondly the Self that ensouls the subtle body. Thirdly Self is that whose existence is being doubted.

3\. It operates through the mouth and the nose.\] '

—————————————————————————————

 ** स होवाचोषस्तश्चाक्रायणो यथा विब्रूयादसौ गौरसावश्व इत्येवमेवैतद्व्यपदिष्टं भवति यदेव साक्षादपरोक्षाद्ब्रह्म य आत्मा सर्वान्तरस्तं मे व्याचक्ष्वेत्येष त आत्मा सर्वान्तरः कतमो याज्ञवल्क्य सर्वान्तरः। न दृष्टेर्द्रष्टारं पश्येर्न श्रुतेः श्रोतारꣳ शृणुयान्न मतेर्मन्तारं मन्वीथा न विज्ञातेर्विज्ञातारं विजानीयाः। एष त आत्मा सर्वान्तरोऽतोऽन्यदार्तं ततो होषस्तश्चाक्रायण उपरराम॥२॥ इति चतुर्थं ब्राह्मणम्॥४॥**

 सः That उषस्तः Ushasta चाक्रायणः the son of Chakra उवाच ह said इति thus : यथा as विब्रूयात् (one) may say, may describe असौ this गौः cow असौ this अश्वः horse एवम् thus, so एव only एतत् it भवति is व्यपदिष्टम् pointed out, indicated (by you). व्याचक्ष्व Tell, explain, मे to me, तत् that ब्रह्म Brahman, यत् which ( is) एव indeed साक्षात् immediate अपरोक्षात् (and) direct आत्मा the Self यः which ( is) सर्वान्तरः within all. एषः This (is) ते your आत्मा Self सर्वान्तरः ( which is) within all,  




 याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. कतमः Which ( is ) सर्वान्तरः within a ll. पश्येः (You) see न not द्रष्टारम् the seer दृष्टेः the function of the eye (of the sight) श्रुणुयात (you) hear न not श्रोतारम् the hearer श्रुतेः the function of the ear (of hearing). मन्वीथाः (You) think the न not मन्तारम् the thinker मतेः of the thought, of the function of the mind. विजानीथाः (You) know न not विज्ञातारम् the knower विज्ञातेः of knowledge, of the function of intellect. एषः This ते your आत्मा Self सर्वान्तरः (is) within all. अन्यत् The other, everything else अतः than this आर्तम् (is) perishable. ततः Thereupon उषस्तः Ushasta चाक्रायणः the son of Chakra उपरराम kept silent, stopped.

 Ushasta, the son of Chakra, said to Yājnavalkya, 'As one describes a cow or a horse through certain characteristics so you have indicated BrahmanTell me the Brahman which is immediate and direct and dwells in all beings as their Self.' Yājnavalkya replied: Your own Self is the very Self of all beings. Ushasta asked: "Which Self is within all?" Yājnavalkya replied: "You cannot see the seer' who pervades the function of the eyes. You cannot hear the hearer who pervades the function of the ear. You cannot think the thinker who pervades the function of the mind. You cannot know the knower who pervades the function of the intellect. This your own Self as specified above is the Self of all beings. Everything else whether it is gross body or subtle body consisting



of organs is perishable. This Self alone is imperishable and changeless." Thereupon Ushasta, the son of Chakra stopped.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The seer has two kinds of sight—one is ordinary and the other is eternal. The ordinary sight is a function of the mind as connected with the eye. It is an act. Hence it has a beginning and an end. But the sight with which the seer—the Self—is endowed is like the heat and light of fire. It is eternal and is the very essence of the seer. It pervades the act of ordinary vision and has neither beginning nor end. The ordinary sight is an effect, a mere function of the eye and is but a limiting adjunct of the eternal sight. When the latter appears to be in contact with the former, it is described as the seer and also las differentiated into seer and sight. The ordinary sight, however, is coloured by the objects seen through the eye and is only a reflection of the eternal sight. The former originates, ends and is pervaded by the latter. It is therefore that the eternal sight of the Self is metaphorically spoken of as the seer and although eternally seeing, is described as sometimes seeing and sometimes not seeing. But as a matter of fact, the sight of the seer is never lost.\]

——————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER THREE: SECTION FIVE**

 ** अथ हैनं कहोलः कौषीतकेयः पप्रच्छ याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यदेव साक्षादपरोक्षाद्ब्रह्म य आत्मा सर्वान्तरस्तं मे व्याचक्ष्वेत्येष त आत्मा सर्वान्तरः। कतमो याज्ञवल्क्य सर्वान्तरो**



**योऽशनायापिपासे शोकं मोहं जरां मृत्युमत्येति। एतं वै तमात्मानं विदित्वा ब्राह्मणाः पुत्रैषणायाश्च वित्तैषणायाश्च लोकैषणायाश्च व्युत्थायाथ भिक्षाचर्यं चरन्ति या ह्येव पुत्रैषणा सा वित्तैषणा या वित्तैषणा सा लोकैषणोभे ह्येते एषणे एव भवतः। तस्माद्ब्राह्मणः पाण्डित्यं निर्विद्य वाल्येन तिष्ठासेत्। बाल्यं च पाण्डित्यं च निर्विद्याथ मुनिरमौनं च मौनं च निर्विद्याथ ब्राह्मणः स ब्राह्मणः केन स्याद्येन स्यात्तेनेदृश एवातोऽन्यदार्तं ततो ह कहोलः कौषीतकेय उपरराम॥१॥ इति पञ्चमं ब्राह्मणम्॥५॥**

 अथ Then कहोलः Kahola कौषीतकेयः the son of Kushitaka पप्रच्छ asked एनं ह him (Yajnavalkya): याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said (he) इति thus: व्याचक्ष्वः tell, explain मे to me तम् that ब्रह्म Brahman यद् which (is) एव verily साक्षात् immediate, unobstructed. अपरोक्षात् Used in a primary sense, direct आत्मा the Self यः which (is) सर्वान्तरः within all. (Yajnavalkya replied) एषः this ते your आत्मा Self सर्वान्तरः (is) within all. (Kahola asked) कतमः which (is) सर्वान्तरः within all याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya? यः (That) which अत्येति transcends, overcomes अशनायापिपासे hunger and thirst शोकम् grief मोहम् delusion जराम् decay मृत्युम् death वै verily विदित्वा realising, knowing तम् that एतम् this आत्मानम् Self ब्राह्मणाः the (ancient) Brahmanas व्युत्थाय having risen, having given up पुत्रैषणायाः च desire for son, marriage वित्तैषणायाः च desire for wealth च and लोकैषणायाः desire for worlds अथ then चरन्ति wander about, lead भिक्षाचर्यम् a mendicant's life. हि For सा that या which (is) पुत्रैषणा desire for son, (is) एवम् indeed



वित्तैषणा desire for wealth. सा That या which (is) वित्तैषणा desire for wealth. लोकैषणा (is) desire for worlds. हि For उभे both एते these भवतः are एव indeed एषणे desires. तस्मात् Therefore ब्राह्मणः the knower of Brahman. निर्विद्य having known, having done away with पाण्डित्यम् learning, scholarship तिष्ठासेत् should try to live, should wish to stand, बाल्येन with strength (of knowledge). अथ Then निर्विद्य having known, having dispensed with बाल्यं च strength च as well as पाण्डित्यम् learning, scholarship मुनिः (becomes) meditative, Muni. अथः Then निर्विद्य having known, having renounced अमौनं च unmeditativeness मौनं च meditativeness ब्राह्मणः (becomes) a knower of Brahman. केन How सः that ब्राह्मणः knower of Brahman स्यात् moves about, behaves? येन Howsoever स्यात् (he) may behave, may move about तेन by that एव indeed ईदृशः (he is) just such. अन्यत् Every thing, all desires, अतः except this आर्तम् (is) unsubstantial, perishable, beset with troubles. ततः ह Thereupon कहोलः Kahola कौषीतकेयः son of Kushitaka उपरराम kept silent, stopped.

 \[This section describes the knowledge of Self as well as renunciation which is the means of attaining that knowledge and thus liberating the Self from bondage.\]

 Then Kahola, the son of Kushitaka, asked questions to Yājnavalkya. He said, ‘Tell me the Brahman that is unobstructed by anything and used in a primary sense’. Yājnavalkya replied: ‘Your own Self which dwells in all beings is that Brahman.’ Kahola asked: Kahola asked: ‘Which Self is within



all? Yājnavalkya replied: ‘That which is beyond hunger and thirst, grief and delusion, decay and death is your own Self. Realising their very Self as Brahman free from all attributes the ancient Brahmanas gave up the desire for sons, desire for wealth and desire for the worlds of the manes and the gods and wandered about as monks living on alms. Every desire for means is a desire for results. Therefore that which is the desire for son, is the desire for wealth, and that which is desire for wealth is the desire for worlds, for both these are indeed desires, one being but a means to the other. Therefore a knower of Brahman does away with learning and tries to stand by the strength which is born of Self-knowledge. Having dispensed with strength and learning he becomes meditative. Having renounced both meditativeness and its opposite he becomes a knower of Brahman. How does the knower of Brahman move about? Howsoever he may move about, he remains a Knower of Brahman. Except this Knowledge of Brahman which is accompanied by eternal satisfaction, all desires are unsubstantial like a dream, illusion or mirage.’ Thereupon Kahola, the son of Kushitaka stopped.

 Those who are ignorant of Self derive their strength from the means and results of actions.



——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Hunger and thirst centre in the vital power.

2\. Grief is desire. It is a kind of discomfort felt by one who reflects on some covetable thing. This discomfort kindles desire.

3\. Delusion is a mistake. It is a sort of a confusion born of wrong perception. Both grief and delusion dwell in the mind.

4\. Decay is that change of body and organs which is marked by wrinkles, grey hair, etc.

5\. Death is ultimate change that overtakes the body and results in the fall of the body. These six from hunger to death work in all beings in an unbroken succession like days and nights or the waves of an ocean. They are in reality attributes of vital power, mind and body. They never belong to the Self which remains untouched by them.

6\. It is the means of winning this world.
