7\. Cattle, etc., which are the means of performing sacrifices.

8\. Monastic life is characterised by renunciation of desires and also abandonment of all work together with their means.

9\. Self-knowledge is the same as the total annihilation of all ideas of non-Self.

10\. The knowledge of Self derived from the teacher and the scriptures.

11\. It is a tribute to the Knowledge of Brahman and does not mean reckless behaviour. Mahabharat (14. 46. 51) says that the Knower of Brahman does not wear signs but practises the principles. Vayu Purana (10) says his signs are not manifest nor his behaviour.

12\. As a rope is fancied to be a snake, a mother of pearl to be silver and the sky to be blue and concave on account of

——————————————————————————————



ignorance, so the Self is ignorantly imagined to be subject of the attributes of body, mind and vital power. All these attributes are unreal. The phenomenal world appears real to those who have conventional ignorant outlook. But this illusion is a fact only to the Knower of Brahman. For him Brahman alone is one absolute Reality without a second and beyond all finite relations.\]

**CHAPTER THREE: SECTION SIX**

** अथ हैनं गार्गी वाचक्नवी पप्रच्छ याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच यदिदꣳ सर्वमप्स्वोतं च प्रोतं च कस्मिन्नु खल्वाप ओताश्च प्रोताश्चेति वायौ गार्गीति कस्मिन्नु खलु वायुरोतश्च प्रोतश्चेत्यन्तरिक्षलोकेषु गार्गीति कस्मिन्नु खल्वन्तरिक्षलोका ओताश्च प्रोताश्चेति गन्धर्वलोकेषु गार्गीति कस्मिन्नु खलु गन्धर्वलोका ओताश्च प्रोताश्चेत्यादित्यलोकेषु गार्गीति कस्मिन्नु खल्वादित्यलोका ओताश्च प्रोताश्चेति चन्द्रलोकेषु गार्गीति कस्मिन्नु खलु चन्द्रलोका ओताश्च प्रोताश्चेति नक्षत्रलोकेषु गार्गीति कस्मिन्नु खलु नक्षत्रलोका ओताश्च प्रोताश्चेति देवलोकेषु गार्गीति कस्मिन्नु खलु देवलोका ओताश्च प्रोताश्चेतीन्द्रलोकेषु गार्गीति कस्मिन्नु खल्विन्द्रलोका ओताश्च प्रोताश्चेति प्रजापतिलोकेषु गार्गीति कस्मिन्नु खलु प्रजापतिलोका ओताश्च प्रोताश्चेति ब्रह्मलोकेषु गार्गीति कस्मिन्नु खलु ब्रह्मलोका ओताश्च प्रोताश्चेति स होवाच**



**गार्गि माऽतिप्राक्षीर्मा ते मूर्धा व्यपप्तदनतिप्रश्न्यां वै देवतामतिपृच्छसि गार्गि माऽतिप्राक्षीरिति ततो ह गार्गी वाचक्नव्युपरराम॥१॥ इति षष्ठं ब्राह्मणम्॥६॥ **

 अथ Then गार्गी Gargi वाचक्नवी the daughter of Vachaknu पप्रच्छ asked एनं ह him (Yajnavalkya). उवाच ह (she) said इति thus: याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya यत् if सर्वम् all इदम् this ओतं च प्रोतं च (is) pervaded, placed like warp and woof in a cloth अप्सु in water कस्मिन् नु in what आपः\* water खलु indeed ओतः च प्रोतः च इति (is) woven, pervaded? वायौः In air, गार्गि इति O Gargi. कस्मिन् नु In what वायुः air खलु indeed ओतः च प्रोतः च (is) woven, pervaded ? अन्तरिक्षलोकेषु In the worlds of the sky, गार्गि इति O Gargi. कस्मिन् नु In what अन्तरिक्षलोकाः खलु worlds of the sky indeed ओताः च प्रोताः च इति (are) pervaded? गन्धर्वलोकेषु In the worlds of the Gandharvas (celestial minstrels) गार्गि इति O Gargi. कस्मिन् नु In what गन्धर्वलोकाः the worlds of the Gandharvas खलु indeed ओताः च प्रोताः च इति (are) pervaded, woven? आदित्य-लोकेषु In the worlds of the Sun गार्गि इति O Gargi. कस्मिन् नु In what आदित्य-लोकाः the worlds of the Sun खलु indeed ओताः च प्रोताः च इति (are) pervaded, woven ? चन्द्रलोकेषु In the worlds of the moon, गार्गि इति O Gargi. कस्मिन् नु In what चन्द्रलोकाः the worlds of the moon खलु indeed ओताः च प्रोताः च (are) woven, pervaded? नक्षत्रलोकेषु In the worlds of the stars, गार्गि इति O Gargi. कस्मिन् नु In what नक्षत्रलोकाः the worlds

——————————————————————————————

\* As fire cannot manifest itself independently like other elements and must take the help of the particles:of earth, or water, fire is not mentioned here as pervading water.

——————————————————————————————



of stars खलु indeed ओताः च प्रोताः च (are) pervaded, woven? देवलोकेषु In the worlds of the gods गार्गि इति O Gargi. कस्मिन् नु In what देवलोकाः the worlds of the gods खलु indeed ओताः च प्रोताः च इति (are) woven, pervaded? इन्द्रलोकेषु इति In the worlds of Indra. कस्मिन् नु In what इन्द्रलोकाः the worlds of Indra खलु indeed ओताः च प्रोताः च इति (are) pervaded, woven? प्रजापति-लोकेषु In the worlds of Prajapati (Viraj) गार्गि इति O Gargi. कस्मिन् नु In what प्रजापतिलोकाः the worlds of Prajapati खलु indeed ओताः च प्रोताः च इति (are ) pervaded, woven? In the worlds of Brahman (Hiranyagarba) गार्गि इति O Gargi. कस्मिन् नु In what ब्रह्मलोकाः the worlds of Brahman (Hiranyagarbha) ओताः च प्रोताः च इति (are) pervaded ? सः ह He (Yajnavalkya) उवाच said गार्गि O Gargi मा do not अतिप्राक्षीः ask too much, push your question too for. ते Your मूर्धा head व्यपप्तत् should fall off मा not गार्गि O Gargi. वै Verily अति पृच्छसि (you) are asking too much, are questioning too far देवताम् a deity अनतिप्रश्न्याम् that should not be reasoned about. मा Not अतिप्राक्षीः इति ask too much, question too far. ततः ह Thereupon गार्गी Gargi वाचक्नवी the daughter of Vachaknu उपरराम
kept silent, stopped.

 \[This passage shows how the aspirant can realise his own Self by taking up each of the relatively external elements from earth up to the ether and eliminating it.\]

 Then Gārgi, the daughter of Vachaknu, asked questions to Yājnavalkya. She said, ‘If all, that is composed of earth is pervaded within and without



by water¹, what pervades water?’ Yājnavalkya replied: Air pervades water. Gārgi asked, ‘What pervades air?’ Yājnavalkya replied: Sky pervades air. Gārgi asked, ‘What pervades the sky?’ Yājnavalkya replied: The worlds of the Gandharvas (celestial minstrels) pervade the sky. Gārgi asked: What pervades the worlds of the Gandharvas? Yājnavalkya replied: The worlds of the sun pervade the world of the Gandharvas. Gārgi asked: What pervades the worlds of the sun? Yājnavalkya replied: The worlds of the moon pervade the worlds of the sun. Gārgi asked: What pervades the worlds of the moon? Yājnavalkya replied: The worlds of the stars pervade the worlds of the moon. Gārgi asked: What pervades the worlds of the stars? Yājnavalkya replied: that worlds of the gods pervade the worlds of the stars. Gārgi asked: What pervades the worlds of the gods? Yājnavalkya replied: The worlds of Indra pervades the worlds of the gods. Gārgi asked: What pervades the worlds of Indra? Yajnavalkya replied that the worlds² of Viraj pervade the worlds of Indra. Gārgi asked: What pervades the worlds of Viraj? Yājnavalkya replied that the worlds of the Hiranyagarbha pervade the worlds of Viraj. Gārgi asked: What pervades the worlds of Hiranyagarbha? Yājnavalkya said, ‘Do not, O Gārgi, ask



too much, lest by so doing your head should fall off. You are questioning about a deity who cannot be known through reasoning. Do not, O Gārgi, question too far unless you wish to die.’ There-upon Gārgi, the daughter of Vachaknu, stopped.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Otherwise the earth would be scattered like a handful of fried barley flour.

2\. i.e., the elements that compose the body of Viraj.

3\. i.e., the elements that compose the Universe.

4\. The plural in ‘worlds’ is used in the Text, because these worlds are arranged in an ascending order of subtlety, and each of them is composed of the same five elements so transformed as to become fit abodes for the enjoyment of beings.

5\. The nature of the deity cannot be known through inference. The deity must be known only from the scriptures.\]

——————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER THREE: SECTION SEVEN**

** अथ हैनमुद्दालक आरुणिः पप्रच्छ याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच मद्रेष्ववसाम पतञ्चलस्य काप्यस्य गृहेषु यज्ञमधीयानास्तस्याऽऽसीद्भार्या गन्धर्वगृहीता तमपृच्छाम कोऽसीति सोऽब्रवीत्कबन्ध आथर्वण इति सोऽब्रवीत्पतञ्चलं काप्यं याज्ञिकाꣳश्च वेत्थ नु त्वं काप्य तत्सूत्रं येनायं च लोकः परश्च लोकः सर्वाणि च भूतानि सन्दृब्धानि भवन्तीति सोऽब्रवीत्पतञ्चलः काप्यो नाहं**



**तद्भगवन्वेदेति सोऽब्रवीत्पतञ्चलं काप्यं याज्ञिकाꣳश्च वेत्थ नु त्वं काप्य तमन्तर्यामिणं य इमं च लोकं परं च लोकꣳसर्वाणि च भूतानि योऽन्तरोयमयतीति सोऽब्रवीत्पतञ्चलः काप्यो नाहं तं भगवन्वेदेति सोऽब्रवीत्पतञ्चलं काप्यं याज्ञिकाꣳश्च यो वै तत्काप्य सूत्रं विद्यात्तं चान्तर्यामिणमिति स ब्रह्मवित्स लोकवित्स देववित्स वेदवित्स भूतवित्स आत्मवित्स सर्वविदिति तेभ्योऽब्रवीत्तदहं वेद तच्चेत्त्वं याज्ञवल्क्य सूत्रमविद्वाꣳस्तं चान्तर्यामिणं ब्रह्मगवीरुदजसे मूर्धा ते विपतिष्यतीति वेद वा अहं गौतम तत्सूत्रं तं चान्तर्यामिणमिति यो वा इदं कश्चिद्ब्रूयाद्वेद वेदेति यथा वेत्थ तथा ब्रूहीति॥१॥**

 अथ Then उद्दालकः Uddalaka आरुणिः the son of Aruna पप्रच्छ asked एनं ह him (Yajnavalkya). उवाच ह (He) said इति this: याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya मद्रेषु in the country of Madra, अवसम् (we) lived, dwelt गृहेषु in the house पतञ्चलस्य of Patanchala काप्यस्य a descendant of Kapi अधीयानाः studying यज्ञम् sacrifice, the scriptures on sacrifice. तस्य His भार्या wife आसीत् was गन्धर्व-गृहीता possessed by a Gandharva. अपृच्छम् (He) asked तम् him (Gandharva) इति thus: कः who असि are (you) ? सः He (Gandharva) अब्रवीत् said इति (I am) कबन्धः Kabandha, आथर्वणः the son of Atharvan. सः He अब्रवीत् said, asked पतञ्चलम् to Patanchala काप्यम् a descendant of Kapi च and याज्ञिकन् students of the scriptures on sacrifices काप्यः a descendant of Kapi नु त्वम् do you वेत्थ know तत् that सूत्रम् thread, cosmic vital power, innermost



entity of the world of Hiranyagarbha येन by which अयम् this लोकः world, life च and परं च the next लोकः world, life च and सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings भवन्ति are सन्दृब्धानि strung together, held together? तत् That पतञ्चलः Patanchala काप्यः a descendant of Kapi अब्रवीत् said भगवन् Venerable Sir अहम् I वेद know न not तत् it. सः He अब्रवीत् said पतञ्चलम् to Patanchal काप्यम् a descendant of Kapi च and यज्ञिकान् the students नु त्वम् do you वेत्थ know. काप्य Kapya तम् that अन्तर्यामिणम् Inner controller यः who यमयति causes them move, makes them perform, controls अन्तरे from within इमम् this लोकम् life च and परं the next लोकम्ः world, life च and सर्वाणि all भूतानि इति beings, creatures. सः That पतञ्चलः Patanchala काप्यः Kapya अब्रवीत् said इति thus भगवन् Venerable Sir अहम् I वेद know न not तम् it. सः He अब्रवीत् said पतञ्चलम् Patanchala काप्यम् Kapya च and यज्ञिकान् the students. वै verily सः he यः who विद्यात् knows काप्य Kapya तत् that सूत्रम् Sutra, thread च and तम् that अन्तर्यामिणम् इति Inner controller, सः he (is) ब्रह्मवित् the knower of Brahman; सः he लोकवित् (is) the knower of the worlds; सः he देववित् (is) the knower of Godsसः he वेदवित् (is) the knower of Vedas सः he भूतवित् (is) the knower of beings; सः he आत्मवित् (is) the knower of the Self; सः he सर्ववित् इति (is) the knower of all, अब्रवीत् (he) said, described (it) तेभ्यः to them अहम् I वेद know तत् it चेत् if त्वम् you याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya अविद्वान् without knowing तत् that सूत्रम् Sutra, तम् that अन्तर्यामिणम् Inner controller उदजसे take away ब्रह्मगवीः the cows belonging. to the knower of Brahmin. ते Your मुर्धा head विपतिष्यति इति will fall off. वै Verily गौतम



Gautam वेद know तत् that सूत्रम् Sutra च and तत् that अन्तर्यामिणम् इति Inner controller, वै indeed यः who इदम् this कश्चित् anyone ब्रूयात् may say वेद (I) know. वेद इति (I) know ब्रूहि tell, describe तथा so यथा as वेत्थ इति (you ) know.

 \[This section describes the Sutra which is the innermost entity of the world of Hiranyagarbha. The following anecdote is introduced to show that the Sutra is to be known through oral instruction.\]

 Then Uddālaka, the son of Aruna, asked questions to Yājnavalkya. He said, “In the country of the Madra, we dwelt in the house of Patanchala, a descendant of Kapi, as students of the scriptures on sacrifices. His wife was possessed by a Gandharva. He asked the Gandharva who he was. The Gandharva replied that he was Kabandha, the son of Atharvan. He asked Patanchala Kapya and his students of the scriptures on sacrifices: ‘Do you know that Sutra by which this world, the next world and all creatures from Hiranyagarbha down to a clump of grass are strung together like a garland with a thread?’ Patanchala Kapya replied to the Gandharva reverentially that he did not know It. The Gandharva again asked him and the students, whether they knew the Inner Controller who governs this world and the next and all beings from within like a wooden puppet? Patanchala Kapya replied



respectfully in the negative. The Gandharva said again to him and the students in praise of the meditation, of Sutra as follows: The Knower of Sutra and Inner Controller as described above is verily the Knower of Brahman (Supreme Self). He is the Knower of the worlds such as the earth controlled by the Sutra. He is the Knower of the gods such as fire who preside over those worlds. He is the Knower of the Vedas which are authorities for all. He is the Knower of all beings upto Viraj. He is the Knower of the Self who is the agent and the experiencer. He is the Knower of all. Thus the Gandharva described the Sutra to them and us. I have known this meditation on Sutra from the Gandharva. If you, Yājnavalkya, do not know the Sutra and the Inner Controller and still take away the cows belonging only to the knowers of Brahman, your head shall fall off.” Yajnavalkya said, I know, O Gautama, that Sutra and the Inner Controller.’ At this Gautama retorted thus: Anybody may laud himself saying, ‘I know, I know.’ Describe to us what you know about It.

 ** स होवाच वायुर्वै गौतम तत्सूत्रं वायुना वै गौतम सूत्रेणायं च लोकः परश्च लोकः सर्वाणि च भूतानि सन्दृब्धानि भवन्ति तस्माद्वै गौतम पुरुषं प्रेतमाहुर्व्यस्रꣳसिषतास्याङ्गानीति वायुना**



**हि गौतम सूत्रेण सन्दृब्धानि भवन्तीत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्यान्तर्यामिणं ब्रूहीति॥२॥**

 सः He (Yajnavalkya) उवाच ह said. गौतम O Gautam वै verily वायुः Vayu (is) तत् that सूत्रम् Sutra. वै Verily गौतम O Gautam वायुना by Vayu (air) by Sutra (thread) अयम् this लोकः च world च and परः the next लोकः world च and सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings, creatures भवन्ति are सन्दृब्धानि held together, strung together. तस्मात् Therefore गौतम O Gautam वै verily आहुः (people) say इति thus पुरुषम् of a person प्रेतम् dead अस्य his अङ्गानि limbs व्यस्रं-सिषत are scattered, are loosened हि because गौतम O Gautam वायुना by Vayu (air) सूत्रेण by Sutra (thread) भवन्ति are सन्दृब्धानि इति held together. एवम् Thus एतत् this याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya ब्रूहि tell, describe अन्तर्यामिणम् the Internal Controller.

 Yājnavalkya said, ‘Vāyu (air) O Gautama, is verily that Sutra (thread) and nothing else. By air as by a thread this world and the next and all creatures are strung together. Therefore, O Gautama people speak of a dead person that his limbs are scattered because they are strung together by air as gems by a thread.’ The other said, ‘It is so, Yājnavalkya. Now tell me about the Internal Controller who is within all.’

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Vāyu is that fine substance which like the ether pervades and supports earth, etc. It is indeed the

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

material of the subtle body with its seventeen parts (such as the ten organs, five vital powers, mind and intellect) in which the past actions and impressions of creatures are stored up. Vāyu has both collective as well as individual aspects. Its external forms like the waves of an ocean are forty-nine Maruts (airs).

2\. Literal meaning of the word is thread. It is so called because it supports everything. It is the principle of Vāyu. The world of Hiranyagarbha is pervaded by it as earth by water.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** यः पृथिव्यां तिष्ठन्पृथिव्या अन्तरो यं पृथिवी न वेद यस्य पृथिवी शरीरं यः पृथिवीमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥३॥ **

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् inhabiting, dwelling पृथिव्याम् in the earth (is) अन्तरः\* inside, within पृथिव्याः of the earth, यम् whom पृथिवी the earth (deity of the earth) न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) पृथिवी the earth, यः who यमयति rules, controls, directs, पृथिवीम् the earth अन्तरः (being) inside, within ते (is) your (also of others) एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self अन्तर्यामी the Inner Ruler.

 Yājnavalkya said: He who dwells in the earth and is within the earth, whom the deity of earth does not know as a distinct entity dwelling within

——————————————————————————————

\*Sankara explains ‘antara’ as ‘abhyantara’. Max Muller following Sankara translates ‘antara’ by within. But Max Muller confesses that he prefers to translate the word as ‘different from’ as Deussen does, particularly as the word governs an ablative.

——————————————————————————————



her, whose body and organs are the same as those of the earth, and who directs the earth to her particular work from within, is the Inner Ruler, Your own immortal Self as also mine and that of all beings.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The body and organs of the deity identified with the earth, etc., which are the result of their past actions, are also the body and organ of the Internal Ruler, who is ever free, and without any past actions as well as body and organs of his own. The body and organs of the deities serve as His.

2. Devoid of all relative attributes.\]

——————————————————————————————

** योऽप्सु तिष्ठन्नद्भ्योऽन्तरो यमापो न विदुर्यस्याऽऽपः शरीरं योऽपोऽन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥४॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling अप्सु in the water, अन्तरः (is) within अद्भ्यः waters, यम् whom आपः water न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body आपः (is) water यः who यमयति controls, directs. आपः water अन्तरः from within. अन्तर्यामी (is) The Inner Ruler, ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the water and is within water, whom the deity of water does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of water and who directs water to its particular work from within, is the Inner Ruler, your own immortal Self as also mine and that of all beings.



 **योऽग्नौ तिष्ठन्नग्नेरन्तरो यमग्निर्न वेद यस्याग्निः शरीरं योऽग्निमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥५॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling अग्नौ in fire अन्तरः (is) inside, within अग्नौ fire, यम् whom अग्निः fire, deity of fire न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) अग्निः fire, यः who यमयति rules, directs, controls fire अन्तरः being inside, from within. अन्तर्यामी (is) The Inner Ruler एषः this ते your अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the fire and is within the fire, whom the deity of fire does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the fire, and who directs the fire from within to its particular work is the Inner Ruler, your own immortal Self as also mine and that of all beings.

 **योऽन्तरिक्षे तिष्ठन्नन्तरिक्षादन्तरो यमन्तरिक्षं न वेद यस्यान्तरिक्षꣳ शरीरं योऽन्तरिक्षमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥६॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling अन्तरिक्षं in the sky अन्तरः (is) अन्तरिक्षात् the sky, यम् whom अन्तरिक्षम् the sky, the presiding deity of the sky न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body अन्तरिक्षम् (is) the sky, यः who यमयति rules, directs अन्तरितम् the sky अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Ruler. ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.



 He who dwells in the sky and is within the sky, whom the deity of the sky does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the sky, and who directs the sky to its particular work from within is the Inner Ruler, Your own immortal Self as also mine and that of all beings.

 **यो वायौ तिष्ठन्वायोरन्तरो यं वायुर्न वेद यस्य वायुः शरीरं यो वायुमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥७॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling वायौ in the air अन्तरः (is) within, inside वायोः the air, यम् whom वायुः the air, deity of air, न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) वायुः the air, यः who यमयति rules, directs वायुम् the air अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Ruler. ते Your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the air and is within the air, whom the deity of air does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the air, and who directs the air to its particular function from within, is the Inner Ruler, your own immortal Self, as also mine and those of all beings.

 ** यो दिवि तिष्ठन्दिवोऽन्तरो यं द्यौर्न वेद यस्य द्यौः शरीरं यो दिवमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥८॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling दिवि in heaven अन्तरः (is) inside, within दिवः heaven, यम् whom द्यौः heaven, deity of



heaven न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) द्यौः heaven, यः who यमयति directs, rules दिवम् heaven अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Ruler ते your एषः this, own अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in heaven and is within heaven, whom the deity of heaven does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of heaven, and who directs heaven from within, is the Inner Ruler, your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.

 **य आदित्ये तिष्ठन्नादित्यादन्तरो यमादित्यो न वेद यस्याऽऽदित्यः शरीरं य आदित्यमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥९॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling आदित्ये in the sun अन्तरः (is) within आदित्यात् the sun, यम् whom आदित्यः the sun, deity of the sun न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body आदित्यः (is) the sun, यः who यमयति directs, controls, rules आदित्यम् the sun अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Ruler ते your एषः this, own अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the sun and is within the sun, whom the deity of the sun does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the sun, and who directs the sun to its particular function from within, is the Inner Ruler, your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.



 ** यो दिक्षु तिष्ठन्दिग्भ्योऽन्तरो यं दिशो न विदुर्यस्य दिशः शरीरं यो दिशोऽन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥१०॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling दिक्षु in the directions अन्तरः (is) within दिग्भ्यः the directions, यम् whom दिशः directions, the deity of directions न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) दिशः directions, यः who यमयति directs, rules दिशः directions अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Ruler ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the directions and is within the directions, whom the deity of directions does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the directions, and who directs the directions to their particular work from within, is the Inner Ruler, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.

** यश्चन्द्रतारके तिष्ठꣳश्चन्द्रतारकादन्तरो यं चन्द्रतारकं न वेद यस्य चन्द्रतारकꣳशरीरं यश्चन्द्रतारकमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥११॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling चन्द्रतारके in the moon and stars अन्तरः (is) within चन्द्रतारकात् the moon and the stars, यम् whom चन्द्रतारकम् moon and stars, deity of the moon and stars न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) चन्द्र-तारकम् the moon and the stars यः who यमयति rules, directs. चन्द्रतारकम् the moon and the stars. अन्तरः from within



अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Ruler ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the moon and stars and is within the moon and stars, whom the deity of moon and stars do not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the moon and stars, and who directs the moon and stars to their particular functions from within, is the Inner Ruler, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.

 **य आकाशे तिष्ठन्नाकाशादन्तरो यमाकाशो न वेद यस्याऽऽकाशः शरीरं य आकाशमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥१२॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling आकाशे in the ether अन्तरः (is) within आकाशात् the ether यम् whom आकाशः the ether, the deity of ether न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) आकाशः the ether यः who यमयति rules, directs, आकाशम् the ether अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Ruler ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal, आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the ether and is within the ether, whom the deity of ether does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the ether and who directs the ether to its particular function from within, is the Inner Ruler, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.



** यस्तमसि तिष्ठꣳस्तमसोऽन्तरो यं तमो न वेद यस्य तमः शरीरं यस्तमोऽन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥१३॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling तमसि in the (eternal) darkness अन्तरः (is) within तमसः of darkness, यम् whom तमः darkness, deity of darkness न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body तमः (is) darkness, यः who यमयति rules, directs, तमः darkness अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner controller ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the external darkness (that obstructs vision) and is within darkness, whom the deity of darkness does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the deity of darkness, who directs darkness from within, is the Inner Ruler, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.

 **यस्तेजसि तिष्ठꣳस्तेजसोऽन्तरो यं तेजो न वेद यस्य तेजः शरीरं यस्तेजोऽन्तरोयमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृत इत्यधिदैवतमथाधिभूतम्॥१४॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling तेजसि in the light अन्तरः (is) within तेजसः of light, यम् whom तेजः light, deity of light न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरं body (is) तेजः light, यः who यमयति rules, directs तेजः light अन्तरः from within, अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner controller ते you एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self. इति This (is) अधि दैवतम् the meditation



(on the Inner Ruler) with regard to the Gods. अथ Now अधिभूतम् meditation (on Him) with regard to the beings.

 He who dwells in the light in general and is within the light, whom the deity of light does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the deity of light, who directs light from within, is the Inner Controller, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings. This is the meditation on the Inner Controller with regard to the gods. Now follows the meditation on the Inner Controller with regard to the various grades of beings (from Hiranyagarbha down to a clump of grass).

 ** यः सर्वेषु भूतेषु तिष्ठन्सर्वेभ्यो भूतेभ्योऽन्तरो यꣳसर्वाणि भूतानि न विदुर्यस्य सर्वाणि भूतानि शरीरं यः सर्वाणि भूतान्यन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृत इत्यधिभूतमथाध्यात्मम्॥१५॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling सर्वेषु in all भूतेषु beings अन्तरः (is) within सर्वेभ्यः all भूतेभ्यः beings, यम् whom सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings न not विदुः know, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings, यः who यमयाति rules, directs सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner controller ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self. इति This अधिभूतम् meditation with regard to the beings. अथ Now अध्यात्मम् meditation with regard to the body.



 He who dwells in all beings and is within all beings, whom the beings do not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of all beings, and who directs all beings to their functions from with- in, is the Inner Controller, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings. This is the meditation on the Inner Controller with regard to the beings. Now follows the meditation with regard to the body.

 ** यः प्राणे तिष्ठन्प्राणादन्तरो यं प्राणो न वेद यस्य प्राणः शरीरं यः प्राणमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥१६॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling प्राणे in the breath, in the vital organ अन्तरः (is) within प्राणात् the breath, the nose, यम् whom प्राणः vital organ, deity of the vital organ, (nose) न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) प्राणः breath, vital organ, यः who यमयति rules, directs प्राणम् the breath, the vital organ अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Controller ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the vital organ and is within the vital organ, whom the deity of the vital organ does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the vital organ, and who directs vital organ (nose) to its function from within, is the Inner Controller, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.



** यो वाचि तिष्ठन्वाचोऽन्तरो यं वाङ् न वेद यस्य वाक्शरीरं यो वाचमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥१७॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling वाचि in the vocal organ, अन्तरः (is) within वाचः of the vocal organ, यम् whom वाक् vocal organ, the deity of vocal organ न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) वाक् the vocal organ, यः who यमयति controls, directs वाक् the vocal organ अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner controller ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the vocal organ and is with- in the vocal organ, whom the deity of the vocal organ does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the deity of the vocal organ, who directs the vocal organ to its function from within, is the Inner Controller, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.

 **यश्चक्षुषि तिष्ठꣳश्चक्षुषोऽन्तरो यं चक्षुर्न वेद यस्य चक्षुः शरीरं यश्चक्षुरन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥१८॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling चक्षुषि in the visual organ, in the eye अन्तरः (is) within चक्षुषः visual organ, the eye, यम् whom चक्षुः the eye न not वेद knows, यः who यमयति controls, directs चक्षुः the eye अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Controller ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.



 He who dwells in the visual organ and is within the visual organ, whom the deity of the visual organ does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the deity of the visual organ, and who directs the visual organ to its function from within, is the Inner Controller, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.

** यः श्रोत्रे तिष्ठञ्छ्रोत्रादन्तरो यꣳ श्रोत्रं न वेद यस्य श्रोत्रꣳ शरीरं यः श्रोत्रमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥१९॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling श्रोत्रे in the ear अन्तरः (is) within श्रोत्रात् the ear, यम् whom श्रोत्रम् the ear, the deity of the ear न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) श्रोत्रम् the ear, यः who यमयति directs, controls श्रोत्रम् the ear अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Controller ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the ear and is within the ear, whom the deity of the ear does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the deity of the ear, and who directs the ear to its functions from within, is the Inner Controller, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.

** यो मनसि तिष्ठन्मनसोऽन्तरो यं मनो न वेद यस्य मनः शरीरं यो मनोऽन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥२०॥**



 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling मनसि in the mind, अन्तर (is) within मनसः the mind, यम् whom मनः mind, the deity of the mind न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) मनः the mind, यः who यमयति controls, directs मनः the mind अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner controller ते you एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the mind and is within the mind, whom the deity of the mind does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the deity of the mind, and who directs the mind to its function from within, is the Inner Controller, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.

** यस्त्वचि तिष्ठꣳस्त्वचोऽन्तरो यं त्वङ् न वेद यस्य त्वक्शरीरं यस्त्वचमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥२१॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling त्वचि in the skin अन्तरः (is) within त्वयः the skin, यम् whom त्वक् skin, deity of the skin न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) त्वक् the skin, यः who यमयति directs, controls त्वचम् the skin अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Controller ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the skin and is within the skin, whom the deity of the skin does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the deity of the skin, and who directs the skin to



its function from within is the Inner Controller, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.

** यो विज्ञाने तिष्ठन्विज्ञानादन्तरो यं विज्ञानं न वेद यस्य विज्ञानꣳ शरीरं यो विज्ञानमन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतः॥२२॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling विज्ञाने\* in the intellect अन्तरः (is) within विज्ञानात् the intellect, यम् whom विज्ञानम् intellect, deity of intellect न not वेद knows, यस्य whose शरीरम् body (is) विज्ञानम् the intellect, यः who यमयति controls, directs, विज्ञानम् intellect अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Controller ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self.

 He who dwells in the intellect and is within the intellect, whom the deity of intellect does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the deity of the intellect and who directs the intellect to its function from within, is the Inner Controller, Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings.

 ** यो रेतसि तिष्ठन्रेतसोऽन्तरो यꣳ रेतो न वेद यस्य रेतः शरीरं यो रेतोऽन्तरो यमयत्येष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतोऽदृष्टो**

——————————————————————————————

\*Max Muller translates this word by 'Knowledge.' The word means 'the individual Self' according to the Madhyandina Sākhā. See Deussen, p. 161.

——————————————————————————————



**द्रष्टाऽश्रुतः श्रोताऽमतो मन्ताऽविज्ञातो विज्ञाता नान्योऽतोऽस्ति द्रष्टा नान्योऽतोऽस्ति श्रोता नान्योऽतोऽस्ति मन्ता नान्योऽतोऽस्ति विज्ञातैष त आत्माऽन्तर्याम्यमृतोऽतोऽन्यदार्तं ततो होद्दालक आरुणिरुपरराम॥२३॥इति सप्तमं ब्राह्मणम्॥७॥**

 यः (He) who तिष्ठन् dwelling रेतसि in the semen, in the organ of generation अन्तरः (is) within रेतसः the semen, the organ of generation, यम् whom रेतः the semen, generative organ, the deity of the seed वेद knows न not, यस्य whose शरीरम् body रेतः (is) the semen, यः who यमयति directs, controller रेतः the semen, the seed अन्तरः from within अन्तर्यामी (is) the Inner Controls ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal आत्मा Self अदृष्टः (He is) unseen द्रष्टा (but is) the seer; अश्रुतः unheard, श्रोता (but) the hearer; अमतः unthought (but) मन्ता the thinker; अविज्ञातः not grasped, unknown (but is) विज्ञाता the knower. अस्ति There is न not अन्यः other द्रष्टा seer; अतः than this अस्ति there is न not अन्यः other श्रोता hearer; अतः than this अस्ति there is न not अन्यः other विज्ञाता knower; अतः than this अन्तर्यामी the Inner Controller ते your एषः this अमृतः immortal, imperishable आत्मा Self. अन्यत् Every thing else अतः than Him आर्तम् (is) perishable. ततः Thereupon उद्दालकः Uddalaka आरुणिः the sun of Aruna उपरराम ह remained silent, stopped.

 Now with regard to the body. He who dwells in the semen and is within semen, whom the deity of semen does not know, whose body and organs are the same as those of the deity of semen, who



directs semen from within is the Inner Controller, is Your own immortal Self, as also mine and that of all beings. He is never the object of any body's ocular perception, but being close to the eye as Intelligence, he is the Seer. He is never perceived by any body by ear, but being close to all ears with His never-failing power of hearing, is the Hearer. He never becomes the object of deliberation by the mind, but He is close to all minds and His thinking power never wanes. He is never definitely grasped like colour, etc. or pleasure and so forth. He Himself is the Knower and His intelligence never fails. Except Him there is no other seer. Except Him there is no other hearer. Except Him there is no other thinker. Except Him there is no other knower. He is the Inner Controller, Your own immortal Self. Except Him everything else is perishable. Thereupon, the son of Aruna, stopped.

**CHAPTER THREE : SECTION EIGHT**

 **अथ ह वाचक्नव्युवाच ब्राह्मणा भगवन्तो हन्ताहमिमं द्वौ प्रश्नौ प्रक्ष्यामि तौ चेन्मे वक्ष्यति न जातु युष्माकमिमं कश्चिद्ब्रह्मोद्यं जेतेति पृच्छ गार्गीति॥१॥**



 अथ ह Then वाचक्नवी Gargi, the daughter of Vachaknu उवाच said भगवन्तः venerable, revered ब्राह्मणाः Brahmans हन्त permit me. अहम् I प्रक्ष्यामि will ask, will interrogate (him) इदम् these द्वौ two प्रश्नौ questions. चेत् If वक्ष्यति (he) answers मे my तौ two (questions) वै verily न not जातु at all कश्चित् any युष्माकम् amongst you जेता will defeat, will beat इदम् this ब्रह्मोद्यम् इति describer of Brahman. (Brahmans said) पृच्छ Ask गार्गि इति O Gargi.

\[This section describes Brahman who is free from hunger and thirst, etc., unconditioned, immediate, direct and within all.\]

Then Gārgi¹, the daughter of Vachaknu, who, previously desisted for fear of losing her head, asked the permission of the venerable Brahmans to ask Yājñavalkya two more questions. She added: If he can answer these two questions of mine, then none amongst you can ever possibly defeat this describer of Brahman. The Brahmans permitted Gārgi to ask question.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Not the wife of Yājñavalkya.\]

——————————————————————————————

**सा होवाचाहं वै त्वा याज्ञवल्क्य यथा काश्यो वा वैदेहो वोग्रपुत्र उज्ज्यं धनुरधिज्यं कृत्वा द्वौ बाणवन्तौ सपत्नातिव्याधिनौ हस्ते कृत्वोपोत्तिष्ठेदेवमेवाहं त्वा द्वाभ्यां प्रश्नाभ्यामुपोदस्थां तौ मे ब्रूहीति पृच्छ गार्गीति॥२॥**



 सा She (Gargi) उवाच ह said याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya वै verily अहम् I (ask) त्वा you यथा as उग्रपुत्रः terrible son, warrior son काश्यः वा of the King of Benares वा or वैदेहः of the King of Videha कृत्वा having made अधिज्यम् strung उज्ज्यम् the unstrung धनुः bow उपात्तिष्ठेत् appears close by, presents in front of कृत्वा doing, taking, carrying हस्ते in hand द्वौ two बाणवन्तौ bamboo-tipped, pointed (arrows) सपत्नातिव्याधिनौ highly painful to the enemy, foe-piercing. एवम् एव Even so अहम् I उपोदस्थाम् confront, rise (to fight) त्वा you द्वाभ्याम् with two प्रश्नाभ्याम् questions. ब्रूहि tell, answer मे me तौ इति those two पृच्छ ask गार्गि इति O Gargi.

 Gārgi said to Yājnavalkya, "I ask you two questions. (Just to indicate the difficult nature of the question she said through this illustration.) As a warrior son of the King of Benares or of the King of Videha, strings his unstrung bow, takes two pointed foe-piercing arrows in hand and presents himself before the enemy, even so, Yājnavalkya, do I rise to ask you two questions (comparable to arrows). Answer these two questions of mine." Yājnavalkya said, "Ask, O Gārgi, those questions."

** सा होवाच यदूर्ध्वं याज्ञवल्क्य दिवो यदवाक्पृथिव्या यदन्तरा द्यावापृथिवी इमे यद्भूतं च भवच्च भविष्यच्चेत्याचक्षते कस्मिꣳस्तदोतं च प्रोतं चेति॥३॥**



 सा She (Gargi) उवाच ह said, asked इति this याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya यत् which (is) उर्ध्वम् above दिवः heaven, यत् which (is) अवाक् below पृथिव्याः the earth, यत् which (is) द्यावापृथिवी heaven and the earth अन्तरा (and) between इमे them च and यत् which भूतम् (was) in the past च and भवत् (is) at present च and भविष्यत् (will be) in future आचक्षते (scriptures) say कस्मिन् by what तत् that (sutra) ओतं च प्रोतं च इति (is) pervaded, woven.

 Gārgi asked Yajnavalkya, "As water pervades the elemental earth, so what pervades the Sutra which is above heaven and below the earth, which embraces heaven and earth as well as which is between them, and which according to the scriptures was in the past, does its function at present and will continue in future?"

** स होवाच यदूर्ध्वं गार्गि दिवो यदवाक्पृथिव्या यदन्तराद्यावापृथिवी इमे यद्भूतं च भवच्च भविष्यच्चेत्याचक्षत आकाशे तदोतं च प्रोतं चेति॥४॥**

 सः He (Yajnavalkya) उवाच ह said, replied इति this गार्गि O Gargi यत् which (is) उर्ध्वम् above दिवः heaven, यत् which (is) अवाक् below पृथिव्याः the earth यत् which (is) द्यावापृथिवी heaven and the earth अन्तरा (and) between इमे them च and यत् which भूतम् (was) in the past च and भवत् (is) at present च and भविष्यत् (will be) in future तत् that ओतं च प्रोतं च इति (is) pervaded, woven, आकाशे in the unmanifested ether आचक्षते (the scriptures) say.



 Yājnavalkya replied : O Gargi, it is the unmanifested ether ¹ that pervades the Sutra which is above heaven and below the earth, which embraces heaven and earth, as well as is between them, and which according to scriptures was in the past, does its function at present and will continue in future.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. As water pervades elemental earth, so the unmanifested ether pervades the manifested universe consisting of Sutra in its origin, continuance and dissolution.\]

——————————————————————————————

** सा होवाच नमस्तेऽस्तु याज्ञवल्क्य यो म एतं व्यवोचोऽपरस्मै धारयस्वेति पृच्छ गार्गीति॥५॥**

सा She (Gargi) उवाच ह said याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya नमः salutation, अस्तु be ते to you यः who व्यवोचः answered fully, solved completely मे my एतम् this (question). (Yajnavalkya said) गार्गि O Gargi पृच्छ इति ask.

 Gārgi said, "Salutation be to you, Yajnavalkya. You have fully solved my question. Now hold yourself steady for the other question. " Yājnavalkya said, " Ask, O Gārgi. "

** सा होवाच यदूर्ध्वं याज्ञवल्क्य दिवो यदवाक्पृथिव्या यदन्तरा द्यावापृथिवी इमे यद्भूतं च भवच्च भविष्यच्चेत्याचक्षते कस्मिंस्तदोतं च प्रोतं चेति॥६॥**



 सा She (Gargi) उवाच ह said इति thus याज्ञवल्क्य O Yajnavalkya यत् which (is) ऊर्ध्वम् above दिवः heaven, यत् which (is) अवाक् below पृथिव्याम् the earth, यत् that (is) द्यावापृथिवी heaven and the earth अन्तरा (and) between इमे them, यत् which (is) आचक्षते (scriptures) say भूतम् (was) in the past च and भवत् (is) at present च and भविष्यत् (will be) in future, कस्मिन् in what तत् that (Sūtra) ओतं च प्रोतं च (is) pervaded, woven.

 Gārgi asked Yājnavalkya ः What pervades the Sūtra which is above heaven and below the earth, which embraces heaven and earth as well as which is between them and which according to scriptures was in the past, does its function and will continue in future? \*

 **स होवाच यदूर्ध्वं गार्गि दिवो यदवाक्पृथिव्या यदन्तरा द्यावापृथिवी इमे यद्भूतं च भवच्च भविष्यच्चेत्याचक्षत आकाश एव तदोतं च प्रोतं चेति कस्मिन्नु खल्वाकाश ओतश्च प्रोतश्चेति॥७॥**

 सः He (Yajnavalkya) उवाच ह said, replied यत् which (is) गार्गि O Gargi ऊर्ध्वम् above दिवः the heaven, यत् which (is) अवाक् below पृथिव्याः the earth, यत् which (is) द्यावापृथिवी this heaven and earth, अन्तरा (and) between इमे them, यत् which (is) इति आचक्षते (scriptures) say भूतं च (was) in the past

——————————————————————————————

\*This repetition which does not occur in the Madhyandina Text is made to emphasise the truth already stated by Yājñavalkya.

——————————————————————————————



च and भवत् (is) at present च and भविष्यत् (will be) in future तत् that (Sutra) ओतं च प्रोतं च (is) pervaded, woven आकाशे इति by unmanifested ether एव only. (Gargi asked) कस्मिन् नु खलु In what आकाशः the unmanifested ether ओतः च प्रोतः च इति (is) pervaded, woven.

 Yājnavalkya replied : "O Gārgi, it is unmanifested ether which pervades that which is above heaven and below the earth, which embraces heaven and earth and is between them, and which according to scriptures was in the past, does its function at present and will continue in the future." Gargi asked : "What pervades the unmanifested ether?"

** स होवाचैतद्वै तदक्षरं गार्गि ब्राह्मणा अभिवदन्त्यस्थूलमनण्वह्रस्वमदीर्घमलोहितमस्नेहमच्छायमतमोऽवाय्वनाकाशमसङ्गमरसमगन्धमचक्षुष्कमश्रोत्रमवामनोऽतेजस्कमप्राणममुखममात्रमनन्तरमबाह्यं न तदश्नाति किञ्चनं न तदश्नाति कश्चन॥८॥**

 सः He (Yajnavalkya) उवाच ह said गार्गि O Gargi ब्राह्मणाः the knowers of Brahman अभिवदन्ति describe, say एतत् this (is) वै verily तत् that (Brahman) अक्षरम् (is) Immutable (undecaying and unchanging), अस्थूलम् not coarse, not gross, अनणु (न + अणु) not minute, not fine, अह्रस्वम् not short, अदीर्घम् not long, अलोहितम् not red, अस्नेहम् not moist, अच्छायम् not shadowy, अतमः not dark, अवायु not air, अनाकाशम् not ether, असङ्गम् unattached, not sticky, अरसम् not savoury,



अगन्धम् not odourous, अचक्षुष्कम् without eyes (instrument of vision), अश्रोत्रम् without ears (organ of hearing) अवाक् without speech (vocal organ), अमनः without mind, अतेजस्कम् not-luminous, non-lustrous, अप्राणम् without the vital power, अमुखम् without mouth (opening) अमात्रम् not a measure, अनन्तरम् without interior, having no within अबाह्यम् without exterior, having no without. तत् That अश्नाति devours, eats, न not किञ्चन anything कः चन one, अश्नाति devours, eats तत् it न not.

 Yājnavalkya said: "O Gārgi, the knowers of Brahman describe It as undecaying and unchanging. They say Brahman is neither coarse nor fine, neither short nor long¹, neither red like fire nor moist like water, neither shadowy nor dark, neither air nor ether. It is not sticky like lac or gum, neither savoury nor odourous. It has neither instrument of vision nor organ of hearing². It is neither speech nor mind. It has neither lustre like that of fire nor vital power, nor any opening. It does not measure anything. It has no within or without like a porous object. It is neither the eater of anything nor the food of anybody. \[In short, It is devoid of all attributes and is only one without a second.\]

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. All the characteristics of substance are denied to Brahman by this four kinds of negation of size. So It is not a substance.

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

2.As the Shvetaswatara Upanishad (3. 19) says, " Brahman sees without eyes and hears without ears. "

——————————————————————————————

** एतस्य वा अक्षरस्य प्रशासने गार्गि सूर्याचन्द्रमसौ विधृतौ तिष्ठत एतस्य वा अक्षरस्य प्रशासने गार्गि द्यावापृथिव्यौ विधृते तिष्ठत एतस्य वा अक्षरस्य प्रशासने गार्गि निमेषा मुहूर्ता अहोरात्राण्यर्धमासा मासा ऋतवः संवत्सरा इति विधृतास्तिष्ठन्त्येतस्य वा अक्षरस्य प्रशासने गार्गि प्राच्योऽन्या नद्यः स्यन्दन्ते श्वेतेभ्यः पर्वतेभ्यः प्रतीच्योऽन्या यां यां च दिशमन्वेतस्य वा अक्षरस्य प्रशासने गार्गि ददतो मनुष्याः प्रशꣳसन्ति यजमानं देवा दवीं पितरोऽन्वायत्ताः॥९॥**

 वै Verily प्रशासने by the mighty rule, by the supreme command एतस्य of this अक्षरस्य Immutable, Imperishable. गार्गि O Gargi सूर्याचन्द्रमसौ the sun and moon तिष्ठतः stand विधृतौ held in (their) course. वै Verily प्रशासने by the command एतस्य of this अक्षरस्य Imperishable गार्गि O Gargi द्यावापृथिवी heaven and earth तिष्ठतः stand विधृतौ held in (their) path. वै Verily प्रशासने by the command एतस्य of this अक्षरस्य Imperishable गार्गि O Gargi निमेषाः moments, मुहूर्ताः Muhurtas, अहोरात्राणि days and nights, अर्धमासाः fort-nights, मासाः months, ऋतवः seasons, संवत्सराः full years तिष्ठन्ति stand इति विधृताः held in (their) places. वै Verily गार्गि O Gargi प्रशासने by the command एतस्य of this अक्षरस्य Imperishable अन्याः other, some नद्यः rivers स्यन्दन्ते flow, प्राच्यः eastward श्वेतेभ्यः from the white पर्वतेभ्यः mountains; अन्याः others प्रतीच्यः



(flow) westward अनु towards यां याम् several दिशम् directions. वै Verily गार्गि Gargi प्रशासने by the command एतस्य of this अक्षरस्य Imperishable मनुष्याः (learned) men प्रशंसन्ति praise ददतः the givers, distributors देवाः Gods (depend on) यजमानम् sacrificer पितरः the Manes अन्वायत्ताः depend on दर्वों ‘Darvi’ homa.

 \[The Upanishad indicates the existence of Brahman by the negation of Its attributes. But It anticipates also the popular mis-conception about Brahman and advances the following inferential proof of Its existence. As from a lamp its maker is inferred, so Brahman is very well inferred from sun and moon.\]

 By the supreme command of this Imperishable Being, O Gārgi, the sun and moon keep to their own course¹. By the supreme command of this Imperishable Being, O Gārgi, heaven² and earth hold their own positions. By the supreme command of this Imperishable Being, moments, muhurtas³, days and nights, fortnights, months, seasons and whole years⁴ are maintained in their respective places. By the supreme command of this Imperishable Being, O Gārgi, some rivers (such as the Ganges) flow eastward from the white mountains (for instance, the Himalayas), and others (such as the Indus) flowing westward do not deviate from original courses. There are still



other rivers which flow to several other directions as before. By the supreme command of this Imperishable Being, O Gārgi, men praise the givers of gold, etc., the gods depend on their sacrificer, (for such means of livelihood as porridge and cakes,) and the manes depend for their subsistence on independent offerings (Darvi Homa).

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. As a kingdom remains unbroken and orderly under the mighty rule of a king, so the sun, moon, etc., are held in their own positions. They being made of parts are naturally subject to disruption, inclined to fall due to weights, liable to separate being, compound, and are independent, each having a conscious deity presiding over and identifying with it. Brahman holds them intact, preserves their distinctions and holds them within their respective limits. None can transgress Its supreme command.

2\. As the Rig Veda (10. 121. 5) says: He has made heaven powerful and the earth firm.

3\. A muhurta is equal to about 48 minutes.

4\. As an accountant appointed by his master carefully calculates all items of income and expenditure, so are these divisions of time which count all things, past, present and future controlled by the Imperishable Being.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** यो वा एतदक्षरं गार्ग्यविदित्वाऽस्मिल्ँ लोके जुहोति यजते तपस्तप्यते बहूनि वर्षसहस्राण्यन्तवदेवास्य तद्भवति यो वा एतदक्षरं गार्ग्यविदित्वाऽस्माल्लोकात्प्रैति स कृपणोऽथ य एतदक्षरं गार्गि विदित्वाऽस्माल्लोकात्प्रैति स ब्राह्मणः॥१०॥**



 गार्गि O Gargi यः whosoever अस्मिन् in this लोके world अविदित्वा not knowing एतत् this अक्षरम् Immutable वै indeed जुहोति offers oblations, यजते performs, sacrifices, तप्यते practises, undergoes तपः penance, austerity बहूनि many वर्ष-सहस्राणि thousands of years तत् all that एव indeed अस्य of him भवति is, becomes अन्तवत् perishable. सः He यः who वै verily गार्गि Gargi एतत् this अक्षरम् Immutable अविदित्वा without knowing प्रैति leaves, departs अस्मात् from this लोकात् world कृपणः (is) miserable. अथ But सः he यः who गार्गि O Gargi विदित्वा knowing एतत् this अक्षरम् Immutable प्रैति departs अस्मात् from this लोकात् world ब्राह्मणः (is) a knower of Brahman.

 O, Gārgi, whosoever, performs sacrifices and practises penances for many thousands of years in this world, all such work of his perish¹. He, O Gārgi, who leaves this world without the knowledge of this Immutable Being is miserable² like a slave. But he, O Gārgi, who leaves this world with the knowledge of this Immutable One, is a Brāhmana —a knower of Brahman.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Because, after the enjoyment of their results, those works are inevitably exhausted.

2\. Because till Brahman is realised, one is bound to suffer transmigration and move in an endless series of births and deaths. Knowledge of Brahman alone stops transmigration and ends all misery. Till then he is helplessly swayed by his karmas as a slave by his master.\]

——————————————————————————————



** तद्वा एतदक्षरं गार्ग्यदृष्टं द्रष्ट्रश्रुतꣳश्रोत्रमतं मन्त्रविज्ञातं विज्ञातृ नान्यदतोऽस्ति द्रष्टृं नान्यदतोऽस्ति श्रोतृ नान्यदतोऽस्ति मन्तृ नान्यदतोऽस्ति विज्ञात्रेतस्मिन्नु खल्वक्षरे गार्ग्याकाश ओतश्च प्रोतश्चेति॥११॥**

 वै Verily गार्गि O Gargi तत् that एतत् this अक्षरम् Immutable अदृष्टम् (is) unseen द्रष्टृ (but) the seer, अश्रुतम् (is) unheard श्रोतृ (but) the Hearer, अमतम् (is) unthought मन्तृ (but) the thinker, अविज्ञातम् (is) unknown विज्ञातृ (but) the knower. अस्ति There is न not अन्यत् other द्रष्टृ seer, अतः than this अस्ति there is न not अन्यत् other श्रोतृ hearer, अतः than this (Immutable) अस्ति there is न not अन्यत् other मन्तृ thinker, अतः than this अस्ति there is न not अन्यत् other विज्ञातृ knower, अतः than this. एतस्मिन् In this नु खलु अक्षरे Immutable गार्गि O Gargi आकाशः Sky, the unmanifested ether, ओतः प्रोतः च इति (is) pervaded, woven.

 \[This passage replies to the contention that the mighty rulership of the Immutable one is natural to the insentient Pradhan of the Sankhyas, and not to Brahman.\]

 This Immutable one, not being an object of sight, O Gārgi, is never seen by anybody, but is Itself the seer, being sight Itself. Likewise, not being an object of hearing, It is never heard by anybody, but is Itself the Hearer being hearing Itself. So also, not being an object of the mind, It is never



thought by anybody, but is Itself the Thinker being thought Itself. Similarly, not being an object of intellect It is never known by anybody, but is Itself the Knower, being Intelligence Itself. This Immutable Itself is everywhere the seer as It sees through all eyes. It is Itself everywhere the Hearer as It hears through all ears. It Itself is everywhere the Thinker as It thinks through all minds. It Itself is everywhere the Knower as It knows through all intellects, neither the insentient Pradhana nor anything else. This Immutable one, O Gārgi, pervades all elements from earth to the (unmanifested) ether.

 **सा होवाच ब्राह्मणा भगवन्तस्तदेव बहु मन्येध्वं यदस्मान्नमस्कारेण मुच्येध्वं न वै जातु युष्माकमिमं कश्चिद्ब्रह्मोद्यं जेतेति ततो ह वाचक्नव्युपरराम॥१२॥इत्यष्टमं ब्राह्मणम्॥८॥**

 सा She (Gargi) उवाच ह said भगवन्तः Venerable ब्राह्मणाः Brahmans, मन्येध्वम् (you) should consider, should think तम् that एव only बहु highly, greatly fortunate यत् if मुच्येध्वम् (you) can get off अस्मात् from him (Yajnavalkya) नमस्कारेण by a salutation. वै Verily न जातु never कश्चित् any युष्माकम् amongst you नेता shall defeat इमम् this ब्रह्मोद्यम् इति describer of Brahman. ततः ह Then वाचक्नवी the daughter of Vachaknu उपरराम stopped.



 Then Gārgi said : "Venerable Brahmanas, you should think it a great thing if you can get off from Yajnavalkya by saluting him. I am convinced that none of you can defeat Yājnavalkya in the description of Brahman." Then the daughter of Vachaknu stopped.

 \[The Supreme Brahman which has no prior or posterior, interior or exterior, and is homogeneous like a lump of salt is called the transmigrating individual Self when It wears the limiting adjuncts of the body and organs characterised by ignorance, desire and work. When the Supreme Self has the limiting adjunct of the power of Maya manifesting through eternal and unlimited knowledge, It is called the Internal Ruler or Ishwara. Similarly, when the Supreme Self puts the particular bodies and organs of Hiranyagarbha, gods, men, animals, spirits, etc. It assumes respective names and forms.\]

**CHAPTER THREE : SECTION NINE**

 **अथ हैनं विदग्धः शाकल्यः पप्रच्छ कति देवा याज्ञवल्क्येति स हैतयैव निविदा प्रतिपेदे यावन्तो वैश्वदेवस्य निविद्युच्यन्ते त्रयश्च त्री च शता त्रयश्च त्री च सहस्रेत्योमिति होवाच कत्येव देवा याज्ञवल्क्येति त्रयस्त्रिꣳशदित्योमिति होवाच कत्येव**



**देवा याज्ञवल्क्येति षडित्योमिति होवाच कत्येव देवा याज्ञवल्क्येति त्रय इत्योमिति होवाच कत्येव देवा याज्ञवल्क्येति द्वावित्योमिति होवाच कत्येव देवा याज्ञवल्क्येत्यध्यर्ध इत्योमिति होवाच कत्येव देवा याज्ञवल्क्येत्येक इत्योमिति होवाच कतमे ते त्रयश्च त्री च शता त्रयश्च त्री च सहस्रेति॥१॥**

 अथ ह Then विदग्धः Vidagdha शाकल्यः the son of Shakala पप्रच्छ asked एनम् him इति thus : याज्ञवल्क्य Yajñavalkya कति howmany देवाः gods (are there) सः He ह प्रतिपेदे decided, replied एतया with this निविदा एव Nivid (group of invocations to the gods) यावन्तः as many as उच्यन्ते are said, are mentioned निविदि in the Nivid वैश्वदेवस्य of the Vishwadevas त्रयः three च and त्री three शता hundred त्रयः three च and त्री three सहस्त्रा इति thousand. ओम् इति Very well, yes उवाच ह इति (he) said, याज्ञवल्क्य Yajñavalkya कति how many देवाः gods एव इति indeed ? त्रयः three त्रिंशत् इति thirty. ओम् इति Very well, yes उवाच ह said (the other). कति Howmany एव indeed याज्ञवल्क्य Yajñavalkya देवाः इति gods ? षट् इति six ओम् इति yes, very well उवाच ह said (the other). कति How many देवाः gods एव indeed याज्ञवल्क्य Yajñavalkya ? त्रयः इति Three ओम् इति yes, very well उवाच ह said (the other). कति How many एव indeed देवाः gods याज्ञवल्क्य इति Yajñavalkya. द्वौ इति Two ओम् इति yes, very well उवाच ह said (the other) याज्ञवल्क्य Yajñavalkya कति how many देवाः gods इति एव indeed ? अध्यर्द्धः इति one and a half, कति howmany देवाः gods एव indeed ? याज्ञवल्क्य इति Yajñavalkya, एकः इति one ओम् इति yes, very well उवाच ह said (the other) कतमे



which (are) ते those त्रयः three च and त्री three शता इति hundred? त्रयः Three च and त्री three सहस्र इति thousand.

 \[This dialogue between Yājnavalkya and Shakalya occurs in a simpler form in the eleventh Book of Shatapath Brāhmana (6. 3. 11) entitled Ashtadhyayi which treats of rituals and is so named as it consists of eight chapters. There it is said that Yājnavalkya cursed Shakalya as follows : 'You shall die in a unholy place, in an inauspicious time and even your bones shall not reach home.' The curse was fulfilled and Shakalya died accordingly. When his disciples were carrying home his dead body for the funeral ceremony, the robbers mistook it to be a treasure under transport and snatched it away. The story extols the Knowledge of Brahman and teaches us to respect a true Knower of Brahman.\]

 Then Vidagdha, the son of Shakal asked questions to Yājnavalkya. He said— 'How many gods are really there, Yājnavalkya ?' Yājnavalkya replied with this very Nivid¹, 'As many as are mentioned in the Nivid, of the hymn of praise addressed to the Vishwadevas, viz. three and three hundred, and three and three thousand.' 'Yes' said Shākalya and asked, 'How many gods are really there, Yājnavalkya ?' Yājnavalkya replied—'There are thirty-three gods.' 'Yes' said Shakalya and



asked—' How many gods are really there, Yājnavalkya ?' Yājnavalkya replied—There are six gods.' Yes' said Shakalya and asked,' How many gods are really there, Yājnavalkya ?' Yājnavalkya replied—There are only three gods.' Yes' said Shakalya and asked,' How many gods are really there, Yājnavalkya ?' Yājnavalkya replied—There are only two gods.' Yes' said Shakalya and asked,' How many gods are really there, Yājnavalkya ?' Yājnavalkya replied—There are only one and a half.' Yes' said Shakalya and asked,' How many gods are really there, Yājnavalkya ?' Yājnavalkya replied—There is only one god. 'Yes' said Shakalya and then asked about their identity :' Which are those² three hundred and three, and three thousand and three ?'

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Nivid is a group of verses that decide the number of the gods. These verses are recited in the eulogistic hymn on the Vishwadevas.

2\. This would make 3306 gods in all.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **स होवाच महिमान एवैषामेते त्रयस्त्रिꣳशत्त्वेव देवा इति कतमे ते त्रयस्त्रिꣳशदित्यष्टौ वसव एकादश रुद्रा द्वादशाऽऽदित्यास्त एकत्रिꣳशदिन्द्रश्चैव प्रजापतिश्च त्रयस्त्रिꣳशाविति॥२॥**

** ** सः He (Yajnavalkya) ह उवाच said, replied इति thus : एते they एव indeed महिमानः (are) glories, the manifestations



एषाम् of them (thirty-three gods) तु only देवाः gods (are) एव only त्रयः three त्रिंशत् thirty इति (Shakalya asked) thus कतमे which (are) ते those त्रयस्त्रिंशत् thirty three ? (The reply) अष्टौ eight वसवः Vasus, एकादश eleven रुद्राः Rudras, द्वादश twelve आदित्याः Adityas. ते They (are) एकत्रिंशत् thirty one. च And इन्द्रः Indra च and प्रजापतिः Prajapati त्रयस्त्रिंशौ इति (make up) thirty three.

 Yājnavalkya replied : They¹ are only the glories of thirty-three gods. Hence really the gods are only thirty-three. Shakalya asked : ' Which are those thirty-three gods ? ' Yājnavalkya replied : Eight Vasus, eleven Rudras and twelve Adityas make thirty-one, and Indra and Prajapati make up the thirty-three.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Three hundred and three, and three thousand and three gods.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **कतमे वसव इत्यग्निश्च पृथिवी च वायुश्चान्तरिक्षं चाऽऽदित्यश्च द्यौश्च चन्द्रमाश्च नक्षत्राणि चैते वसव एतेषु हीदꣳसर्वꣳहितमिति तस्माद्वसव इति॥३॥**

 इति (Shakalya asked) thus कतमे which (are) वसवः (eight) Vasus ? (Yajnavalkya replied) अग्निः च fire, पृथिवी च and earth, वायुः च and air, अन्तरिक्षं च and sky, आदित्यः च and sun, द्यौः च and heaven, चन्द्रमाः च the moon, नक्षत्राणि च and the stars. एते These (are) वसवः the Vasus. हि For,



because एतेषु in these सर्वम् all इदम् this, these हितम् इति rests. तस्मात् Therefore वसवः इति (they are) known as Vasus.

 Shakalya asked: ‘ Which are eight Vasus? ’ Yājñavalkya replied: Fire, the earth, the air, the sky, the sun, heaven, the moon and the stars are the eight Vasus. Because all this consisting of work and its fruition rests in them, they are known as Vasus¹.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The Vasus are gods who take the form of the bodies and organs as also the abodes of all beings which are the support for the work and its result of Vasus. Thus the Vasus live and enable all beings to live. The etymological explanation of Vasu occurs in two places of the Shatapatha Brahmana.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **कतमे रुद्रा इति दशेमे पुरुषे प्राणा आत्मैकादशस्ते यदास्माच्छरीरान्मर्त्यादुत्क्रामन्त्यथ रोदयन्ति तद्यद्रोदयन्ति तस्माद्रुद्रा इति॥४॥**

 इति (Shakalya asked) thus कतमे which (are) रुद्राः the (ten) Rudras. (Yajnavalkya replied) इमे these दश the ten (five sensory and five motor) organs पुरुषे of a man, in the human body; आत्मा Self, mind एकादशः the eleventh, यत् when ते they (these organs) उत्क्रामन्ति go out, leave अस्मात् from this मर्त्यात् mortal शरीरात् body अथ then रोदयन्ति make cry. यत् Because तत् then रोदयन्ति (they) make weep, तस्मात् therefore रुद्राः इति (they are called) Rudras.



 Shakalya asked : 'Which are the eleven Rudras?' Yājnavalkya replied : Five sensory and five motor organs of man and mind as the eleventh are the eleven Rudras. When these organs leave this mortal body after one has fully worked out the results of his past work, they make his relatives cry. Because they make them cry, they are called Rudras.

** कतम आदित्या इति द्वादश वै मासाः संवत्सरस्यैत आदित्या एते हीदꣳसर्वमाददाना यन्ति ते यदिदꣳसर्वमाददाना यन्ति तस्मादादित्या इति॥५॥**

 इति (Shakalya said) thus कतमे which (are) आदित्याः twelve Adityas ? (Yajnavalkya replied) वै verily द्वादश the twelve मासाः months संवत्सरस्य of the whole year. एते They (are) आदित्याः Adityas. हि Because एते they यन्ति go आददाना taking सर्वम् all इदम् this (longevity and results of one’s work). यत् Because ते they यन्ति move along आददाना taking सर्वम् all इदम् this तस्मात् therefore आदित्याः इति (they are called) Adityas.

 Shakalya asked : 'Which are the twelve Adityas?' Yājnavalkya replied that the twelve months that form parts of a year are the twelve Adityas. Because, as they move they take along with them one’s longevity and the results of his work. As they rotate taking all this with them, they are called Adityas.



** कतम इन्द्रः कतमः प्रजापतिरिति स्तनयित्नुरेवेन्द्रो यज्ञः प्रजापतिरिति कतमः स्तनयित्नुरित्यशनिरिति कतमो यज्ञ इति पशव इति॥६॥**

 इति (He) asked) thus कतमः which (is) इन्द्रः Indra. कतमः which (is) प्रजापतिः Prajapati. इति (Yajnavalkya replied) thus स्तनयित्नुः the cloud (is) एव indeed इन्द्रः Indra ; यज्ञः the sacrifice (is) प्रजापतिः Prajapati. इति (He asked) thus कतमः which (is) स्तनयित्नुः cloud ? इति (the other replied) thus अशनिः the thunder. इति (He asked) thus कतमः which (is) यज्ञः the sacrifice ? इति (the other replied) thus पशवः the animals.

 He asked: 'Which is Indra, and which is Prajapati?' The other replied: 'Cloud is Indra, and the sacrifice is Prajapati.' The one asked— 'Which is the cloud?' The other replied that it was thunder.¹ The one asked— 'Which is the sacrifice?' The other replied that the animals² are the sacrifice.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Thunder means here vigour of strength that kills others. As thunder is the function of Indra, the latter is signified by the former.

2\. A sacrifice having no form of its own depends on its means, the animals. Therefore the animals are called sacrifice.\]

——————————————————————————————

** कतमे षडित्यग्निश्च पृथिवी च वायुश्चान्तरिक्षं चाऽऽदित्यश्च द्यौश्चैते षडेते हीदꣳ सर्वꣳ षडिति॥७॥**



 इति (He asked) thus कतमे which (are) षट् the six (gods) ? (The other replied) अग्निः च Fire, पृथिवी च and the earth, वायुः च and the air, अन्तरिक्षं च and the sky, आदित्यः च and the sun, द्यौः च and heaven. एते They (are) षट् the six (gods) हि Because सर्वम् all इदम् this (are) एते these (thirty three and other gods) षट् इति six (gods).

 He asked: 'Which are the six gods? ' The other replied : 'Fire, the earth, the air, the sky, the sun and heaven are the six gods. Because the thirty-three and other gods are included in these six.'

 ** कतमे ते त्रयो देवा इतीम एव त्रयो लोका एषु हीमे सर्वे देवा इति कतमौ तौ द्वौ देवावित्यन्नं चैव प्राणश्चेति कतमोऽध्यर्ध इति योऽयं पवत इति॥८॥**

 इति (He asked) thus कतमे which (are) ते those त्रयः three देवाः gods ? (The other replied) इमे these एव indeed त्रयः three लोकाः worlds (earth, sky and heaven) हि because एषु in these सर्वे all देवाः इति gods. इति (The other asked) thus कतमौ which (are) तौ those द्वौ two देवौ gods ? इति (The other replied) thus अन्नं च food, matter एव indeed च and प्राणः the (cosmic) vital power. इति (The one asked) thus कतमः which (are) अध्यर्द्धः the one and a half. इति (The other replied) thus अयम् this (air) यः that पवते blows.

 He asked : 'Which are the three gods? ' The other replied: The earth and fire together make



one god, the sky and air another, and heaven and the sun make the third. These are the three gods. All are included in these three gods. The one asked: 'Which are the two gods?' The other replied that matter and the cosmic vital power (Hiranyagarbha) are the two gods that include all the gods set forth. The one asked—'Which are the one and a half?' The other replied the air (the gross form of the cosmic vital power) that blows.

** तदाहुर्यदेक इवैव पवतेऽथ कथमध्यर्ध इति यदस्मिन्निदꣳ सर्वमध्यार्ध्नोत्तेनाध्यर्ध इति कतम एको देव इति प्राण इति स ब्रह्म त्यदित्याचक्षते॥९॥**

 तत् (Regarding) this (view) आहुः (some) say (raise objection) इति thus; यत् since अयम् this (air) एव indeed पवते blows इव as एकः one अथ then कथम् how अध्यर्द्धः one and a half यत् because अस्मिन् in it (in its presence) सर्वम् all इदम् this अधि + आध्नौत् grow, obtains, increase, attains glory तेन so अध्यर्द्धः इति one and a half इति (He asked) thus कतमः which (is) एकः the one देवः God. इति (The other replied) thus प्राणः the (cosmic) vital power. सः It (is) ब्रह्म Brahman आचक्षते (It) is called त्यत् that.

 As regards this view some raise this objection: 'How is it that the air that blows as one can be one and a half?' The reply is that because all this grows in and through it, it is one and a half. The



one asked: 'Which is the one god?' The other replied that the one god is the cosmic vital power (Hiranyagarbha). It is Brahman ; because it is vast and the sum total of all the gods¹. It being infinite is denoted by the pronoun 'that.'

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The cosmic vital power is the one god as well as the infinite gods. Though one it expands into all those gods whose numbers are upto infinite. On account of different qualifications of individual gods it assumes infinite names, forms, activities, attributes and powers.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **पृथिव्येव यस्याऽऽयतनमग्निर्लोको मनोज्योतिर्यो वै तं पुरुषं विद्यात्सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणꣳ स वै वेदिता स्यात्। याज्ञवल्क्य वेद वा अहं पुरुषꣳ सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणं यमात्थ य एवायꣳ शारीरः पुरुषः स एष वदैव शाकल्य तस्य का देवतेत्यमृतमिति होवाच॥१०॥**

 वै Verily सः he यः who विद्यात् knows तम् that पुरुषम् being, god यस्य whose आयतनम् abode एव indeed पृथिवी (is) the earth, लोकः (whose) instrument of vision अग्निः (is) fire, ज्योतिः (whose) light (is) मनः the mind परायणम् the ultimate resort सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organ). वै Verily वेदिता a knower, a teacher स्यात् is याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. वै Verily अहम् I वेद know तम् that पुरुषम् God, being यम् whom आत्थ (you) call परायणम् the ultimate resort सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs). सः It (is) एषः this यः who (is) एव indeed अयम् this शारीरः earth, corporeal पुरुषः being. एव Indeed



वद speak, ask about (it) शाकल्य Shakalya. का who (is) तस्य his देवता इति deity, cause अमृतम् इति nectar (chyle, the watery essence of eaten food that produces blood) उवाच ह said (he).

 Shakalya said : 'Verily he who is the knower of that god, who has the earth for his body, who sees through fire and weighs over things through the mind, and who is the final support of all bodies and organs is a real knower (teacher), O Yājnavalkya.' Yājnavalkya replied : 'Verily I am a knower of that god whom you call the final support of all bodies and organs. This god is identified with the corporeal form that preponderates in earthly elements. Ask about it, Shākalya.' Thus challenged he became furious (like a goaded elephant) and asked, 'Who is the cause of that god (the corporeal form) ?' Yājnavalkya replied that the cause of that corporeal form is chyle which produces blood.

 **काम एव यस्याऽऽयतनꣳ हृदयं लोको मनोज्योतिर्यो वै तं पुरुषं विद्यात्सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणꣳ स वै वेदिता स्यात्। याज्ञवल्क्य वेद वा अहं तं पुरुषꣳ सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणं यमात्थ य एवायं काममयः पुरुषः स एष वदैव शाकल्य तस्य का देवतेति स्त्रिय इति होवाच॥११॥**

 वै Verily सः He यः who विद्यात् knows तम् that पुरुषम् person, being, deity कामः lust, desire for sex-pleasures एव



indeed यस्य whose आयतनम् abode, body लोकः world, eye, instrument of vision हृदयम् intellect मनः mind ज्योतिः the light परायणम् final refuge, ultimate resort सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs). वै Verily वेदिता knower, teacher स्यात् is याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. वै Indeed अहम् I वेद know तम् that पुरुषम् person, being, deity, यम् whom आहुः (you) call परायणम् the final support सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs). सः He (is) एषः this यः who (is) पुरुषः being full of lust, identified with lust वद speak on एव indeed शाकल्य Shakalya का who (is) तस्य his देवता deity उवाच ह (Shākalya) said इति thus स्त्रियः women.

 Shākalya said—'Verily he who is the knower of that deity who has lust as his body, who sees through the intellect and weighs over things through the mind, and who is the final support of all body and organs is verily, O Yajnavalkya, a true knower (teacher)’. Yajnavalkya replied—I am indeed a knower of the deity whom you call the final support of all bodies and the organs. It is the deity who is united with lust and the same in the body as well. Speak on, Shakalya and tell me who is his deity. Shakalya replied that women are his deity; for they excite the desire of lust.

** रूपाण्येव यस्याऽऽयतनं चक्षुर्लोको मनोज्योतिर्यो वै तं पुरुषं विद्यात्सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणꣳ स वै वेदिता स्यात्। याज्ञ-**



**वल्क्य वेद वा अहं तं पुरुषꣳ सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणं यमात्थ य एवासावादित्ये पुरुषः स एष वदैव शाकल्य तस्य का देवतेति सत्यमिति होवाच॥१२॥**

 वै Verily सः He यः who विद्यात् knows तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यस्य whose आयतनम् body, abode (is) रूपाणि colours (in general) एव indeed लोकः world, instrument of vision (is) चक्षुः the eye ज्योति light (is) मनः the mind परायणम् the final support सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs) वै verily स्यात् is वेदिता the knower याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. वै Verily अहम् I वेद know तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यम् whom आत्थ (you) call सर्वस्य final support सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs). सः That एषः this यः who एव indeed (is) असौ this पुरुषः being, deity आदित्ये in the sun वद speak on एव indeed शाकल्य Shakalya का who (is) तस्य his देवता इति deity. सत्यम् इति Truth (eye) उवाच ह said (Shakalya).

 Shākalya said he who is the knower of that deity who has colours in general (such as black, white, etc.) as his body, who sees through the eye and weighs over things through the mind and who is the final support of all bodies and organs, is verily a true knower (teacher), O Yājnavalkya. Yājnavalkya replied—' I am indeed a knower of that deity whom you call the final resort of all bodies and organs. It is this deity who is identified with the sun. Speak on, Shākalya, Who is his deity? ' Shākalya replied that eye¹ is his deity.



——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The sun-god is the product of the eye in one's body. So says the Rig Veda (10. 90. 13).\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** आकाश एव यस्याऽऽयतनꣳ श्रोत्रं लोको मनोज्योतिर्यो वै तं पुरुषं विद्यात्सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणꣳ स वै वेदिता स्यात्। याज्ञवल्क्य वेद वा अहं तं पुरुषꣳ सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणं यमात्थ य एवायꣳ श्रौत्रः प्रातिश्रुत्कः पुरुषः स एष वदैव शाकल्य तस्य का देवतेति दिश इति होवाच॥१३॥**

 वै Verily सः he यः who विद्यात् knows तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यस्य whose आयतनम् body, abode (is) आकाशः the ether एव indeed लोकः world, instrument of vision श्रोत्रम् the ear ज्योतिः light (is) मनः the mind परायणम् final support, the ultimate resort सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs) वै verily स्यात् is वेदिता the knower, teacher याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. वै Verily अहम् I वेद know तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यम् whom आत्थ (you) call परायणम् the ultimate resort सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs). सः That (is) एषः this यः who एव indeed (is) अयम् this पुरुषः being, deity श्रौत्रः identified with the ear प्रातिश्रुत्कः\* identified with the time of hearing वद speak on एव indeed शाकल्य Shakalya का who (is) तस्य his देवता इति God दिशः इति the quarters, directions उवाच ह said (Shākalya).

 Shākalya said—Verily he who is the knower of that deity who has ether as his body, who sees

——————————————————————————————

\* Max Muller translates this word as that which answers.

——————————————————————————————



through the ear and weighs over things through the mind and who is the final support of all bodies and organs is the true knower (teacher), O Yājnavalkya. Yājnavalkya replied—Verily I am the knower of that deity whom you call the ultimate resort of all bodies and organs. It is the deity who is identified with the ear and particularly with the time of hearing. Speak on, Shākalya, who is his deity? Shākalya replied that directions¹ are his deity.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. That from which he is produced is his deity. Directions from which this particular deity within the body is produced are his deity.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** तम एव यस्याऽऽयतनꣳ हृदयं लोको मनोज्योतिर्यो वै तं पुरुषं विद्यात्सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणꣳ स वै वेदिता स्यात्। याज्ञवल्क्य वेद वा अहं तं पुरुषꣳ सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणं यमात्थ य एवायं छायामयः पुरुषः स एष वदैव शाकल्य तस्य का देवतेति मृत्युरिति होवाच॥१४॥**

 वै Verily सः he यः who विद्यात् knows तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यस्य whose आयतनम् body, abode (is) तमः darkness एव indeed लोकः world, instrument of vision (is) हृदयम् heart, intellect ज्योतिः light (is) मनः the mind परायणम् the ultimate resort सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs) स्यात् is वै verily वेदिता the knower याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. वै Verily अहम् I वेद know तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यम् whom आत्थ (you) call आयतनम् the ultimate resort सर्वस्य



of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs). सः That एषः (is) this यः who एव indeed अयम् this पुरुषः deity, being छायामयः identified with shadow वद speak on एव indeed शाकल्य Shakalya का who (is) तस्य his देवता इति deity ? मृत्युः इति death उवाच ह said (Shākalya).

 Shakalya said—'Verily he who is the knower of that deity who has darkness, such as that of the night, as his body, who sees through the intellect and weighs over things through the mind and who is the ultimate support of all bodies and organs is a true knower (teacher), O Yajnavalkya, 'Yajnavalkya replied : 'Verily I am a knower of that deity whom you call that final support of all bodies and organs. It is the deity who is identified with shadow (ignorance). Speak on Shākalya, who is his deity ?' Shakalya replied that death among the gods is his deity (cause) according to Shrutis.

 ** रूपाण्येव यस्याऽऽयतनं चक्षुर्लोको मनोज्योतिर्यो वै तं पुरुषं विद्यात्सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणꣳ स वै वेदिता स्यात्। याज्ञवल्क्य वेद वा अहं तं पुरुषꣳ सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणं यमात्थ य एवायमादर्शे पुरुषः स एष वदैव शाकल्य तस्य का देवतेत्यसुरिति होवाच॥१५॥**

 वै Verily सः he यः who विद्यात् knows तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यस्य whose आयतनम् body, abode (is) एव indeed



रूपाणि the (particular) colours लोकः instrument of vision (is) चक्षुः the eye, ज्योतिः light (is) मनः the mind वै verily स्यात् is वेदिता the knower याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. वै Verily अहम् I वेद know तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यम् whom आत्थ (you) call आयतनम् final support सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs). सः That एषः this (is) यः who (is) एव indeed अयम् this पुरुषः being, deity आदर्शो in the looking glass वद speak on एव indeed शाकल्य Shakalya का who (is) तस्य his देवता इति deity? असुः इति The vital power उवाच ह said (Shākalya).

 Shakalya said : 'Verily he who is the knower of that deity, who has particular colours¹ (that reflects) as his body, who sees through the eye and weighs over things through the mind, and who is the final support of all bodies and organs, is a true knower, O Yajnavalkya.' Yajnavalkya replied— 'Verily I am a knower of that deity whom you call the ultimate resort of all bodies and organs. It is this deity² who is identified with the looking-glass. Speak on, Shakalya, who is his deity?' Shakalya replied that vital power is his deity (cause).'

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Reflecting objects such as a looking glass.

2\. It is called reflection which emanates from the vital power. Reflection depends on friction, etc. which requires strength (vital power). Hence vital power is said to be the cause of reflection.—Anandagiri.\]

——————————————————————————————



** आप एव यस्याऽऽयतनꣳ हृदयं लोको मनोज्योतिर्यो वै तं पुरुषं विद्यात्सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणꣳ स वै वेदिता स्यात्। याज्ञवल्क्य वेद वा अहं तं पुरुषꣳ सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणं यमात्थ य एवायमप्सु पुरुषः स एष वदैव शाकल्य तस्य का देवतेति वरुण इति होवाच॥१६॥**

 वै Verily सः he यः who विद्यात् knows तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यस्य whose आयतनम् body, abode (is) एव indeed आपः waters लोकः instrument of vision (is) हृदयम् the intellect ज्योतिः light मनः (is) the mind वै verily स्यात् is वेदिता the knower याज्ञवल्क्य O Yajñavalkya. वै Verily अहम् I वेद know तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यम् whom आत्थ (you) call परायणम् the ultimate resort सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs). सः That एषः this यः who एव indeed अयम् this पुरुषः being, deity अप्सु in waters वद् speak on एव indeed शाकल्य Shākalya का who (is) तस्य his देवता इति deity वरुणः इति Varuṇa (rain) उवाच ह said (Shākalya).

 Shakalya said—'Verily he who is the knower of that deity who has waters¹ in general as his body, who sees through the intellect and weighs over things through the mind, and who is the final support of all bodies and organs, is a true knower, O Yajnavalkya.' Yajnavalkya replied: 'Verily I am a knower of that deity whom you call the ultimate resort of all bodies and organs, It is this deity who is identified with waters in general.



Speak on, Shākalya, who is his deity? ’ Shakalya replied that rain² is deity.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. He specially dwells in the waters of reservoirs, wells, tanks, etc. 2. The water of reservoir, etc. that is drunk and assimilated in the body comes from rain. Rain is therefore the deity (cause) of the water in general.\]

——————————————————————————————

  **रेत एव यस्याऽऽयतनꣳ हृदयं लोको मनो ज्योतिर्यो वै तं पुरुषं विद्यात्सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणꣳ स वै वेदिता स्यात् । याज्ञवल्क्य वेद वा अहं तं पुरुषꣳ सर्वस्याऽऽत्मनः परायणं यमात्थ य एवायं पुत्रमयः पुरुषः स एष वदैव शाकल्य तस्य का देवतेति प्रजापतिरिति होवाच॥१७॥**

 वै Verily सः he यः who विद्यात् knows तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यस्य whose आयतनम् body, abode (is) एव indeed रेतः semen, लोकः instrument of vision (is) हृदयम् the intellect, ज्योतिः light (is) मनः the mind, वै verily स्यात् is वेदिता the knower याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. वै verily अहम् I वेद know तम् that पुरुषम् being, deity यम् whom आत्थ (You) call आयतनम् the ultimate resort सर्वस्य of all आत्मनः bodies (and organs). सः That एषः this यः who एव indeed (is) अयम् this पुरुषः being, deity पुत्रमयः identified with the son वद Speak on एव indeed शाकल्य Shākalya का who (is) तस्य his देवता इति deity प्रजापतिः इति Prajāpati (the father) उवाच ह said (Shākalya).

 Shakalya said—‘ Verily he who is the knower of that deity who inhabits the semen, who sees



through the intellect and weighs over things through the mind and who is the ultimate resort of all bodies and organs is the true knower (teacher) O Yajnavalkya.' Yajnavalkya replied—'Verily I am a knower of that deity whom you call the final support of all bodies and organs. It is this deity¹ who is identified with the son. Speak on, Shakalya, who is his deity ? ' Shakalya replied that the father is his deity.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Deity here meant the bones, marrow and semen that are derived from the father.\]

——————————————————————————————

  **शाकल्येति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यस्त्वाꣳ स्विदिमे ब्राह्मणा अङ्गारावक्षयणमक्रन्ता३ इति॥१८॥**
