याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said इति this शाकल्य Shakalya इमे these ब्राह्मणाः Brahmanas, Vedic scholars अक्रँता have made त्वाम् You अङ्गारावक्षयणम् \* इति the instrument for burning charcoal, a vessel in which coal is extinguished स्वित् deliberately शाकल्यः Shakalya उवाच ह said याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya यत् since इदम् this किम् what ब्रह्म-विद्वान् the knower of Brahman.

 \[Eight different forms of the vital power have already been described for the purpose of meditation.

——————————————————————————————

\* Anandagiri adds that Yajnavalkya in saying that Shakalya was made an Angaravakshayana by his fellow Brahmans meant that he was given up by them as a victim, in fact that he was being consumed by Yajnavalkya. Max Muller prefers to take the word in the sense of an instrument with which one takes burning coal from the fire to extinguish them, a pair of tongs.\]

——————————————————————————————



Each form is a deity having three divisions—general body, special manifestation and cause. Now the text describes five more forms of the vital power divided according to the directions and shows that they are all unified in the mind.\]

 Yajnavalkya asked—'Shakalya, have these Brahmans deliberately made you their fire-tongs to extinguish burning coal? Don't you perceive that you are being consumed by me?'

 **याज्ञवल्क्येति होवाच शाकल्यो यदिदं कुरुपञ्चालानाम्ब्राह्मणानत्यवादिः किं ब्रह्म विद्वानिति। दिशो वेद सदेवाः सप्रतिष्ठा इति यद्दिशो वेत्थ सदेवाः सप्रतिष्ठाः॥११॥**

 अत्यवादिः have flouted, have decried ब्राह्मणान् इति Brahmanas, Vedic scholars कुरुपञ्चालानाम् of Kuru and Panchal. वेद (I) Know दिशः (the meditation concerning) the quarters, directions सदेवाः with (presiding) deities समतिष्ठाः with support (results) इति with support (results) यत् which वेथ (You) Know दिशः of (the meditation) the quarters सदेवाःः with the (presiding) deities समतिष्ठाः with the supports.

 Shakalya replied—'Yajnavalkya, since you are a knower of Brahman that you have decried these Brahmanas of Kuru and Panchala by suggesting that they were afraid of you and made me their fire-tongs'. Yajnavalkya said—'I know the meditation on the directions with their presiding



deities as well as their results.’ The other said—‘If you know the meditation on the directions with their presiding deities as also the results of such meditation.—

——————————————————————————————

\[Notes—1. Yajnavalkya realised that his mind was divided in five forms according to directions and was united with the directions and through the directions with the whole Universe as his own Self. He stood with his face turned eastward with the realisation that he was the directions. Sankar asserts that the Vedas repeatedly declare that in this very life one attains identity with and realises the deity one meditates upon.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **किन्देवतोऽस्यां प्राच्यां दिश्यसीत्यादित्यदेवता इति स आदित्यः कस्मिन्प्रतिष्ठित इति चक्षुषीति कस्मिन्नु चक्षुः प्रतिष्ठितमिति रूपेष्विति चक्षुषा हि रूपाणि पश्यति कस्मिन्नु रूपाणि प्रतिष्ठितानीति हृदय इति होवाच हृदयेन हि रूपाणि जानाति हृदये ह्येव रूपाणि प्रतिष्ठितानि भवन्तीत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्यः॥२०॥**

 अस्याम् In this प्राच्याम् eastern दिशि direction असि (you) are किन्देवतः united with which deity ? आदित्यदेवतः इति united with sun-god. कस्मिन् In what सः that आदित्यः sun प्रतिष्ठितः इति abides, rests ? चक्षुषि इति In the eye. कस्मिन् तु In what चक्षुः the eye प्रतिष्ठितम् इति abides, rests. रूपेषु इति In colours हि for पश्यति (one) sees रूपाणि colours चक्षुषा with the eye. कस्मिन् तु In what रूपाणि colours प्रतिष्ठितानि इति abide, rest ? हृदये इति In the heart (mind) उवाच ह (he) said हि



for जानाति (one) knows रूपाणि colours हृदयेन through the heart (mind) हि for हृदये in the heart एव indeed रूपाणि colours भवन्ति are प्रतिष्ठितानि इति resting, supported. याज्ञवल्क्य Yājnavalkya एतत् it (is) एवम् एव just so.

 Shākalya asked Yājnavalkya, ‘Which deity you are united with in the eastern quarter?’ Yājnavalkya replied that he was united with the Sun god in the east. Shākalya asked—‘On what does the sun abide?’ Yājnavalkya replied that the sun rests on the eye. Shākalya asked—‘On what does the eye¹ rest?’ Yājnavalkya replied that the eye rests on colours²; for one sees colours with the eye. Shākalya asked—‘On what do these colours abide?’ Yājnavalkya replied that the colours abide in the mind³; for one knows colours through the mind. Colours rest on the mind⁴. Shākalya told Yājnavalkya that the latter was right

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The sun is produced from the eye that is in the body. For the Rig Veda (10. 90. 13) says that the sun was created from the eye. Aitareya Upanishad (1. 4) says that the sun came from the eye.

2\. The eye is produced by those very colours that direct it to perceive them. The eye is a transformation of colours.

3\. Mind makes the colours—mind is modified into the colours.

4\. Since one remembers through the mind the colours that lie as impressions, colours are said to rest in the mind.\]

——————————————————————————————



** किन्देवतोऽस्मि दक्षिणायां दिश्यसीति यमदेवता इति स यमः कस्मिन्प्रतिष्ठित इति यज्ञ इति कस्मिन्नु यज्ञः प्रतिष्ठित इति दक्षिणायामिति कस्मिन्नु दक्षिणा प्रतिष्ठितेति श्रद्धायामिति यदा ह्येव श्रद्धत्तेऽथ दक्षिणां ददाति श्रद्धायाꣳ ह्येव दक्षिणा प्रतिष्ठितेति कस्मिन्नु श्रद्धा प्रतिष्ठितेति हृदय इति होवाच हृदयेन हि श्रद्धां जानाति हृदये ह्येव श्रद्धा प्रतिष्ठिता भवन्तीत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्यः॥२१॥**

 अस्याम् In this दक्षिणायाम् southern दिशि direction असि (you) are किन्देवतः identified with which god ? यमदेवतः इति yama, the god of justice. सः That यमः yama प्रतिष्ठितः rests, abides कस्मिन् इति in what ? यज्ञे इति In the sacrifice. कस्मिन् तु In what यज्ञः sacrifice प्रतिष्ठितः इति abides, rests ? दक्षिणायाम् इति In the gifts, in the remuneration (of the priests). कस्मिन् तु In what दक्षिणा remuneration प्रतिष्ठिता इति abides, rests ? श्रद्धायाम् इति In faith ; हि Because यदा एव whenever श्रद्धत्ते (a man) believes, has faith अथ then ददाति (he) gives, offers दक्षिणाम् gifts, remuneration (to the priests). हि Therefore श्रद्धायाम् in faith एव indeed दक्षिणा remuneration प्रतिष्ठिता इति abides, rests. कस्मिन् तु In what श्रद्धा faith प्रतिष्ठिता इति abides, rests ? हृदये इति In the heart उवाच ह said (he) ; हि Because हृदयेन through the heart जानाति (one) knows श्रद्धाम् faith. हि Therefore श्रद्धा faith भवति is प्रतिष्ठिता abiding, supported हृदये एव इति in the heart. एवम् एव just so याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya.



 Shākalya asked Yājnavalkya, 'Which is your deity in the southern direction?' Yājnavalkya replied—'I am the south and Yama the god of justice is my deity.' Shākalya—'In what does Yama abide?' Yājnavalkya—'Yama abides in the sacrifice.' Shākalya—'In what does the sacrifice abide?' Yājnavalkya—'Sacrifice abides in the remuneration of the priests.' Shākalya—'In what does the remuneration abide?' Yājnavalkya—'Remuneration abides in faith; for whenever a man has faith (liberality) in the Vedas coupled with devotion, he offers gifts to the priests. If he has no faith, he does not give them. Therefore remuneration rests on faith.' Shākalya—'In what does faith abide?' Yājnavalkya said—'Faith abides in the heart, the former being a modification of the latter. Because one knows faith through the heart; therefore faith abides in the heart.' Shākalya—'So it is indeed, Yājnavalkya.'

 **किन्देवतोऽस्यां प्रतीच्यां दिश्यसीति वरुणदेवत इति स वरुणः कस्मिन्प्रतिष्ठित इत्यप्स्विति कस्मिन्न्वापः प्रतिष्ठिता इति रेतसीति कस्मिन्नु रेतः प्रतिष्ठितमिति हृदय इति तस्मादपि प्रतिरूपं जातमाहुर्हृदयादिव सृप्तो हृदयादिव निर्मित इति हृदये ह्येव रेतः प्रतिष्ठितं भवतीत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्य॥२२॥**



 अस्याम् In this प्रतीच्याम् western दिशि direction किन्देवतः with what god असि (you) are वरुण-देवतः इति with Varuna, the god of rain. सः That वरुणः Varuna कस्मिन् in what प्रतिष्ठितः इति rests, abides? अप्सु इति In water. कस्मिन् In what आपः water प्रतिष्ठिताः इति rests, abides? रेतसि इति In the semen. कस्मिन् नु In what रेतः the semen प्रतिष्ठितम् इति rests, abides? हृदये इति In the heart. तस्मात् अपि Therefore आहुः (people) speak जातम् the new-born (child) प्रतिरूपम् closely resembles (his father). हृदयात् From heart इव as it were सृप्तः (he) has sprung, has been created, निर्मितः इति (he) has been made हृदयात् out of heart इव as it were. हि For हृदये एव on the heart रेतः semen भवति is प्रतिष्ठितम् abides, supports. एतत् It (is) एवम् just so एव indeed याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya.

 Shākalya asked Yājnavalkya, 'What deity you are united with in the western direction?' Yājnavalkya—'Varuna the god of rain is my presiding deity in that direction. Shākalya—In what does Varuna abide? Yājnavalkya—Varuna rests on water¹, the former being the effect of the latter. Shākalya—In what does water abide? Yājnavalkya—Water rests on the semen.² Shākalya—On what does the semen rest? Yājnavalkya—The semen abides in the heart.³ Therefore people speak that a new-born child who closely resembles his father has been created from his father's heart, as it were, (as an ear-ring is made



out of gold). Therefore the semen abides in the heart. Shākalya: You are right, Yājnavalkya.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. As Taittiriya Samhita (1. 6. 8. 1) says—He created Varuna from faith.

2\. Aitereya Upanishad (1. 1. 4) says—Water was produced from semen.

3\. Lust is a modification of the heart and semen issues from the heart of a man under the influence of lust. Therefore semen is said to be the effect of heart.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **किन्देवतोऽस्यामुदीच्यां दिश्यसीति सोमदेवत इति स सोमः कस्मिन्प्रतिष्ठत इति दीक्षायामिति कस्मिन्नु दीक्षा प्रतिष्ठितेति सत्य इति तस्मादपि दीक्षितमाहुः सत्यं वदेति सत्ये ह्येव दीक्षा प्रतिष्ठितेति कस्मिन्नु सत्यं प्रतिष्ठितमिति हृदय इति होवाच हृदयेन हि सत्यं जानाति हृदये ह्येव सत्यं प्रतिष्ठितं भवतीत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्य॥२३॥**

  अस्याम् In this उदीच्याम् northern दिशि direction किन्देवतः united with what god असि इति (you) are ? सोमदेवतः इति with the deity, Soma (the moon, the soma creeper). कस्मिन् In what सः that सोमः moon प्रतिष्ठितः इति abides ? दीक्षायाम् इति In initiation. कस्मिन् नु In what दीक्षा initiation प्रतिष्ठिता इति rests, abides ? सत्ये इति In truth. तस्मात् अपि Therefore आहुः (they) say, ask इति thus दीक्षितम् to be initiated वद speak सत्यम् the truth. हि For सत्ये In truth एव indeed दीक्षा initiation प्रतिष्ठिता इति abides, rests. कस्मिन् नु In what सत्यम् truth प्रतिष्ठितम् इति rests, abides ? हृदये इति In the heart उवाच ह



said (he); हि For हृदयेन through the heart जानाति (one) knows सत्यम् truth; हृदये in the heart सत्यम् truth भवति is प्रतिष्ठितम् इति abides, supported. एतत् It (is) एवम् एव just so याज्ञवल्क्य Yājnavalkya.

 Shākalya asked Yājnavalkya, 'Who is your presiding deity in the northern direction?' Yājnavalkya: Moon is my deity in that direction. Shākalya: On what does moon abide? Yājnavalkya—The moon rests on initiation¹. Shākalya: In what does initiation abide? Yājnavalkya—Initiation abides in truth. Because initiation rests on truth they ask the initiated one to speak the truth. Shākalya: In what does truth abide? Yājnavalkya said: Truth abides in the heart; for one knows truth through the heart. Therefore truth rests on the heart. Shākalya—It is just so, Yājnavalkya.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The initiated sacrificer purchases the Soma creeper, performs sacrifice with the Soma creeper along with the meditation and becomes identified with the northern direction which is presided over by moon called Soma after the creeper.\]

——————————————————————————————

  **किन्देवतोऽस्यां ध्रुवायां दिश्यसीत्यग्निदेवत इति सोऽग्निः कस्मिन्प्रतिष्ठित इति वाचीति कस्मिन्नु वाक् प्रतिष्ठितेति हृदय इति कस्मिन्नु हृदयं प्रतिष्ठितमिति॥२४॥**



 इति (Shakalya asked) this अस्याम् In this ध्रुवायाम् fixed दिशि direction किम् which देवतः deity असि is there? इति (Yajnavalkya said) thus अग्नि-देवतः the fire deity. इति (The one asked) thus सः that अग्निः fire प्रतिष्ठितः rests, abides कस्मिन् in what? इति (The other replied) thus वाचि in speech. कस्मिन् नु In what वाक् speech प्रतिष्ठिता इति abides, rests? हृदये इति In the heart. कस्मिन् नु In what हृदयम् heart, mind प्रतिष्ठितम् इति abides, rests?

  Shākalya asked Yājnavalkya—Which is the deity in the fixed direction i.e. over head? Yājnavalkya replied that fire is the deity in the Zenith; for there is more light and fire is luminous in the direction above. Shākalya asked, 'In what does fire abide?' Yājnavalkya replied that the fire abides in speech. The one asked--In what does the speech abide? The other replied that the speech abides¹ in the heart.² The one asked again—'In what abides the heart which is the embodiment of everything.'

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. All names together with the Zenith come to heart through speech.

2\. The entire Universe is comprised of form, name and action which are nothing but modifications of the heart. The heart extends to all directions, and the deities presiding over the directions are part and parcel of the heart.\]

——————————————————————————————



** अहल्लिकेति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यो यत्रैतदन्यत्रास्मन्मन्यासै यद्ध्येतदन्यत्रास्मत्स्याच्छ्वानो वैनदद्युर्वयाꣳसि वैनद्विमथ्नीरन्निति॥२५॥**

 याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said अहल्लिक \* इति (you) ghost यत्र when मन्यासै (you) think एतत् it (the heart) अन्यत्र (is) elsewhere अस्मात् than in us (i.e., body) हि For यत् if एतत् it (mind) स्यात् be अन्यत्र elsewhere अस्मात् than in us (body) श्वानः the dogs वै verily अद्युः would eat एनत् this (body) वयांसि the birds वै verily विमथ्नीरन् would churn, tear to pieces एनत् इति it (body).

 Yājnavalkya said reproachfully to Shākalya, 'You ghost, when you think that the mind which is the Self of the body, as it were, is elsewhere than in the body, then the body is dead. If the mind be elsewhere than in the body, then the dogs would eat this body, or birds would tear it to pieces¹.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The body which consists of name, form and action abide in the body.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **कस्मिन्नु त्वं चाऽऽत्मा च प्रतिष्ठितौ स्थ इति प्राण इति कस्मिन्नु प्राणः प्रतिष्ठित इत्यपान इति कस्मिन्न्वपानः प्रतिष्ठित इति व्यान इति कस्मिन्नु व्यानः प्रतिष्ठित इत्युदान इति**

——————————————————————————————

\* The word is a term of reproach. Its literal meaning is a ghost. Ahani liyate i.e. that disappears by day.

——————————————————————————————



**कस्मिन्नूदानः प्रतिष्ठित इति समान इति स एष नेति नेत्यात्माऽगृह्यो नहि गृह्यतेऽशीर्यो नहि शीर्यतेऽसङ्गो नहि सज्यतेऽसितो न व्यथते न रिष्यति। एतान्यष्टावायतनान्यष्टौ लोका अष्टौ देवा अष्टौ पुरुषाः स यस्तान्पुरुषान्निरुह्य प्रत्युह्यात्यक्रामत्तं त्वौपनिषदं पुरुषं पृच्छामि तं चेन्मे न विवक्ष्यसि मूर्धा ते विपतिष्यतीति। तꣳ ह न मेने शाकल्यस्तस्य ह मूर्धा विपपातापि हास्य परिमोषिणोऽस्थीन्यपजहुरन्यन्मन्यमानाः॥२६॥**

 कस्मिन् नु In what त्वं च you (i.e., the body) आत्मा च and (your) self (mind, heart) स्थः are प्रतिष्ठितौ इति established ? प्राणे इति In the Prāna. कस्मिन् नु In what प्राणः the Prāna प्रतिष्ठितः इति (is) established ? अपाने इति In the Apāna. कस्मिन् नु In what अपानः the Apāna प्रतिष्ठित इति rests ? व्याने इति In the Vyāna. कस्मिन् नु In what व्यानः the Vyāna प्रतिष्ठितः इति rests ? उदाने इति In the Udāna. कस्मिन् नु In what उदानः the Udāna प्रतिष्ठितः इति rests ? समाने इति In the Samān. एषः This आत्मा self (is) सः (that which is described) न + इति Not this न + इति इति Not this. अगृह्यः (It is) imperceptible, not perceivable ; हि because न (It is) not गृह्यते perceived. अशीर्यः (It is) undecaying ; हि because न (it is) not शीर्यते decays. असङ्गः (It is) unattached ; हि because न (It is) not सज्यते related, attached. असितः (It is) unfettered, free न not व्यथते (It) feels pain, न not रिष्यति (It) is destroyed, suffers injury. एतानि These (are) अष्टौ eight आयतनानि abodes, अष्टौ eight लोकाः instruments of vision अष्टौ eight देवताः deities, अष्टौ eight पुरुषाः beings. पृच्छामि (I) ask त्वा



you तम् that पुरुषम् being औपनिषदम् (who is) known from the Upanishads. सः He यः who निरुह्य projecting तान् those पुरुषान् beings, deities प्रत्युह्य (and) withdrawing (them) अत्यक्रामत् transcends (them). चेत् if न not विवक्ष्यसि (you) tell मे me तम् of him ते your मूर्धा head विपतिष्यति इति will fall off. शाकल्यः Shākalya न not मेने obeyed, knew तम् him. तस्य His मूर्धा head विपपात fell off. परिमोषिणः The robbers अपजह्नुः ह took away अपि even अस्य his अस्थीनि bones मन्यमानाः thinking, mistaking (them) अन्यत् for something (treasure).

 Shākalya said—'Yājnavalkya, you have already stated that the body and the mind rest on each other. Now tell me, in what do the body and the mind rest?' Yājnavalkya replied that the body and the mind rest on the vital power called Prana. Shākalya—'In what does the Prana rest?' Yājnavalkya—The Prana rests on the vital power called Apāna¹. Shākalya—In what does the Apāna rest? Yājnavalkya—Apāna rests on the vital power called Vyāna², which occupies an intermediate position. Shākalya—In what does Vyāna rest? Yājnavalkya—Vyāna rests on the vital power called Udāna³. Shākalya—In what does the Udāna rest? Yājnavalkya—'Udāna rests on Samāna.⁴ This Self is That which has been described⁵ as 'Not This', 'Not This'. The Self is not perceivable, being beyond the attributes of effects. The Self



not being a differentiated object is never perceived by the organs. The Self is undecaying, for It never decays like the body which is gross and made up of parts. The Self is unattached, for It is not related with anything like a gross object. The Self is ever free for It is not bound like what is gross. For that reason It is never pained and is never destroyed. These are the eight abodes (the earth, etc.); the eight instruments of vision (fire, etc.); the eight deities and the eight beings described above⁶. Now I ask You, Shākalya, of that Being who is devoid of hunger, etc. and known only from the Upanishads. He projects these deities and again withdraws them into His mind and also transcends them. If you cannot clearly tell me of Him, I give the curse that your head shall fall off.' Shākalya did not know Him and so could not describe Him to Yājnavalkya. Therefore his head fell off and he died. The robbers mistook his bones for a treasure under transport and snatched them away from his disciples who were carrying home the dead body for funeral rites.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The Prāna would go out through the mouth and nostrils if it were not held back by the Apāna.

2\. The Apāna would also depart through the lower orifice, as the Prāna would through the mouth and nostrils, if they were not held back by the Vyāna.

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

3.Prāna, Apāna and Vyāna would go out in all directions, if they were not fixed, as to a post, to the Udāna.

4.Not only Udāna but also other three vital powers are also held by Sāmana. The idea is that the body, mind and the five vital powers are inter-dependent and work together as an orderly aggregate dominated by the purpose of the individual Self.

5.In the first two chapters called Madhukanda.

6.In passage from 10 to 17.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** अथ होवाच ब्राह्मणा भगवन्तो यो वः कामयते स मा पृच्छतु सर्वे वा मा पृच्छत यो वः कामयते तं वः पृच्छामि सर्वान्वा वः पृच्छामीति ते ह ब्राह्मणा न दधृषुः॥२७॥**

 अथ Then उवाच (Yajnavalkya) said, addressed भगवन्तः venerable ब्राह्मणाः Brahmanas वः amongst you सः he यः whosoever कामयते desires पृच्छतु may ask मे me वा or सर्वे all पृच्छत may ask मे me. पृच्छामि (I) shall ask तम् him वः amongst you यः who वः amongst you कामयते desires वा or, otherwise पृच्छामि (I) shall ask सर्वान् all वः of you. ते ह Those ब्राह्मणाः Brahmanas दधृषुः dared न not.

 When the Brāhmanas were silent Yājnavalkya addressed them thus: 'Venerable Brāhmanas, whichsoever amongst you desires to ask me questions you may do so or all of you may ask. Otherwise I shall ask questions to whichsoever amongst you desires me to ask him or I shall ask all of you.' The Brāhmanas thus addressed dared not give any reply whatsoever.



** तान्द्हेतैः श्लोकैः पप्रच्छ—यथा वृक्षो वनस्पतिस्तथैव पुरुषोऽमृषा। तस्य लोमानि पर्णानि त्वगस्योत्पाटिका बहिः॥१॥**

 पप्रच्छ (Yajnavalkya) asked तान् them (Brahmanas) एतैः with these श्लोकैः verses—यथा as (is) वनस्पतिः large, mighty वृक्षः tree, तथा so एव indeed पुरुषः (is) a man. अमृषा (This is) true तस्य his लोमानि hairs पर्णानि (are its) leaves, अस्य its त्वक् skin (is) बहिः outer उत्पाटिका bark.

 Yājnavalkya asked the Brāhmanas the following verses : As a mighty tree in a forest, so indeed is a man. This is true that his hairs correspond to the leaves of the tree and his skin to its outer bark.

 **त्वच एवास्य रुधिरं प्रस्यन्दि त्वच उत्पटः। तस्मात्तदा तृण्णात्प्रैति रसो वृक्षादिवाऽऽहतात्॥२॥**

 त्वचः From skin अस्य of him रुधिरम् blood प्रस्यन्दि flows, त्वचः from the bark उत्पटः sap. तस्मात् Therefore तदा so आतृण्णात् from the wounded प्रैति flows तत् that (blood) इव as आहतात् from the cut, from the struck वृक्षात् tree रसः sap (exudes).

 It is from a man's skin that blood flows and it is from the bark of a mighty tree sap exudes. Since a man and a mighty tree are similar in so many ways, therefore when a man is wounded blood flows, as sap exudes from a tree that is struck.



** माꣳसान्यस्य शकराणि किनाटꣳ स्नाव तत्स्थिरम्। अस्थीन्यन्तरतो दारूणि मज्जा मज्जोपमा कृता॥३॥**

 अस्य His मांसानि flesh शकराणि (its) inner bark, स्नावः nerves किनाटम् inner most layer of bark. तत् It (is) स्थिरम् tough, strong अस्थीनि (its) bones अन्तरतः (lie) within दारूणि (as) wood मज्जा (its) marrow कृता (is) made मज्जा-उपमा comparison with pith.

 Similarly a man's flesh is the inner bark of a mighty tree. His nerves are innermost layer of bark in a tree. That layer of bark which is attached to the wood is strong. As a man's bones lie under the nerves, so does the innermost bark of a tree is the wood. A man's marrow corresponds to the pith of a tree.

** यद्वृक्षो वृक्णो रोहति मूलान्नवतरः पुनः। मर्त्यः स्विन्मृत्युना वृक्णः कस्मान्मूलात्प्ररोहति॥४॥**

 यद् While वृक्षः a tree वृक्णः (is) felled रोहति springs, grows up पुनः again मूलात् from (its) root नवतरः newer, more young कस्मात् from what मूलात् root मर्त्यः a mortal वृक्णः cut off मृत्युना by death स्वित् प्ररोहति does spring, is reborn.

 \[The similarity between a man and a tree has already been shown. Now the difference between them is pointed out.\]



 But while a tree, when it is felled, grows up again from its root in a newer form. From what root a mortal is reborn, after he is cut off by death ?

** रेतस इति मा वोचत जीवतस्तत्प्रजायते। धानारुह इव वै वृक्षोऽञ्जसा प्रेत्य सम्भवः॥५॥**

 मा Do not वोचत say रेतसः इति from the semen ; तत् (for) it प्रजायते is produced जीवतः in a living man. वै Verily इव as वृक्षः a tree (springs) धानारुहः from the seed अञ्जसा certainly प्रेत्य being felled सम्भवः springs.

 You should not say that the man springs forth after death from semen. For semen is produced in a living man, not in a dead man. A tree grows up also from the seed, not from the trunk only. A mighty tree when it is dead certainly grows up again from the seed as well.

** यत्समूलमावृहेयुर्वृक्षं न पुनराभवेत्। मर्त्यः स्विन्मृत्युना वृक्णः कस्मान्मूलात्प्ररोहति॥६॥**

 यत् Since; while वृक्षम् a tree आवृहेयुः is pulled out समूलम् with root आभवेत् grows, sprouts न not पुनः again, any more. कस्मात् From what मूलात् root मर्त्यः a mortal वृक्णः cut off, felled मृत्युना by death स्वित् प्ररोहति does spring forth, does grow up.



 If a tree is pulled out with its root or its seed, it does not grow up again. From what root does a mortal grow up after he is felled by death ?

 **जात एव न जायते को न्वेनं जनयेत्पुनः। विज्ञानमानन्दं ब्रह्म रातिर्दातुः परायणं तिष्ठमानस्य तद्विद इति॥७॥२८॥ इति नवमं ब्राह्मणम्॥९॥ इति बृहदारण्यकोपनिषदि तृतीयोऽध्यायः॥३॥**

 एव (If you say he is) ever जातः born ; न (I say) not जायते (he) is born. कः नु who पुनः again जनयेत् should create, should bring forth एनम् him (dead man) विज्ञानम् knowledge, pure intelligence आनन्दम् bliss ब्रह्म Brahman परायणम् the supreme goal, bestower of the fruits of actions दातुः of the distributor, of the sacrificer रातेः of wealth तत्-विदः (as well as) of the knower of that (Brahman) तिष्ठमानस्य of one who lives in (It).

 If you say he is never born, I say, no. After death he is certainly born again¹. Now who should again create the dead man ? The Shruti² declares : After death man is reborn from Brahman who is the root of the Universe. He is characterised by Pure Intelligence and Absolute Bliss³. He is the bestower of the fruits of actions of the sacrificer who engages himself in rites. He is the Supreme goal of one who has realised Brahman and lives in Brahman.



——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Otherwise it is to be taken for granted that a man enjoys the result of works never done by him and does not get the results of those works actually done by him.

2\. Brāhmanas could not answer this question and were defeated. Then Yajnavalkya took away the cows. The story is completed. Now Shruti answers the question and reveals the truth.

3\. Absolute bliss is not smitten with pain like sense-perception. It is a sort of indescribable and incomparable serenity, satisfaction and sweetness which is not obstructed by any thing.\]

——————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER FOUR : SECTION ONE**

** ॐ जनको ह वैदेह आसाञ्चक्रेऽथ ह याज्ञवल्क्य आवव्राज। तꣳ होवाच याज्ञवल्क्य किमर्थमचारीः पशूनिच्छन्नण्वन्तामिति। उभयमेव सम्राडिति होवाच॥१॥**

 ॐ Om. जनकः ह Janaka वैदेहः king of Videha आसाञ्चक्रे took seat (to give audience). अथ Then याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya आवव्राज arrived, came (there). उवाच ह (the King) said to, asked तम् him याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya अर्थम् for reason of किम् what (object) अचारीः (you) have come (here) ? इच्छन् wishing पशून् (some) cattle अण्वन्तान् इति (or) some subtle qestions. सम्राड् O King उभयम् both एव इति ह indeed उवाच said (he).



  \[The two following sections give further instruction about the Supreme Being who is to be known only from the Upanishad by referring to the deities of speech and the rest. The story indicates the custom to be followed on such occasions.\]

  Om. King Janaka of Videha took his seat to give audience when Yājnavalkya arrived there. The King asked him, 'Yājnavalkya, what for have you come here ? Do you wish to have some cattle or hear some subtle questions from me ?' Yājnavalkya replied that he came indeed for both cattle and questions.

  **यत्ते कश्चिदब्रवीत्तच्छृणवामेत्यब्रवीन्मे जित्वा शैलिनिर्वाग्वै ब्रह्मेति यथा मातृमान्पितृमानाचार्यवान्ब्रूयात्तथा तच्छैलिनिरब्रवीद्वाग्वै ब्रह्मेत्यवदतो हि किꣳ स्यादित्यब्रवीत्तु ते तस्याऽऽयतनं प्रतिष्ठां न मेऽब्रवीदित्येकपाद्वा एतत्सम्राडिति स वै नो ब्रूहि याज्ञवल्क्य। वागेवाऽऽयतनमाकाशः प्रतिष्ठा प्रज्ञेत्येनदुपासीत। का प्रज्ञता याज्ञवल्क्य। वागेव सम्राडिति होवाच। वाचा वै सम्राड्बन्धुः प्रज्ञायत ऋग्वेदो यजुर्वेदः सामवेदोऽथर्वाङ्गिरस इतिहासः पुराणं विद्या उपनिषदः श्लोकाः सूत्राण्यनुव्याख्यानानि व्याख्यानानीष्टꣳ हुतमाशितं पायितमयं च लोकः परश्च लोकः सर्वाणि च भूतानि वाचैव सम्राट्प्रज्ञायन्ते वाग्वै सम्राट्परमं ब्रह्म नैनं वाग्जहाति सर्वाण्येनं भूतान्यभिक्षरन्ति देवो**



**भूत्वा देवानप्येति य एवं विद्वानेतदुपास्ते। हस्त्यृषभꣳ सहस्रं ददामीति होवाच जनको वैदेहः। स होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः पिता मेऽमन्यत नाननुशिष्य हरेतेति॥२॥**

 शृणवाम Let (me) hear तत् that यत् which कश्चित् any one (of your teachers) अब्रवीत् may have told (taught) ते इति you. जित्वा Jitwan शैलिनिः the son of Shilina अब्रवीत् has told (taught) मे me वै verily वाक् the speech (i.e., its presiding deity, Fire) ब्रह्म इति (is) Brahman. यथा As मातृमान् one having a mother, पितृमान् one having a father, आचार्यवान् one having a teacher ब्रूयात् should say तथा so शैलिनिः the son of Shilina अब्रवीत् has told (taught) तत् that वाक् the organ of speech (is) वै verily ब्रह्म इति Brahman. हि Because किम् what अवदतः of a dumb person, of one unable to speak स्यात् इति may be. अब्रवीत् तु Did (he) tell ते you तस्य its आयतनम् abode, body प्रतिष्ठाम् support, permanent resort अब्रवीत् (he) told मे me न not. सम्राड् O Emperor एतत् it (is) एकपात् one-footed. वै verily याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya ब्रूहि tell, teach नः us. वाक् The speech एव indeed आयतनम् its abode, body, आकाशः the (undifferentiated) ether प्रतिष्ठा (its) support, resort. एतत् It उपासीत should be meditated upon प्रज्ञा इति as intelligence, consciousness. याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya का what (is) प्रज्ञता intelligence, consciousness ? सः He उवाच ह said वाक् the speech एव indeed सम्राड् इति O Emperor. वाचा By the speech वै verily सम्राड् O Emperor बन्धुः a friend प्रज्ञायते is known. ऋग्वेदः The Rig-Veda, यजुर्वेदः the Yajur-Veda, सामवेदः the Sāma-Veda अथर्वाङ्गिरसः Atharvangirasa, इतिहासः (Vedic) History, पुराणम् mythology विद्या arts, उपनिषदः Upanishads, श्लोकाः



verses, सूत्राणि aphorisms, अनुव्याख्यानानि elucidations, व्याख्यानानि explanations, इष्टम् sacrifices, the spiritual effects produced by them, हुतम् pouring oblations (in the fire), आशितम् offering food, पायितम् offering drink अयम् this, present लोकः च world, life च and परम् the next, future लोकः world, life च and सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings सम्राड् O Emperor वाचा by the speech एव indeed प्रज्ञायन्ते are known. वै Verily वाक् speech, its duty fire (is) परमम् the Supreme ब्रह्म Brahman. वाक् The speech जहाति leaves न not एनम् him. सर्वाणि All भूतानि beings अभिक्षरन्ति eagerly approach एनम् him, भूत्वा Being, becoming देवः a god अप्येति (he) attains, is merged in देवान् the gods, यः who विद्वान् knowing एवम् thus उपास्ते meditates upon एनम् it. जनकः Janaka वैदेहः Emperor of Videha उवाच said ददामिः (I) give, offer (you) सहस्त्रम् a thousand (cows) हस्ति-ऋषभम् इति with a bull as big as an elephant. सः That याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said मे my पिता father अमन्यत thought, held the view अननुशिष्य (न + अनुशिष्य) without fully instructing, not truly satisfying (a pupil) हरेत इति (one) should accept न not (reward from him).

 Yajnavalkya asked : Let me hear what anyone of your teachers may have taught you. Janaka replied : My teacher Jitwan, Shilina's son, has taught me that Fire, the presiding deity of speech, is Brahman. Yajnavalkya : As he who has a mother (to adequately instruct him in childhood), a father (to do so after that) and a teacher (to teach him from the initiation with holy thread up to the



completion of studies) should say to his disciple, so has Shilina’s son taught you that fire the deity of speech is Brahman. What can a dumb person achieve here? But did he teach you about the body and permanent Resort of fire? Janaka said that his teacher did not teach him about them. Yajnavalkya: This Brahman has only one foot and lacks the remaining three feet, O Emperor. Janaka: Then you please teach us. Yajnavalkya: The speech is indeed the body and the undifferentiated ether the resort of fire which is a form of Brahman. It should be meditated upon as consciousness. Janaka: Do you mean consciousness itself or its effect which is speech? Yajnavalkya: I mean speech itself, O Emperor. Because it is not different from speech. By speech, O Emperor, a friend is known. By speech alone, O Emperor, the Rig-Veda, Yajur-Veda, Sāma-Veda, Atharvan-girasa, Vedic history, mythology, arts, Upanishads, verses, aphorisms, elucidations and explanations, the spiritual effects produced by sacrifices, pouring oblations in the fire, and offering food and drink, the present life and the future life and all beings are known. Therefore fire that presides over speech, O Emperor, is a form of the Supreme Brahman. The speech never leaves him who knows Brahman as fire and meditates upon it likewise.



All beings eagerly approach him with offerings, etc. Such a knower becomes a god in this very life and is merged in the gods after death. Janaka of Videha said: I offer you a thousand cows with a bull as big as elephant. Yajnavalkya replied—'My father held the view that one should not accept reward from a pupil without fully satisfying him. I am of the same opinion.'

 **यदेव ते कश्चिदब्रवीत्तच्छृणवामेत्यब्रवीन्म उदङ्कः शौल्बायनः प्राणो वै ब्रह्मेति यथा मातृमान्पितृमानाचार्यवान्ब्रूयात्तथा तच्छौल्बायनोऽब्रवीत्प्राणो वै ब्रह्मेत्यप्राणतो हि किꣳ स्यादित्यब्रवीत्तु ते तस्याऽऽयतनं प्रतिष्ठां न मेऽब्रवीदित्येकपाद्वा एतत्सम्राडिति स वै नो ब्रूहि याज्ञवल्क्य प्राण एवाऽऽयतनमाकाशः प्रतिष्ठा प्रियमित्येनदुपासीत का प्रियता याज्ञवल्क्य प्राण एव सम्राडिति होवाच प्राणस्य वै सम्राट्कामाययाज्यं याजयत्यप्रतिगृह्यस्य प्रतिगृह्णात्यपि तत्र वधाशङ्कं भवति यां दिशमेति प्राणस्यैव सम्राट्कामाय प्राणो वै सम्राट्परमं ब्रह्म नैनं प्राणो जहाति सर्वाण्येनं भूतान्यभिक्षरन्ति देवो भूत्वा देवानप्येति य एवं विद्वानेतदुपास्ते हस्त्यृषभꣳ सहस्रं ददामीति होवाच जनको वैदेहः स होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः पिता मेऽमन्यत नाननुशिष्य हरेतेति॥३॥**



 (Yajnavalkya asked): शृणवाम Let (me) hear तत् that यत् which एव indeed कश्चित् any one else (of your teachers) अब्रवीत् may have told (taught) ते इति you. (Janaka): उदङ्कः Udanka शौल्बायनः the son of Shulba अब्रवीत् has told (taught) मे m: वै verily प्राणः the vital power (its presiding deity, Vayu) ब्रह्म इति (is) Brahman. (Yajnavalky:) यथा As मातृमान् one having a mother, पितृमान् one having a father, आचार्यवान् one having a teacher ब्रूयात् should tell (teach), तथा so तत् that शौल्बायनः Shulba's son अब्रवीत् has told (taught) प्राणः the vital power, Vayu वै verily ब्रह्म (is) Brahman. हि Because किम् what स्यात् may be, is the use अप्राणतः इति of one without life? तु But अब्रवीत् (he) told, taught ते you तस्य its आयतनम् abode, body प्रतिष्ठाम् support, resort अब्रवीत् told न not मे इति me. सम्राड् O Emperor एतत् this (is) वै verily एकपात् one-footed. याज्ञवल्क्य O Yājnavalkya सः that वै verily ब्रूहि tell नः us. प्राणः The vital power, Vayu एव indeed (is) आयतनम् abode, body आकाशः ether, undifferentiated ether प्रतिष्ठा the support, resort. उपासीत Meditate एतत् upon it प्रियम् इति as dear. का What (is) प्रियता dearness याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya? उवाच ह (He) said सम्राड् O Emperor प्राणः इति the vital power, Vayu, एव indeed, कामाय for the sake प्राणस्य of the vital power सम्राड् O Emperor वै verily याजयति causes to sacrifice अयाज्यम् for one unworthy of sacrifice अपि even प्रतिगृह्णाति accepts, presents अप्रतिगृह्यस्य from one unworthy to bestow presents एव indeed कामाय for the sake प्राणस्य of the vital power सम्राड् O Emperor तत्र then भवति (one) is वधाशङ्कम् afraid of being hurt याम् whichever दिशम् direction एति इति (one) goes. वै Verily प्राणः the vital power, Vayu (is)



सम्राट् O Emperor परमम् highest, Supreme ब्रह्म Brahman. प्राणः The vital power जहाति leaves न not एनम् him. सर्वाणि All भूतानि beings अभिक्षरन्ति eagerly approach एनम् him. भूत्वा Being, becoming देवः a god अप्येति (he) attains, is merged in देवान् the gods यः who विद्वान् knowing एवम् thus उपास्ते meditates एतत् upon it. जनकः Janaka वैदेहः the Emperor of Videha उवाच ह said ददामि (I) offer, give (you) सहस्रम् a thousand cows हस्ति-ऋषभम् इति with a bull as big as an elephant. सः That याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said—मे my पिता father अमन्यत thought, held (this view) हरेत (one) should accept न not (reward) अननुशिष्य इति without fully instructing, satisfying.

 Yajnavalkya said : Let me hear whatever anyone else of your teachers may have taught you. Janaka replied : Udanka, Shulba’s son, has taught me that Vayu who presides over the vital power is Brahman. Yajnavalkya : As one who has a mother, father and teacher to instruct in various stages of life should tell, so has Shulba’s son told you that Vayu, the deity of the vital power, is Brahman. Because what is the use of a lifeless man? But did he tell you about the body and the resort of Vayu ? Janaka said that he was not told those things. Yajnavalkya : This Brahman has only one foot, O Emperor. Janaka then requested Yajnavalkya to tell him what he knows. Yajnavalkya : The vital power is the body and the



undifferentiated ether the permanent resort of Vayu. It should be meditated upon as dear. Janaka : What is the nature of dearness? Yajnavalkya : The vital power itself, O Emperor. Because for the sake of the vital power, O Emperor, one sacrifices, for one unworthy of sacrifice (such as even an outcaste) and accepts presents from one¹ who is unworthy to bestow them. And for the sake of the vital power, O Emperor, one is afraid of going to any direction infested by robbers, etc. Vayu, the deity of Vital power, O Emperor, is a form of the Supreme Brahman. The vital power never leaves him who knows thus and meditates upon it. All beings eagerly approach him with offerings. He becomes god in this very life and is merged in other gods after death. Emperor Janaka, "I offer you a thousand cows with a bull as big as an elephant." Yajnavalkya : My father held the view that one should not accept rewards from a pupil without fully satisfying him.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. For instance, an Ugra—one born of Kshatriya father and Shudra mother.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **यदेव ते कश्चिदब्रवीत्तच्छृणावामेत्यब्रवीन्मे बर्कुर्वार्ष्षश्चक्षुर्वै ब्रह्मेति यथा मातृमान्पितृमानाचार्यवान्ब्रूयात्तथा तद्वार्ष्षोऽब्रवीच्चक्षुर्वै ब्रह्मेत्यपश्यतो हि किꣳ स्यादित्यब्रवीत्तु ते तस्याऽऽयतनं**



**प्रतिष्ठां न मेऽब्रवीदित्येकपाद्वा एतत्सम्राडिति स वै नो ब्रूहि याज्ञवल्क्य चक्षुरेवाऽऽयतनमाकाशः प्रतिष्ठा सत्यमित्येतदुपासीत का सत्यता याज्ञवल्क्य चक्षुरेव सम्राडिति होवाच चक्षुषा वै सम्राट्पश्यन्तमाहुरद्राक्षीरिति स आहाद्राक्षमिति तत्सत्यं भवति चक्षुर्वै सम्राट्परमं ब्रह्म नैनं चक्षुर्जहाति सर्वाण्येनं भूतान्यभिक्षरन्ति देवो भूत्वा देवानप्येति य एवं विद्वानेतदुपास्ते हस्त्यृषभꣳ सहस्रं ददामीति होवाच जनको वैदेहः स होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः पिता मेऽमन्यत नाननुशिष्य हरेतेति॥४॥**

  (Yajnavalkya said:) श्रृणवाम Let (me) hear एव indeed तत् that यत् which कश्चित् any one else (of your teachers) अब्रवीत् have told (taught) ते इति you. (Janaka) बर्कुः Barku वार्ष्णः the son of Vrishna वै verily चक्षुः the eye (i.e., its deity-the sun) ब्रह्म इति (is) Brahman. (Yajnavalkya:) यथा As मातृमान् one having a mother, पितृमान् one having a father आचार्यवान् one having a teacher, ब्रूयात् should tell (teach) तथा so तत् that वार्ष्णः Vrishna's son अब्रवीत् has told (taught) चक्षुः eye (sun) वै verily ब्रह्म इति (is) Brahman. हि Because किम् what स्यात् may be, is the use अपश्यतः इति of one without vision, of a sightless person ? तु But अब्रवीत् (he) told, taught ते you तस्य its आयतनम् abode, body प्रतिष्ठाम् resort, support (Janaka :) अब्रवीत् (he) told, taught न not मे इति me. सम्राट् O Emperor वै verily एतत् this एकपात् इति one footed. याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya सः that वै verily ब्रूहि tell नः us. चक्षुः The eye (is) एव indeed आयतनम् abode, body आकाशः the (undifferentiated) ether प्रतिष्ठा resort, support. उपासीत



Meditate एतत् upon it सत्यम् इति as truth. (Janaka asked) याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya का what (is) सत्यता truth? उवाच ह (Janaka) said चक्षुः the eye एव verily सम्राड् इति O Emperor. आहुः (They) say, ask पश्यन्तम् to one who has seen चक्षुषा by the eye वै indeed सम्राट् O Emperor अद्राक्षीः इति have (you) seen? सः He आह says, replies अद्राक्षम् इति (I) have seen. (Then) तत् it भवति is सत्यम् true. वै Verily चक्षुः eye, sun सम्राट् O Emperor (is) परमम् Supreme ब्रह्म Brahman. चक्षुः The eye न not जहाति deserts, leaves एनम् him. सर्वाणि All भूतानि beings अभिक्षरन्ति eagerly approach एनम् him. भूत्वा Being, becoming देवः a god अप्येति attains, is merged in देवान् the gods यः who विद्वान् knowing एवम् thus उपास्ते meditates एनम् upon it. जनकः Janaka वैदेहः the Emperor of Videha उवाच ह said ददामि (I) offer, give (you) सहस्रम् a thousand (cows) हस्ति-ऋषभम् इति with a bull as big as an elephant. सः That याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said—मे my पिता father अमन्यत thought, held the view न not हरेत (one) should accept (rewards) अननुशिष्य इति without fully instructing (satisfying him).

 Yajnavalkya said: ‘ Let me hear whatever anyone else of your teachers may have taught you. ’ Janaka replied: Barku, Vrishna’s son has taught me that the sun who is the presiding deity of the eye is Brahman. Yajnavalkya: As one has a mother, father and teacher to instruct him in different stages of life should tell, so has Vrishna’s son told that the sun the deity of the eye is Brahman. Because what is the use of a sightless person? But



did he teach you about the body and resort of the deity ? Janaka said that his teacher did not do so. Yājnavalkya : This Brahman has only one foot, O Emperor. Janaka : Then you teach me what you know about It. Yājnavalkya : The eye is the body and the undifferentiated ether is the resort of that deity. It should be meditated upon as truth.¹ Janaka : What is the nature of truth ? Yājnavalkya : The eye itself, O Emperor, is truth. Because if one who has seen an object is asked whether he has seen it, he always replies in the affirmative. When one sees it then it is considered true. The sun-god who is the deity of the eye, O Emperor, is a form of the Supreme Brahman. The eye never deserts him who knows thus and meditates upon it. All beings eagerly approach him with offerings, etc. He becomes a god in this very life and is merged in the gods after death. Emperor Janaka of Videha : 'I offer you a thousand cows with a bull as big as an elephant.' Yājnavalkya said—'My father held the view that one should not accept presents from a pupil without fully satisfying him. I am of this opinion.'

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. For, what is heard through the ears may not always correspond with fact. But what is seen by the eyes is always true.\]

——————————————————————————————



** यदेव ते कश्चिदब्रवीत्तच्छृणवामेत्यब्रवीन्मे गर्दभीविपीतो भारद्वाजः श्रोत्रं वै ब्रह्मेति यथा मातृमान्पितृमानाचार्यवान्ब्रूयात्तथा तद्भारद्वाजोऽब्रवीच्छ्रोत्रं वै ब्रह्मेत्यशृण्वतो हि किꣳ स्यादित्यब्रवीत्तु ते तस्याऽऽयतनं प्रतिष्ठां न मेऽब्रवीदित्येकपाद्वा एतत्सम्राडिति स वै नो ब्रूहि याज्ञवल्क्य श्रोत्रमेवाऽऽयतनमाकाशः प्रतिष्ठाऽनन्त इत्येनदुपासीत काऽनन्तता याज्ञवल्क्य दिश एव सम्राडिति होवाच तस्माद्वै सम्राडपि यां कां च दिशं गच्छति नैवास्या अन्तं गच्छत्यनन्ता हि दिशो दिशो वै सम्राट् श्रोत्रंꣳ श्रोत्रं वै सम्राट्परमं ब्रह्म नैनꣳ श्रोत्रं जहाति सर्वाण्येनं भूतान्यभिक्षरन्ति देवो भूत्वा देवानप्येति य एवं विद्वानेतदुपास्ते हस्त्यृषभꣳ सहस्रं ददामीति होवाच जनको वैदेहः स होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः पिता मेऽमन्यत नाननुशिष्य हरेतेति॥५॥**

 (Yajnavalkya said): श्रृणवाम Let (me) hear एव indeed तत् that यत् which कश्चित् any one else (of your teachers) अब्रवीत् have told (taught) ते इति you. गर्दभीविपीतः Garda- bhivipita, भारद्वाजः a descendant of Bharadwaja अब्रवीत् has told (taught) मे me श्रोत्रम् the ear वै verily ब्रह्म इति (is) Brahman. (Yajnavalkya): यथा As मातृमान् one having a mother, पितृमान् one having a father, आचार्यवान् one having a teacher, ब्रूयात् should tell (teach) तथा so तत् that भारद्वाजः descendant of Bharadwaja अब्रवीत् has told श्रोत्रम् ear, directions वै verily ब्रह्म इति (is) Brahman. हि Because किम् what स्यात् may be, is the use of अश्रृण्वतः इति of one without



hearing ? तु But अब्रवीत् (he) told, taught ते you तस्य his आयतनम् abode, body प्रतिष्ठाम् resort, support ? (Janaka :) अब्रवीत् (he) told, taught न not मे इति me. एतत् This (Brahman) वै (is) verily एकपात् इति one-footed. सः That ब्रूहि tell, teach नः us याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. श्रोत्रम् The ear (is) एव indeed आयतनम् the abode, body आकाशः the (undifferentiated) ether प्रतिष्ठा resort, support, उपासीत Meditate एनत् upon it अनन्तम् इति as infinite. (Janaka) का what (is) अनन्तता infinity याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya ? दिशः The directions एव indeed सम्राड् इति O Emperor ह उवाच said (he). तस्मात् Therefore वै verily यां कामु to whatever दिशाम् direction गच्छति (one) goes गच्छति (one) reaches न not अस्याः its अन्तम् end एव indeed, हि because दिशः the directions (are) अनन्ताः infinite, दिशः the directions वै (is) verily श्रोत्रम् the ear सम्राट् O Emperor. श्रोत्रम् The ear (is) वै verily सम्राट् O Emperor परमम् Supreme ब्रह्म Brahman. श्रोत्रम् The ear जहाति deserts, leaves न not एनम् him. सर्वाणि All भूतानि beings अभिक्षरन्ति eagerly approach एनम् him. भूत्वा Being, becoming देवः a god अप्येति attains, is merged in देवान् the gods यः who विद्वान् knowing एवम् thus उपास्ते meditates एनम् upon it. जनकः Janaka वैदेहः Emperor of Videha उवाच ह said ददामि (I) give, offer (you) सहस्रम् a thousand (cows) हस्ति-ऋषभम् इति with a bull as big as an elephant. सः That याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said—मे my पिता father अमन्यत thought, held the view हरेत (one) should accept न not अननुशिष्य इति without fully instructing (satisfying him).

 Yājnavalkya said: 'Let me hear whatever anyone else of your teachers may have taught you.'



Janaka : Gardarbhivipita, a descendant of Bharad-waja, has taught me that the Directions which are the presiding deities of the ear are Brahman. Yājnavalkya replied : As one who has a mother, father and teacher to instruct him in various stages of life should teach, so has the descendant of Bharad-waja taught that Directions, the deities of the ear, are Brahman. Because, what is the use of a person who is devoid of hearing ? But did he teach you about the body and resort of the deities ? Janaka said that his teacher did not do so. Yājnavalkya : This Brahman has only one foot, O Emperor. Janaka : Then you teach me what you know about it. Yājnavalkya : The ear is the abode and the undifferentiated ether is the resort of the directions. It should be meditated upon as infinite. Janaka : What is infinity of the ear ? Yājnavalkya : The directions are indeed infinity. Therefore, O Emperor, to whatever direction east or west, north or south one goes, one never reaches its end. Hence directions are infinite. The directions, O Emperor, are the ear. Directions, the presiding deities of the ear, O Emperor, is a form of the Supreme Brahman. The ear never deserts him who knows thus and meditates upon it. All beings eagerly approach him. He becomes a god in this very life and is merged in the gods after death.



'I offer you a thousand cows with a bull as big as an elephant.' Said Emperor Janaka. Yajnavalkya replied, 'My father held the view that one should not accept presents from a pupil without fully satisfying him.'

** यदेव ते कश्चिदब्रवीत्तच्छृणवामेत्यब्रवीन्मे सत्यकामो जाबालो मनो वै ब्रह्मेति यथा मातृमान्पितृमानाचार्यवान्ब्रूयात्तथा तज्जाबालोऽब्रवीन्मनो वै ब्रह्मेत्यमनसो हि किꣳ स्यादित्यब्रवीत्तु ते तस्याऽऽयतनं प्रतिष्ठां न मेऽब्रवीदित्येकपाद्वा एतत्सम्राडिति स वै नो ब्रूहि याज्ञवल्क्य मन एवाऽऽयतनमाकाशः प्रतिष्ठाऽऽनन्द इत्येनदुपासीत काऽऽनन्दता याज्ञवल्क्य मन एव सम्राडिति होवाच मनसा वै सम्राट्स्त्रियमभिहार्यते तस्यां प्रतिरूपः पुत्रो जायते स आनन्दो मनो वै सम्राट्परमं ब्रह्म नैनं मनो जहाति सर्वाण्येनं भूतान्यभिक्षरन्ति देवो भूत्वा देवानप्येति य एवं विद्वानेतदुपास्ते हस्त्यृषभꣳ सहस्रं ददामीति होवाच जनको वैदेहः स होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः पिता मेऽमन्यत नाननुशिष्य हरेतेति॥६॥**

 (Yajnavalkya said :) शृणवाम Let (me) hear तत् that यत् which एव indeed कश्चित् anyone (of your teachers) अब्रवीत् have told (taught) ते इति you. सत्यकामः Satyakama जाबालः the son of Jabala अब्रवीत् has told (taught) मे me वै verily मनः the mind (is) ब्रह्म इति Brahman. (Yajnavalkya) : यथा As



मातृमान् one having a mother, पितृमान् one having a father, आचार्यवान् one having a teacher, ब्रूयात् should tell (teach) तथा so तत् that जाबालः son of Jabala अब्रवीत् has told (taught) मनः the mind वै verily (is) ब्रह्म इति Brahman. हि Because किम् what may be, is the use अमनसः इति of one having no mind? तु But अब्रवीत् (he) told, taught ते you तस्य its आयतनम् abode, body प्रतिष्ठाम् resort, support? न Not अब्रवीत् इति (he) told taught, मे इति me. एतत् This (Brahman) वै (is) verily एकपात् इति one footed. सः That (you) वै verily ब्रूहि tell, teach नः us याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. मनः The mind एव indeed (is) आयतनम् abode, body आकाशः the (undifferentiated) ether (is) प्रतिष्ठा support. उपासीत Meditate एनत् upon it आनन्दः इति as bliss. (Janaka) : का what (is) आनन्दता nature of bliss याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. मनः The mind वै indeed सम्राट् O Emperor उवाच ह said (he). वै Verily मनसा with the mind सम्राट् O Emperor अभिहार्यते (one) woos स्त्रियम् a woman, पुत्रः a son प्रतिरूपः like, resembling (him) जायते is born तस्याम् of her (the woman). सः He (is) आनन्दः (the cause of) bliss वै verily मनः the mind (is) सम्राट् O Emperor परमम् supreme ब्रह्म Brahman. मनः The mind जहाति deserts, leaves न not एनम् him. सर्वाणि All भूतानि beings अभिक्षरन्ति eagerly approach एनम् him. भूत्वा Being, becoming देवः a god अप्येति attains, is merged in देवान् gods यः who विद्वान् knowing एवम् thus उपास्ते meditates एनम् upon it. जनकः Janaka वैदेहः the Emperor of Videha उवाच ह said ददामि (I) give, offer (you) सहस्रम् a thousand (cows) हस्ति-ऋषभम् इति with a bull as big as an elephant. सः That याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said मे my पिता father अमन्यत thought, held the view हरेत (one)



should accept न not (presents) अननुशिष्य इति without fully instructing, satisfying (him).

 Yājnavalkya said: Let me hear whatever anyone else of your teachers may have taught you. Janaka replied: Satyakama, Jabala's son has taught me that the moon who is the presiding deity of the mind is Brahman. Yājnavalkya: As one who has a mother, father and teacher to instruct in different times of life should teach, so has Jabala's son taught you that moon the deity of the mind is Brahman. Because what is the use of a person who has no mind? But did he teach you about the body and resort of it? Janaka said that he did not. Yājnavalkya: This Brahman has only one foot, O Emperor. Janaka: Then you teach us what you know about it. Yājnavalkya: The mind is the body and the undifferentiated ether is the resort of this deity. It should be meditated upon as bliss. Janaka: What is the nature of bliss? Yājnavalkya: The mind itself, O Emperor, is bliss. With the mind, O Emperor, a man fancies and woos a woman. A son like him is born of that woman and he is the cause of bliss. The moon who is the presiding deity of the mind, O Emperor, is a form of the Supreme Brahman. The mind never deserts him who knows thus and



meditates upon it. All beings eagerly approach him with offerings, etc. He becomes a god in this very life and is merged in the gods after death. Janaka : I offer you a thousand cows with a bull as big as an elephant. Yajnavalkya replied, ' My father held the view that one should not accept presents from a pupil without fully satisfying him.'

 **यदेव ते कश्चिदब्रवीत्तच्छृणवामेत्यब्रवीन्मे विदग्धः शाकल्यो हृदयं वै ब्रह्मेति यथा मातृमान्पितृमानाचार्यवान्ब्रूयात्तथा तच्छाकल्योऽब्रवीद्धृदयं वै ब्रह्मेत्यहृदयस्य हि किꣳ स्यादित्यब्रवीत्तु ते तस्याऽऽयतनं प्रतिष्ठां न मेऽब्रवीदित्येकपाद्वा एतत्सम्राडिति स वै नो ब्रूहि याज्ञवल्क्य हृदयमेवाऽऽयतनमाकाशः प्रतिष्ठा स्थितिरित्येनदुपासीत का स्थितता याज्ञवल्क्य हृदयमेव सम्राडिति होवाच हृदयं वै सम्राट् सर्वेषां भूतानामायतनꣳ हृदयं वै सम्राट् सर्वेषां भूतानां प्रतिष्ठा हृदये ह्येव सम्राट् सर्वाणि भूतानि प्रतिष्ठितानि भवन्ति हृदयं वै सम्राट् परमं ब्रह्म नैनꣳ हृदयं जहाति सर्वाण्येनं भूतान्यभिक्षरन्ति देवो भूत्वा देवानप्येति य एवं विद्वानेतदुपास्ते हस्त्यृषभं सहस्रं ददामीति होवाच जनको वैदेहः स होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः पिता मेऽमन्यत नाननुशिष्य हरेतेति॥७॥ इति प्रथमं ब्राह्मणम्॥१॥**

 (Yajnavalkya said :) शृणवाम Let (me) hear एव indeed तत् that यत् which कश्चित् anyone (of your teachers) अब्रवीत्



have told (taught) ते इति you. विदग्धः Vidagdha शाकल्यः the son of Shakala अब्रवीत् told, taught मे me हृदयम् the heart वै verily (is) ब्रह्म इति Brahman. (Yajnavalkya :) यथा as मातृमान् one having a mother, पितृमान् one having a father, आचार्यवान् one having a teacher ब्रूयात् should tell (teach) तथा so तत् that शाकल्यः son of Shakal अब्रवीत् has told ते you हृदयम् the heart वै verily (is) ब्रह्म इति Brahman. हि Because किम् what (one) स्यात् may be, is the use अहृदयस्य इति of one having no heart ? तु But अब्रवीत् (he) told taught ते you तस्य his आयतनम् abode, body प्रतिष्ठाम् resort, support ? न Not अब्रवीत् (he) told, taught मे इति me. एतत् This (Brahman) वै verily सम्राट् O Emperor एकपात् इति (is) one-footed याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya सः that (you) ब्रूहि tell, teach नः us वै verily हृदयम् the heart एव indeed आयतनम् (is) abode, body आकाशः the (undifferentiated) ether प्रतिष्ठा resort, support. उपासीत Meditate एनत् upon it स्थितिः इति as stability, का what (is) स्थितता the nature of stability याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya उवाच ह (He) said हृदयम् the heart एव indeed सम्राट् O Emperor, हृदयम् the heart वै verily (is) आयतनम् resting place, abode सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings सम्राट् O Emperor हृदयम् the heart वै verily (is) सम्राट् O Emperor प्रतिष्ठा resort, support सर्वेषाम् of all भूतानाम् beings. हि Because हृदये in the heart एव indeed सम्राट् O Emperor सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings भवति are प्रतिष्ठितानि established, dependent. हृदयम् The heart वै verily (is) सम्राट् O Emperor परमम् supreme, highest ब्रह्म Brahman. हृदयम् The heart जहाति does not leave, deserts न not एनम् him. सर्वाणि All भूतानि beings अभिक्षरन्ति eagerly approach एनम् him. भूत्वा Being, becoming देवः a god अप्येति



attains, is merged in देवान् the gods यः who विद्वान् knowing एवम् thus उपास्ते meditates एतत् upon it. जनकः Janaka वैदेहः Emperor of Videha उवाच ह said—ददामि (I) give, offer (you) सहस्रम् a thousand (cows) हस्ति-ऋषभम् इति with a bull as big as an elephant. सः That याज्ञवल्क्यः Yājnavalkya उवाच ह said मे my पिता father अमन्यत thought, held the view हरेत (one) should accept (presents) न not अननुशिष्य इति without fully instructing, satisfying (him).

 Yājnavalkya said: Let me hear whatever anyone else of your teachers may have taught you. Janaka replied: Vidagdha, Shakala's son, has taught me that Prajāpati (Hiranyagarbha) the presiding deity of the heart is Brahman. Yājnavalkya: As one who has a mother, father and teacher to instruct him in life should teach, so has Shakala's son taught you that Prajāpati the deity of the heart is Brahman. Because what is the use of a person who is heartless? But did he teach you about the body and resort of the deity? Janaka: No, he did not. Yājnavalkya: This Brahman has only one foot, O Emperor. Janaka: Then you teach us what you know about it. Yājnavalkya: The heart is the body and the undifferentiated ether is the resort of Prajāpati. It should be meditated upon as stability. Janaka: What is the nature of stability? Yājnavalkya: The heart is indeed, O Emperor, stability. The heart, O Emperor,



is the resting place of all beings. In the heart, O Emperor, all beings depend. Hiranyagarbha who is the presiding deity of the heart, O Emperor, is a form of the highest Brahman. The heart never deserts him who knows thus and meditates upon it. All beings eagerly approach him with offerings. He becomes a god in this very life and is merged in the gods after death. Janaka said : I offer you a thousand cows with a bull as big as an elephant. Yajnavalkya replied : My father held the view that one should not accept presents from a pupil without fully satisfying him.

**CHAPTER FOUR : SECTION TWO**

** जनको ह वैदेहः कूर्चादुपावसर्पन्नुवाच नमस्तेऽस्तु याज्ञवल्क्यानु मा शाधीति स होवाच यथा वै सम्राण्महान्तमध्वानमेष्यन्रथं वा नावं वा समाददीतैवमेवैताभिरुपनिषद्भिः समाहितात्माऽस्येवं वृन्दारक आढ्यः सन्नधीतवेद उक्तोपनिषत्क इतो विमुच्यमानः क्व गमिष्यसीति नाहं तद्भगवन्वेद यत्र गमिष्यामीत्यथ वै तेऽहं तद्वक्ष्यामि यत्र गमिष्यसीति ब्रवीतु भगवानिति॥१॥**

 जनकः Janaka वैदेहः ह Emperor of Videha उपावसर्पन् rising, descending कूर्चात् from lounge, from throne उवाच said याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya ते to you नमः salutation अस्तु be



अनु + शाधि teach, instruct मे इति me. सः He उवाच ह said— यथा as वै verily सम्राट् O Emperor एष्यन् going महान्तम् a long अध्वानम् way, journey समादद्दीत would secure, would provide रथम् a chariot वा or नावम् a boat एवम् so एव indeed एताभिः with these उपनिषद्भिः Upanishads असि (you) are समाहितात्मा (समाहित + आत्मा) fully equipped (prepared) in mind एवम् likewise सन् being वृन्दारकः respected honoured आढ्यः wealthy अधीत-वेदः (you) have learnt the Vedas उक्तोपनिषत्कः (and) told the Upanishads विमुच्यमानः being separated, freed इतः from this (body) क्व where गमिष्यसि इति will (you) go ? भगवन् Venerable Sir अहम् I वेद know न not तत् that यत्र where गमिष्यामि इति (I) will go. अथ Then वै verily अहम् I वक्ष्यामि will tell ते you तत् that यत्र where गमिष्यसि इति (you) will go. भगवान् Venerable Sir ब्रवीतु इति tell me.

 Emperor Janaka of Videha descended from his throne and prostrating at the feet of Yajnavalkya said—" I bow to you, Venerable Sir. Kindly teach me." Yajnavalkya replied—' As one wishing to make a long journey, O Emperor, should provide himself with a chariot or a boat, so have you fully prepared your mind by meditating upon Brahman in many aspects as taught in the Upanishads. You are likewise honoured and wealthy and you have learnt the Vedas and been told the Upanishads by the teachers. But where will you go when you are freed from this body ? Janaka said :



I do not know, Venerable Sir, where I shall go. Yajnavalkya said: Then I will tell you where you will go. Janaka said: Tell me, Venerable Sir, graciously.

 **इन्धो ह वै नामैष योऽयं दक्षिणेऽक्षन्पुरुषस्तं वा एतमिन्धꣳ सन्तमिन्द्र इत्याचक्षते परोक्षेणैव परोक्षप्रिया इव हि देवाः प्रत्यक्षद्विषः॥२॥**

 वै ह Verily एषः He अयम् this पुरुषः being, deity यः who (is) दक्षिणे in the right अक्षन् eye नाम (is) named, called इन्धः Indha. आचक्षते (They) call तं वा him इन्द्रः Indra एव indeed परोक्षेण indirectly एतम् this सन्तम् being, existing इन्धम् Indha हि for देवाः the gods परोक्षप्रियाः (are) fond of indirect names इव as it were प्रत्यक्षद्विषः (and) dislike direct names.

 Yājnavalkya said—This deity who is specially located in the right eye is called Indha as he is resplendent. Though he is obviously called Indha, his indirect name is Indra; for gods are, as it were, fond of indirect names and dislike direct names.

 \[Vishwa (or Vaishwanara), Taijasa and Prajna are the names of the Self as identified with the gross, subtle and causal body respectively in the states of wakefulness, dream and dreamless sleep. The Self called Vaishwanara is described here.—Anandagiri.\]



** अथैतद्वामेऽक्षणि पुरुषरूपमेषाऽस्य पत्नी विराट्तयोरेष सꣳस्तावो य एषोऽन्तर्हृदय आकाशोऽथैनयोरेतदन्नं य एषोऽन्तर्हृदये लोहितपिण्डोऽथैनयोरेतत्प्रावरणं यदेतदन्तर्हृदये जालकमिवाथैनयोरेषा सृतिः सञ्चरणी यैषा हृदयादूर्ध्वा नाड्युच्चरति यथा केशः सहस्रधा भिन्न एवमस्यैता हिता नाम नाड्योऽन्तर्हृदये प्रतिष्ठिता भवन्त्येताभिर्वा एतदास्रवदास्रवति तस्मादेष प्रविविक्ताहारतर इवैव भवत्यस्माच्छारीरादात्मनः॥३॥**

 अथ Now वामे in the left अक्षणि eye एतत् this पुरुषरूपम् shape of person (is) अस्य his पत्नी wife विराट् Viraj (matter). एषः This आकाशः sky, ether एषः that यः which (is) अन्तर्हृदये within the heart तयोः (is) their संस्तावः meeting ground, place of union. अथ Now एनयोः of them both एतत् this अन्नम् food, means of sustenance लोहित-पिण्डः the lump of blood एषः that यः which (is) अन्तर्हृदये within the heart. अथ Now एतयोः of them both एतत् this प्रावरणम् wrap covering एतत् (is) that इव like जालकम् net-work यः which (is) अन्तर्हृदये within the heart. अथ Now एनयोः of the two एषा this सञ्चरणी the passage (is) एषा this नाडी nerve यः which उच्चरति moves, rises ऊर्ध्वा upward हृदयात् from the heart. एवम् (It is) so यथा as केशः a hair भिन्नः split, divided सहस्रधा into thousand parts. अस्य Of this (body) एता these नाड्यः nerves नाम named हिता Hita भवन्ति are प्रतिष्ठिता placed, situated अन्तर्हृदये within the heart. एताभिः Through these एतत् that (essence of food) वै verily आस्रवति passes, flows आस्रवत् moving, flowing. तस्मात् Therefore एषः this (subtle body) भवति is,



lives on प्रविविक्ताहारतरः finer, purer food इव as it were एव indeed अस्मात् than शरीरात् corporal, gross आत्मनः body.

 Now that which is situated in the left eye in the shape of a person is Viraj (matter) who is the wife¹ of Indra (the Self called Vaishwanara). The couple are united in dreams in the space which lies within the lump of flesh called heart. They are sustained by blood² which is in the heart in the form of a lump. Their covering which is like a net-work³ is also in the heart. Their passage from dream to waking is the nerve that rises upward from the heart. This nerve is as fine as the thousandth part of a hair. The extremely fine nerves of this body are situated in the heart.⁴ Through these very fine nerves the essence of food passes in a flow. This gross body has fine food but the subtle body has finer⁵ food than gross body.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Because both matter and its enjoyer, Indra, are objects of enjoyment.

2\. The food that is eaten is changed into gross and subtle forms. The gross form goes down and is excreted. The subtle form again is metabolised into two subtler forms of chyle under the action of the heat that is in the body. One subtle form of the chyle goes into blood and sustains the gross body that is made up of the five elements. The other subtler form of the chyle is a lump of blood that sustains the fine

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

nerves and the subtle body and consequently makes Indra, who is united with the subtle body, to live in the body.

3\. In the heart there are numerous openings of the nerves.

4\. These very fine nerves branch off to all directions like the filaments of a Kadamba flower.

5\. Dvivedanga explains that food when it is eaten is first of all changed into the coarse food which goes away downwards and into subtler food. This subtler food is again divided into the middle juice that feeds the body and the finest which is called the red-lump.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **तस्य प्राची दिक्प्राञ्चः प्राणा दक्षिणा दिग्दक्षिणे प्राणाः प्रतीची दिक्प्रत्यञ्चः प्राणा उदीची दिगुदञ्चः प्राणा ऊर्ध्वा दिगूर्ध्वाः प्राणा अवाची दिगवाञ्चः प्राणाः सर्वा दिशः सर्वे प्राणाः स एष नेति नेत्यात्माऽगृह्यो न हि गृह्यतेऽशीर्यो न हि शीर्यतेऽसङ्गो न हि सज्यतेऽसितो न व्यथते न रिष्यत्यभयं वै जनक प्राप्तोऽसीति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः। स होवाच जनको वैदेहोऽभयं त्वा गच्छताद्याज्ञवल्क्य यो नो भगवन्नभयं वेदयसे नमस्तेऽस्त्विमे विदेहा अयमहमस्मि॥४॥ इति द्वितीयं ब्राह्मणम्॥२॥**

 तस्य Of him (the sage united with the vital power) प्राची the eastern दिक् direction प्राञ्चः (is) the eastern प्राणाः vital power ; दक्षिणा the southern दिक् direction दक्षिणे (is) the southern प्राणाः vital power ; प्रतीची the western दिक् direction प्रत्यञ्चः (is) the western प्राणाः vital power ; उदीची the northern दिक् direction उदञ्चः (is) the northern प्राणाः vital power ऊर्ध्वा



the direction ऊर्ध्वा above, upper ऊर्ध्वाः the upper प्राणाः vital power ; दिक् the direction अवाची below, lower अवाञ्चः (is) the nether प्राणाः vital power सर्वाः all दिशः directions सर्वे all, various प्राणाः vital powers. सः That एषः this आत्मा Self (described as) न इति not this न इति not this ; अग्रह्यः (it is) imperceptible, incomprehensible हि for गृह्यते (it is) comprehended, perceived न not ; अशीर्यः undecaying, हि for शीर्यते (it) decays न not ; असङ्गः Unattached, हि for सज्यते (it) is attached न not ; असितः unfettered, व्यथते (it) is pained, feels) pain न not ; रिष्यति suffers injury न not, याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya उवाच ह said वै verily जनक O Janaka असि (you) are प्राप्तः possessed of, reached अभयम् इति fearlessness. सः That जनकः Janaka वैदेहः Emperor of Videha उवाच ह said भगवन् Venerable Sir! याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya अभयम् fearlessness गच्छतात् may come त्वा to you यः who वेदयसे has made known (accessible) नः to us अभयम् fearlessness नमः salutations अस्तु be ते to you इमे this विदेहाः empire of Videha अयम् this अहम् I अस्मि am (at your feet).

 The sage who has first attained the Vaishwanara, and then Taijasa the Self united with mind becomes one with Prajna whose limiting adjunct is the vital power. Of that sage the eastern direction is the vital power of the east, the southern direction is the vital power of the south, the western direction is the vital power of the west, the northern direction is the vital power of the north, the upper direction is the vital power of the Zenith,



the lower direction is the nether vital power, and all directions are the various vital powers. This Self can be best described negatively. He is incomprehensible, for he cannot be comprehended. He is undecaying, for he cannot decay. He is unattached, for he cannot be attached to anything. He is never pained. He is never injured. You are possessed of fearlessness, O Janaka—said Yajnavalkya. Janaka, Emperor of Videha, said : May that fearlessness come to you who have made accessible to us that fearlessness by removing the root of ignorance created by the limiting adjuncts. Venerable Sir, I salute you, and offer you this empire of Videha and myself at your feet.

**CHAPTER FOUR : SECTION THREE**

** जनकꣳ ह वैदेहं याज्ञवल्क्यो जगाम स मेने न वदिष्य इत्यथ ह यज्जनकश्च वैदेहो याज्ञवल्क्यश्चाग्निहोत्रे समूदाते तस्मै ह याज्ञवल्क्यो वरं ददौ स ह कामप्रश्नमेव वव्रे तꣳ हास्मै ददौ तꣳ ह सम्राडेव पूर्वं पप्रच्छ॥१॥**

 याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya जगाम ह went जनकम् to Janaka वैदेहम् King of Videha. सः He मेने meant, thought इति thus न not वदिष्ये (I) will say (anything). अथ ह Now जनकः Janaka वैदेहः King of Videha च and याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya



यत् when, formerly समूदाते talked अग्निहोत्रे on the Agnihotra याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya ददौ granted, offered तस्मै ह him वरम् a boon. सः ह He (Janaka) वव्रे had begged, had asked काम-प्रश्नम् एव the liberty of asking (any questions) ददौ (Yajnavalkya) gave, granted अस्मै him तं ह that (boon). सम्राट् एव The King पप्रच्छ asked पूर्वम् first तं ह him.

 \[This section is introduced to prove the existence of the Self by removing the doubt raised against It and also to establish the nature of the Self as pure, effulgent, one without a second and identical with Supreme Bliss and Intelligence. The story is here related as an eulogy on the knowledge of Brahman and indicates the way in which this knowledge is imparted by the teacher and received by the student.\]

 Yājnavalkya went to Janaka, King of Videha. He did not mean to ask anything to the king. Now formerly there had been a talk between Janaka and Yājnavalkya on the subject of the Agnihotra sacrifice. On that occasion, Yājnavalkya was pleased with Janaka's knowledge on the subject and offered him a boon. Janaka chose for a boon the liberty of asking him any question he liked, and Yājnavalkya had granted him the boon. On the strength of that boon King Janaka first asked a question to Yājnavalkya.



  **याज्ञवल्क्य किञ्ज्योतिरियं पुरुष इति। आदित्यज्योतिः सम्राडिति होवाचाऽऽदित्येनैवायं ज्योतिषाऽऽस्ते पल्ययते कर्म कुरुते विपल्येतीत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्य॥२॥**

 इति (Janaka asks) thus—याज्ञवल्क्य Yājnavalkya अयम् this पुरुषः man किम्-ज्योतिः (has) what light ? उवाच ह (he) said सम्राट् O King आदित्य-ज्योतिः the light of the sun. एव Indeed ज्योतिषा by this light आदित्येन of the sun अयम् this (man) आस्ते sits, पल्ययते goes out, कुरुते does work, विपल्येति इति (and) returns. याज्ञवल्क्य Yājnavalkya एतत् it (is) एवम् एव just so.

 Janaka asked Yājnavalkya, 'What serves as a light for a man?' Yājnavalkya said to the king that sun-light which is external and extra-corporeal serves as a light for a man. 'It is by the light of the sun that a man sits, goes out to the field or forest, and going there works and returns the way he went.' Janaka said—'It is just so, Yājnavalkya.'

** अस्तमित आदित्ये याज्ञवल्क्य किञ्ज्योतिरेवायं पुरुष इति चन्द्रमा एवास्य ज्योतिर्भवतीति चन्द्रमसैवायं ज्योतिषाऽऽस्ते पल्ययते कर्म कुरुते विपल्येतीत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्य॥३॥**

 इति (Janaka asks) thus—याज्ञवल्क्य Yājnavalkya आदित्ये the sun अस्तमिते having set अयम् this पुरुषः man किम्-ज्योतिः (has) what light ? एव Indeed चन्द्रमा the moon भवति becomes अस्य his ज्योतिः light. एव Indeed ज्योतिषा by the light चन्द्रमसा



of the moon अयम् it आस्ते sits, पल्ययते goes out, कुरुते does कर्म work, विपल्येति इति (and) returns. याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya एतत् it (is) एवम् एव just so.

Janaka again asked Yajnavalkya—' When the sun has set, what serves as the light for a man ?' Yajnavalkya said to the king, ' The moon serves as the light for a man after sunset. It is by the light of the moon that he sits, goes out to the field or forest and going there works and returns home in the same way.' Janaka said—' It is just so, Yajnavalkya.'

** अस्तमित आदित्ये याज्ञवल्क्य चन्द्रमस्यस्तमिते किञ्ज्योतिरेवायं पुरुष इत्यग्निरेवास्य ज्योतिर्भवतीत्यग्निनैवायं ज्योतिषाऽऽस्ते पल्ययते कर्म कुरुते विपल्येतीत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्य॥४॥**

 आदित्ये The sun अस्तमिते having set याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya, चन्द्रमसि the moon अस्तमिते having set अयम् this पुरुषः man किम्-ज्योतिः इति (has) what light ? अग्निः The fire भवति is अस्य his ज्योतिः इति light. अग्निना By the fire एव indeed अयम् this आस्ते sits, पल्ययते goes out, कुरुते does कर्म work, विपल्येति इति (and) returns याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya एतत् it (is) एवम् एव just so.

 Janaka asked : When the sun has set, Yājnavalkya, and the moon has set, what serves as the light for a man ? Yājnavalkya replied that fire



serves as the light for a man after the sun and moon have set. It is by the fire that he sits, goes out, to field or forest and going there works and returns home in the same way. Janaka said—' It is just so, Yājnavalkya.'

** अस्तमित आदित्ये याज्ञवल्क्य चन्द्रमस्यस्तमिते शान्तेऽग्नौ किञ्ज्योतिरेवायं पुरुष इति वागेवास्य ज्योतिर्भवतीति वाचैवायं ज्योतिषाऽऽस्ते पल्ययते कर्म कुरुते विपल्येतीति तस्माद्वै सम्राडपि यत्र स्वः पाणिर्न विनिर्ज्ञायतेऽथ यत्र वागुच्चरत्युपैव तत्र न्येतीत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्य॥५॥**

 आदित्ये The sun अस्तमिते having set याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya, चन्द्रमसि the moon अस्तमिते having set अग्नौ the fire शान्ते having gone out, being extinguished अयम् this पुरुषः man किम्-ज्योतिः इति (has) what as the light ? एव Indeed वाक् speech (sound) भवति is, becomes अस्य his ज्योतिः इति light. एव Indeed ज्योतिषा by the light वाचा of speech (sound) अयम् he आस्ते sits, पल्ययते moves about, कुरुते does कर्म work, विपल्येति इति (and) comes back. तस्मात् Therefore वै verily सम्राट् O Emperor यत्र when अपि even स्वः his own पाणिः hand न not विनिर्ज्ञायते is distinctly known (seen) अथ now यत्र if वाक् sound उच्चरति is uttered उप + न्येति (one) can go, can reach एव indeed तत्र इति there. याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya एतत् it (is) एव indeed एवम् so.

 Janaka asked : When the sun has set, O Yājnavalkya, the moon has gone out and the fire is



extinguished, what acts as the light for a man ? Yājnavalkya replied: It is sound¹ that acts then as the light of man. With the help of sound that acts as the light he sits, moves about and does work and comes back. Therefore, O Emperor, even when (as in the rainy season) all lights are blotted out frequently by the darkness created by the clouds and one’s hand is not distinctly seen, if a sound² is uttered (as for instance, a dog barks or an ass brays) one can reach his destination. Janaka said : It is indeed so, Yājnavalkya.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Sound stimulates the ear, its organ. This produces discrimination in the mind and by that a man is engaged in action. Thus man lives and moves in the world by the help of sound. Thus sound does the function of light and acts as light for man.

2\. As sound helps the ear so odour, etc., also help the nose and other organs.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **अस्तमित आदित्ये याज्ञवल्क्य चन्द्रमस्यस्तमिते शान्तेऽग्नौ शान्तायां वाचि किञ्ज्योतिरेवायं पुरुष इत्यात्मैवास्य ज्योतिर्भवतीत्यात्मनैवायं ज्योतिषाऽऽस्ते पल्ययते कर्म कुरुते विपल्येतीति॥६॥**

 आदित्ये The sun अस्तमिते having set याज्ञवल्क्य O Yajnavalkya, चन्द्रमसि the moon अस्तमिते having set अग्नौ the fire शान्ते having gone out, being extinguished वाचि speech शान्तायाम् having stopped, hushed अयम् this पुरुषः man किम्-



ज्योतिः इति (is) united with what light ? इति (Yajnavalkya said) thus : आत्मा The self एव indeed भवति becomes अस्य his ज्योतिः light. ज्योतिषा By light, by effulgence आत्मना of the self अयम् this (man) आस्ते sits, पल्ययते moves about, कुरुते does कर्म work, विपल्येति इति (and) comes back.

 Janaka asked : ' When the sun has set, O Yājnavalkya, and the moon too has gone out, the fire is extinguished and the speech is hushed, what acts as the light of man ? ' Yājnavalkya replied : The Self indeed acts then as the light of man. Then by the light of the effulgent¹ Self he sits, moves about, does his work and comes back.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. When all external lights are blotted out and all activities of the eyes and other organs with their outgoing tendencies are stopped, it is the immaterial effulgence of the Self that helps a man to do everything. This light is different from all material lights, such as that of the sun, moon the stars, etc. and is not perceived by the eye. That this light is not extinguished in deep sleep is proved by the fact that we awake from deep sleep with the remembrance that we had a happy sleep and were aware of nothing. This light does not belong to the body. Because even a blind man who has had his eyes taken out while dreaming sees things already seen by him and not unseen objects. Similarly in the case of remembrance, a person after closing his eyes remembers the things seen before. That this light is not bodily is proved by the fact that it is absent in a dead body. This light is not mental also. The mind being an object cannot have like the body\]

——————————————————————————————



any light. Therefore, it is concluded that this light must be within the body and belongs to the Self. This light illumines all other objects but is never illumined by anything. It is Self-effulgent and eternal.\]

** कतम आत्मेति योऽयं विज्ञानमयः प्राणेषु हृद्यन्तर्ज्योतिः पुरुषः स समानः सन्नुभौ लोकावनुसञ्चरति ध्यायतीव लेलायतीव स हि स्वप्नो भूत्वेमं लोकमतिक्रामति मृत्यो रूपाणि॥७॥**

 इति (Janaka asks) thus कतमः which (is) आत्मा the self ? (Yājnavalkya replies) अयम् this पुरुषः being, self यः that (is) विज्ञानमयः united with the intellect, full of intellect प्राणेषु (is) amidst the organs, अन्तर्ज्योतिः self-effulgent light हृदि within the heart (intellect) सन् being, assuming समानः the same, the like, the form (of the intellect) अनुसञ्चरति moves, wanders उभौ along the two लोकौ worlds ध्यायति (it) thinks इव as if लेलायति (it) moves इव as if. हि Because सः it भूत्वा being स्वप्नः the dream अतिक्रामति goes beyond इमम् this लोकम् world रूपाणि the forms मृत्योः of death.

 (Unable to decide whether the Self is one of the organs or different) Janaka asks : 'Which is the Self ?' 'This being which is united¹ with the intellect and is surrounded² by the organs (as a rock by the trees) and is the self-effulgent light within the intellect.³ It assumes⁴ the form of the intellect and wanders⁵ along the two worlds, as if their King,⁶ as if moving⁷. Being united⁸ with dreams,



it goes beyond this world and transcends the various forms of death (such as work, ignorance, etc.).

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The Self is perceived as identified with intellect, as the planet Rahu is associated with the sun and the moon. As a lamp is in darkness so is the intellect in the realm of perceptions. It is the intellect that perceives everything and other organs are verily its channels. On account of its transparent nature and proximity to Self it catches the reflection of the effulgent Self easily. Next to intellect is the mind which reflects the light of the Self through the intellect. Next to mind come the organs that catch the light of the Self through contact with the mind, and lastly the body through the instrumentality of organs. Thus the Self successively illumines with its own light the entire aggregate of body and organs. That is why the body and organs appear conscious as a jar placed in the sun reflects sun-light. As an emerald or any other gem dropped (for testing) into milk, etc. imparts its lustre to them, so does this luminous Self being finer than even the intellect imparts its light to the body and organs. But it resides in and is associated with the intellect and is innermost of them all.

2\. The Self is different from the modifications of the intellect and the organs.

3\. As the Self is closely associated with the various functions of both external and internal organs it cannot be easily perceived as distinct from them, like a stalk of grass from its sheath.

4\. The light of the Self being pure assumes the likeness of what it illumines. When it illumines something coloured, it assumes the likeness of that colour.

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

5.The Self leaves the body and organs and takes them anew repeatedly.

6.Assuming the likeness of the intellect the Self seems to think just as light looks coloured through a coloured glass. Hence the people misconceive that the Self thinks. In reality the Self does not think.

7.When wind moves and blows it is the Self that enables it to do so. Then the Self becomes like it and appears to move like it. But in fact the Self has no motion and makes no movement.

8.The Self appears to assume the form of whatever the intellect, which it resembles, becomes. Therefore, when intellect is transformed into a dream, the Self also assumes its form.

9.Death has no forms of its own. The body and organs are its forms. The Self transcends these forms of death on which actions and their results depend.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **स वा अयं पुरुषो जायमानः शरीरमभिसम्पद्यमानः पाप्मभिः सꣳसृज्यते स उत्क्रामन्म्रियमाणः पाप्मनो विजहाति॥८॥**

 वै Verily सः that अयम् this पुरुषः man, individual self जायमानः having been born अभिसम्पद्यमानः attains, becomes identified with शरीरम् a body संसृज्यते is united, is connected पाप्मभिः with the forms of evils (the body and organs). सः He उत्क्रामन् going out, departing म्रियमाणः dies विजहाति discards, leaves पाप्मनः the forms of evil.

 Verily the individual self on birth becomes identified with the body and organs which are the



veritable forms of evil¹. When it dies and departs from the body it leaves behind those forms of evil.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The body and organs being the support of merit and demerit are called the forms of evil.\]

——————————————————————————————

  **तस्य वा एतस्य पुरुषस्य द्वे एव स्थाने भवत इदं च परलोकस्थानं च सन्ध्यं तृतीयꣳ स्वप्नस्थानं तस्मिन्सन्ध्ये स्थाने तिष्ठन्नेते उभे स्थाने पश्यतीदं च परलोकस्थानं च। अथ यथाक्रमोऽयं परलोकस्थाने भवति तमाक्रममाक्रम्योभयान्पाप्मन आनन्दाꣳश्च पश्यति स यत्र प्रस्वपित्यस्य लोकस्य सर्वावतो मात्रामुपादाय स्वयं विहत्य स्वयं निर्माय स्वेन भासा स्वेन ज्योतिषा प्रस्वपित्यत्रायं पुरुषः स्वयं ज्योतिर्भवति॥९॥**

 वै Verily तस्य of that एतस्य this पुरुषस्य person, individual self भवतः are एव indeed द्वे two स्थाने abodes, states इदं च this, present च and परलोक-स्थानम् next world, future life सन्ध्यम् the intermediate तृतीयम् the third स्वप्न-स्थानम् the dream state. तिष्ठन् Staying, Being तस्मिन् at that intermediate state पश्यति (he) sees उभे both एते these स्थाने places, states. इदं च This च and परलोकस्थानम् the next world. अथ Now अयम् he भवति is यथाक्रमः with whatever outfit (work, knowledge etc.) परलोक-स्थाने for the next world आक्रम्य equipping, providing (himself) तम् with that आक्रमम् outfit, support पश्यति (he) sees उभयान् both पाप्मनः evils, sufferings च and आनन्दान् blessings, joys. यत्र When सः he (self) प्रस्वपिति dreams उपादाय taking away, being tinged with मात्राम् a little अस्य of



this सर्वावतः all-embracing, protecting, taking care of everything लोकस्य of world, of life स्वयम् himself विहत्य killing, making inert (the body) स्वयम् himself निर्माय building, creating, (a dream-body) स्वेन by own भासा lustre स्वेन by own ज्योतिषा light प्रस्वपिति (he) dreams. अत्र Here (in this state) अयम् this पुरुषः person (individual) self भवति becomes ज्योतिः the light स्वयम् himself.

 The individual self has only two states, the one here in this world,¹ and the other in the next world.² The dream state which is the third³ is intermediate between the two. Being in that in- termediate state, the dreamer sees the two states of this world and the next.
