Whatever knowledge, work and past experience he may have as support for the attainment of the next world, he equips himself with them that are just ready for this end like a seed about to sprout, and he sees both the sufferings and blessings. When the Self is in the state of dream, he is tinged⁴ with the mass of impressions of this all-embracing world experienced in the waking state. In dream the Self makes this body inert and himself builds up a new body composed of past impressions like one created by magic. That dream body which is a mass of impressions of the waking state is illumined by the light of the Self. This is the state of dreaming.



In this state of dream the individual self becomes self-effulgent⁵ witness and free from the contact of elements and their derivatives.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The present life that consists of the body, organs, objects and impressions which are now perceived by us.

2\. The future life which is experienced after the body, organs, etc. are given up.

3\. Dvivedanga uses a curious argument in support of the existence of another world. He says, in early childhood our dreams consist of the impressions of a former world, later on they are filled with the impressions of this world and in old age they contain visions of a world to come.

4\. Because dream is not entirely a new experience. It is most often memory of the previous experience of the waking state.

5\. In dream the Self becomes distinct from the body and organs like a sword drawn from its sheath. It is then unrelated to anything, yet reveals everything and is realised as it is.\]

——————————————————————————————

** न तत्र रथा न रथयोगा न पन्थानो भवन्त्यथ रथान्रथयोगान्पथः सृजते न तत्राऽऽनन्दा मुदः प्रमुदो भवन्त्यथाऽऽनन्दान्मुदः प्रमुदः सृजते न तत्र वेशान्ताः पुष्करिण्यः स्रवन्त्यो भवन्त्यथ वेशान्तान्पुष्करिणीः स्रवन्तीः सृजते स हि कर्ता॥१०॥**

 तत्र There (in dream) भवन्ति are न not रथाः chariots, न not रथ-योगाः animals, न not पन्थानः roads. अथ But सृजते (the self) creates रथान् chariots, रथ-योगान् animals, पथः roads.



तत्र There भवन्ति are न not आनन्दाः pleasures, kinds of happiness, मुदः joys प्रमुदः delights. अथ But सृजते (the self) creates आनन्दान् pleasures, मुदः joys प्रमुदः delights, magnified joys. तत्र There न not भवन्ति are वेशान्ताः pools, पुष्करिण्यः tanks, स्रवन्त्यः rivers. अथ But सृजते (the self) creates वेशान्तान् pools, पुष्करिणीः tanks, स्रवन्त्यः rivers ; हि because सः he (is) कर्त्ता the creator.

 In dream there are in reality neither objects such as chariots, nor animals (such as horses) yoked to them, nor roads for the chariots, but the Self creates,¹ the chariots, animals and roads. There are no kinds of happiness, no joys (such as those due to the birth of a son, etc.), no magnified joys in dream. But the Self creates the happinesses, joys and magnified joys. There are no pools, no tanks, no rivers in dream. But the Self creates the pools, tanks and rivers in the form of impressions. Because the self is the sole creator² in dream.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. In dream the mental modifications which are nothing but the impressions of the experiences of the

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

apart from those palpable impressions. The constant light of the self, on account of the freedom from the body and organs, is fully isolated in dream like a sword separated from its sheath.

2.The agency of the Self is merely figurative there. His agency simply consists in causing the activity that creates mental modifications representing those impressions. Direct activity is impossible in dream as there are no means of activity such as the organs.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** तदेते श्लोका भवन्ति। स्वप्नेन शारीरमभिप्रहत्यासुप्तः सुप्तानभिचाकशीति। शुक्रमादाय पुनरैति स्थानꣳ हिरण्मयः पुरुष एकह सः॥११॥**

 तत् (Regarding) this एते these, the following श्लोकाः verses, mantras भवन्ति are (there). हिरण्मयः The golden, the radiant पुरुषः Person, being एकहंसः lonely traveller, one mover अभिप्रहत्य putting aside, making inert शारीरम् the body स्वप्नेन in the dream असुप्तः not asleep, awake आदाय taking शुक्रम् pure, shining अभिचाकशीति reveals, watches सुप्तान् sleeping, dormant (impressions) पुनः again एति (he) comes, returns स्थानम् to the place, to the state (of waking).

 On this subject just treated of the following mantras are there: The golden person who is a lonely traveller through waking and dream states, this world and the next, makes the body inert in the dream. Being possessed of constant vision he never falls asleep but remains eternally awake. In



dream he takes pure impressions¹ of the mind that are asleep and reveals them through his constant vision. Again he returns to the state of waking.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Mental modifications of external and internal things that have ceased to exist in their own forms appear as impressions.\]

——————————————————————————————

** प्राणेन रक्षन्नवरं कुलायं बहिष्कुलायादमृतश्चरित्वा। स ईयतेऽमृतो यत्र कामꣳ हिरण्मयः पुरुष एकहꣳ सः॥१२॥**

  हिरण्मयः The golden पुरुषः person, Being एकहंसः lonely traveller अमृतः (and is) immortal रक्षन् preserving, guarding अवरम् worthless, unclean, extremely loathsome कुलायम् nest (the body) प्राणेन by the vital power चरित्वा wandering, roaming बहिः outside, out of कुलायम् the nest, the body अमृतः immortal सः he ईयते goes यत्र wherever कामम् (he) desires.

 The golden person is immortal and a lonely traveller through the waking and dream states. In dream he guards¹ by means of the vital power having a five-fold function, the body that is extremely loathsome as it consists of many filthy things ; but being immortal he wanders² out of it whenever he desires.³

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Otherwise it would be considered dead.

2\. Though he stays in the body in dream he then keeps no connection with it like the ether in the body.

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

3.Whatever things he desires he gets them in the form of impressions.

——————————————————————————————

** स्वप्नान्त उच्चावचमीयमानो रूपाणि देवः कुरुते बहूनि। उतेव स्त्रीभिः सह मोदमानो जक्षदुतेवापि भयानि पश्यन्॥१३॥**

 स्वप्नान्ते In the dream state देवः the shining one, the golden person ईयमानः attaining उच्चावचम् higher (and) lower (states) कुरुते puts forth, assumes बहूनि innumerable, manifold रूपाणि forms, shapes उत एव sometimes मोदमानः rejoicing सह with स्त्रीभिः women उत एव sometimes जक्षत् laughing अपि even पश्यन् seeing भयानि terrible, frightful (sights).

 In dream the golden person attains higher and lower states such as gods and animals, and assumes manifold shapes in the form of impressions. Then he rejoices sometimes with women, laughs sometimes with friends, sometimes even sees terrible sights (such as lions and tigers).

 **आराममस्य पश्यन्ति न तं पश्यति कश्चनेति। तं नाऽऽयतं बोधयेदित्याहुः। दुर्भिषज्यꣳ हास्मै भवति यमेष न प्रतिपद्यते। अथो खल्वाहुर्जागरितदेश एवास्यैष इति यानि ह्येव जाग्रत्पश्यति तानि सुप्त इत्यत्रायं पुरुषः स्वयं ज्योतिर्भवति सोऽहं भगवते सहस्रं ददाम्यत ऊर्ध्वं विमोक्षाय ब्रूहीति॥१४॥**

** ** पश्यन्ति (People) see अस्य his आरामम् play, sport न not कः चन anyone पश्यति sees तम् इति him. आहुः (Physicians



and others) say न not बोधयेत् (one) should rouse, should wake तम् him (a sleeping man) आयतम् suddenly, violently. (If) एषः he (self) न not प्रतिपद्यते gets, finds यम् that (the proper organ) ह indeed भवति (the body) is, becomes दुर्भिषज्यम् difficult to remedy (doctor or treat). अथ However खलु indeed आहुः (others) say, hold इति thus अस्य his एषः this (dream) जागरितदेशः (is) the waking state. हि For पश्यति (one) sees सुप्ते in dream तानि those यानि which (he sees) जाग्रत् इति in the waking. तत्र There (in the dream state) अयम् this पुरुषः man स्वयम् himself भवति is ज्योतिः light (self-luminous). भगवते Venerable Sir, सः that अहम् I ददामि offer, give (you) सहस्रम् a thousand (cows). ब्रूहि Teach, instruct (me) विमोक्षाय about liberation ऊर्ध्वम् beyond अतः this.

 People see the play consisting of the villages, etc. conjured by the Self, but none sees him. Physicians and others say that a sleeping man should not be roused¹ violently. If the Self that is outside the body in dream does not get back to the proper organ through which it went out, the body will find it difficult to treat it.² There are others who hold that the dream state is the same as the waking state ; for one sees in dreams only those objects (such as elephants, etc.) that he sees in the waking. It is not so ; because in dream the organs are at rest.³ In dreams the Self himself undoubtedly becomes luminous. Janaka said to Yajnavalkya : I offer you a thousand cows,



Venerable Sir, I request you to teach me more about liberation.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Because in dreams, the Self leaves the body of the waking state through the gates of the sense-organs and stays outside.

2\. If the Self does not get the right organ to re-enter the body it may misplace their functions. If such a case happens then it may result in blindness, deafness and other serious defects.

3\. One dreams only when organs cease to function.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **स वा एष एतस्मिन्सम्प्रसादे रत्वा चरित्वा दृष्ट्वैव पुण्यं च पापं च। पुनः प्रतिन्यायं प्रतियोन्याद्रवति स्वप्नायैव स यत्तत्र किञ्चित्पश्यत्यनन्वागतस्तेन भवत्यसङ्गो ह्ययं पुरुष इत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्य सोऽहं भगवते सहस्रं ददाम्यत ऊर्ध्वं विमोक्षायैव ब्रूहीति॥१५॥**

 सः That एषः this (self) वै verily रत्वा enjoying (himself), चरित्वा roaming, sporting एव merely दृष्ट्वा seeing (results of) पुण्यम् good च and पापम् evil (stays) एतस्मिन् in this सम्प्रसादे highest serenity, profound sleep पुनः again आद्रवति hastens back retraces its steps प्रतियोनि in the inverse way प्रतिन्यायम् as he went एव indeed स्वप्नाय for the dream state. तत्र There यत्किञ्चित् whatever सः he (self) पश्यति sees, witnesses तेन by that भवति is अनन्वागतः not followed, unaffected. हि For अयम् this पुरुषः Self, Being असङ्गः इति (is) untouched, याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya. एतत् It (is) एव indeed एवम् so. भगवते



Venerable Sir. सः that अहम् I ददामि offer, give (you) सहस्रम् a thousand (cows) ; ब्रूहि teach (me) एव indeed विमोक्षाय about liberation ऊर्ध्वम् इति beyond अतः this.

 The Self in dream enjoys himself by having a sight of his friends, etc. and sports in various ways and experiences fatigue due to it and merely sees, but does not enjoy pleasure and pain, the results of good and evil actions. Then he goes to profound sleep where he gets profound serenity.¹ From sleep he retraces his steps to his previous state—the dream—in the same way as he went. In dream the Self is unaffected by pleasure and pain. There he simply witnesses them but never enjoys them. Because the Self is by nature untouched.² Janaka said to Yājñavalkya : It is indeed so, Venerable Sir. I offer you a thousand cows for what you taught me. Please teach me more about liberation itself.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. In the waking state the Self owing to its contact with impurities due to innumerable activities of the body and organs does not get purity and peace. He discards them in dreams and gets a little joy there. But in deep sleep he gets the highest serenity. Activity is not the nature of Self, because activity is absent from him in dreams and profound sleep. In waking state activity is superimposed on the Self and so he has no peace.

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

2.If the Self actually does anything in dreams, he would be bound by it, and it would follow him even in the waking. But it never happens so in everyday life. It is a well known fact that a man is not followed by deeds done in dreams. No body considers himself a sinner on account of the sins committed in dreams ; nor do people who have heard of them condemn or shun him. Hence the Self only appears to be doing things in dreams, but actually there he has no activity. An action is caused by the contact of body and organs, which have some shape, with something else which also must have shape. A formless thing is never seen to be active. The Self being formless can have no activity.

——————————————————————————————

 **स वा एष एतस्मिन्स्वप्ने रत्वा चरित्वा दृष्ट्वैव पुण्यं च पापं च पुनः प्रतिन्यायं प्रतियोन्याद्रवति बुद्धान्तायैव स यत्तत्र किञ्चित्पश्यत्यनन्वागतस्तेन भवत्यसङ्गो ह्ययं पुरुष इत्येवमेवैतद्याज्ञवल्क्य सोऽहं भगवते सहस्रं ददाम्यत ऊर्ध्वं विमोक्षायैव ब्रूहीति॥१६॥**

 सः That एषः this (self) वै verily एतस्मिन् in this स्वप्ने dream रत्वा enjoying चरित्वा moving about, roaming एव merely दृष्ट्वा seeing, witnessing पुण्यं च the good च and पापम् bad (results) आद्रवति hastens back, returns पुनः again प्रतिन्यायं as he came प्रतियोनि in the inverse way एव indeed बुद्धान्ताय to the waking. सः He भवति is अनन्वागतः not followed, not affected तेन by that यत्किञ्चित् whatever पश्यति (he) sees तत्र there. हि Because अयम् this पुरुषः person, Being असङ्गः इति (is) untouched. (Janaka said) याज्ञवल्क्य Yajnavalkya एतत्



It (is) एव indeed एवम् just so. सः That अहम् I भगवते Venerable Sir ददामि give (you) सहस्रम् a thousand (cows). ऊर्ध्वम् Beyond अतः this ब्रूहि speak on विमोक्षाय about liberation एव alone.

 Yājnavalkya said: That being enjoys himself, moves about and merely witnesses the results of his good and bad actions and then returns in the inverse way to his previous state—that of waking. He is not affected by whatever he sees in dream. Because this being is by nature unattached. Janaka said: It is indeed so, Yājnavalkya. I give you a thousand cows, Venerable Sir. Kindly speak on more about liberation alone.

 **स वा एष एतस्मिन्बुद्धान्ते रत्वा चरित्वा दृष्ट्वैव पुण्यं च पापं च पुनः प्रतिन्यायं प्रतियोन्याद्रवति स्वप्नान्तायैव ॥१७॥**

 सः That वै verily एषः this (self) एतस्मिन् in this बुद्धान्ते waking state रत्वा enjoying चरित्वा wandering, roaming एव merely दृष्ट्वा seeing पुण्यं च merits च and पापम् demerits आद्रवति hastens back पुनः again प्रतिन्यायम् as he came प्रतियोनि in the inverse way स्वप्नान्ताय to the state of dreamless sleep एव only.

 Yājnavalkya said: He enjoys himself and wanders in the state of waking, merely seeing the merits and demerits, but does not¹ do them actually



on account of his nonattached nature, and hastens back in the inverse way as he came to his previous state of dreamless sleep.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. He is not pursued by the good and bad results of the waking state as he is distinct from the attributes of the three states. These relative attributes do not belong to it per se and are superimposed by the limiting adjuncts due to ignorance. Agency which really belong to the body and organs is figuratively attributed to Self. Desire and work are attributes of non-Self, never of Self.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **तद्यथा महामत्स्य उभे कूले अनुसञ्चरति पूर्वं चापरं चैवमेवायं पुरुष एतावुभावन्तावनुसञ्चरति स्वप्नान्तं च बुद्धान्तं च॥१८॥**

 तत् That यथा just as महामत्स्यः a large fish अनुसञ्चरति swims उभे to both कूले the banks पूर्वं च eastern right च and अपरम् western the left एवम् एव so अयम् this पुरुषः (infinite) Being, Self अनुसञ्चरति moves about एतौ these उभौ two अन्तौ states स्वप्नान्तं च the dream state बुद्धान्तं च and the waking state.

 \[The idea set forth in the above passage is illustrated in the following passage.\]

 As a large fish swims freely to both the right and left banks of a river, is never swayed by the intervening currents of water but rather stem them,



so the Self moves about in these states of dream and waking.

** तद्यथाऽस्मिन्नाकाशे श्येनो वा सुपर्णो वा विपरिपत्य श्रान्तः सꣳ हत्य पक्षौ संलयायैव ध्रियत एवमेवायं पुरुष एतस्मा अन्ताय धावति यत्र सुप्तो न कञ्चन कामं कामयते न कञ्चन स्वप्नं पश्यति॥१९॥**

 तत् That (the example is) यथा just as श्येनः वा a hawk वा or सुपर्णः a falcon, swifter kind of hawk विपरिपत्य flying अस्मिन् in this (external) आकाशे sky श्रान्तः (becomes) tired, (is) exhausted संहत्य stretching पक्षौ the wings एव indeed ध्रियते is bound, directs itself towards संलयाय for nest, for abode of perfect rest एवम् एव so अयम् this पुरुषः being, individual self धावति runs, hastens एतस्मै for this अन्ताय (sleep) state यत्र where सुप्तः (being) asleep न not कामयते desires, craves कञ्चन any कामम् desire पश्यति sees, dreams न not कञ्चन any स्वप्नम् dream.

 As a hawk or a falcon roaming in the external sky, is fatigued and stretching its wings directs itself towards its abode of perfect rest, so does the individual Self in order to remove his fatigue¹ hastens to the state of sleep² where he falls asleep and desires no more desires and dreams no more dreams.³

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Fatigue is due to exertion caused by his actions with their factors and results.

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

2.In deep sleep the individual Self distinct from all relative attributes and devoid of all exertions of actions is united with Supreme Self.

3.Waking experiences are considered by the Upanishad to be mere dreams. As Aitareya Upanishad (3. 12) says—The individual Self has three abodes—the three states which are all dream.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** ता वा अस्यैता हिता नाम नाड्यो यथा केशः सहस्रधा भिन्नस्तावताऽणिम्ना तिष्ठन्ति शुक्लस्य नीलस्य पिङ्गलस्य हरितस्य लोहितस्य पूर्णा अथ यत्रैनं घ्नन्तीव जिनन्तीव हस्तीव विच्छाययति गर्तमिव पतति यदेव जाग्रद्भयं पश्यति तदत्राविद्यया मन्यतेऽथ यत्र देव इव राजेवाहमेवेदꣳ सर्वोऽस्मीति मन्यते सोऽस्य परमो लोकः॥२०॥**

 अस्य Of him (dreamer) ताः those एताः these वै verily तिष्ठन्ति are नाड्यः nerves, veins नाम named हिताः Hita तथा so अणिम्ना fine यथा as केशः a hair भिन्नः split, divided सहस्रधा into a thousand parts पूर्णा full शुक्लस्य of white नीलस्य of blue पिङ्गलस्य of brown हरितस्य of green लोहितस्य of red (serums). अथ Now यत्र when (in dream) एनम् him (dreamer) घ्नन्ति (they) are killing इव as if जिनन्ति are overpowering इव as if हस्ती an elephant विच्छादयति is chasing, is pursuing इव as if पतति (he) is falling इव as if गर्तम् in a pit, in a well जाग्रत् in the waking यत् whatever भयम् fear, objects of fear एव indeed पश्यति (one) sees. मन्यते (one) conjures तत्र there अविद्यया by ignorance. अथ And यत्र when (in dream) देवः a God इव as it were राजा a King इव as it were मन्यते



(or) thinks, imagines इति thus इदम् this (Universe) अहम् (is) myself एव verily अस्मि (I) am सर्वः all सः that (the identity with all) अस्य (is) his परमः highest लोकः world, state.

 There are in the body of the dreamer those nerves named Hita,¹ which are so fine as the thousandth part of a hair. Those nerves are full of white, blue, brown, green and red² serums. (They are the seat of the subtle³ body, the store-house of past impressions.) Now in dream one conjures as if he were being killed or over-powered by enemies, or he is being chased by an elephant,⁴ or he is falling into a well, in short, fancies through the past impressions created by ignorance those objects of fear he has experienced in the waking. And in dream one considers himself a god,⁵ or a king as it were. But when ignorance is extremely attenuated he realises that he is this Universe and comprises all. That identity with all is his highest state.⁶

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. These nerves are referred to in 2. 1. 19 and 4. 2. 3.

2\. Sankar says that the colours of the serum are many and various due to the inter-mixture of wind, file and phlegm in various proportions. Anandagiri observes that excess of wind turns the serum (neel), excess of file (pingal), excess of phlegm white (Shukla), scarcity of biles (Harit), and

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

equality of elements (lohita). Anandagiri then quotes a verse of Sushruta (an authority on Ayurveda) which means: (Aruna) veins carry wind, (neela) veins carry bile, (rohini) veins carry blood and the white (gouri) ones carry phlegm. Dvivedanga explains that if phlegm predominates qualified by wind and bile, the juice in the veins is white ; if wind predominates qualified by phlegm and bile, it is blue ; if bile predominates qualified by wind and phlegm, it is yellow ; if wind and phlegm predominate with little bile only, it is green ; and if the three elements are equal, it is red.

3.The subtle body, which has its seat in the nerves is extremely fine and is transparent like a crystal. But on account of its contact with the serums in the nerves, it becomes modified under the influence of past merit and demerit and manifests itself as impressions which take the form of women, chariots or elephants, etc. in dream.

4.These objects are not really there. They are the manifested images of past impressions.

5.On account of impressions generated by meditation on the gods prevailing in waking. Now ignorance decreases and knowledge increases.

6.This is the state of liberation in which ignorance is totally eliminated and knowledge reaches its perfection. When one views the Universe as other than himself even by a hair's breadth, one is in ignorance and not in perfect knowledge.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **तद्वा अस्यैतदतिच्छन्दा अपहतपाप्माभयꣳ रूपम्। तद्यथा प्रियया स्त्रिया सम्परिष्वक्तो न बाह्यं किञ्चन वेद नाऽऽन्तरमेवमेवायं पुरुषः प्राज्ञेनाऽऽत्मना सम्परिष्वक्तो न बाह्यं किञ्चन वेद**



**नाऽऽन्तरं तद्वा अस्यैतदाप्तकाममात्मकाममकामꣳ रूपं शोकान्तरम्॥२१॥**

 तत् That (the identity) एतत् this (is) वै verily अस्य his रूपम् form, state अतिच्छन्दा (= अतिच्छन्दम्) free from desires अपहतपाप्मा free from evils (merits and demerits) अभयम् fearlessness. तत् That यथा as (a man) सम्परिष्वक्तः fully embraced, united प्रियया by the dear स्त्रिया wife वेद knows न not किञ्चन anything बाह्यम् external न not आन्तरम् internal एवम् एव so अयम् this पुरुषः Self सम्परिष्वक्तः fully embraced, united प्राज्ञेन by the supreme आत्मना self वेद knows न not किञ्चन anything बाह्यम् outside external न nor आन्तरम् internal, within. तत् That (is) वै verily अस्य his रूपम् form, state आप्तकामम् satisfied of desires, with desires fulfilled आत्मकामम् with the desire of self, अकामम् desireless शोकान्तरम् devoid of grief.

 \[This passage directly points out the liberation which consists in identity with all and is beyond desires and grief.\]

 This identity with all is the highest state of Self. This state is devoid of merits and demerits and is free from all desire and fear. As a man fully united by his dear wife, knows nothing external or internal, so this individual¹ Self fully unified with the Supreme Self knows nothing outside or within himself. That is his highest state in which all desires² are fulfilled and only the desire of the



Self remains. This state is beyond desires. It is also beyond grief.³

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The separation of the individual Self from the Supreme Self is like the reflection of the moon in water from the real moon.

2\. Because the desire of Self comprises all desires.

3\. In waking and dream objects are, as it were, separated from the Self. So they are desired as such. But in deep sleep ignorance being undifferentiated cannot project the idea of difference.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **अत्र पिताऽपिता भवति माताऽमाता लोका अलोका देवा अदेवा वेदा अवेदाः। अत्र स्तेनोऽस्तेनो भवति भ्रूणहाऽभ्रूणहा चाण्डालोऽचाण्डालः पौल्कसोऽपौल्कसः श्रमणोऽश्रमणस्तापसोऽतापसोऽनन्वागतं पुण्येनानन्वागतं पापेन तीर्णो हि तदा सर्वाञ्छोकान्हृदयस्य भवति॥२२॥**

 अत्र Here, in this (state) पिता a father भवति is अपिता no father, माता a mother (is) अमाता no mother, लोकाः the worlds (are) अलोकाः no worlds, देवाः the gods अदेवाः (are) no gods, वेदाः the Vedas (are) अवेदाः no Vedas. अत्र Here, in this (state) स्तेनः a thief भवति is अस्तेनः no thief, भ्रूणहा a murderer (is) अभ्रूणहा no murderer, चाण्डालः (= चण्डालः) a chandāl (is) अचाण्डालः no Chandāl, पौल्कसः (= पुल्कसः) a Pulkasa (is) अपौल्कसः no Pulkasa, श्रमणः a monk (is) अश्रमणः no monk, तापसः a recluse, a hermit (is) अतापसः no hermit, अनन्वागतम् untouched, unaffected पुण्येन by good



action, अनन्वागतम् untouched, not followed पापेन by bad action : हि for तदा then भवति (Self) is तीर्णः beyond सर्वान् all शोकान् grief हृदयस्य of heart.

 \[The text asserts that though desire, grief and fear do not exist in deep sleep the eternal effulgence of the Self is certainly present then.\]

 Since in profound sleep, the Self attains a state that is free from desire and fear, merit and demerit, therefore in that state, a father is not¹ a father, a mother is not a mother, the worlds² are not worlds,³ the gods⁴ are not gods, the Vedas are not⁵ Vedas. In deep sleep, a thief is not a thief, a murderer is not a murderer, a chandāla⁶ is not a chandala, a Pulkasa⁷ is not a Pulkasa, a monk is not a monk, a recluse is not a recluse. The Self in that state is neither unaffected by good or bad actions done in this or previous life; because the Self is then free from the woes⁸ abiding in the heart.⁹

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Fatherhood, motherhood, sonhood, etc. are relations based on actions from which the Self is dissociated in deep sleep. Therefore in that state these relations cease to exist.

2\. Which are attained or to be attained by sacrifices.

3\. Owing to dissociation from the rites the worlds cease to exist.

4\. Gods are a part of the rites.

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

5.Because the Vedas that form part of the rites are then transcended.

6.One born of a Shudra father and a Brāhman mother.

7.One born of a Shudra father and a Khatriya mother.

8.Desires for wished-for objects are turned into woes in the absence of those objects.

9.The lotus-shaped lump of flesh which is the seat of the internal organ—intellect.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **यद्वै तन्न पश्यति पश्यन्वै तन्न पश्यति नहि द्रष्टुर्दृष्टेर्विपरिलोपो विद्यतेऽविनाशित्वात्। न तु तद्द्वितीयमस्ति ततोऽन्यद्विभक्तं यत्पश्येत्॥२३॥**

 वै Verily तत् it (Self) न not पश्यति sees यत् because वै although पश्यन् seeing तत् it न not पश्यति sees हि for विपरिलोपः loss दृष्टेः of sight, of vision द्रष्टुः of the seer न not विद्यते takes place, happens अविनाशित्वात् due to imperishability. तु But अस्ति there is न not तद् that द्वितीयम् second अन्यत् other (object) विभक्तम् different, separate ततः from it यत् which पश्येत् (it) can see, can perceive.

 The Self verily does not see in the state of profound sleep. The sight of the seer is imperishable and its loss never takes place.¹ Though the Self retains its sight in deep sleep, it cannot see with eye. Then the eyes and their forms being unified there is no second² object (different from Self) that it can see (perceive).



——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. As the fire never loses its character of burning, and the sun its nature of shining, so the Seer, the eternal Self, does not lose its power of sight in deep sleep as in waking and dream.

2.In profound sleep the individual Self is embraced by the Supreme Self, and so the organs and their objects are unified in the unmanifested ignorance which still persists then.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **यद्वै तन्न जिघ्रति जिघ्रन्वै तन्न जिघ्रति न हि घ्रातुर्घ्रातेर्विपरिलोपो विद्यतेऽविनाशितवान्न तु तद्द्वितीयमस्ति ततोऽन्यद्विभक्तं यज्जिघ्रेत्॥२४॥**

 वै Verily तत् it (Self) न not जिघ्रति smells यत् because वै although जिघ्रन् smelling तत् it न not जिघ्रति smells ; हि for विपरिलोपः loss, absence घ्रातेः power of smelling घ्रातुः of the smeller न not विद्यते takes place अविनाशित्वात् due to its imperishability. तु But तत् that द्वितीयम् second अन्यत् other (object) विभक्तम् different, separate ततः from it यत् which जिघ्रत् (it) can smell.

 The Self verily does not smell in the state of profound sleep. The smelling power of the smeller is imperishable and its loss never happens. Though the smelling power is still there, the Self cannot smell through the nose. The nose and smelling are unified in unmanifested ignorance, there is no second object (different from the Self) which it can smell.



** यद्वै तन्न रसयते रसयन्वै तन्न रसयते न हि रसयितू रसयतेर्विपरिलोपो विद्यतेऽविनाशित्वान्न तु तद्द्वितीयमस्ति ततोऽन्यद्विभक्तं यद्रसयेत्॥२५॥**

 वै Verily तत् it (self) न not रसयते tastes यत् because वै although रसयन् tasting तत् it न not रसयते tastes हि for विपरिलोपः loss, absence रसयतेः power of tasting रसयितुः of the taster न not विद्यते happens अविनाशित्वात् due to immortality. तु But अस्ति there is न not तत् that द्वितीयम् second अन्यत् other (object) विभक्तम् separate, different ततः from it यत् which रसयेत् (It) can taste.

 Verily the Self does not taste in the state of profound sleep. The tasting power of the taster is imperishable and its loss never takes place. Though the tasting power then exists, the Self cannot taste then through the tongue. Tongue and its object being unified then in unmanifested ignorance, there is no second object (different from Self) which It can taste.

 **यद्वै तन्न वदति वदन्वै तन्न वदति न हि वक्तुर्वक्तेर्विपरिलोपो विद्यतेऽविनाशित्वान्न तु तद्द्वितीयमस्ति ततोऽन्यद्विभक्तं यद्वदेत्॥२६॥**

 वै Verily तत् It (Self) न not वदति speaks यत् because वै although वदन् speaking तत् It न not वदति speaks ; हि for



विपरिलोपः loss वक्तेः power of speech वक्तुः of the speaker न never विद्यते takes place अविनाशित्वात् due to imperishability. तु But अस्ति there is न not तत् that द्वितीयम् second अन्यत् other (object) विभक्तम् different, separate ततः from it यत् which वदेत् (it) can speak.

 Verily the Self does not speak in the state of profound sleep. The speaking power of the speaker is imperishable and its loss never happens. Though the speaking power then exists, the Self cannot speak through the vocal organ. The vocal organ and the object of speech being then unified in unmanifested ignorance, there is not that second object which It can speak.

 **यद्वै तन्न शृणोति शृण्वन्वै तन्न शृणोति न हि श्रोतुः श्रुतेर्विपरिलोपो विद्यतेऽविनाशित्वान्न तु तद्द्वितीयमस्ति ततोऽन्यद्विभक्तं यच्छृणुयात्॥२७॥**

 वै Verily तत् It (Self) न not शृणोति hears यत् because वै although शृण्वन् hearing तत् It न not शृणोति hears ; हि for विपरिलोपः loss, absence श्रुतेः of the hearing power श्रोतुः of the listener, of the hearer न not विद्यते takes place अविनाशित्वात् due to imperishability. तु But न not अस्ति there is तत् that द्वितीयम् second अन्यत् other (object) विभक्तम् different, separate ततः from It यत् which शृणुयात् (It) can hear.

 Verily the Self does not hear in the state of profound sleep. The hearing power of the hearer



is imperishable and its loss never happens. Though the hearing power then exists the Self cannot hear through the ear. Ear and its object being then unified in unmanifested ignorance, there is no second object (different from the Self) that It can hear.

 **यद्वै तन्न मनुते मन्वानो वै तन्न मनुते न हि मन्तुर्मतेर्विपरिलोपो विद्यतेऽविनाशित्वान्न तु तद्द्वितीयमस्ति ततोऽन्यद्विभक्तं यन्मन्वीत॥२८॥**

 वै Verily तत् It (Self) न not मनुते thinks यत् because वै although मन्वानः thinking तत् It मनुते thinks न not. हि For विपरिलोपः absence, loss मतेः of thinking power मन्तुः of the thinker विद्यते happens न not अविनाशित्वात् due to imperishability. तु But अस्ति there is न not तत् that द्वितीयम् second अन्यत् other (object) विभक्तम् separate, different ततः from it यत् which मन्वीत (it) can think.

 Verily the Self does not think in the state of profound sleep. The thinking power of the thinker is imperishable and its loss never happens. Though the thinking power exists then, the Self cannot think through the mind. Mind and thoughts being then unified in original ignorance, there is no second object different from Self that It can think.



** यद्वै तन्न स्पृशति स्पृशन्वै तन्न स्पृशति न हि स्प्रष्टुः स्पृष्टेर्विपरिलोपो विद्यतेऽविनाशित्वान्न तु तद्द्वितीयमस्ति ततोऽन्यद्विभक्तं यत्स्पृशेत्॥२९॥**

 वै Verily तत् It (Self) स्पृशति touches न not यत् because वै although स्पृशन् touching तत् It स्पृशति touches न not. हि For विपरिलोपः loss स्पृष्टेः of touching power स्प्रष्टुः of the toucher विद्यते happens न not अविनाशित्वात् due to imperishability. तु But अस्ति there is न not तद् कियत् that द्वितीयम् second अन्यत् other (object) विभक्तम् separate, different ततः from It यत् which स्पृशेत् (It) can touch.

 Verily the Self does not touch in the state of profound sleep. The touching power of the toucher is imperishable and its loss never happens. Though the touching power exists then, the Self cannot touch through the skin. Skin and its object being then unified in original ignorance there is no second object different from the Self that It can touch.

** यद्वै तन्न विजानाति विजानन्वै तन्न विजानाति न हि विज्ञातुर्विज्ञातेर्विपरिलोपो विद्यतेऽविनाशित्वान्न तु तद्द्वितीयमस्ति ततोऽन्यद्विभक्तं यद्विजानीयात्॥३०॥**

 वै Verily तत् It (Self) विजानाति knows न not यत् because वै although विजानन् knowing तत् It विजानाति knows न not.



हि For विपरिलोपः loss, absence विज्ञातेः of the knowing power विज्ञातुः of the knower न not विद्यते takes place अविनाशित्वात् due to imperishability. तु But अस्ति there is न not तत् that द्वितीयम् second अन्यत् other (object) विभक्तम् separate, different ततः from It यत् which विजानीयात् (It) can know.

 Verily the Self does not know in the state of profound sleep. The knowing power of the knower is imperishable and its loss never happens. Though the knowing power exists then, the Self cannot know through the mind. Mind and its thoughts being then unified in original ignorance there is no second object different from the Self that It can know.

** यत्र वा अन्यदिव स्यात्तत्रान्योऽन्यत्पश्येदन्योऽन्यज्जिघ्रेदन्योऽन्यद्रसयेदन्योऽन्यद्वदेदन्योऽन्यच्छृणुयादन्योऽन्यन्मन्वीतान्योऽन्यत्स्पृशेदन्योऽन्यद्विजानीयात्॥३१॥**

 यत्र When (in waking or dream) वै verily स्यात् there is अन्यत् another, something else, a second thing इव as it were ; अन्यः one पश्येत् can see अन्यत् the other, something ; अन्यः one जिघ्रेत् can smell अन्यत् the other, something ; अन्यः one रसयेत् can smell अन्यत् the other, something ; अन्यः one वदेत् can say अन्यत् the other, something ; अन्यः one शृणुयात् can hear अन्यत् the other, something ; अन्यः one मन्वीत can think अन्यत् the other, something ; अन्यः one स्पृशेत् can touch अन्यत् the other, something ; अन्यः one विजानीयात् can know अन्यत् something, the other.



As in the waking or dream ¹ there is a second thing differentiated from the Self, as it were, presented by ignorance, so then one thinking of one's Self different from that thing can see the other, can smell the other, can taste the other, can tell the other, can hear the other, can think the other, can touch the other and can know the other.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. In profound sleep there is nothing different from the Self so the Self then knows no particulars. But undifferentiated ignorance does persist in deep sleep.\]

——————————————————————————————

** सलिल एको द्रष्टाऽद्वैतो भवत्येष ब्रह्मलोकः सम्राडिति हैनमनुशशास याज्ञवल्क्य एषाऽस्य परमा गतिरेषाऽस्य परमा सम्पदेषोऽस्य परमो लोक एषोऽस्य परम आनन्द एतस्यैवाऽऽनन्दस्यान्यानि भूतानि मात्रामुपजीवन्ति॥३२॥**

 सलिलः (As) water, ocean एकः one (so) द्रष्टा the seer, self अद्वैतः one without a second. एषः This (is) ब्रह्मलोकः the world (state) of Brahman सम्राड् इति O Emperor. याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya अनुशशास instructed, taught एनं ह him (Janaka). एषा This (is) अस्य its (of the individual self) परमा supreme, highest गतिः goal, attainment. एषा This (is) अस्य its परमा highest, supreme सम्पत् success, splendour. एषः This (is) अस्य its परमः supreme, highest लोकः world. एषः This (is) अस्य its परमः supreme आनन्दः bliss. अन्यानि Other भूतानि beings उपजीवन्ति live मात्राम् on a fraction, on a particle एव indeed एतस्य of this आनन्दस्य bliss.



 In profound sleep the Self becomes free from all limiting adjuncts and relations and remains like the ocean, one¹ without a second. This is the world that is Brahman, O Emperor. Thus did Yājnavalkya teach Janaka : of the individual Self this is the highest goal, the highest splendour,² the highest world,³ the highest bliss.⁴ Indeed all other beings from Hiranyagarbha down to men live on fraction⁵ of this supreme bliss.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Because ignorance that creates multiplicity and thereby presents things other than the Self is then at rest. Therefore there is no second entity different from the Self to be seen.

2\. Because this is natural and others are artificial.

3\. Because other worlds are the result of past work and are impermanent. But this world is permanent and not attainable by action.

4\. Because sense-pleasure is momentary and this bliss is everlasting.

5\. Put forward by ignorance and perceived only during the contact of the senses with their respective objects.

——————————————————————————————

 **स यो मनुष्याणाꣳ राद्धः समृद्धो भवत्यन्येषामधिपतिः सर्वैर्मानुष्यकैर्भोगैः सम्पन्नतमः स मनुष्याणां परम आनन्दोऽथ ये शतं मनुष्याणामानन्दाः स एकः पितृणां जितलोकानामानन्दोऽथ ये शतं पितृणां जितलोकानामानन्दाः स एको गन्धर्वलोक आनन्दोऽथ ये शतं गन्धर्वलोक आनन्दाः स एकः कर्मदेवानामा-**



**नन्दो ये कर्मणा देवत्वमभिसम्पद्यन्तेऽथ ये शतं कर्मदेवानामानन्दाः स एक आजानदेवानामानन्दो यश्च श्रोत्रियोऽवृजिनोऽकामहतोऽथ ये शतमाजानदेवानामानन्दाः स एकः प्रजापतिलोक आनन्दो यश्च श्रोत्रियोऽवृजिनोऽकामहतोऽथ ये शतं प्रजापतिलोक आनन्दाः स एको ब्रह्मलोक आनन्दो यश्च श्रोत्रियोऽवृजिनोऽकामहतोऽथैष एव परम आनन्द एष ब्रह्मलोकः सम्राडिति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः सोऽहं भगवते सहस्रं ददाम्यत ऊर्ध्वं विमोक्षायैव ब्रूहीत्यत्र ह याज्ञवल्क्यो विभयाञ्चकार मेधावी राजा सर्वेभ्यो माऽन्तेभ्य उदरौत्सीदिति॥३३॥**

 सः He यः who भवति is राद्धः perfect of body, having no physical defects समृद्धः prosperous, provided with luxuries, मनुष्याणाम् of men अधिपतिः ruler, lord अन्येषाम् of others सम्पन्नतमः surrounded सर्वैः with all मानुष्यकैः human भोगैः enjoyments सः he (is) परमः highest, supreme आनन्दः joy मनुष्याणाम् of men. अथ Now सः that ये which (are) शतम् a hundred times आनन्दाः the joys मनुष्याणाम् of men एकः one (measure) आनन्दः of joy पितृणाम् of the Manes जितलोकानाम् who have conquered the world (of theirs). अथ Now सः that ये which (are) शतम् a hundred-fold आनन्दाः the joys पितृणाम् of the Manes जितलोकानाम् who have conquered the world (of theirs) एकः one (measure) आनन्दः of joy गन्धर्वलोकः of the world of the celestial minstrels. अथ Now सः that ये which (are) शतम् a hundred-fold आनन्दाः the joys गन्धर्वलोकः of the



world of the celestial minstrels (is) एकः one (measure) आनन्दः of joy कर्मदेवानाम् of the gods by actions ये who अभिसम्पद्यन्ते attain देवत्वम् godhood कर्मणा by action : अथ Now सः that ये which (is) शतम् a hundred times आनन्दा the joys कर्मदेवाणाम् of the gods by action (is) एकः one measure आनन्दः of joy आजानदेवाणाम् of the gods by birth च and यः (of one) who (is) श्रोत्रियः well-up in the vedas अवृजिनः sinless अकामहतः not overcome by desires. अथ Now सः that ये which (is) शतम् a hundred times आनन्दाः the joys आजानदेवाणाम् of the gods by birth एकः (is) one measure आनन्दः of joy प्रजापतिलोकः in the world of Prajāpati (Viraj) च and यः (of one) who (is) श्रोत्रियः well-up in the Vedas अवृजिनः sinless अकामहतः free from desires. अथ Now सः that ये which शतम् hundred times आनन्दाः the joys प्रजापतिलोकः of the world of Prajāpati एकः (is) one measure आनन्दाः of joy ब्रह्मलोकः of the world of Brahman (Hiranyagarbha) ; च as well as यः (of one) who (is) श्रोत्रियः well-up in the Shrutis (Vedas) अवृजिनः sinless अकामहतः not overcome by desires. अथ Now एषः this एव indeed (is) परमः the supreme आनन्दः bliss याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya ह उवाच said सम्राट् O Emperor एषः this (is) ब्रह्मलोकः इति the world of Brahman. सः That अहम् I भगवते Venerable Sir ददामि offer, give (you) सहस्रम् a thousand (cows). ब्रूहि Teach (me) ऊर्ध्वम् beyond अतः this एव indeed विमोक्षाय about liberation. अत्र ह At this (request) याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya बिभयाञ्चकार got afraid (thinking) मेधावी intelligent राजा King उदौत्सीत् should prevail upon, should constrain मा me सर्वेभ्यः with all अन्तेभ्यः इति (my) conclusions (knowledge).



 \[This passage conveys an idea of the Supreme bliss of Self-knowledge as a whole through its parts, as of a rock of salt through its grains.\]

 He who has no physical defects and is provided with luxuries among men, the lord of others, and surrounded with all human¹ enjoyments, is the supreme joy² among men. This human joy increased a hundred-fold equals one measure of joy for the manes who have conquered their world. That joy of these manes who have conquered their world increased a hundred-fold equals one measure of joy in the world of the celestial minstrels. That joy in the world of the celestial minstrels increased a hundred-fold equals one measure of joy for the gods by action—those who have won their godhood by actions (such as the Agnihotra). That joy of the gods by action increased a hundred-fold equals one measure of joy for those who are gods from their very birth as well as that which is experienced by one who is well up in the Vedas, without sin and not overcome by desire³. That joy of the gods by birth increased a hundred-fold equals one measure of joy in the world of Prajāpati (Viraj) as well as that which is experienced by one who is well up in the Vedas, without sin and not overcome by desires. That joy in the world of Prajāpati increased a hundred-fold equals one measure of joy in the



world of Brahman (Hiranyagarbha), as well as that which is experienced by one who is well up in the Vedas, without sin and not overcome by desires. This indeed is the Supreme bliss.' This is the world that is Brahman, O Emperor, said Yājnavalkya. Janaka said, "I offer you a thousand cows, Venerable Sir. Kindly teach me more about liberation." At this request Yājnavalkya got afraid lest this intelligent emperor should prevail upon him to possess all his knowledge.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Excluding enjoyments of heaven.

2\. The identity of joy and the enjoyer points out that this joy is not different from the joy of Self. It is indeed the joys of Self. The lower degrees of bliss have emanated from the Supreme bliss in the form of subject and object.

3\. Doing what is prescribed by the scriptures.

4\. Veda Vyāsa also says in the Mahabharat (12. 173. 47) "The sense-pleasures of this world and the supreme joys of heaven are not worth one-sixteenth part of the bliss that comes of the cessation of desire."\]

——————————————————————————————

** स वा एष एतस्मिन्स्वप्नान्ते रत्वा चरित्वा दृष्ट्वैव पुण्यं च पापं च पुनः प्रतिन्यायं प्रतियोन्याद्रवति बुद्धान्तायैव॥३४॥**

 सः That एषः this (self) वै verily एतस्मिन् in this स्वप्नान्ते dream state रत्वा enjoying himself चरित्वा roaming, moving about दृष्ट्वा merely seeing, witnessing पुण्ययः च merits च and पापम् demerits पुनः again आद्रवति hastens back प्रतिन्यायम्



as he came प्रतियोनि in the inverse way बुद्धान्ताय to the waking state एव indeed.

 And Yājnavalkya said : The individual Self enjoys himself, moves about and merely witnesses merits and demerits of his actions in dream, and then hastens back in the inverse way to his previous state—the waking.

 **तद्यथाऽनः सुसमाहितमुत्सर्जद्यायादेवमेवायꣳ शारीर आत्मा प्राज्ञेनाऽऽत्मनाऽन्वारूढ उत्सर्जन्याति यत्रैतदूर्ध्वोच्छ्वासी भवति॥३५॥**

 तत् That यथा just as अनः a cart सुसमाहितम् fully loaded यायात् goes on, moves on उत्सर्जत् cracking एवम् एव so अयम् this शारीरः embodied आत्मा Self अन्वारूढः presided over, revealed by प्राज्ञेन by the all knowing, by the Supreme आत्मना Self याति goes उत्सर्जत् making noises, groaning यत्र when एतत् thus भवति (he) is ऊर्ध्व-उच्छ्वासी gasping for breath (at the time of death).

 \[The passing of Self from this body to the next as from dream to waking is illustrated as follows :\]

 Just as a cart, fully loaded, moves on cracking under the load, so does the Self that is identified with the subtle body, revealed by the Self-luminous Supreme Self, groans under pain when he gasps¹ for breath at the time of death.



——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. So miserable is this embodied existence! Since at the time of death terrible pain is felt as a consequence of the slashing of vital parts, one must be alert and practise detachment from both gross and subtle bodies, so that he may get over that suffering and attain liberation.\]

——————————————————————————————

** स यत्रायमणिमानं न्येति जरया वोपतपता वाऽणिमानं निगच्छति तद्यथाऽऽम्रं वोदुम्बरं वा पिप्पलं वा बन्धनात्प्रमुच्यत एवमेवायं पुरुष एभ्योऽङ्गेभ्यः सम्प्रमुच्य पुनः प्रतिन्यायं प्रतियोन्याद्रवति प्राणायैव॥३६॥**

 यत्र When सः that अयम् this (body) न्येति becomes, grows अणिमानम् thin, lean निगच्छति goes, is अणिमानम् emaciated, worn out जरया वा by old age वा or उपतपता illness, that which causes affliction (such as fever) तत् then यथा as आम्रं वा a mango वा or उदुम्बरम् a fig वा or पिप्पलम् a peepul fruit प्रमुच्यते is detached, is separated बन्धनात् from (its) stalk, sap एवम् एव so अयम् this पुरुषः being, self सम्प्रमुच्य completely separating, detaching (himself) एभ्यः from these अङ्गेभ्यः members, parts (of the body) पुनः again आद्ववति hastens back प्रतिन्यायम् in the same way प्रतियोनि to particular bodies प्राणाय for (a new) life एव indeed.

 \[This text describes when, how, and why does the difficulty of breath takes place.\]

 When this human body grows lean, is worn out by old age (like a fruit ripened by time) or afflicted¹ with disease (such as fever, etc.), then as



a mango, or a fig or peepul fruit² is separated from its stalk³ to which it is attached, so does this Self identified with the subtle body separates itself from the members of the body (such as the eye), again⁴ hastens back⁵ in the same way (as he came to his present body) to particular bodies according to his past work and experience for a new life.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. At that stage when a man moves, he makes noises like an overloaded cart. The description is meant to stimulate renunciation in us.

2\. Or from the sap by which it is bound to the stalk.

3\. The examples are cited to point out the brute fact that one is always in the jaws of death and that causes of death are indefinite and innumerable and that we should practise renunciation.

4\. The word 'again' indicates that the Self has gone before this also from one body to another many times.

5\. While going into deep sleep he does so.\]

——————————————————————————————

** तद्यथा राजानमायान्तमुग्राः प्रत्येनसः सूतग्रामण्योऽन्नैः पानैरावसथैः प्रतिकल्पन्तेऽयमायात्ययमागच्छतीत्येवꣳ हैवंविदꣳ सर्वाणि भूतानि प्रतिकल्पन्त इदं ब्रह्माऽऽयातीदमागच्छतीति॥३७॥**

 तत् That (the illustration) यथा just as उग्राः the Ugras, a particular caste of fierce deeds प्रत्येनसः set against particular offences, appointed to punish thieves सूत-ग्रामण्यः the Sutas and the leaders of the villages प्रतिकल्पन्ते await राजानम् the King आयान्तम् coming अन्नैः with food पानैः with drink आवसथैः



with places इति (saying) thus अयम् he आयाति comes अयम् he आगच्छति comes एवं ह thus सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings प्रतिकल्पन्ते wait for एवंविदम् such a knower इति (saying) thus इदम् this ब्रह्म Brahman आयाति comes इदम् this आगच्छति comes.

Just as when a king duly installed on the throne comes to some place within his kingdom the fierce Ugras appointed to punish thieves, etc., the Sutas (a hybrid caste) and the leaders of the village anticipating his visit wait for his arrival with various foods¹ and drink² and palaces ready, saying, ' Here he comes, here he comes ', so for the person³ who is a knower of the fruits of his actions all the elements⁴ that make up his body are impelled by his works made ready for fruits, and wait, saying, ' Here the Brahman comes, here he comes. '

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Such as those that are chewed or otherwise eaten.

2\. Wine, for example.

3\. The individual Self that transmigrates.

4\. Elements together with Indra and other presiding deities who help the organs to function.\]

——————————————————————————————

** तद्यथा राजानं प्रयियासन्तमुग्राः प्रत्येनसः सूतग्रामण्योऽभिसमायन्त्येवमेवेममात्मानमन्तकाले सर्वे प्राणा अभिसमायन्ति यत्रैतदूर्ध्वोच्छ्वासी भवति॥३८॥ इति तृतीयं ब्राह्मणम्॥३॥**



 तत् That (the illustration is). यथा Just as उग्राः the Ugras, a fierce caste प्रत्येनसः set against particular offences, appointed to punish thieves सूत-ग्रामण्यः the Sutas and the leaders of villages अभिसमायन्ति approach, gather round राजानम् the King प्रयियासन्तम् wishing to depart एवम् एव so, thus सर्वे all प्राणाः the organs अभिसमायन्ति approach, gather round इमम् this आत्मानम् Self अन्तकाले at the time of death यत्र when एतत् this (dying man) भवति gets, feels ऊर्ध्व-उच्छ्वासी difficulty in breathing.

 Just as the fierce Ugras appointed to punish thieves, etc., the Sutas (a hybrid caste) and the leaders of the village gather round a king about to depart, so do all the organs gather round a dying man¹ at the time of death, when breathing difficulty takes place.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The individual Self who experiences fruits of his actions.\]

——————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER FOUR : SECTION FOUR**

 **स यत्रायमात्माऽबल्यं न्येत्य सम्मोहभिव न्येत्यथैनमेते प्राणा अभिसमायन्ति स एतास्तेजोमात्राः समभ्याददानो हृदयमेवान्ववक्रामति स यत्रैष चाक्षुषः पुरुषः पराङ्पर्यावर्ततेऽथारूपज्ञो भवति॥१॥**



 यत्र When सः that अयम् this आत्मा Self न्येत्य becoming, having sunk अबल्यम् into weakness न्येति becomes, sink सम्मोहम् unconscious, senseless इव as it were अथ then एते these प्राणाः senses, organs अभिसमायन्ति approach, gather एनम् it (Self). सः It (Self) समभ्याददानः completely withdrawing, taking with himself एताः these तेजोमात्राः elements (particles) of light अवक्रामति descends, goes एव only अनु towards, into हृदयम् the heart. यत्र When सः that एषः this पुरुषः person, deity चाक्षुषः occular, associated with the eye (organ of vision) पर्यावर्त्तते turns back पराङ् from all sides अथ then भवति (it) is, becomes अरूपज्ञः unconscious of any form (colour).

 \[This section describes in detail the process of transmigration in order to state when and how the individual Self withdraws itself from the members of the body at the time of death.\]

 When the transmigrating Self at the time of death becomes¹, as it were, weak and unconscious², the organs (such as that of speech) gather round It. The Self completely³ withdraws these⁴ elements of light and descends into the ether of the heart.⁵ When the deity⁶ which presides over the organ of vision turns back from all sides, the dying man becomes unconscious of all forms.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The Self due to its natural formlessness can never become weak. In fact it is the body that becomes weak. Weakness of the body is figuratively spoken of as belonging to the Self.

——————————————————————————————



——————————————————————————————

2.It fails to discriminate. The Self cannot by itself be unconscious or otherwise; on account of its nature of eternal intelligence.

3.The adverb 'completely' shows the distinction of death from a dream. In dream the organs are just drawn in, but in death they are absolutely withdrawn.

4.The organs such as the eye are so called, because the colours are revealed by them.

5.The intelligence of Self is manifested in the lotus of the heart.

6.This deity which is a portion of the sun remains in the eye, while the latter is active but at the time of death goes back to the sun.\]

——————————————————————————————

** एकीभवति न पश्यतीत्याहुरेकीभवति न जिघ्रतीत्याहुरेकीभवति न रसयत इत्याहुरेकीभवति न वदतीत्याहुरेकीभवति न शृणोतीत्याहुरेकीभवति न मनुत इत्याहुरेकीभवति न स्पृशतीत्याहुरेकीभवति न विजानातीत्याहुस्तस्य हैतस्य हृदयस्याग्रं प्रद्योतते तेन प्रद्योतेनैष आत्मा निष्क्रामति चक्षुष्टो वा मूर्ध्नो वाऽन्येभ्यो वा शरीरदेशेभ्यस्तमुत्क्रामन्तं प्राणोऽनूत्क्रामति प्राणमनूत्क्रामन्तꣳ सर्वे प्राणा अनूत्क्रामन्ति सविज्ञानो भवति सविज्ञानमेवान्ववक्रामति। तं विद्याकर्मणी समन्वारभेते पूर्वप्रज्ञा च॥२॥**

 (When) भवति (the eye) is एकी united (with the subtle body) आहुः (people) say पश्यति इति (he) sees न not (when) भवति (the nose) is एकी united आहुः (people) say जिघ्रति इति



(he) smells न not. (When) भवति (the tongue) is एकी united आहुः (people) say रसयते इति (he) tastes न not. (When) भवति (the vocal organ) is एकी united आहुः (people) say वदति इति (he) speaks न not. (When) भवति (the ear) is एकी united आहुः (people) say शृणोति इति (he) hears न not. (When) भवति (the mind) is एकी united आहुः (people) say मनुते इति (he) thinks न not. (When) भवति (the skin) is एकी united आहुः (people) say स्पृशति इति (he) touches न not. When भवति (the intellect) is एकी united आहुः (people) say जानाति इति (he) knows न not, तस्य of that ह एतस्य this अग्रम् the top, nerve end हृदयस्य of the (orifice of) heart प्रद्योतते is lighted up, brightens up. एषः This आत्मा Self तेन by that (brightened top) आत्मा the Self निष्क्रामति departs, leaves चक्षुष्टः वा through the eye वा or मूर्ध्नः through the head वा or अन्येभ्यः through other शरीर-देशेभ्यः parts of the body. प्राणाः The vital power अनुत्क्रामति follows, accompanies तम् it उत्क्रामन्तम् going out, departing सर्वे all प्राणाः the organs अनुत्क्रामन्ति follow, accompany तम् it अनुत्क्रामन्तम् departing (the Self) भवति is सविज्ञानः endowed with (particular) consciousness अनु + अवक्रामति takes, goes to (that body) सविज्ञानम् एव related to (revealed by) that consciousness विद्याकर्मणी knowledge, work च and पूर्वप्रज्ञा past experience समन्वारभेते accompany, follow तम् it.

 When the eye is united with the subtle body of the dying man, then people at his side say of him, ' He does not see. ' When the nose on the withdrawal of its presiding deity is united with his subtle body¹, they say of him, ' He does not smell. '



When the tongue with the withdrawal² of its deity is united with the subtle body, then they say, ' He does not taste. ' When the vocal organ with the withdrawal of its deity is united, then they say, ' He does not speak. ' When the ear with the withdrawal of its deity is united with the subtle body, then they say, ' He does not hear. ' When the mind with the withdrawal of its deity is united with the subtle body, then they say, ' He does not think. ' When the skin with the withdrawal of its deity is united with the subtle body, then they say, ' He does not touch. ' When the intellect is thus united with the subtle body, then they say, ' He does not know. ' When the nerve-end of the orifice of the heart³ is lighted up as in the dream state by the light of the Atman, the individual Self with subtle body as its limiting adjunct leaves the body. It departs through the eye if it has a store of work or knowledge that would lead it to the sun. It goes out through the head if its past work and experience would entitle it to attain the world of Hiranyagarbha. It departs through other parts of the body according to its past work and knowledge. When it goes out for the next world, the vital power accompanies it; when the vital power goes out all the organs accompany it. Then the Self is endowed with particular consciousness as in dreams and



takes the body that is revealed by that consciousness. In its journey to the next world the Self is accompanied by knowledge of all sorts ¹, work and the impressions ⁵ of past experience.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Intelligence of the effulgent Self is particularly manifest in the subtle body. This limiting adjunct of the Self is the chief instrument of embodiment, of birth and death. It is the store-house of past impressions that cause transmigration.

2\. Stopping of its functions.

3\. It is the exit of the Self.

4\. Those that are enjoined or forbidden and those that are neither enjoined nor forbidden.

3\. It is these impressions of past experiences that prompt the organs to work. With them one is expert in something and without them one is not so in the same. It is for this reason that some are found skilful in some work such as painting or music from their very childhood even without practice in this life, while others are unskilful even in some very easy task.\]

——————————————————————————————

** तद्यथा तृणजलायुका तृणस्यान्तं गत्वाऽन्यमाक्रममाक्रम्याऽऽत्मानमुपसꣳ हरत्येवमेवायमात्मेदꣳ शरीरं निहत्याविद्यां गमयित्वाऽन्यमाक्रममाक्रम्याऽऽत्मानमुपसꣳ हरति॥३॥**

 तत् That (the illustration is), यथा Just as तृणजलायुका a caterpillar, a leech resting on a straw गत्वा going अन्तम् to the end तृणस्य of the straw, of a blade of grass आक्रमत् taking,



holding अन्यम् another आक्रमम् support (straw) उपसंहरति contracts, withdraws आत्मानम् itself एवम् एव so अयम् this आत्मा Self निहत्य killing, making senseless इदम् this शरीरम् body गमयित्वा having thrown off, set aside or dispelled अविद्याम् all ignorance (i.e., the body) आक्रम्य taking, holding अन्यम् another (new) आक्रमम् support (body) उपसंहरति contracts, withdraws एनम् itself.

 \[The passing on of the transmigrating Self from one body to another is illustrated as follows :\]

 Just as a leech resting on a blade of grass goes to the end of it, holds another blade of grass as support and withdraws one part of its body to where the other part is, so the transmigrating Self sets aside the body already taken, as it does when entering a dream state, and make it senseless by withdrawing itself from it and takes a new body ¹ and identifies itself with it.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. As in dream the individual Self creates a new body and dwells as it were in it. The new body is formed of new materials like one made of straw and clay. The organs enter the new body and under the influence of past actions join together and manifest their functions. When the organs are thus confined, fire and other deities that preside over them come to them to help their functions.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** तद्यथा पेशस्कारी पेशसो मात्रामुपादायान्यन्नवतरं कल्याणतरꣳ रूपं तनुत एवमेवायमात्मेदꣳ शरीरं निहत्याविद्यां गम-**



**यित्वाऽन्यन्नवतरं कल्याणतरꣳ रूपं कुरुते पित्र्यं वा गान्धर्वं वा दैवं वा प्राजापत्यं वा ब्राह्मं वाऽन्येषां वा भूतानाम्॥४॥**

 तत् That (the example is), यथा Just as पेशस्कारी a goldsmith उपादाय taking मात्राम् a piece, a little quantity पेशसः of gold तनुते makes, fashions अन्यत् another नवतरम् newer कल्याणतरम् better, more beautiful रूपम् shape, form एवम् so एव indeed अयम् this आत्मा Self निहत्य killing, making senseless इदम् this शरीरम् body गमयित्वा having thrown off, having dispelled अविद्याम् all ignorance (i.e., body) कुरुते makes अन्यत् another नवतरम् newer कल्याणतरम् better रूपम् form, body पित्र्यं वा fit for the world of the manes वा or गान्धर्वम् fit for the heavenly minstrels वा or दैवम् fit for the gods वा or प्राजापत्यम् fit for Viraj वा or ब्राह्मम् fit for Brahman (Hiranyagarbha) वा or अन्येषाम् of other भूतानाम् beings.

 Just as a goldsmith taking apart a piece of gold makes another shape, newer and more beautiful than the previous model, so the individual Self throwing this body away (in death), or making it senseless (in dream) makes another body newer and more beautiful fit for the enjoyment in the world of the manes, or fit for the heavenly minstrels, or fit for the gods, or Viraj, or Hiranyagarbha or other beings according to its past work and experience.

** स वा अयमात्मा ब्रह्म विज्ञानमयो मनोमयः प्राणमयश्चक्षुर्मयः श्रोत्रमयः पृथिवीमय आपोमयो वायुमय आकाशमय-**



** स्तेजोमयोऽतेजोमयः काममयोऽकाममयः क्रोधमयोऽक्रोधमयो धर्ममयोऽधर्ममयः सर्वमयस्तद्यदेतदिदम्मयोऽदोमय इति यथाकारी यथाचारी तथा भवति साधुकारी साधुर्भवति पापकारी पापो भवति पुण्यः पुण्येन कर्मणा भवति पापः पापेन। अथो खल्वाहुः काममय एवायं पुरुष इति स यथाकामो भवति तत्क्रतुर्भवति यत्क्रतुर्भवति तत्कर्म कुरुते यत्कर्म कुरुते तदभिसम्पद्यते॥५॥**

 सः That अयम् this आत्मा Self वै (is) verily ब्रह्म Brahman, the supreme self विज्ञानमयः united with the intellect, मनोमयः united with the mind, full of mind, प्राणमयः united with the vital power, चक्षुर्मयः united with the eyes, श्रोत्रमयः united with the ears, पृथिवीमयः united with earth, आपोमयः united with water, वायुमयः united with air, आकाशमयः united with the ether, तेजोमयः united with fire, अतेजोमयः united with no fire, काममयः united with desire, अकाममयः united with desirelessness, क्रोधमयः identified with anger, अक्रोधमयः united with no anger, धर्ममयः united with righteousness, अधर्ममयः united with unrighteousness, सर्वमयः united with all. तत् That यत् which एतत् this इदमयः (is) united with this (the perceptible) अदोमयः इति united with that (the imperceptible, the inferred) यथाकारी as (it) does, यथाचारी as (it) acts, तथा so भवति (it) becomes साधुकारी the doer of good भवति becomes साधुः good पापकारी the doer of evil भवति becomes पापः evil पुण्येन by good कर्मणा acts भवति (it) becomes पुण्यः virtuous, पापेन by evil (acts) पापः (it) becomes vicious. अथ खलु However आहुः (others) say अयम्



this पुरुषः being, self काममयः इति united with desires. सः It भवति is यथा-कामः as desires भवति is तत्क्रतुः of that will यत् which क्रतुः will भवति (he) is तत् that कर्म work कुरुते (it) does यत् which कर्म work कुरुते (it) does अभिसम्पद्यते (it) gets, attains तत् that.

 This transmigrating Self is indeed the Supreme Self. It also becomes united ¹ with the intellect when noticed through it. It becomes united with the mind because of its proximity to that. It becomes united with the vital power that has the fivefold function. It becomes united with the eye when it sees forms. It becomes united with the ear when it hears sounds. It gets united with the earth when it wants an earthly ² body. It is united with the water when creating a watery body in the world of Varuna or so. It is united with the air when an aerial body has to be made. It becomes united with ether when making an ethereal body. It is united with fire when it makes for gods bodies that preponderate in the elements of fire. It becomes united with materials other than fire when making bodies for animals, etc. It is identified with desires when it wants something. It is united with desirelessness when it is serene and calm. It becomes full of anger when desire is somehow frustrated. It is united with absence of desire when



its anger is appeased. Thus the Self is united with righteousness and unrighteousness, and with every-thing. In short it is united, as is well known, with what is perceived, and with what is inferred. As it does³ and acts⁴, so it becomes. By doing good it becomes good and by doing evil it becomes bad. It becomes virtuous through good deeds⁵ and vicious through evil actions. Other authorities, however, opine that the Self is united with desire alone. What it desires⁶, it wills; what it wills as a result of the desire it does; what it does, it gets as its results.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The self resembles the intellect and is so called because it is conceived of having the attributes of intellect.

2\. Preponderating in earthly elements.

3\. Following injunctions and prohibitions of scriptures.

4\. It is not so prescribed as doing.

5\. The long and short of it is that performance of good and bad deeds under the impulse of desire, anger, etc. is the cause of self's identification with everything and consequent transmigration.

6\. Desire manifests itself as the slightest longing for a certain thing. If it is unchecked, it takes a more definite form and turns into will. Will is a sort of determination which is followed by action. It is said in the Manu Samhita (2-4) that whatever action a man does is the outcome of desire.\]

——————————————————————————————



** तदेष श्लोको भवति। तदेव सक्तः सह कर्मणैति लिङ्गं मनो यत्र निषक्तमस्य। प्राप्यान्तं कर्मणस्तस्य यत्किञ्चेह करोत्ययम्। तस्माल्लोकात्पुनरैत्यस्मै लोकाय कर्मण इति नु कामयमानोऽथाकामयमानो योऽकामो निष्काम आप्तकाम आत्मकामो न तस्य प्राणा उत्क्रामन्ति ब्रह्मैव सन्ब्रह्माप्येति॥६॥**

 तत् (On) that (subject) भवति there is एषः this श्लोकः verse: तत् That एव indeed सक्तः being attached कर्मणा सह इति together with the work यत्र where अस्य his लिङ्गम् subtle body मनः the mind निषक्तम् (is) attached अयम् this प्राप्य getting अन्तम् end, exhaustion तस्य of his कर्मणः work यत् किञ्चित् whatever करोति (he) does इह in this world एति comes पुनः again तस्मात् from that लोकात् world अस्मै to this लोकाय world कर्मणे for (fresh) work. इति नु Thus कामयमानः desiring (man) अथ now अकामयमानः (he) who does not desire. यः (He) who अकामः (is) without desires, निष्कामः free from desires, आप्तकामः whose desires are fulfilled, आत्मकामः whose desire is but the self, तस्य his प्राणाः organs उत्क्रामन्ति goes up, depart न not सन् being, becoming ब्रह्म Brahman एव indeed अप्येति is merged, unified ब्रह्म in Brahman.

 On this subject there is this verse: The man who transmigrates having his desire roused for the result of the work he did, attains the same as his subtle body or mind¹ yearns² for. Experiencing in that world the results of whatever work he did in this life, he comes again to this³ world for fresh



work. Thus does the man who craves, desires, transmigrates. But the man who has no desire does not transmigrate anywhere. Of him who is bereft of desires, whom desires have left, whose desires are all fulfilled and whose only desire is the Self—his organs do not go up from the body. He becomes Brahman. He is one with Brahman in this very life.⁴

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The mind is called the subtle body because it is the principal part of the subtle body. The word 'Linga' also means 'an index'. This body indicates the self.

2\. Attachment of mind is the cause of attaining the result of action and consequent transmigration. A knower of the self, who has no desires, may work; but his work will not produce any result.

3\. For work holds the most important place in this world.

4\. He has not to wait for the fall of the body. The knower of Brahman is no other than Brahman although he seems to have a body. His conditions in life and after death are same.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** तदेष श्लोको भवति। यदा सर्वे प्रमुच्यन्ते कामा येऽस्य हृदि श्रिताः। अथ मर्त्योऽमृतो भवत्यत्र ब्रह्म समश्नुत इति। तद्यथाऽहिनिर्ल्वयनी वल्मीके मृता प्रत्यस्ता शयीतैवमेवेदꣳ शरीरꣳ शेतेऽथायमशरीरोऽमृतः प्राणो ब्रह्मैव तेज एव सोऽहं भगवते सहस्रं ददामीति होवाच जनको वैदेहः॥७॥**



 तत् On that (subject) एषः this, following श्लोकः verse, mantra भवति is there : यदा when सर्वे all कामाः desires, forms of yearning ये That श्रिताः dwell, abide अस्य in his हृदि heart, mind प्रमुच्यते are gone, are destroyed अथ then मर्त्सः the mortal भवति becomes अमृतः immortal अत्र here (in this very body) समश्नुते attains ब्रह्म इति Brahman. तत् that यथा just as मृता dead, lifeless अहिनिर्ल्वयनी slough of a snake प्रत्यस्ता (being) cast off, thrown off शयीत lies वल्मीके in the ant hill एवम् so एव indeed इदम् this शरीरम् body शेते lies. अथ Then अयम् this (self) अशरीरः (becomes) disembodied अमृतः immortal प्राणः that which lives, Supreme Self ब्रह्म Brahman एव indeed तेजः the Light एव indeed. जनकः Janaka वैदेहः Emperor of Videha उवाच said— सः that अहम् I ददामि give (you) सहस्रम् a thousand (cows) भगवते इति Venerable Sir.

 On this theme the following mantra is there: When all the forms of yearning for wealth, children, etc. that abide in the mind are destroyed together with their root, then the mortal becomes immortal¹ and attains the identity² with Brahman living in this very body. Just as the slough of a snake lies dead and cast off in the ant-hill or any other nest of a snake so this body is discarded as non-self by the liberated man. Then although the individual Self resides in the body. It becomes disembodied³ and immortal, the Supreme Self, Brahman, the Light of Pure Intelligence. Emperor Janaka of



Videha said to Yājnavalkya, 'Venerable Sir, thus delivered I give you a thousand cows as requital for the instructions received.'

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. Desires are forms of death. On the cessation of them death is overcome and immortality is attained.

2\. This is liberation. Liberation, therefore, does not require going to any world.

3\. It no longer undergoes embodiment or is connected with this body.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** तदेते श्लोका भवन्ति। अणुः पन्था विततः पुराणो माꣳ स्पृष्टोऽनुवित्तो मयैव। तेन धीरा अपियन्ति ब्रह्मविदः स्वर्गं लोकमित ऊर्ध्वं विमुक्ताः॥८॥**

 तत् On that एते these श्लोकाः verses भवन्ति are there: अनुः The subtle, difficult to comprehend विततः**\*** extensive पुराणः primaeval, ancient, not modern पन्थाः path (of knowledge) स्पृष्टः has touched माम् me अनुवित्तः found, realised एव indeed मया by me. तेन By that (path of knowledge) धीराः the sages, men of illumination ब्रह्मविदः the knowers of Brahman अपियन्ति go, attain स्वर्गं लोकम् heaven-world (liberation) ऊर्ध्वम् higher on, beyond इतः from this (body) विमुक्ताः (being) freed.

 On the subject of liberation attained by the knower of Brahman these verses are there: This path of knowledge which leads to liberation is

——————————————————————————————

**\*** The Madhyandin reading is 'Vitara' which means 'leading across' i.e. effectively leading to liberation.

——————————————————————————————



extensive, primaeval¹ and difficult of comprehension. I have reached it. Nay, I have realised² it myself. By that path of knowledge men of illumination become free from the body and attains liberation even while living.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. It is the path revealed by the Vedas which are eternal. It is not modern and misleading like the path which emanates from the intellect of the logicians.

2\. Realisation is the attainment which, as the knowledge of self ripens, culminates in ultimate satisfaction, as eating culminates in satiety. It gives one the conviction of complete blessedness. It is an experience which requires no other testimony except one's own. It is not reserved for the chosen few but is accessible to all.\]

——————————————————————————————

** तस्मिञ्छुक्लमुत नीलमाहुः पिङ्गलꣳ हरितं लोहितं च। एष पन्था ब्रह्मणा हानुवित्तस्तेनैति ब्रह्मवित्पुण्यकृत्तैजसश्च॥९॥**

 आहुः (Some) say, describe तस्मिन् of it शुक्लम् उत (as) white, pure, limpid नीलम् (others as) blue पिङ्गलम् grey हरितम् green लोहितं च red. एषः This पन्था path (of knowledge) अनुवित्तः ह (is) realised ब्रह्मणा by a Brahman (a knower of Brahman) ब्रह्मवित् (any other) knower of Brahman पुण्यकृत् a doer of good deeds च and तेजसः**\* **metamorphosed into supreme Light एति goes, travels तेन by that (path).

——————————————————————————————

\*Anandagiri explains the word 'Taijasa' and the sentence containing it a bit differently. According to him Taijasa means the organs and the sentence would mean: The Yogin who withdraws his organs and meditates on Dahara (the ether in the heart) attains extraordinary powers such as anima, etc.

—————————————————————————————



 Some seekers after liberation describe this path¹ of knowledge as white; others as blue, grey, green or red according to their experience. This path of knowledge is realised by a knower of Brahman. Any other knower of Brahman who has first of all done good deeds and then has given up the three-fold desire (for progeny, prosperity and worlds) and finally metamorphosed into the Supreme Light in this very life also travels by this path of knowledge.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. In reality this path has no colour. These colours experienced by the seekers are really the colours of Sushumna and other nerves which are filled with phlegm and other liquids. The colours of the nerves are given before in this Upanishad (4. 3. 20).\]

——————————————————————————————

** अन्धं तमः प्रविशन्ति येऽविद्यामुपासते। ततो भूय इव ते तमो य उ विद्याया‍ꣳ रताः॥१०॥**

** **तमः Into darkness अन्धम् blinding, obstructing vision प्रविशन्ति enter (those) ये who उपासते worship, follow, practise अविद्याम् ignorance, rites भूयः into greater तमः darkness ततः than that इव as it were ये उ (those) who रताः (is) devoted, attached विद्यायाम् to knowledge, ritualistic practice.

 Those who practise rites consisting of ends and means enter into darkness that obstructs their vision (of Self-knowledge). And those that are



attached to the ceremonial portion of the Vedas (and disregard the Upanishads) enter into greater darkness, as it were.

** अनन्दा नाम ते लोका अन्धेन तमसाऽऽवृताः। ताꣳस्ते प्रेत्याभिगच्छन्त्यविद्वाꣳ सोऽबुधो जनाः॥११॥**

 नाम Named, called अनन्दाः miserable (are) ते those लोकाः worlds आवृताः enveloped, covered अन्धेन by deep, by blinding तमसा darkness. तान् To them प्रेत्य departing, dying अभिगच्छन्ति go, enter ते those जनाः people, common folk अविद्वांसः ignorant (and) अबुधः unwise, devoid of self-knowledge.

 Those worlds are covered with deep darkness of ignorance and are very miserable. Common folk who are ignorant and devoid of Self-knowledge enter those worlds after death.

** आत्मानं चेद्विजानीयादयमस्मीति पूरुषः। किमिच्छन्कस्य कामाय शरीरमनुसञ्ज्वरेत्॥१२॥**

 चेत् If पुरुषः a man विजानीयात् knows आत्मानम् the self अस्मि (I) am अयम् इति this इच्छन् desiring किम् what कामाय for the desire कस्य of whom अनुसञ्ज्वरेत् (he) will become miserable, will suffer, will imbibe afflictions शरीरम् in the wake of the body.



 If¹ a man in a thousand knows the Self as 'I am this Supreme Seif', then he will not imbibe² the afflictions of the body for the sake of any object or for the need of any person.³

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. The word 'if' shows that self-knowledge is rare.

2\. To deviate from the nature of the supreme self and go the round of births and deaths.

3\. Because he sees all objects and all persons as his own Self. He does not see any of them different from his Self.\]

——————————————————————————————

** यस्यानुवित्तः प्रतिबुद्ध आत्माऽस्मिन्सन्देह्ये गहने प्रविष्टः। स विश्वकृत्स हि सर्वस्य कर्ता तस्य लोकः स उ लोक एव॥१३॥**

 सः He (the knower of Self) यस्य who अनुवित्तः has seen प्रतिबुद्धः (and) intimately known आत्मा the self प्रविष्टः (that) has entered, has got अस्मिन् in this सन्देह्ये inaccessible (with obstacles to enlightenment) गहने perilous, beset with dangers (body) विश्वकृत् is the maker of the universe; हि for सः he (is) कर्ता the maker सर्वस्य of all तस्य his लोकः world, self. सः उ He (is) एव indeed लोकः the self (of all).

 He who has seen and intimately known the Supreme Self that has got into the body which is beset with numerous dangers and inaccessible with endless obstacles to enlightenment is the maker of the Universe.¹ He is indeed the maker of all. All is his Self. He is indeed the Self of all.²



 ——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. He is not under the influence of any extraneous agency.

2\. The gist of the verse is that one should meditate upon his own Self as the Supreme Self, the Self of all beings, the Self who is the one only without a second.\]

——————————————————————————————

** इहैव सन्तोऽथ विद्मस्तद्वयं न चेदवेदीर्महती विनष्टिः। ये तद्विदुरमृतास्ते भवन्त्यथेतरे दुःखमेवापियन्ति॥१४॥**

 सन्तः Being इह in this (body) एव indeed अथ somehow वयम् we विद्मः have known, have realised तत् that (Brahman). चेत् If न not अवेदीः (I should have been) ignorant (of It). महती (It is) great, of infinite magnitude विनष्टिः loss, destruction (consisting in births, deaths, etc.) ते those ये who विदुः know तत् It (Brahman) भवन्ति are, become अमृताः immortal. अथ While इतरे others अपियन्ति attain, suffer दुःखम् misery एवः alone.

 Further being¹ in this very body, so full of dangers, we have somehow realised Brahman as our own self and have escaped all misery. Otherwise, we would have been ignorant, and loss of infinite magnitude (consisting of births, deaths, etc.) would have happened to us. The knowers of Brahman become immortal and are saved from such loss. While other people who are ignorant of It suffer infinite misery.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. Being under the spell of the long sleep of ignorance.\]

——————————————————————————————



** यदैतमनुपश्यत्यात्मानं देवमञ्जसा। ईशानं भूतभव्यस्य न ततो विजुगुप्सते॥१५॥**

 यदा When अनुपश्यति (one) sees एतम् this देवम् effulgent आत्मानम् self अञ्जसा directly ईशानम् the lord भूतभव्यस्य of all that has been and will be ततः from It न not विजुगुप्सते (he) wishes to hide (himself).

 When a man (after receiving instructions and grace from a merciful teacher) directly sees this effulgent self, the Lord of the past, present and future, he no longer wishes¹ particularly to hide himself from It.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. The knower of Self does not blame anybody because he sees all as his Self, one blames another when one sees another different from him. But the knower of Self does not see anybody different from Him.\]

——————————————————————————————

** यस्मादर्वाक्संवत्सरोऽहोभिः परिवर्तते। तद्देवा ज्योतिषां ज्योतिरायुर्होपासतेऽमृतम्॥१६॥**

 अर्वाक् Below यस्मात् which संवत्सरः the year अहोभिः with (its) days परिवर्त्तते changes, revolves देवाः the gods उपासते worship, meditate upon तत् that अमृतम् immortal ज्योतिः light ज्योतिषाम् of all lights, of all luminaries (such as sun) आयुः ह as longevity.

 The gods worship Him as longevity.¹ Below him the year² with its days and nights revolve.³ He is the revealer of the luminaries such as the sun.



 ——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. He alone being imperishable, he is the longevity of all. Gods become long-lived by meditating upon Him as longevity. Therefore one who desires long life should meditate upon Him through the attribute of longevity.

2\. That represents time which conditions everything that is born.

3\. Occupies a lower position unable to limit It.\]

——————————————————————————————

** यस्मिन्पञ्च पञ्चजना आकाशश्च प्रतिष्ठितः। तमेव मन्य आत्मानं विद्वान्ब्रह्मामृतोऽमृतम्॥१७॥**

 तम् That यस्मिन् in whom पञ्च five पञ्चजनाः groups of five च and आकाशः the (unmanifested) ether प्रतिष्ठितः (are) placed एव verily आत्मानम् self मन्ये (I) regard, believe अमृतम् (as) the immortal ब्रह्म Brahman. विद्वान् The knower (of Brahman) अमृतः (is) immortal.

 Verily I believe to be the immortal Brahman, that Self in whom the five groups¹ of five and the unmanifested ether rest. I am immortal² by the knowledge of Brahman.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. Brahmana, Kshatriya, Vaishya, Shudra and the Chandalas; or vital power, eye, ear, food and the mind; or celestial minstrels, the manes, the gods, the asuras and the rakshasas.

2\. I was mortal only through my ignorance of Brahman. Since that ignorance is gone and I am blessed with the knowledge of Brahman I am immortal.\]

——————————————————————————————

** प्राणस्य प्राणमुत चक्षुषश्चक्षुरुत श्रोत्रस्य श्रोत्रं मनसो ये मनो विदुः। ते निचिक्युर्ब्रह्म पुराणमग्र्यम्॥१८॥**



 ते Those ये who विदुः have known, have comprehended प्राणम् उत the life प्राणस्य of life, चक्षुः उत the Eye चक्षुषः of the eye, श्रोत्रम् the Ear श्रोत्रस्य of the ear, मनः the Mind मनसः of the mind निचिक्युः have realised, have known with certainty पुराणम् ancient, eternal अग्र्यम् primordial ब्रह्म Brahman.

 Those who have comprehended the Life¹ of life, the Eye² of the eye, the Ear of the ear, and the Mind³ of the mind have known with certainty the eternal primordial Brahman.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. Because the life force functions by the light of the Self.

2\. The eye and the other organs are enabled to function by the energy of Self. Being divested of the energy of Self they are by themselves like wood or clods of earth.

3\. Brahman is realised not as a sense-object but as the innermost Self.\]

——————————————————————————————

** मनसैवानुद्रष्टव्यं नेह नानाऽस्ति किञ्चन। मृत्योः स मृत्युमाप्नोति य इह नानेव पश्यति॥१९॥**

 अनुद्रष्टव्यम् (The self is) realised, known मनसा by the mind एव alone. इह in It अस्ति there is न not नाना separateness, diversity किञ्चन whatsoever. सः He यः who पश्यति sees इह in It नाना diversity, difference इव as it were आप्नोति attains, goes मृत्युम् to death मृत्योः from death.

 The Self is known by the mind purified by means of Knowledge. There is no diversity¹



whatsoever in It. He who sees diversity, as it were, in It, goes from death to death.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. The diversity that is perceived is apparent and is superimposed on It through ignorance.\]

——————————————————————————————
