** एकधैवानुद्रष्टव्यमेतदप्रमेयं ध्रुवम्। विरजः पर आकाशादज आत्मा महान्ध्रुवः॥२०॥**

 अनुद्रष्टव्यम्(Self is) known, cognised by means of knowledge एकधा in one way, as one entity एव alone (for) एतत् It (is) अप्रमयम् unknowable ध्रुवम् (and) immovable, eternal, unchangeable आत्मा The self (is) विरजः taintless, free from the impurities of good and evil परः beyond, subtler, more pervasive आकाशात् than the ether अजः unborn महान् infinite, vaster than anything ध्रुवः (and) constant, indestructible.

 The Self is known as one homogeneous entity without any break like ether. Being one It is unknowable by another like a sense-object. The Self is unchangeable and free from impurities of good and evil. It is more pervasive than ether, unborn¹, vaster than everything and indestructible.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. The negation of birth implies the negation of all the six successive changing conditions of a thing which to Yāska are— coming into being, existence, growth, beginning to decline, decay and death.\]

——————————————————————————————



** तमेव धीरो विज्ञाय प्रज्ञां कुर्वीत ब्राह्मणः। नानुध्यायाद्बहूञ्छब्दान्वाचो विग्लापन‍ꣳ हि तदिति॥२१॥**

 धीरः The intelligent, the wise ब्राह्मणः seeker of Brahman विज्ञाय knowing तम् about this एव alone कुर्वीत should attain, practise प्रज्ञाम् knowledge. अनुध्यायात् (He) should repeat न not बहून् too many शब्दान् words; हि for तत् that (is) विग्लापनम् weariness, particularly fatiguing वाचः इति to the organ of speech, to the tongue.

 The wise seeker of Brahman should first know about the nature¹ of Supreme Self alone from the teacher and the scriptures and should practise the means of Self-knowledge (so as to put an end to all questioning of the mind). He should not repeat too many words, because that is weariness of the tongue².

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Such as, renunciation, calmness, Self-control, withdrawal of the senses, fortitude and concentration.

2\. This restriction implies that all other speech should be given up and few words such as Om that deals exclusively with Self should be repeated. As the Mundaka Upanishad (2-2-6) says: 'Meditate on the Self by repeating Om.'\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** स वा एष महानज आत्मा योऽयं विज्ञानमयः प्राणेषु य एषोऽन्तर्हृदय आकाशस्तस्मिञ्छेते सर्वस्य वशी सर्वस्येशानः सर्वस्याधिपतिः स न साधुना कर्मणा भूयान्नो एवासाधुना**



**कनीयानेष सर्वेश्वर एष भूताधिपतिरेष भूतपाल एष सेतुर्विधरण एषां लोकानामसम्भेदाय तमेतं वेदानुवचनेन ब्राह्मणा विविदिषन्ति यज्ञेन दानेन तपसाऽनाशकेनैतमेव विदित्वा मुनिर्भवति। एतमेव प्रव्राजिनो लोकमिच्छन्तः प्रव्रजन्ति। एतद्धस्म वै तत्पूर्वे विद्वाꣳसः प्रजां न कामयन्ते किं प्रजया करिष्यामो येषां नोऽयमात्माऽयं लोक इति ते ह स्म पुत्रैषणायाश्च वित्तैषणायाश्च लोकैषणायाश्च व्युत्थायाथ भिक्षाचर्यं चरन्ति या ह्येव पुत्रैषणा सा वित्तैषणा या वित्तैषणा सा लोकैषणोभे ह्येते एषणे एव भवतः। स एष नेति नेत्यात्माऽगृह्यो न हि गृह्यतेऽशीर्यो न हि शीर्यतेऽसङ्गो न हि सज्यतेऽसितो न व्यथते न रिष्यत्येतमु हैवैते न तरत इत्यतः पापमकरवमित्यतः कल्याणमकरवमित्युभे उ हैवैष एते तरति नैनं कृताकृते तपतः॥२२॥**

 सः That (described before) वै verily एषः this महान् great infinite अजः unborn, birthless अयम् this आत्मा self यः which (is) विज्ञानमयः consisting of knowledge, identified with the intellect प्राणेषु (is) surrounded by the organs एषः this आकाशः ether यः that (is) अन्तर्हृदये within the heart शेते lies, lives तस्मिन् in that वशी the controller सर्वस्य of all, ईशानः the lord सर्वस्य of all, अधिपतिः the ruler सर्वस्य of all. सः It (self) न not भूयात् becomes better, improve from the previous state साधुना by food कर्मणा work न not उ एव indeed कनीयान् worse, does not fall from the previous state असाधुना by bad कर्मणा work. एषः It (Self) सर्वेश्वरः (is) the Lord of all एषः



It (is) भूताधिपतिः the ruler of beings. एषः It (is) भूतपालः the protector of beings. एषः It (Self) सेतुः bridge, bank विधरणः boundary असम्भेदाय for non-separation एषाम् of these लोकानाम् worlds. ब्राह्मणाः the Brahmans विविदिषन्ति desire to know, wish to realise तम् that एतम् this (Self) वेदानुवचनेन by (daily) reading of the Vedas, यज्ञेन by sacrifices, by rites, दानेन by charity, तपसा by austerity अनाशकेन by starvation, by fasting. विदित्वा Knowing एतम् it एव alone भवति (one) is, becomes मुनिः a sage, a man of meditation. इच्छन्तः Desiring, seeking एतम् this लोकम् world (Self) एव indeed प्रव्राजिनः the monks प्रव्रजन्ति go, leave home, renounce the world तत् that एतत् ह this. वै Verily पूर्वे the ancient विद्वांसः knowers (of Self) न not कामयन्ते स्म desired प्रजाम् progeny, offspring किम् what करिष्यामः shall (we) do प्रजया with progeny, with offspring नः we येषाम् whose (is) अयम् this लोकः world अयम् this आत्मा इति Self. ते ह They चरन्ति स्म wandered about, lived भिक्षाचर्यम् (as) mendicants, monastic life अथ and व्युत्थाय rising above, renouncing पुत्रैषाणायाः च desire for sons वित्तैषणायाः च desire for wealth लोकैषणायाः च desire for worlds. हि For सा that या एव which (is) पुत्रैषणा desire for sons वित्तैषणा (is) the desire for wealth. सा That या which (is) वित्तैषणा desire for wealth लोकैषणा (is) the desire for worlds; हि for उभे both एते these भवतः are एव indeed एषणे desires. एषः This आत्मा self सः (is) that (which has been described as) न इति not this न इति not this. अगृह्यः (It is) incomprehensible, imperceptible; हि for गृह्यते (It) is comprehended, is perceived न not. अशीर्यः (It is) undecaying, imperishable हि for शीर्यते (It) perishes, decays



न not. असङ्गः (It is) unattached; हि for सज्यते (it) is attached न not. असितः (It is) unfettered व्यथते (it) is pained, feels pain न not. रिष्यति (It) suffers misery न not. एतम् उ That एते these two (thoughts) एव ह indeed न not तरतः इति overtakes, overcomes (the knower). अतः For this अकरवम् (I) did पापम् इति a sinful act अतः for this अकरवम् (I) did कल्याणम् a meritorious act. एषः He (the knower) तरति ह conquers, goes beyond उभे उ both एते एव these कृताकृते things committed or omitted न not तपतः troubles, affects एनम् him.

 \[This passage seeks to show that the entire Vedas except the portion that deals with rites having material ends are applicable to the subject of Self by demonstrating that desire, work and ignorance are attributes of the non-Self.\]

 The infinite unborn Self which consists of knowledge and is surrounded by the organs lives in the ether that is within the Lotus of the heart¹. The Self is the controller of all (Hiranyagarbha, Indra and the rest), their Lord, their Ruler. It does not improve from the previous state by the accession of some attributes through good work enjoined by the scriptures, nor falls from the previous state through bad work forbidden by the scriptures². The Self is the supreme Lord of all, the independent Ruler and absolute Protector of all beings from Hiranyagarbha down to a clump of grass. The Self is the bank, the boundary for



the non-separation of these worlds (from the earth to the world of Hiranyagarbha) distinct from one another. The Brahmana³ as well as the Kshatriyas and the Vaishyas wish to realise this Self by daily reading of the Vedas, by rites performed with things and those consisting of knowledge, by charity⁴, by all forms of austerity such as Krichhra, Candrayana, etc. as well as by fasting⁵. One becomes a man of meditation by the Knowledge of this Self. Seeking this Self alone, monks relinquish all rites and renounce their homes. The ancient knowers of the Self did not desire progeny, as also rites and meditation on conditioned Brahman, the three means respectively to the three external worlds. They thought— What shall we do with them? We have already realised the Self who is without hunger or thirst, prior or posterior, interior or exterior. They renounced their desire for sons, for wealth and for the worlds and wandered about as mendicants⁶. The desire for sons is the same as the desire for wealth. Again, the desire for the wealth is the same as the desire for the worlds. Both are indeed desires and cannot lead us to Self-knowledge. The Self is that infinite entity which has been described as 'Not this, Not this.' The Self is incomprehensible, for It is never comprehended



by the intellect. The Self is imperishable for It never perishes. The Self is unattached, for It never gets attached to any object. The Self is unfettered, for It is never pained nor suffers misery. That is why the knower of the Self is never overcome by the two following thoughts— 'I did a sinful act for this reason, for example, the maintenance of the body'; and 'I did a meritorious act such as the performance of sacrifice or charity for this reason.' The Knower of Brahman goes beyond both the good and evil actions. Things committed or omitted do not affect him.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. Ether is the seat of the intellect. The Self identified with the intellect lies there.

2\. The Self is not connected with any work and therefore is not modified by any merit or demerit.

3\. Three higher castes that are equally entitled to the study of the Vedas are implied by the word 'Brahmanas'.

4\. It destroys sins and increases one's merits.

5\. Real meaning is the dispassionate enjoyment of sense-objects.

6\. Because this world consists of ends and means; but the Self cannot be realised by any means whatsoever. To try to realise the Self by any means would be like swimming on land under the impression that it is water or like looking for the foot-prints of birds in the sky.\]

——————————————————————————————

** तदेतदृचाऽभ्युक्तम्। एष नित्यो महिमा ब्राह्मणस्य न वर्धते कर्मणा नो कनीयान्। तस्यैव स्यात्पदवित्तं विदित्वा न**



**लिप्यते कर्मणा पापकेनेति। तस्मादेवंविच्छान्तो दान्त उपरतस्तितिक्षुः समाहितो भूत्वाऽऽत्मन्येवाऽऽत्मानं पश्यति सर्वमात्मानं पश्यति नैनं पाप्मा तरति सर्वं पाप्मानं तरति नैनं पाप्मा तपति सर्वं पाप्मानं तपति विपापो विरजोऽविचिकित्सो ब्राह्मणो भवत्येष ब्रह्मलोकः सम्राडेनं प्रापितोऽसीति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः सोऽहं भगवते विदेहान्ददामि मां चापि सह दास्यायेति॥२३॥**

 तत् That एतत् this अभ्युक्तम् is said, is expressed ऋचा by the (following) Rik (verse): एषः It (is) नित्यः eternal, changeless महिमा glory ब्राह्मणस्य of a knower of Brahman. वर्धते (The glory) increases, undergoes growth न not कनीयान् decreases, undergoes decay न not उ indeed कर्मणा by work. स्यात् (One) should be पदवित् \* the knower of the nature तस्य of that (glory) एव alone विदित्वा knowing तम् It (glory) लिप्ययते (one) is touched (affected) न not पापकेन इति by evil कर्मणा action. तस्मात् Therefore एवंवित् such a knower भूत्वा becoming शान्तः self-controlled, desisting from the sense activities, दान्तः calm averse to desires उपरतः withdrawn (into himself), free from all desires तितिक्षुः painstaking, indifferent to the pairs of opposites समाहितः concentrated, attaining one-pointedness पश्यति sees आत्मानम् the self आत्मनि एव in (his own) self पश्यति sees सर्वम् all आत्मानम् as the seif पाप्मा evil न not तरति overwhelms एनम् him, the knower तरति (but he goes beyond, transcends सर्वम् all पाप्मानम् evil

——————————————————————————————

\* 'Pada' literally means what is attained or known. Real meaning of the word is the nature of the glory of Self-Knowledge.

——————————————————————————————



पाप्मा evil न not तपति troubles, affects एनम् him तपति (he) consumes, burns सर्वम् all पाप्मानम् evil; भवति (he) becomes विपापः sinless, free from merit and demerit विरजः taintless, free from desires अविचिकित्सः free from doubts ब्राह्मणः (and) a knower of Brahman. एषः This (identity) ब्रह्मलोकः (is) the world of Brahman सम्राट् O Emperor; असि (you) are प्रापितः possessed of एनम् इति It उवाच ह said याज्ञवल्क्यः Yājnavalkya सः That अहम् I ददामि give (you) विदेहान् the dominion of Videha भगवते Venerable Sir, च and माम् myself अपि too सह with (it) दास्याय इति to attend on (you) as a servant.

 What has been stated by the Brahmana is said by this verse: This is the changeless¹ glory of a Knower of Brahman who has given up all desires. The glory of Self-Knowledge undergoes no growth by merit nor decay by demerit. Therefore one should know the nature of that glory alone. Knowing this glory alone one is not affected by good and evil; for both are evil to a Knower of Self. Therefore such a knower desists from the activities of the external organs, becomes averse to activities of the internal organ and free from desires of the mind and indifferent to the pairs of the opposites, attains one-pointedness by dissociating the mind from the movement of the organs. He sees the Supreme Self in his own Self. He sees nothing different even by a hair's breadth from the Self². Evil does not overwhelm the Knower



of Self for he goes beyond all good and evil by realising them as his Self. Evil consisting of what has been done or not done does not affect him by producing the desired result or sin; but he burns all good and evil to ashes with the fire of Self-Knowledge. He becomes devoid of merit and demerit as well as free from doubts and desires. He becomes a Knower of Brahman with the firm conviction that he is the Self of all, the Supreme Brahman. 'This identity with Supreme Self is the world of Brahman, O Emperor, and you are possessed of It.'— Said Yājnavalkya. Janaka replied. "Venerable Sir, I give the whole dominion of Videha and myself too with it to attend on you as a servant."

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. Other glories due to work are impermanent, but the glory of Self-Knowledge is permanent.

2\. By the power of that Knowledge the three states of waking, dream and sleep become same to him.\]

——————————————————————————————

** स वा एष महानज आत्माऽन्नादो वसुदानो विन्दते वसु य एवं वेद॥२४॥**

 सः That वै verily एषः this महान् great अजः birthless, unborn आत्मा self (is) अन्नादः the eater of food वसुदानः (and) the giver (enjoyer) of wealth. यः (He) who वेद knows एवम् thus विन्दते receives, obtains वसु wealth (fruits of one's work).



 This great unborn Self verily dwells in all beings and eats all foods and enjoys all fruits of the works. He who knows this unborn Self as endowed with the above attributes obtains the fruits of every body's actions as their Self.

 \[This passage sums up the gist of the whole Upanishad.\]

 **स वा एष महानज आत्माऽजरोऽमरोऽमृतोऽभयो ब्रह्माभयं वै ब्रह्माभय‍ꣳ हि वै ब्रह्म भवति य एवं वेद॥२५॥ इति चतुर्थं ब्राह्मणम्॥४॥**

 सः That वै verily एषः this महान् great अजः birthless, unborn आत्मा self (is) अजरः undecaying, अमरः immortal, अमृतः undying, अभयः fearless, ब्रह्म Brahman, vast, infinite; हि for ब्रह्म Brahman वै indeed (is) अभयम् devoid of fear हि because यः (He) who वेद knows एवम् thus वै verily भवति becomes अभयम् the fearless ब्रह्म Brahman.

 This great unborn Self is verily undecaying,¹ immortal, undying and fearless Brahman. Brahman indeed is devoid of fear. He who knows this unborn Self as described above becomes verily fearless Brahman.²

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. It does not wear off.

2\. This is the purport of the whole Upanishad put in a nutshell.\]

——————————————————————————————



**CHAPTER FOUR: SECTION FIVE**

 ** अथ ह याज्ञवल्क्यस्य द्वे भार्ये बभूवतुर्मैत्रेयी च कात्यायनी च तयोर्ह मैत्रेयी ब्रह्मवादिनी बभूव स्त्रीप्रज्ञैव तर्हि कात्यायन्यथ ह याज्ञवल्क्योऽन्यद्वृत्तमुपाकरिष्यन्॥१॥**

 अथ Now ह it is said द्वे two भार्ये wives बभूवतुः were there याज्ञवल्क्यस्य of Yājnavalkya— मैत्रेयी च Maitreyi च and कात्यायनी Kātyāyani. तयोः ह Of these two (wives) मैत्रेयी Maitreyi बभूव was ब्रह्मवादिनी conversant with Brahman, fond of discussing about Brahman तर्हि while, then कात्यायनी Kātyāyani एव was only स्त्रीप्रज्ञा possessed with domestic wisdom, wise in feminine (household) duties. अथ ह Now, one day याज्ञवल्क्यः Yājnavalkya उपाकरिष्यन् wishing to embrace अन्यत् another (monastic) वृत्तम् life.

 \[Madhukanda predominates in scriptural statements while the Yājnavalkya Kanda preponderates in logical reasoning. What was ascertained in the former in the light of the scriptures is established by arguments in the latter. This section which is relating to Maitreyi concludes the same topic after the method of the authorities on logic. It is rightly said in 'Gautama Nyaya Sutras' (1-1-39)—Conclusion is confirmed by restatement of a proposition after giving the reason.\]

 Now the sage Yājnavalkya, it is said, had two wives named Maitreyi and Kātyāyani. of these



two wives Maitreyi was conversant with discussions on Brahman while Kātyāyani was wise in feminine duties. One day wishing to renounce the world and to embrace monastic life,

** मैत्रेयीति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः प्रव्रजिष्यन्वा अरेऽहमस्मात्स्थानादस्मि हन्त तेऽनया कात्यायन्याऽन्तं करवाणीति॥२॥**

 याज्ञवल्क्यः Yājnavalkya उवाच ह said इति thus अरे my dear मैत्रेयि Maitreyi अहम् I अस्मि am प्रव्रजिष्यन् going to renounce, about to give up वै verily अस्मात् from this स्थानात् place, life हन्त permit me करवाणि to make अन्तम् end, settlement ते with you अनया with this कात्यायन्या इति Kātyāyani.

 Yājnavalkya said to Maitreyi, "My dear, I am about to give up this householder's life and take up the monk's robe. Permit me to make a settlement between you and that Kātyāyani."

 **सा होवाच मैत्रेयी यन्नु म इयं भगोः सर्वा पृथिवी वित्तेन पूर्णा स्यात्स्यां न्वहं तेनामृताऽऽहो३ नेति नेति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यो यथैवोपकरणवतां जीवितं तथैव ते जीवित‍ꣳ स्यादमृतत्वस्य तु नाऽऽशाऽस्ति वित्तेनेति॥३॥**

 सा That मैत्रेयी Maitreyi उवाच ह said भगोः Venerable Sir यत्नु if इयम् this सर्वा all, entire पृथिवी earth पूर्णा full वित्तेन by wealth स्यात् be, belong मे mine आहो well अहम् I स्यां नु shall become अमृता immortal तेन by it न इति (or)



not याज्ञवल्क्यः Yājnavalkya उवाचह said न इति no यथा एव just as जीवितम् the life उपकरणवताम् of those having plenty of things, abundance of objects तथा एव so ते your जीवितम् life स्यात् will be तु but वित्तेन by wealth न not अस्ति there is आशा hope अमृतत्वस्य of immortality.

 Maitreyi said, "Venerable Sir, if indeed this entire earth full of wealth belonged to me, tell me, should I attain immortality by it or not?" 'No' replied Yājnavalkya 'your life will be just like the life of people enriched with abundance of objects. But there is no hope of immortality by wealth.'

** सा होवाच मैत्रेयी येनाहं नामृता स्यां किमहं तेन कुर्यां यदेव भगवान्वेद तदेव मे ब्रूहीति॥४॥**

 सा That मैत्रेयी Maitreyi उवाच ह said किम् what अहम्I कुर्याम् shall do तेन with that (rites to be performed through wealth) येन by which अहम् I न not स्याम् shall be अमृता immortal. ब्रूहि Tell मे me भगवान् revered Sir तत् that एव only यत् which एव alone वेद (you) know.

 Then Maitreyi said— 'What shall I do with the rites to be performed through wealth? For they are unable to make me immortal. Tell me, revered Sir, the means of immortality which you know so well.'



 ** स होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः प्रिया वै खलु नो भवती सती प्रियमवृधद्धन्त तर्हि भवत्येतद्व्याख्यास्यामि ते व्याचक्षाणस्य तु मे निदिध्यासस्वेति॥५॥**

 सः That याज्ञवल्क्यः Yājnavalkya उवाचह said वै खलु verily भवती you सती being नः our, my प्रियम् dear, beloved अवृधत् have increased प्रियम् (what is) dear (to me in you). भवति my dear हन्त well तर्हि therefore व्याख्यास्यामि (I) will explain एतत् it ते to you तु but निदिध्यासस्व meditate मे upon me व्याचक्षाणस्य while explaining.

 Yājnavalkya said—You have been truly dear to me even before. Now you have increased what is dear to me in you. If you wish, my dear, to know the means of immortality, I will explain them to you. While I explain them please meditate upon their meaning.

 ** स होवाच न वा अरे पत्युः कामाय पतिः प्रियो भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय पतिः प्रियो भवति। न वा अरे जायायै कामाय जाया प्रिया भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय जाया प्रिया भवति। न वा अरे पुत्राणां कामाय पुत्राः प्रिया भवन्त्यात्मनस्तु कामाय पुत्राः प्रिया भवन्ति। न वा अरे वित्तस्य कामाय वित्तं प्रियं भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय वित्तं प्रियं भवति। न वा अरे पशूनां कामाय पशवः प्रिया भवन्त्यात्मनस्तु कामाय पशवः प्रिया भवन्ति। न**



**वा अरे ब्रह्मणः कामाय ब्रह्म प्रियं भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय ब्रह्म प्रियं भवति। न वा अरे क्षत्त्रस्य कामाय क्षत्त्रं प्रियं भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय क्षत्त्रं प्रियं भवति। न वा अरे लोकानां कामाय लोकाः प्रिया भवन्त्यात्मनस्तु कामाय लोकाः प्रिया भवन्ति। न वा अरे देवानां कामाय देवाः प्रिया भवन्त्यात्मनस्तु कामाय देवाः प्रिया भवन्ति। न वा अरे वेदानां कामाय वेदाः प्रिया भवन्त्यात्मनस्तु कामाय वेदाः प्रिया भवन्ति। न वा अरे भूतानां कामाय भूतानि प्रियाणि भवन्त्यात्मनस्तु कामाय भूतानि प्रियाणि भवन्ति। न वा अरे सर्वस्य कामाय सर्वं प्रियं भवत्यात्मनस्तु कामाय सर्वं प्रियं भवति। आत्मा वा अरे द्रष्टव्यः श्रोतव्यो मन्तव्यो निदिध्यासितव्यो मैत्रेय्यात्मनि खल्वरे दृष्टे श्रुते मते विज्ञात इद‍ꣳ सर्वं विदितम्॥६॥**

 सः He (Yajnavalkya) उवाचह said न not कामाय for the sake पत्युः of the husband वै verily अरे my dear (Maitreyi) पतिः the husband भवति is प्रियः dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self पतिः the husband भवति is प्रियः dear. न Not कामाय for the sake जायायै of the wife वै verily अरे my dear (Maitreyi) जाया the wife भवति is प्रिया dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self जाया the wife भवति is प्रिया dear. न Not कामाय for the sake पुत्राणाम् of the sons वै verily अरे my dear (Maitreyi) पुत्राः the sons भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self पुत्राः the sons भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear. न Not कामाय for the sake वित्तस्य



of wealth वै verily अरे my dear (Maitreyi) वित्तम् the wealth भवति is प्रियम् dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self वित्तम् the wealth भवति is प्रियम् dear. न Not कामाय for the sake पशूनाम् of the animals वै verily अरे my dear पशवः the animals भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self पशवः the animals भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear. न Not कामाय for the sake ब्रह्मणः of the Brahman वै verily अरे my dear ब्रह्म the Brahman भवति is प्रियम् dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self ब्रह्म the Brahman भवति is प्रियम् dear. न Not कामाय for the sake क्षत्त्रस्य of the Kshatriya वै verily अरे my dear क्षत्त्रम् the Kshatriya भवति is प्रियम् dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self क्षत्त्रम् the Kshatriya भवति is प्रियम् dear. न Not कामानाम् for the sake लोकानाम् of the worlds वै verily अरे my dear लोकाः the worlds भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self लोकाः the worlds भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear. न Not कामाय for the sake देवानाम् of the gods वै verily अरे my dear देवाः the gods भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self देवाः the gods भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear. न Not कामाय for the sake वेदानाम् of the Vedas वै verily अरे my dear वेदाः the Vedas भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self वेदाः the Vedas भवन्ति are प्रियाः dear. न Not कामाय for the sake भूतानाम् of the beings वै verily अरे my dear भूतानि the beings भवन्ति are प्रियाणि dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self भूतानि the beings भवन्ति are प्रियाणि dear. न Not कामाय for the sake सर्वस्य of all वै verily अरे my dear सर्वम् all भवति are प्रियम् dear तु but कामाय for the sake आत्मनः of the self



सर्वम् all भवति is प्रियम् dear. वै Verily अरे my dear आत्मा the self द्रष्टव्यः should be seen, realised श्रोतव्यः should be heard of मन्तव्यः should be reflected on निदिध्यासितव्यः should be meditated upon. सर्वम् All इदम् this विदितम् (is) known, realised खलु indeed अरे my dear आत्मनि the self दृष्टे being seen, realised— श्रुते being heard of मते being reflected on विज्ञाते known, ascertained, meditated upon.

 Yajnavalkya said, 'Verily the husband is dear not for the sake of the husband, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self that he is dear. Verily the wife is dear not for the sake of the wife, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self that she is dear. Verily the sons are dear not for the sake of the sons, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self they are dear. Verily the wealth is dear not for the sake of the wealth, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self that it is dear. Verily the animals are dear not for the sake of the animals, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self that they are dear. Verily the Brahman is dear not for the sake of the Brahman, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self that he is dear. Verily the Kshatriya is dear not for the sake of the Kshatriya, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self that he is dear. Verily the worlds are dear not for the sake of the worlds, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self that they



are dear. Verily the gods are dear not for the sake of the gods, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self that they are dear. Verily the Vedas are dear not for the sake of the Vedas, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self that they are dear. Verily the beings are dear not for the sake of the beings, Maitreyi, but for the sake of the Self that they are dear. Verily all are dear not for the sake of all, Maitreyi, but for the sake of Self that all are dear. The Self, my dear, should be realised—by being first heard of from teachers and scriptures, then reflected¹ on through reasoning and lastly meditated upon. When the Self, my dear, is known by being heard of, reflected on and meditated upon, all this that is other than the Self is known for there is nothing other than the Self.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Discussed through reasoning.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **ब्रह्म तं परादाद्योऽन्यत्राऽऽत्मनो ब्रह्म वेद क्षत्त्रं तं परादाद्योऽन्यत्राऽऽत्मनः क्षत्त्रं वेद लोकास्तं परादुर्योऽन्यत्राऽऽत्मनो लोकान्वेद देवास्तं परादुर्योऽन्यत्राऽऽत्मनो देवान्वेद वेदास्तं परादुर्योऽन्यत्राऽऽत्मनो वेदान्वेद भूतानि तं परादुर्योऽन्यत्राऽऽत्मनो भूतानि वेद सर्वं तं परादाद्योऽन्यत्राऽऽत्मनः सर्वं वेदेदं ब्रह्मेदं क्षत्त्रमिमे लोका इमे देवा इमे वेदा इमानि भूतानीद‍ꣳ सर्वं यदयमात्मा॥७॥**



 ब्रह्म The Brahman परादात् ousts, abandons तम् him यः who वेद knows, looks on ब्रह्म the Brahman अन्यत्र different आत्मनः from the self. क्षत्रम् The Kshatriya परादात् ousts, abandons तम् him यः who वेद knows, looks on क्षत्रम् the Kshatriya अन्यत्र different आत्मनः from the self. लोकाः The worlds परादुः oust, abandon तम् him यः who वेद knows, looks on लोकान् the worlds अन्यत्र different आत्मनः from the self. देवाः The gods परादुः oust, abandon तम् him यः who वेद knows देवान् the gods अन्यत्र different आत्मनः from the self. वेदाः The Vedas परादुः oust तम् him यः who वेद knows वेदान् the Vedas अन्यत्र different आत्मनः from the self. भूतानि creatures, beings परादुः oust तम् him यः who वेद knows भूतानि the beings अन्यत्र different आत्मनः from the self. सर्वम् All परादात् oust तम् him यः who वेद knows सर्वम् all अन्यत्र different आत्मनः from all. इदम् This ब्रह्म Brahman इदम् this क्षत्रम् Kshatriya इमे these लोकाः worlds इमे these देवाः gods इमे these वेदाः Vedas इमानि these भूतानि creatures, beings सर्वम् all इदम् this (is) यत् that अयम् this आत्मा Self.

  The Brahman abandons him who looks on the Brahman as different from the Self. The Kshatriya abandons him who looks on the Kshatriya as different from the Self. The worlds abandon him who looks on the worlds as different from the Self. The gods abandon him who looks on the gods as different from the Self. The Vedas abandon him who looks on the Vedas as different from the Self. The creatures abandon him who



looks on the creatures as different from the Self. All abandon¹ him who looks on all as different from the Self. This Brāhmana, this Kshatriya, these worlds, these gods, these Vedas, these creatures and this all are indeed that Self.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES— 1. Bar him from the absolute aloofness of the Self.\]

——————————————————————————————

** स यथा दुन्दुभेर्हन्यमानस्य न बाह्याञ्शब्दाञ्छक्नुयाद्ग्रहणाय दुन्दुभेस्तु ग्रहणेन दुन्दुभ्याघातस्य वा शब्दो गृहीतः॥८॥**

 यथा As सः he (a man) न not शक्नुयात् is able ग्रहणाय for seizure बाह्यान् of the external शब्दान् sounds दुन्दुभेः of a drum हन्यमानस्य being beaten तु but शब्दः the sound गृहीतः (is) seized ग्रहणेन by the seizure दुन्दुभेः of the drum वा or दुन्दुभ्याघातस्य the drum-beater.

 As the sounds of a drum when it is beaten cannot be seized externally by themselves but the sound is seized when the drum or its beater is seized;

** स यथा शङ्खस्य ध्मायमानस्य न बाह्याञ्छब्दाञ्छक्नुयाद्ग्रहणाय शङ्खस्य तु ग्रहणेन शङ्खध्मस्य वा शब्दो गृहीतः॥ ९॥**

 यथा As सः he (a man) न not शक्नुयात् is able ग्रहणाय for seizure बाह्यान् of the external शब्दान् sounds शङ्खस्य of a conch ध्मायमानस्य being blown तु but शब्दः the sound गृहीतः (is)



seized ग्रहणेन by the seizure शङ्खस्य of the conch वा or शङ्खध्मस्य of the conch blower.

 As the sounds of a conch when it is blown cannot be seized externally by themselves but the sound is seized when the conch or its blower is seized;

** स यथा वीणायै वाद्यमानायै न बाह्याञ्छब्दाञ्छक्नुयाद्ग्रहणाय वीणायै तु ग्रहणेन वीणावादस्य वा शब्दो गृहीतः॥१०॥**

 यथा As स he (a man) न not शक्नुयात् is able ग्रहणाय for seizure बाह्यान् of the external शब्दान् sounds वीणायै of a Vina (lute) वाद्यमानायै being played तु but ग्रहणेन by the seizure वीणायै of the lute वा or वीणावादस्य the lute played शब्दः the sound गृहीतः (is) seized.

 As the sounds of a lute when it is played cannot be seized externally by themselves but the sound is seized when the lute or its player is seized;

 ** स यथाऽऽर्द्रैधाग्नेरभ्याहितस्य पृथग्धूमा विनिश्चरन्त्येवं वा अरेऽस्य महतो भूतस्य निःश्वसितमेतद्यदृग्वेदो यजुर्वेदः सामवेदोऽथर्वाङ्गिरस इतिहासः पुराणं विद्या उपनिषदः श्लोकाः सूत्राण्यनुव्याख्यानानि व्याख्यानानीष्टꣳ हुतमाशितं पायितमयं च लोकः परश्च लोकः सर्वाणि च भूतान्यस्यैवैतानि सर्वाणि निःश्वसितानि॥११॥**



 सः That (the example is) यथा as अभ्याहितस्य from a blazing आर्द्रैधाग्नेः fire lighted with damp fuel पृथक् different धूमाः smokes विनिश्चरन्ति issue, proceed एवं वा even so अरे my dear (Maitreyi) अस्य of this महतः great, infinite भूतस्य being, reality निःश्वसितम् (has) breathed out, issued forth एतत् that यत् which (is) ऋग्वेदः the Rig-Veda, यजुर्वेदः Yajur-Veda, सामवेदः Sama-Veda, अथर्वाङ्गिरसः Atharvāngirasa, इतिहासः history, पुराणम् mythology, विद्या arts, उपनिषदः Upanishads, श्लोकाः verses, सूत्राणि aphorisms अनुव्याख्यानानि elucidations, व्याख्यानानि explanations, इष्टम् sacrifices, हुतम् oblations in the fire, आशितम् food, पायितम् drink च and अयम् this लोकम् world च and परः the next लोकः world सर्वाणि all भूतानि creatures, beings अस्य of this एव alone एतानि these सर्वाणि all निःश्वसितानि (are) the out-breaths.

 As clouds of smoke proceed from a blazing fire lighted with damp fuel, even so, dear Maitreyi, the Rig-Veda, Sāma-Veda, Atharvangirasa, history, mythology, arts, Upanishads, verses, aphorisms, elucidations, explanations, sacrifices, oblations in the fire, food, drink, this world, the next world and all creatures have issued forth from this great Being. These are all indeed the out-breaths of this Infinite Reality—the Supreme Self.

 ** स यथा सर्वासामपाꣳ समुद्र एकायनमेवꣳ सर्वेषाꣳ स्पर्शानां त्वगेकायनमेव‍ꣳ सर्वेषां गन्धानां नासिके एकायनमेवꣳ सर्वेषाꣳ रसानां जिह्वैकायनमेवꣳ सर्वेषाꣳ रूपाणां चक्षुरेकायनमेव‍ꣳ**



**सर्वेषाꣳ शब्दानाꣳ श्रोत्रमेकायनमेव‍ꣳ सर्वेषाꣳ सङ्कल्पानां मन एकायनमेवꣳ सर्वासां विद्यानाꣳ हृदयमेकायनमेवꣳ सर्वेषां कर्मणाꣳ हस्तावेकायनमेवꣳ सर्वेषामानन्दानामुपस्थ एकायनमेवꣳ सर्वेषां विसर्गाणां पायुरेकायनमेव‍ꣳ सर्वेषामध्वनां पादावेकायनमेवꣳ सर्वेषां वेदानां वागेकायनम्॥१२॥**

 सः That (the example is) यथा as सर्वासाम् of all अपाम् waters समुद्रः the ocean (is) एकायनम् (= एक + अयनम्) the one goal, sole receptacle; एवम् as सर्वेषाम् of all स्पर्शानाम् touch त्वक् the skin (is) एकायनम् the one goal, sole centre; एवम् as सर्वेषाम् of all गन्धानाम् odours नासिके the nostrils (are) एकायनम् the one goal, sole receptacle; एवम् as सर्वेषाम् of all रसानाम् tastes, savours जिह्वा the tongue (is) एकायनम् the one goal, sole centre; एवम् as सर्वेषाम् of all रूपाणाम् colours चक्षुः the eye (is) एकायनम् the one goal; एवम् as सर्वेषाम् of all शब्दानाम् sounds श्रोत्रम् the ear (is) एकायनम् the one goal, one source; एवम् as सर्वेषाम् of all सङ्कल्पानाम् deliberations, determinations मनः the mind (is) एकायनम् the one goal; एवम् as सर्वासाम् of all विद्यानाम् knowledges हृदयम् the intellect (is) एकायनम् the one goal; एवम् as सर्वेषाम् all कर्मणाम् actions हस्तौ the hands (are) एकायनम् the one goal; एवम् as सर्वेषाम् of all आनन्दानाम् enjoyment उपस्थः the generative organ (is) एकायनम् the one goal; एवम् as सर्वेषाम् of all विसर्गाणाम् excretions पायुः the arms (is) एकायनम् the one goal; एवम् as सर्वेषाम् of all अध्वनाम् movements पादौ the legs (are) एकायनम् the one goal; एवम् (and) as सर्वेषाम् of all वेदानाम् Vedas वाक् the speech (is) एकायनम् the one goal.



 As all waters find their only source in the ocean, all touches in the skin, all odours in the nostrils, all tastes in the tongue, all colours in the eyes, all sounds in the ear, all deliberations in the mind, all knowledge in the heart, all actions in the hands, all enjoyments in the generative organ, all excretions in the anus, all movements in the feet and all Vedas in speech.

** स यथा सैन्धवघनोऽनन्तरोऽबाह्यः कृत्स्त्रो रसघन एवैवं वा अरेऽयमात्माऽनन्तरोऽबाह्यः कृत्स्त्रः प्रज्ञानघन एवैतेभ्यो भूतेभ्यः समुत्थाय तान्येवानुविनश्यति न प्रेत्य सञ्ज्ञाऽस्तीत्यरे ब्रवीमीति होवाच याज्ञवल्क्यः॥१३॥**

 यथा As सैन्धवघनः a mass of salt अनन्तरः (is) without inside, अबाह्यः without outside. कृत्स्नः entire, whole एव indeed रसघनः a mass of taste एवं वै even so अरे my dear अयम् this आत्मा Self अनन्तरः (is) without inside, अबाह्यः without outside, कृत्स्नः entire, whole एव verily प्रज्ञानघनः a mass of knowledge (it) समुत्थाय appearing, coming out (as a separate entity) एतेभ्यः from these भूतेभ्यः elements अनुविनश्यति is destroyed, vanishes तानि with them प्रेत्य attaining (this oneness) अस्ति there is न not सञ्ज्ञा इति (particular) knowledge, name ब्रवीमि (I) say अरे इति my dear (Maitreyi) उवाच ह said याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya.

 Yajnavalkya said— as a mass of salt has neither inside nor outside, is indeed an entire mass



of taste, even so the Self has neither the inside nor the outside, is verily an entire mass of knowledge. The Self appears as a separate entity from these elements and Its separateness is dissolved with them through knowledge. After It attains this oneness, It has no more particular¹ knowledge. This is what I say, dear Maitreyi.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. Formerly It had particular knowledge owing to the particular combinations with the elements. Those combinations being lost now, particular knowledge is destroyed.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** सा होवाच मैत्रेय्यत्रैव मा भगवान्मोहान्तमापीपिपन्न वा अहमिमं विजानामीति स होवाच न वा अरेऽहं मोहं ब्रवीम्यविनाशी वा अरेऽयमात्माऽनुच्छित्तिधर्मा॥१४॥**

 सा That मैत्रेयी Maitreyi उवाच ह said इति thus एव just अत्र here भगवान् Venerable Sir आपीपिपत् have thrown, have landed मा me मोहान्तम् in the midst of confusion अहम् I न not विजानामि वै at all comprehend, understand clearly इमम् it सः he (Yajnavalkya) उवाचह said, replied अहम् I न not ब्रवीमि say वै verily अरे my dear, beloved मोहम् confusion anything bewildering वै verily अरे my dear, beloved अयम् this आत्मा Self (is) अनुच्छित्तिधर्मा of indestructible nature, undying अविनाशी imperishable.

 Maitreyi said, 'Venerable Sir, just here you have confounded me. I do not clearly understand



this Self that you have described.' Yajnavalkya replied: Beloved Maitreyi, I say nothing that is bewildering. This Self is verily imperishable and indestructible.¹

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES—1. Not subject to destruction either in the form of change or extinction.\]

——————————————————————————————

** यत्र हि द्वैतमिव भवति तदितर इतरं पश्यति तदितर इतरं जिघ्रति तदितर इतरꣳ रसयते तदितर इतरमभिवदति तदितर इतरꣳ शृणोति तदितर इतरं मनुते तदितर इतरꣳ स्पृशति तदितर इतरं विजानाति यत्र त्वस्य सर्वमात्मैवाभूत्तत्केन कं पश्येत्तत्केन कं जिघ्रेत्तत्केन कꣳ रसयेत्तत्केन कमभिवदेत्तत्केन कꣳ शृणुयात्तत्केन कं मन्वीत तत्केन कꣳ स्पृशेत्तत्केन कं विजानीयाद्येनेदꣳ सर्वं विजानाति तं केन विजानीयात्स एष नेति नेत्यात्माऽगृह्यो न हि गृह्यतेऽशीर्यो न हि शीर्यतेऽसङ्गो न हि सज्यतेऽसितो न व्यथते न रिष्यति विज्ञातारमरे केन विजानीयादित्युक्तानुशासनाऽसि मैत्रेय्येतावदरे खल्वमृतत्वमिति होक्त्वा याज्ञवल्क्यो विजहार॥१५॥ इति पञ्चमं ब्राह्मणम्॥५॥**

 हि For यत्र when भवति there is द्वैतम् duality इव as it were तत् then इतरः one पश्यति sees इतरम् the other, something तत् then इतरः one जिघ्रति smells इतरम् the other, something तत् then इतरः one रसयते tastes इतरम् the other, something तत् then इतरः one अभिवदति speaks इतरम् the other, something



तत् then इतरः one शृणोति hears इतरम् the other, something तत् then इतरः one मनुते thinks इतरम् the other, something तत् then इतरः one स्पृशिति touches इतरम् the other, something तत् then इतरः one विजानाति knows इतरम् the other, something तु but यत्र when अस्य his (of a knower of Brahman) सर्वम् all अभूत् has become आत्मा the Self एव only तत् then केन by what कम् what पश्येत् (one) should see तत् then केन by what जिघ्रेत् should smell कम् what तत् then केन by what रसयेत् (one) should taste कम् what तत् then कम् what अभिवदेत् (one) should speak केन by what तत् then केन by what शृणुयात् (one) should hear केन by what कम् what तत् then केन by what मन्वीत (one) should think कम् what तत् then केन by what स्पृशेत् (one) should touch कम् what तत् then केन by what विजानीयात् (one) should know कम् what येन by which विजानाति (one) knows सर्वम् all इदम् this केन by what विजानीयात् (one) should know तत् that (self) एषः this आत्मा Self (is) सः that (which has been described as) न इति not this न इति not this. अगृह्यः (It is) incomprehensible, imperceptible हि for न not गृह्यते (It is) perceived, comprehended अशीर्यः (It is) imperishable, undecaying हि for न not शीर्यते (It) decays, perishes असङ्गः (It is) unattached हि for न not सज्यते (It is) attached असितः (It is) unfettered न not व्यथते (It) is pained, feels pains न not रिष्यति is injured, अरे my dear केन by what विजानीयात् (one) should know विज्ञातारम् the knower मैत्रेयि Maitreyi इति असि (you) are उक्तानुशासना told the instruction, given the teaching अरे my dear (Maitreyi) एतावत् this (knowledge of self) खलु indeed (is) अमृतत्वम् इति immortality उक्त्वा



ह saying, describing (this) याज्ञवल्क्यः Yajnavalkya विजहार left home, became a monk.

 \[The text brings out the conclusion that all the four chapters are exclusively devoted to Self alone and that Self is the last word of the entire Upanishad and that renunciation of everything is the only means of attaining this Self and immortality.\]

 For when there is duality, as it were, then one sees the other, one smells the other, one tastes the other, one speaks the other, one hears the other, one thinks the other, one touches the other, one knows the other. But when one's all has become the Self, then what should one see by what, what should one smell by what, what should one taste by what, what should one speak by what, what should one hear by what, what should one think by what, what should one touch by what, what should one know by what? By what should one know the Self by which all this is known? The Self is that Absolute Entity which has been described as 'Not this, not this.' It is incomprehensible, for It is never comprehended as a senseobject. The Self is imperishable, for It never perishes. The Self is unattached, for It is never attached to anything. The Self is unfettered for



It is neither pained nor injured. By what, O Maitreyi, should one know the Knower¹? So, you have been given the instructions about the Self-Knowledge, Maitreyi. This Knowledge of Self is indeed the only means of attaining immortality, my dear Maitreyi. Describing this Self-Knowledge Yājnavalkya became a monk.²

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The Knower which is the Self is never known as an object or an idea.

2\. Monastic life enjoins absolute freedom from rites and Self-Knowledge is totally independent of rites. Renunciation is the culmination of the renunciation of all household duties and rites.\]

——————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER FOUR: SECTION SIX**

 **अथ वꣳशः पौतिमाष्यो गौपवनाद्गौपवनः पौतिमाष्यात्पौतिमाष्यो गौपवनाद्गौपवनः कौशिकात्कौशिकः कौण्डिन्यात्कौण्डिन्यः शाण्डिल्याच्छाण्डिल्यः कौशिकाच्च गौतमाच्च गोतमः॥१॥**

 अथः Now बंशः the line (of teachers)— पौतिमाष्यः Pautimāshya गौपवनात् (received it) from Gaupavana, गौपवनः Gaupavana पौतिमाष्यात् from (another) Pautimāshya पौतिमाष्यः Pautimāshya गौपवनात् from (another) Gaupavana, गौपवनः Gaupavana कौशिकात् from Kaushika, कौशिकः Kaushika कौण्डिन्यात् from Kaundinya, कौण्डिन्यः Kaundinya



शाण्डिल्यात् from Shandilya, शाण्डिल्यः Shāndilya कौशिकात् च from Kaushika, च and गौतमात् from Gautama. गौतमः Gautama, (from Āgniveshya).

 Now follows the line of teachers and pupils by whom the Yājnavalkya Kānda (i.e. third and fourth chapters relating to Yājnavalkya) was handed down: Pautimāshya¹ received it from Gaupavana. Gaupavana from another Pautimāshya. This Pautimāshya from another Gaupavana. This Gaupavana from Kaushika. Kaushika from Kaundinya. Kaundinya from Shāndilya. Shādilya from Kaushika and Gautama. Gautama (from Āgniveshya).

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. From 1-10 the line of teachers agrees with that of the Madhu Kanda.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **आग्निवेश्यादाग्निवेश्यो गार्ग्याद्गार्ग्यो गार्ग्याद्गार्ग्यो गौतमाद्गौतमः सैतवात्सैतवः पाराशर्यायणात्पाराशर्यायणो गार्ग्यायणाद्गार्ग्यायण उद्दालकायनादुद्दालकायनो जाबालायनाज्जाबालायनो माध्यन्दिनायनान्माध्यन्दिनायनः सौकरायणात्सौकरायणः काषायणात्काषायणः सायकायनात्सायकायनः कौशिकायनेः कौशिकायनिः॥२॥**

 आग्निवेश्यात् (Gautama) from Āgniveshya. आग्निवेश्यः Āgniveshya गार्ग्यात् from Gārgya. गार्ग्यः Gārgya गार्ग्यात् from (another) Gārgya. गार्ग्यः (This) Gārgya गौतमात् from (another)



Gautama. गौतमः (This) Gautama सैतवात् from Saitava. सैतवः Saitava पाराशर्य्यायणात् from Pārāsharyāyana. पाराशर्य्यायणः Pārāsharyāyana गार्ग्यायणात् from Gārgyāyana. गार्ग्यायणः Gārgyāyana उद्दालकायनात् from Uddālakāyana. उद्दालकायनः Uddālākayana जाबालायनात् from Jābālāyana. जाबालायनः Jābālāyana मध्यन्दिनायनात् Mādhyandināyana. मध्यन्दिनायनः Mādhyandināyana सौकरायणात् from Saukarāyana. सौकरायणः Saukarāyana काषायणात् from Kāshāyana. काषायणः Kashāyana सायकायनात् from Sāyakāyana. सायकायनः Sāyakāyana कौशिकायनेः Kaushikayani. कौशिकायनिः Kaushikāyani (from Ghrita Kaushika).

 Gautama received it from Āgniveshya. Āngniveshya from Gārgya. Gārgya from another Gārgya. This Gārgya from another Gautama. This Gautama from Saitava. Saitava from Pārāsharyāyana. Pārāsharyāyana from Gārgyāyana. Gārgyāyana from Uddālakāyana. Uddālakāyana from Jābālāyana. Jābālāyana from Mādhyandināyana. Mādhyandināyana from Saukarāyana. Saukarāyana from Kāshāyana. Kāshāyana from Sāyakāyana. Sāyakāyana from Kaushikāyani¹. Kaushikāyani (from Ghritakaushika).

——————————————————————————————

\]\[NOTES— 1. From here the line of teaches agrees again with that of the Madhu Kanda.\]

——————————————————————————————

** घृतकौशिकाद्घृतकौशिकः पाराशर्यायणात्पाराशर्यायणः पाराशर्यात्पाराशर्यो जातूकर्ण्याज्जातूकर्ण्य आसुरायणाच्च यास्का- **



**च्चाऽऽसुरायणस्त्रैवणेस्त्रैवणिरौपजन्धनेरौपजन्धनिरासुरेरासुरिर्भारद्वाजाद्भारद्वाज आत्रेयादात्रेयो माण्टेर्माण्टिर्गौतमाद्गौतमो गौतमाद्गौतमो वात्स्याद्वात्स्यः शाण्डिल्याच्छाण्डिल्यः कैशोर्यात्काप्यात्कैशोर्यः काप्यः कुमारहारितात्कुमारहारितो गालवाद्गालवो विदर्भीकौण्डिन्याद्विदर्भीकौण्डिन्यो वत्सनपातो बाभ्रवाद्वत्सनपाद्बाभ्रवः पथः सौभरात्पन्थाः सौभरोऽयास्यादाङ्गिरसादयास्य आङ्गिरस आभूतेस्त्वाष्ट्रादाभूतिस्त्वाष्ट्रो विश्वरूपात्त्वाष्ट्राद्विश्वरूपस्त्वाष्ट्रोऽश्विभ्यामश्विनौ दधीच आथर्वणाद्दध्यङ्ङाथर्वणोऽथर्वणो दैवादथर्वा दैवो मृत्योः प्राध्वꣳसनान्मृत्युः प्राध्वꣳसनः प्रध्वꣳसनात्प्रध्वꣳसन एकर्षेरेकर्षिर्विप्रचित्तेर्विप्रचित्तिर्व्यष्टेर्व्यष्टिः सनारोः सनारुः सनातनात्सनातनः सनगात्सनगः परमेष्ठिनः परमेष्ठी ब्रह्मणो ब्रह्म स्वयम्भु ब्रह्मणे नमः॥३॥ इति षष्ठं ब्राह्मणम्॥६॥ इति श्रीबृहदारण्यकोपनिषदि चतुर्थोऽध्यायः॥४॥**

 घृतकौशिकः (Kaushikayani) from Ghritakaushika. घृतकौशिकः Ghritakaushika पाराशर्यायणात् from (Pārāsharyāyana. पाराशर्यायणः Pārāsharyāyana पाराशर्यात् from Pārāsharya. पाराशर्यः Pārāsharya जातूकर्ण्यात् from Jātukarnya. जातूकर्ण्यः Jātukarnya आसुरायणात् च from Asurāyana, च and यास्कात् from Yaska. आसुरायणः Asurāyana त्रैवणेः from Traivani. त्रैवणिः Traivani औपजन्धनेः from Aupajandhani. औपजन्धनिः Aupajandhani आसुरेः from Asuri. आसुरिः Asuri भारद्वाजात् from Bhāradwāja. भारद्वाजः Bhāradwāja आत्रेयात् from



Atreya. आत्रेयः Ātreya माण्टेः from Mānti. माण्टिः Mānti गौतमात् from Gautama. गौतमः Gautama गौतमात् from (another) Gautama. गौतमः Gautama वात्स्यात् from Vātsya. वात्स्यः Vātsya शाण्डिल्यात् from Shāndilya. शाण्डिल्यः Shāndilya कैशोर्यात् काप्यात् from Kaishorya Kāpya कैशोर्यः काप्यः Kaishorya Kāpya कुमारहारितात् from Kumārahārita. कुमारहारितः Kumārhārita गालवात् from Gālava. गालवः Gālava विदर्भीकौण्डिन्यात् from Vidarbhi Kaundinya. विदर्भीकौण्डिन्यः Vidarbhikaundinya वात्सनपातः बाभ्रवात् from Vātsanapāt Bābhrava. वात्सनपात् बाभ्रवः Vātsanapāt Bābhrava पथः सौभरात् from Pathin Saubhara पन्थाःसौभरः Pathin Saubhara अयास्यात् आङ्गिरसात् from Ayāsya Āngirasa. अयास्यः आङ्गिरसः Ayāsya Āngirasa आभूतेः त्वाष्ट्रात् from Ābhuti Twāshtra. आभूतिः त्वाष्ट्रः Abhuti Twāshtra विश्वरूपात् त्वाष्ट्रात् from Vishwarupa Twāshtra. विश्वरूपः त्वाष्ट्रः Vishwarupa Twashtra अश्विभ्याम् from the two Ashwins. अश्विनौ The two Ashwins दधीचः आथवर्णात् from Dadhyach Ātharvana. दध्यच् आथर्वणः Dadhyach Ātharvana आथर्वणः दैवात् from Atharvan Daiva. अथर्वा दैवः Atharva Daiva मृत्योः प्राध्वंसनात् from Mrityu Prādhamsana. मृत्युः प्राध्वंसनः Mrityu Prādhamsana प्रध्वंसनः एकर्षेः from Pradhamsana Ekarshi. एकर्षिः Ekarshi विप्रचित्तेः from Viprachitti. विप्रचित्तिः Viprachitti व्यष्टेः from Vyashti. व्यष्टिः Vyashti सनारोः from Sanāru. सनारुः Sanāru सनातनात् from Sanātana. सनातनः Sanātana सनगात् from Sanaga. सनगः Sanaga परमेष्ठिनः from Parameshthin (Viraj). परमेष्ठी Parameshthi (Viraj) ब्रह्मणः from Brahman (Hiranyagarbha). ब्रह्म Brahman (is) स्वयम्भूः Self-existent, नमः adoration, salutation ब्रह्मणे to Brahman.



 (Kaushikāyani) from Ghritakaushika. Ghritakaushika from Pārāsharyāyana. Pārāsharyāyana from Pārāsharya. Pārāsharya from Jātukarnya. Jātukarnya from Asurāyana and Yāska. Asurāyana from Traivani. Traivani from Aupajandhani. Aupajandhani from Āsuri. Āsuri from Bhrādwāja. Bhāradwāja from Ātreya. Ātreya from Mānti. Mānti from Gautama. Gautama from another Gautama. This Gautama from Vātsya. Vātsya from Shāndilya. Shāndilya from Kaishorya Kāpya. Kaishorya Kāpya from Kumārahārita. Kumārahārita from Gālava. Gālava from Vidarbhikaundinya. He from Vatsanapat Bābhrava. He from Pathin Sawvara. He from Ayasya Angirasa. He from Ābhuti Twashtra. He from Vishwarupa Twashtra. He from the two Ashwins. The Ashwins from Dadhyach Ātharvana. He from Ātharvana Daiva. He from Mrityu Prādhvamsana. He from Prādhvamsana. Prādhvamsana from Ekarshi. Ekarshi from Viprachitti. He from Vyashti. Vyashti from Sanāru. Sānaru from Sanātana. Sanātana from Sanaga. Sanaga from Parameshthin (Viraj). Parameshthin from Brahman (Hiranyagarbha). Brahman is Self-existent. Adoration to Brahman.



**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION ONE**

** ॐ पूर्णमदः पूर्णमिदं पूर्णात्पूर्णमुदच्यते। पूर्णस्य पूर्णमादाय पूर्णमेवावशिष्यते। ॐ खं ब्रह्म। खं पुराणं वायुरं खमिति ह स्माऽऽह कौरव्यायणीपुत्रो वेदोऽयं ब्राह्मणा विदुर्वेदैनेन यद्वेदितव्यम्। इति प्रथमं ब्राह्मणम्॥१॥**

  ॐ Om. अदः That, something remote (Supreme Brahman) पूर्णम् (is) full, infinite. इदम् This, something direct (phenomenal Universe) पूर्णम् (is) complete, unlimited. पूर्णम् The full, the boundless, उदच्यते—emanates, proceeds पूर्णात् from the full, आदाय Taking, पूर्णम् the full, the infinite, पूर्णस्य of the full, of the infinite, पूर्णम् the full, the infinite, एव only अवशिष्यते is left, remains. ॐ Om (is) खं the sky, ब्रह्म Brahman. खं The sky (is), पुराणम् ancient, eternal, Absolute. कौरव्यायणीपुत्रः The son of Kauravyāyani आह स्म says, holds, ह indeed, इति this, खम् the (material) sky, वायुरम् containing air. अयम् It (Om). वेदः the Veda ब्राह्मणाः the knowers of Brahman, विदुः know, realise. अनेन Through it (Om) वेद (one) knows, realises, यत् that वेदितव्यम् (which) is to be known.\*

 The Supreme Brahman is infinite. phenomenal Universe also is infinite. The infinite Universe of name and form emanates from the Absolute Brahman.¹ Taking the infinite Universe

——————————————————————————————

\* These two paragraphs are called Mantras.

——————————————————————————————



of apparent otherness from the infinite Absolute, the unconditioned infinite Brahman alone is left.² Om is the sky-Brahman³, the sky that is absolute. The son of Kauravyāyani holds that the sky contained air, but that sky must be material, not absolute. The knowers of Brahman know that the entire Vedas are but Om;⁴ because by meditation⁵ on Om one realises Brahman.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. Similarly Katha Upanishad (4.10) says: 'Whatever is there is here, and whatever is here is there.'

2\. Although the infinite phenomenon proceeds from Brahman; It does not give up its nature, nor becomes less, nor grows more. It remains the same Absolute Reality without interior or exterior, prior or posterior, homogeneous like a lump of salt, and continuous like the sky.

3\. Brahman is the entity specified and sky is the description like blue lotus.

4\. The Vedas issue out of Om. For the Chhandyogya Upanishad (2. 23. 4) says: Om is differentiated into the divisions of Rik, Yajur, Sāman, etc. As by a stick all leaves are pierced, so all speech is pierced by Om.

5\. Om is the best and highest means of Self-knowledge. As the Mahanarayan Upanishad (24.1) says: "One should meditate on the Self repeating Om." Similarly Prasna Upanishad (5. 5) say: "One should meditate on the Supreme Being only through the syllable Om."\]

——————————————————————————————



**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION TWO**

** त्रयाः प्राजापत्याः प्रजापतौ पितरि ब्रह्मचर्यमूषुर्देवा मनुष्या असुरा उषित्वा ब्रह्मचर्यं देवा ऊचुर्ब्रवीतु नो भवानिति तेभ्यो हैतदक्षरमुवाच द इति व्यज्ञासिष्टा ३ इति व्यज्ञासिष्मेति होचुर्दाम्यतेति न आत्थेत्योमिति होवाच व्यज्ञासिष्टेति॥१॥**

 त्रयाः Three (kinds) प्राजापत्याः the sons of Prajāpati ऊषुः lived ब्रह्मचर्यम् student life, life of continence प्रजापतौ पितरि with the father Prajapati; देवाः the Gods, मनुष्याः the men, असुराः the demons. देवाः The Gods उषित्वा living ब्रह्मचर्यम् the period of continence ऊचुः said इति thus: भवान् you, Venerable Sir ब्रवीतु be pleased to instruct नः us; उवाच (He) said तेभ्यः ह to them एतत् this अक्षरम् syllable 'द' इति 'Da' इति (He asked) this : व्यज्ञासिष्टाः 'Have you understood'? ऊचुः (They) said इति this; व्यज्ञासिष्म (we) have understood. आत्थ (You) tell नः us, दाम्यत इति control (yourselves) उवाच ह (the other) said. ॐ इति Yes; व्यज्ञासिष्टाः इति (you) have understood.

 Three kinds of Prajapati's sons, the gods, men and demons in particular, lived as students with their father, Prajapati. Of them, the gods after finishing their period sought the instruction of their father who told them only the syllable 'Da.' Saying it the father asked them whether they had understood the meaning of the syllable. The gods replied in the affirmative and said that



you instruct us to control our nature which is unruly. The other said that they had understood rightly.

 **अथ हैनं मनुष्या ऊचुर्ब्रवीतु नो भवानिति तेभ्यो हैतदेवाक्षरमुवाच द इति व्यज्ञासिष्टा ३ इति व्यज्ञासिष्मेति होचुर्दत्तेति न आत्थेत्योमिति होवाच व्यज्ञासिष्टेति॥२॥**

 अथ Then मनुष्याः the men ऊचुः said एनम् to him इति thus : भवान् you, revered, Sir, ब्रवीतु please tell नः us. उवाच (He) told तेभ्यः them एतत् this अक्षरम् syllable एव only. 'द' इति 'Da'. इति (He asked) thus व्यज्ञासिष्टाः have (you) understood ? ऊचुः ह (They) said इति thus व्यज्ञासिष्म (we) have understood. आत्थ इति (You) tell नः us : दत्त इति give, distribute उवाच ह (he) said. ॐ इति Yes, व्यज्ञासिष्टाः इति (you) have understood.

 Then the men sought the instruction of their venerable father who told them only the syllable 'Da.' Saying it he asked them whether they had understood the meaning of the syllable. They replied in the affirmative and said that you instruct us to distribute wealth to the best of our might and thus control our avaricious nature. The other said that they had understood rightly.

** अथ हैनमसुरा ऊचुर्ब्रवीतु नो भवानिति तेभ्यो हैतदेवाक्षरमुवाच द इति व्यज्ञासिष्टा ३ इति व्यज्ञासिष्मेति होचुर्दयध्व-**



**मिति न आत्थेत्योमिति होवाच व्यज्ञासिष्टेति तदेतदेवैषा दैवी वागनुवदति स्तनयित्नुर्द द द इति दाम्यत दत्त दयध्वमिति तदेतत्त्रयꣳ शिक्षेद्दमं दानं दयामिति॥३॥ इति द्वितीयं ब्राह्मणम्॥२॥**

 अथ ह Then असुराः the demons ऊचुः said इति thus एनम् to him: भवान् you, Vernerable Sir व्रवीतु please tell नः us. उवाच ह (He) said तेभ्यः to them एतत् this अक्षरम् syllable 'द' इति 'Da'. व्यज्ञासिष्टाः इति Have (you) understood? ऊचुः (They) said : व्यज्ञासिष्टाः इति (we) have understood; आत्थ (you) tell नः इति us दयध्वम् इति be kind, have compassion उवाच ह (they) said: ॐ इति yes, व्यज्ञासिष्टाः इति (you) have understood. तत् That एतत् this एव only; एषा this दैवी divine, heavenly वाक् voice स्तनयित्नुः the cloud अनुवदति imitates, repeates'द' 'द' 'द' इति 'Da','Da','Da' – दाम्यत Control (yourself), दत्त give; दयध्वम् have compassion. तत् Therefore शिक्षेत् (one) should learn एतत् this त्रयम् three : दमम् self-control, दानम् charity, दयाम् इति (and) compassion, kindness.

 Similarly the demons sought the instruction of their revered father who told them the very syllable 'Da." Saying it he asked them whether they had understood the meaning of the syllable. They replied in the affirmative and said that you teach us to be kind. The other said that you had understood rightly. That very instruction of Prajapati is repeated even today by the heavenly



voice of the cloud 'Da,' 'Da,' 'Da': which means control yourselves, distribute wealth and be kind. Therefore one should learn these three instructions² of Prajapati—Self-control, charity and kindness.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES— 1. When one is aware of his defects, one can be weaned from them by the briefest advice as the gods, etc., were.

2\. In the opinion of Sankar there are no gods and demons other than men. The same species of men, according to their degrees of self-control, charity and compassion, and according to their tendencies of balance (Sattwa), activity (Rajas) and inertia (Tama), are called gods, men and demons. That is why the same instruction was understood in three different ways according to their dominant tendencies. Those men who lack self-control but are otherwise endowed with many good qualities are the gods. Those who have got excessive greed are men. While those who are cruel and injure others are the demons. Hence all the three disciplines are meant for men who should practise them.\]

——————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION THREE**

** एष प्रजापतिर्यद्धृदयमेतद्ब्रह्मैतत्सर्वं तदेतत्त्र्यक्षरꣳ हृदयमिति हृ इत्येकमक्षरमभिहरन्त्यस्मै स्वाश्चन्ये च य एवं वेद द इत्येकमक्षरं ददत्यस्मै स्वाश्चान्ये च य एवं वेद यमित्येकमक्षरमेति स्वर्गं लोकं य एवं वेद॥१॥ इति तृतीयं ब्राह्मणम्॥३॥**



 एषः This (is) प्रजापतिः Prajāpati, यत् which (is) हृदयम् heart, intellect having (its) seat in the heart एतत् It (is) ब्रह्म Brahman एतत् it (is) सर्वम् all, every thing.तत् That, एतत् this हृदयम् इति Hridaya, intellect (has) त्र्यक्षरम् three syllables. हृ इति 'Hri, to bring (is) एकम् one अक्षरम् syllables. अस्मै To him (the sage ) यः who वेद knows एवम् as above स्वाः च (his) own च and अन्ये others अभिहरन्ति bring (presents). 'द' इति 'Da', to give (is) एकम् one, another अक्षरम् syllable. अस्मै To him (sage) यः who वेद knows एवम् thus स्वाः च (his) own अन्ये च and others ददति give (powers). यम् इति 'Ya' (is) एकम् one, another अक्षरम् syllable : यः (The sage) who वेद knows एवम् thus एति goes to, attains स्वर्गम् heaven,लोकम् world.

 This is Prajāpati (creator) which is the intellect having its seat in the heart. The intellect is Brahman and is identified with all. The name Hridaya (intellect) consists of three syllables. 'Hri' is one syllable. The meaning of the root 'Hri' is to bring. The sage who knows thus receives presents from his relatives and others. 'Da' is the second syllable of Hridaya. The root meaning of 'Da' is 'to give.' To the sage who knows this his relatives and others give their powers. 'Ya' is the last syllable of Hridaya. The form 'Ya' is derived from the root' In' meaning 'to go.' The sage who knows thus attains the heaven world.



 \[This is an eulogy of the intellect which has been described as everything in the third chapter. If the results of meditation on the syllables of the name are so conspicuous, one can easily imagine the result of meditation on the reality of intellect itself.\]

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION FOUR**

** तद्वै तदेतदेव तदास सत्यमेव स यो हैतं महद्यक्षं प्रथमजं वेद सत्यं ब्रह्मेति जयतीमाल्ँ लोकाञ्जित इन्न्वसावसद्य एवमेतन्महद्यक्षं प्रथमजं वेद सत्यं ब्रह्मेति सत्यꣳ ह्येव ब्रह्म॥१॥ इति चतुर्थं ब्राह्मणम्॥४॥ **

 वै Verily तत्\* that तत् that तत् that (intellect-Brahman) आस was एव but एतत् this सत्यम् satya, एव only. सः He, any one यः who वेद knows एतं ह this महत् great, pervasive, यक्षम् adorable प्रथमजम् first-born (Brahman), इति as सत्यम् ब्रह्म satya-Brahman जयति conquers, attains, इमान् these लोकान् worlds. असौ This (enemy) इत् नु as if, even, जितः (is) conquered, Vanquised असत् (and) non-entity, non-existent यः (He) who वेद knows, realises एवम् thus एतत् this, महत् great, pervasive यक्षम् adorable ; प्रथमजम् first-born (being) सत्यम् ब्रह्म इति as Satya Brahman हि for, because सत्यम् satya एव Verily ब्रह्म (is) Brahman.

——————————————————————————————

\* First 'Tat' (That) recalls the intellect-Brahman stated in the last section. Second 'Tat' means that he is being described in another way. Third 'Tat' is connected with 'Atat' (this) which refers to something in the mind to be presently stated.

——————————————————————————————



 The intellect-Brahman was verily the Satya Brahman only. Anyone who realises this pervasive, adorable, first-born Brahman identified with Satya (gross and subtle elements) attains these worlds, and his enemy becomes vanquished and non-entity. He who realises this pervasive, adorable, first-born being as the Satya-Brahman indeed gets this result; because Satya' is verily Brahman.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. See foot-note of 1. 6. 3 on satya.\]

——————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION FIVE**

 **आप एवेदमग्र आसुस्ता आपः सत्यमसृजन्त सत्यं ब्रह्म ब्रह्म प्रजापतिं प्रजापतिर्देवाꣳस्ते देवाः सत्यमेवोपासते तदेतत्र्यक्षरꣳसत्यमिति स इत्येकमक्षरं तीत्येकमक्षरं यमित्येकमक्षरं प्रथमोत्तमे अक्षरे सत्यं मध्यतोऽनृतं तदेतदनृतमुभयतः सत्येन परिगृहीत‍ꣳ सत्यभूयमेव भवति नैवं विद्वाꣳ समनृतꣳ हिनस्ति॥१॥**

 इदम् This (Universe) आसुः was एव but, indeed आपः water; अग्रे before (manifestation), in the beginning ताः that आपः water असृजन्त created सत्यम् satya. सत्यम् Satya ब्रह्म (is) Brahman, Hiranyagarbha, Sutratman.ब्रह्म Brahman (created) प्रजापतिम् Prajāpati (Viraj). प्रजापतिः Prajāpati (created) देवान् the gods. ते Those देवाः gods उपासते adore, meditate upon सत्यम् satya, एव alone, तत् that एतत् this सत्यम् satya (consists



of) त्र्यक्षरम् इति three syllables. सः इति 'Sa' (is) एकम् one अक्षरम् syllable. ति इति 'Ti' (is) एकम् one अक्षरम् syllable. यम् इति 'Ya' (is) एकम् one, अक्षरम् syllable, प्रथम-उत्तमे the first and last अक्षरे syllables सत्यम् (are) truth, immortality. मध्यतः In the middle, the middle syllable (is) untruth, death. तत् That एतत् this अनृतम् untruth, death परिगृहीतम् (is) enclosed,encompassed उभयतः on both sides सत्येन् by truth, by immortality. भवति Is,becomes सत्यभूयम् prevalence, preponderance of truth एव indeed अनृतम untruth न not हिनस्ति harms, hurts एवम् such विद्वान् knower.

 This entire Universe of name and form was indeed water' before manifestation and there was no other manifested object. That water created Satya. Satya-Brahman is Hiranyagarbha (Sutratman). Satya Brahman created Viraj, of which the sun, etc. are the organs. Viraj created the gods. The gods thus created adore Satya-Brahman who even supersedes Viraj, their creator. This name, Satya, consists of three syllables: 'sa' is the first syllable, 'ti' is the second syllable, and 'ya' is the third syllable. The first and last syllables 'sa' and 'ya' are truth, being free from the form of death. In the middle syllable, 'ti' is untruth, a form of death; for the words 'Mrityu' (death) and 'Anrita' (untruth) have both a letter 't' common in them. This untruth being encompassed on both sides by truth is insignificant. Therefore there is



prevalence of truth and the insignificance of untruth. One who realises the preponderance of truth and negligibility of untruth is never hurt by untruth.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Water here means the liquid oblations connected with the Agnihotra and other sacrifices. The oblations being liquid are called water. After the sacrifices are over these oblations maintain their connections with the sacrifices in some invisible subtle form as well as their union with other elements. They are the seed of the Universe.\]

——————————————————————————————

** तद्यत्तत्सत्यमसौ स आदित्यो य एष एतस्मिन्मण्डले पुरुषो यश्चायं दक्षिणेऽक्षन्पुरुषस्तावेतावन्योन्यस्मिन्प्रतिष्ठितौ रश्मिभिरेषोऽस्मिन्प्रतिष्ठितः प्राणैरयममुष्मिन्स यदोत्क्रमिष्यन्भवति शुद्धमेवैतन्मण्डलं पश्यति नैनमेते रश्मयः प्रत्यायन्ति॥२॥**

 तत् That यत् which (is) तत् that सत्यम् Satya Brahman. असौ This सः that आदित्यः sun, एषः this पुरुषः being च and यः who ( is) एतस्मिन् in that मण्डले orb अयम् this पुरुषः being, यः who (is), दक्षिणे in the right अक्षन् eye. तौ These एतौ two (beings) प्रतिष्ठितौ rest, depend अन्योन्यस्मिन् on each other. एषः This, the former प्रतिष्टितः remains, abides, अस्मिन् on the latter, रश्मिभिः by the rays, (light). अयम् This, the latter (rests), अमुष्मिन् on the former प्राणैः by life-forces (here) by the eye and other organs. यदा When सः that (the individual self) भवति is उत्क्रमिष्यन् about to leave (the body) पश्यति (he) sees एतत् that मण्डलम् (solar) orb एव indeed शुद्धम् clear, shorn of



beams एते these रश्मयः rays न not प्रत्यायन्ति reach, come एनम् to him.

 That which is Satya-Brahman the first-born is the deity identified with the sun. He is the being who dwells in the solar orb and also dwells in the right eye in different forms. Both the solar and ocular beings rest on each other. The solar being rests on the ocular being by helping the latter with its light. The ocular being who is the experiencer inhabiting this body rests on the solar being and helps it by means of the eyes and other organs. When the individual Self is about to depart from the body he sees the solar orb shorn of its beams. like the moon. Then the solar being who is the presiding deity of the eyes withdraws its rays which no longer reach the dying man.¹

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. This incidental mention of the omen of death is made to forewarn a man to be careful and take necessary steps in time.\]

——————————————————————————————

** य एष एतस्मिन्मण्डले पुरुषस्तस्य भूरिति शिर एकꣳ शिर एकमेतदक्षरं भुव इति बाहू द्वौ बाहू द्वे एते अक्षरे स्वरिति प्रतिष्ठा द्वे प्रतिष्ठे द्वे एते अक्षरे तस्योपनिषदहरिति हन्ति पाप्मानं जहाति च य एवं वेद॥३॥**

 एषः This पुरुषः being यः who (is) एतस्मिन् in that मण्डले (solar) orb, तस्य his शिरः head (is) भूः इति the (syllable)



' Bhur.' एकम् One शिरः head, एतत् this एकम् one अक्षरम् syllable भुवः इति the (syllable) ' Bhuvar ' बाहू (is) the arms द्वौ Two बाहू arms एते these द्वे two अक्षरे syllables, स्वः इति the (word) 'Swar' (is) प्रतिष्ठा support, the legs; द्वे two प्रतिष्ठे legs, द्वे two एते these अक्षरे syllables, तस्य his उपनिषद् secret name अहः इति (is) 'Ahar.' यः Who वेद knows एवम् thus हन्ति kills, destroys च and जहाति shuns पाप्मानम् sin, evil.

 Satya-Brahman who is in the solar orb, has as its limbs the three Vyahritis — ' Bhur'. ' Bhuvar ' and ‘Swar'. The Vyahriti ' Bhur' is his head ; for every body has only one head, and there is this one syllable. The Vyahriti ' Bhuvar' is his arms ; for everybody has only two arms and there are these two syllables. The Vyahriti 'Swar' is his legs; for every body has two legs and there are these two syllables. The secret name of solar being who has Vyahritis as limbs is 'Ahar.' ' Ahar' is derived from the root 'har' or 'ha' meaning to kill or shun. He who knows this secret name kills and shuns sins.

 **योऽयं दक्षिणेऽक्षन्पुरुषस्तस्य भूरिति शिर एकꣳ शिर एकमेतदक्षरं भुव इति बाहू द्वौ बाहू द्वे एते अक्षरे स्वरिति प्रतिष्ठा द्वे प्रतिष्ठे द्वे एते अक्षरे तस्योपनिषदहमिति हन्ति पाप्मानं जहाति च य एवं वेद॥४॥ इति पञ्चमं ब्राह्मणम् ॥५॥**

 अयम् This पुरुषः being यः who (is) दक्षिणे in the right अक्षन् eye तस्य his शिरः head (is) भूः इति the (syllable) ' Bhur.



(There is) एकम् one शिरः head. (There is) एतत् this एकम् one अक्षरम् syllable. भुवः इति The (word) ' Bhuvar' (is) बाहू the two arms. (There are) द्वौ two बाहु arms. (There are) द्वे two एते these अक्षरे syllables स्वः इति The (word) 'Swar' (is) प्रतिष्ठा the legs. (There are) द्वे two प्रतिष्ठा legs. (There are) द्वे two एते these अक्षरे syllables. तस्य His उपनिषद् secret name (is) अहम् इति the 'Aham.' यः (He) who एवम् thus वेद knows हन्ति destroys जहाति (and) shuns पाप्मानम् evils, sins.

 Similarly the Satya-Brahman who is in the right eye, has these Vyahritis as its limbs. The Vyahriti 'Bhur' is his head; because every body has only one head and it has this one syllable. The Vyahriti 'Bhuvar' is his arms; because every body has only two arms and it has two syllables. The Vyahriti 'Swar' is his legs; because every body has two legs and it has two syllables. The secret name of the ocular being is 'Aham' (I); because he is the inner Self. He who knows the secret name of the ocular being as such kills and shuns sins.

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION SIX**

** मनोमयोऽयं पुरुषो भाःसत्यस्तस्मिन्नन्तर्हृदये यथा व्रीहिर्वा यवो वा स एष सर्वस्येशानः सर्वस्याधिपतिः सर्वमिदं प्रशास्ति यदिदं किञ्च॥१॥ इति षष्ठं ब्राह्मणम्॥६॥**



 अयम् This पुरुषः being मनोमयः full of mind, identified with the mind भाः सत्यः resplendent, lustrous तस्मिन् in that अन्तर्हृदये interior of the heart यथा as, like व्रीहिः वा a grain of rice वा or यवः a grain of barley. सः That एषः this ईशानः lord सर्वस्य of all (things) अधिपतिः the ruler, governor सर्वस्य of all प्रशास्ति rules, governs सर्वम् all इदम् this यद् इदम् whichever च and किम् whatever.

 This being is full of the mind; for he is perceived by the mind and he also perceives through it. Lustre is his real nature. He is realised by the Yogins in the interior of the heart like a grain of rice or a grain of barley in size. He is the lord of all things which are only his variations. He being the independent governor of all governs the whole Universe.

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION SEVEN**

** विद्युद्ब्रह्मोत्याहुर्विदानाद्विद्युद्विद्यत्येनं पाप्मनो य एवं वेद विद्युद्ब्रह्मेति विद्युद्ध्येव ब्रह्म॥१॥ इति सप्तमं ब्राह्मणम्॥७॥**

 आहुः (They) say इति thus विद्युत् lightning (is) ब्रह्म Brahman,विद्युत् (it is called) lightning विदानात् from clearing or scattering (darkness),विद्यति releases, sets free पप्मनः sins, evils एनम् him यः who वेद knows एवम् thus विद्युत् lightning ब्रह्म इति as Brahman; हि for विद्युत् lightning एव verily ब्रह्म (is) Brahman.



 They say that lightning is Brahman. The lightning is so called because its flashes cleave the darkness due to clouds. He who knows that lightning is Brahman as possessed of the above attributes dispels all the evils that are set against him. Because lightning is verily Brahman.

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION EIGHT**

** वाचं धेनुमुपासीत तस्याश्चत्वारः स्तनाः स्वाहाकारो वषट्कारो हन्तकारः स्वधाकारस्तस्य द्वौ स्तनौ देवा उपजीवन्ति स्वाहाकारं च वषट्कारं च हन्तकारं मनुष्याः स्वधाकारं पितरस्तस्याः प्राण ऋषभो मनो वत्सः॥१॥ इत्यष्टमं ब्राह्मणम्॥८॥**

** **उपासीत (One) should meditate वाचम् upon speech (Vedas) धेनुम् as a cow. तस्याः Her चत्वारः four स्तनाः teats (are) स्वाहाकारः the sound 'Swāhā', वषट्कारः the sound Vashat', हन्तकारः the sound Hanta', स्वधाकारः (and) the sound ‘Swadhā.' देवाः The gods उपजीवन्ति live on तस्य her द्वौ two स्तनौ teats स्वाहाकारम् the sound 'Swaha' च and वषट्कारं च the sound 'Vashat,' मनुष्याः men हन्तकारम् on the sound 'Hanta,' पितरः the Manes स्वधाकारम् on the sound 'Swadhā.' तस्याः Her ऋषभः bull (is) प्राणः the vital power वरसः (her) calf मनः the mind.

 The Vedas should be meditated upon as if she was a cow. The sounds 'Swāhā', ' Vashat',



Hanta' and 'Swadhā' are the four teats of the cow' (Vedas). The gods live on her two teats—the sounds ‘Swāhā' and ' Vashat', through which oblations are offered to them. Men live on the sound ‘Hanta' (if you want) with the use of which food is given to them. The Manes live on the sound 'Swadha', with the utterance of which food is offered to them. The bull for that cow is the vital power (by which the Vedas are made fruitful). Her calf is the mind (that stimulates her to secretion).

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. As milk is secreted by the cow through her four teats for her calf, so food is supplied by the Vedas through these four sounds to gods, Manes and men. Food is comparable to milk.\]

——————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER FIVE : SECTION NINE**

** अयमग्निर्वैश्वानरो योऽयमन्तःपुरुषे येनेदमन्नं पच्यते यदिदमद्यते तस्यैष घोषो भवति यमेतत्कर्णावपिधाय शृणोति स यदोत्क्रमिष्यन्भवति नैनं घोषꣳ शृणोति॥१॥ इति नवमं ब्राह्मणम्॥९॥**

** **अयम् This अग्निः fire यः that (is) अन्तः within पुरुषे a man येन by which इदम् this अन्नम् food यत् which पच्यते is digested. इदम् This यत् which अद्यते is eaten अयम् this वैश्वानरः (is) Vaishwānara. तस्य Its एषः this घोषः sound भवति is, यम्



that शृणोति (one) hears अपिधाय shutting, closing कर्णौ the ears एतत् this (here) thus, यदा when सः he (a man) भवति is उत्क्रमिष्यन् about to pass away न not शृणोति hears एनम् this घोषम् sound.

 The fire that dwelling within everybody, digests the food which is taken by men is called Vaishwanara (Viraj). The sound that is heard by shutting the ears with one's fingers is emitted by it. It is not the elemental fire that is one of the five components of the body but it is the heat in the stomach. When a man is about to pass away from.this world, he does not hear this sound.\*

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION TEN**

 **यदा वै पुरुषोऽस्माल्लोकात्मैति स वायुमागच्छति तस्मै स तत्र विजिहीते यथा रथचक्रस्य स्वं तेन स ऊर्ध्व आक्रमते स आदित्यमागच्छति तस्मै स तत्र विजिहीते यथा लम्बरस्य खं तेन स ऊर्ध्व आक्रमते स चन्द्रमसमागच्छति तस्मै स तत्र विजिहीते यथा दुन्दुभेः खं तेन स ऊर्ध्व आक्रमते स लोकमागच्छत्यशोकमहिमं तस्मिन्वसति शाश्वतीः समाः॥१॥ इति दशमं ब्राह्मणम् ॥१०॥**

——————————————————————————————

  \*This mention of a portent of death is incidental. Another portent is mentioned in 5. 5.2.

——————————————————————————————



 वै Verily यदा when पुरुषः a man (the sage) प्रेति passes away, departs, अस्मात् from this लोकात् world सः he आगच्छति goes to, reaches वायुम् the air, तस्मै for him सः it विजिहीते makes up a hole यथा as, like खम् opening, hole, रथचक्रस्य of a chariot-wheel. तेन Through that सः he आक्रमते attacks, goes, ऊर्ध्वम् upward सः he आगच्छति goes to reaches, आदित्यम् the sun, तस्मै for him सः it विजिहीते makes an aperture तत्र there, यथा as, like, खम् the hole, लम्बरस्य of tabor. तेन Through that सः he आक्रमते goes ऊर्द्धः upward. सः He आगच्छति goes चन्द्रमसम् the moon, तस्मै for him सः it विजिहीते makes an opening यथा as, like खम् the hole, दुन्दुभेः of a drum तेन Through that सः he आक्रमते goes ऊर्ध्वः upward. सः He आगच्छति goes to लोकम् a world अशोकम् free from grief (mental troubles) अहिमम् from cold (physical sufferings). तस्मिन् There वसति (he) lives शाश्वतीः eternal समाः years.

 When a sage who knows those meditations gives up the body he goes to the air, which lies crosswise in the sky. The air that is motionless and impenetrable makes for him a way like the opening of a chariot-wheel by separating the parts of its own body. He goes upward through that opening and reaches the sun, who blocks the way for the aspirant bound for the world of Brahman. The sun too lets the sage pass by making a hole in its body like that of a tabor (a musical instrument). He goes upward through that hole and reaches the



moon who also allows him to go by making an opening in its body like that of a drum. He travels upwards through that opening and goes to the world of Hiranyagarbha which is beyond the reach of mental troubles and physical sufferings. The sage lives there for many cycles of ours that constitute the life time of Hiranyagarbha.

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION ELEVEN**

** एतद्वै परमं तपो यद्व्याहितस्तप्यते परमꣳ हैव लोकं जयतिय एवं वेदैतद्वै परमं तपो यं प्रेतमरण्यꣳ हरन्ति परमꣳ हैव लोकं जयति य एवं वेदैतद्वै परमं तपो यं प्रेतमग्नावभ्यादधति परमꣳ हैव लोकं जयनि य एवं वेद॥१॥ इत्येकादशं ब्राह्मणम्॥११॥**

 एतत् This वै indeed (is) परमम् great, excellent, तपः penance, austerity, यत् that तप्यते practises, suffers, व्याहितः diseased, ill (person). यः (He) who एवम् thus वेद knows एव हृ indeed जयतिः conquers, wins, परमम् great, high, लोकम् world. एतत् This वै verily (is) परमम् great तपः penance यम् which प्रेतम् the dead हरन्ति carry अरण्यम् to the forest. यः (He) who वेद knows एवम् thus जयति conquers, attains, परमम् high लोकम् world एव indeed एतत् this वै indeed (is) परमम् great तपः penance यम् which प्रेतम् the dead अभ्यादधति (they) place अग्नौ on fire. यः (He) who एवम् thus वेद knows जयति ह conquers, wins परमम् great लोकम् world एव verily.



 It is verily a great penance to suffer during the attack of an illness without condemning the illness or being dejected over it. The suffering entailed by the illness burns one's evils. He who gets his evils burnt by the penance of meditation conquers a high world. Similarly if the dying man thinks calmly that he is carried to the forest by the priests for funeral ceremony that is a great penance for him. He who knows thus conquers a great world. Likewise it is also a great penance that a dead man is placed on fire. He who knows thus conquers a great world.

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION TWELVE**

** अन्नं ब्रह्मेत्येक आहुस्तन्न तथा पूयति वा अन्नमृते प्राणात्प्राणो ब्रह्मेत्येक आहुस्तन्न तथा शुष्यति वै प्राण ऋतेऽन्नादेते ह त्वेव देवते एकधाभूयं भूत्वा परमतां गच्छतस्तद्ध स्माऽऽह प्रातृदः पितरं किꣳस्विदेवैवं विदुषे साधु कुर्यां किमेवास्मा असाधु कुर्यामिति स ह स्माऽऽह पाणिना मा प्रातृदः कस्त्वेनयोरेकधाभूयं भूत्वा परमतां गच्छतीति तस्मा उ हैतदुवाच वीत्यन्नं वै व्यन्ने हीमानि सर्वाणि भूतानि विष्टानि रमिति प्राणो वैरं प्राणे हीमानि सर्वाणि भूतानि रमन्ते सर्वाणि ह वा अस्मिन्भूतानि विशन्ति सर्वाणि भूतानि रमन्ते य एवं वेद॥१॥ इति द्वादशं ब्राह्मणम् ॥१२॥**



 एके Some (teachers) आहुः say, hold इति thus अन्नम् food, what is eaten (is) ब्रह्म Brahman तत् It (is) न not तथा so. वै For अन्नम् food, पूयति rots, is decomposed ऋते without प्राणात् the vital power. एके Some आहुः say इति this प्राणः the vital power (is) ब्रह्म Brahman तत् It (is) न not तथा so. वै For प्राणः the vital power शुष्यति dries up ऋते without अन्नात् the food. तु But एते ह these two देवते deities एव indeed भूत्वा being एकधाभूयम् identified, united गच्छतः attain, get परमताम् the highest (Brahmanhood). तत् ह So प्रातृदः Prātrida आहः स्म said पितरम् to father, किं स्वित् what एव indeed साधु good, worship कुर्याम् (I) can do, can offer एवम् to such विदुषे knower किम् what असाधु offence, evil एव indeed कुर्याम् (I) can do अस्मै इति to him? सः ह He आह स्म said पाणिना with hand, मा no प्रातृद oh Prātrida तु for कः who गच्छति goes to, attains परमताम् the highest, perfection भूत्वा being एकधाभूयम् united, identified अनयोः इति with either. तस्मात् उ then एतत् to him उवाच ह (he) said, वि इति (it is) ‘Vi.' अन्नम् Food (is) वै verily वि 'Vi' ; हि for सर्वाणि all इमानि these भूतानि beings विष्टानि rest अन्ने on food, on body रम् इति (it is) 'ram', हि for सर्वाणि all इमानि these भूतानि beings रमन्ते delight प्राणे in the vital power वै ह indeed सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings विशन्ति enter, rest सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings रमन्ते delight यः who एवम् thus वेद knows.

 Some teachers hold that what is eaten is Brahman. Food is not to be understood as Brahman since it is decomposed without the vital power. Other teachers say that the vital power is



Brahman. That also should not be taken as true, because the vital power becomes dry without food. Vital power being the eater it cannot live without eatables. But these two deities, food and the vital power, being identified attain their Brahmanhood. So one named Pratrida asked his father, "What worship indeed can I offer to one who knows that food and the vital power together constitute Brahman or what offence indeed can I do to him? Because such a sage is neither elated by honour nor slighted by offence?" The father beckoned him with his hands to stop and said, 'Pratrida, do not say so; because one does not attain perfection by identity with food and the vital force.' Then he told his son that it is "Vi". Food is "Vi", because all these beings rest on body which is a modification of the food that is eaten. It is "ram." The vital power is "ram", because all these beings take delight in the vital power which is the abode of strength. All beings rest in one who possesses the knowledge of the virtue of food. All creatures take delight in one who knows this virtue of the vital power.



** CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION THIRTEEN**

** उक्थं प्राणो वा उक्थं प्राणो हीदंꣳ सर्वमुत्थापयत्युद्धास्मादुक्थविद्वीरस्तिष्ठत्युक्थस्य सायुज्य‍ꣳ सलोकतां जयति य एवं वेद॥१॥**

 उक्थम (A meditation on the vital power as) the Uktha. प्राणः The vital power वै verily उक्थम (is) the Uktha (a hymn of praise) हि for प्राणः the vital power, उत्थापयति raises, upholds सर्वम् all इदम् this (universe). अस्मात् From him यः who एवम् thus वेद knows उत् + तिष्ठति ह raises up, is born वीरः hero, heroic son. उक्थवित् A knower of the Uktha (vital power) जयति conquers, attains, सायुज्यम् the same nature of, सलोकताम् (and) abode in the same world, उक्थस्य of the Uktha (vital power).

 The vital power should be meditated upon as the hymn of praise called Uktha (which is the main part of the Mahāvrata sacrifice'). The vital power is verily the Uktha, because it upholds this Universe. To him who knows this is born a heroic son who is a knower of the vital power. He attains the same nature of and abode in the same world with the vital power.

——————————————————————————————

 \[NOTES 1. See Kaushitaki Upanishad (3. 3) and Aitareya Aranyaka (2. 1. 2).\]

——————————————————————————————



** यजुः प्राणो वै यजुः प्राणे हीमानि सर्वाणि भूतानि युज्यन्ते युज्यन्ते हास्मै सर्वाणि भूतानि श्रेष्ठ्याय यजुषः सायुज्य‍ꣳ सलोकतां जयति य एवं वेद॥२॥**

 यजुः (A meditation on the vital power as) the Yajus, प्राणः the vital power वै verily यजुः (is) the Yajus हि for सर्वाणि all इमानि these, भूतानि beings युज्यन्ते are joined, are united प्राणे in the vital power, सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings, युज्यन्ते are joined, are united, श्रेष्ट्याय for eminence, for superiority अस्मै ह of him यः who, एवम् thus, वेद knows, जयति conquers, attains सायुज्यम् same state, सलोकताम् (and) abode in the same world यजुषः of the Yajus (vital power).

 The vital power should be meditated upon as the Yajus. The vital power is called Yajus, because it unites¹ (or joins) all these beings. All beings try to make him their chief who knows thus. He attains the same state of and abode in the same world with the vital power.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. In this and next paragraphs the figurative meanings of ' Yajus' and 'Saman' are given.—Anandagiri.\]

——————————————————————————————

** साम प्राणो वै साम प्राणे हीमानि सर्वाणि भूतानि सम्यञ्चि सम्यञ्चि हास्मै सर्वाणि भूतानि श्रैष्ठ्याय कल्पन्ते साम्नः सायुज्यꣳ सलोकतां जयति य एवं वेद॥३॥**



** ** साम (A meditation on the vital force as) the Sāman. वै Indeed, प्राणः the vital power (is) साम Sāman, हि because, सर्वाणि all इमानि these भूतानि beings सम्यञ्चि harmonise, are united, प्राणे in the vital power. अस्मे ह For him, यः who वेद knows एवम् thus सर्वाणि all भूतानि beings सम्यञ्चि harmonise, are united, कल्पन्ते (and) are able, serve श्रैष्ट्याय for superiority, for eminence. जयति (He) conquers, attains, सायुज्यम् union सलोकताम् abode in the world साम्नः of the Sāman.

 The vital power should be meditated upon as the Saman. It is verily the Saman, because all these beings harmonise in the vital power.
