All beings harmonise and serve for the superiority of him who knows that the vital power causes people to harmonise. Such a knower attains union with the Saman and abode in the same world.

** क्षत्त्रं प्राणो वै क्षत्त्रं प्राणो हि वै क्षत्त्रं त्रायते हैनं प्राणः क्षणितोः प्र क्षत्त्रमन्नमाप्नोति क्षत्त्रस्य सायुज्य‍ꣳ सलोकतां जयति य एवं वेद॥४॥ इति त्रयोदशं ब्राह्मणम् ॥१३॥**

** **क्षत्त्रम् (A meditation on the vital power as) the Kshatra. प्राणः The vital power वै indeed (is) क्षत्त्रम् the Kshatra, हि for प्राणः the vital power वै (is) indeed क्षत्त्रम् the Kshatra. प्राणः The vital power त्रायते ह protects एनम् it (its body) क्षणितोः from wounds, injuries, यः (he) who एवम् thus वेद



'knows प्र+अप्नोति attains, obtains क्षत्त्रम्\* identity with the Kshatra. जयति (He) conquers, attains सायुज्यम् union with सलोकताम् abode in the world क्षत्त्रस्य of the Kshatra (vital power).

 The vital power should be meditated upon as the Kshatra. The vital power is verily the Kshatra, as is well-known. Because the vital power protects the body from injuries inflicted with weapons, etc., by filling them up with new flesh. He who knows this healing power of the vital force obtains union and abode in the same world with it.

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION FOURTEEN**

** भूमिरन्तरिक्षं द्यौरित्यष्टावक्षराण्यष्टाक्षरꣳ ह वा एकं गायत्र्यै पदमेतदु हैवास्या एतत्स यावदेषु त्रिषु लोकेषु तावद्ध जयतियोऽस्या एतदेवं पदं वेद ॥१॥**

 भुमिः Bhumi, the earth, अन्तरिक्षम् Antariksha, the sky, द्यौः Dyaus, heaven, इति (are) thus अष्टौ eight अक्षराणि syllables. एकम् The first, पदम् foot गायत्र्यै of the Gayatri (metre), अष्ट-अक्षरं ह वा (are) eight syllables. एतत् This (three worlds) उ only ह एव (is) certainly, एतत् this (first foot),

——————————————————————————————

\* This reading is according to the Madhyandina Sākhā. Dvivedanga in his commentary explains the word as meaning 'the nature of Kshatra.

——————————————————————————————



अस्याः of her, (of Gayatri). सः He, यः who वेद knows एतत् this पदम् foot एव only अस्याः of her (Gayatri), एवम् as such, जयति conquers, wins, यावत् whatever तावत् ह all that एषु in these त्रिषु three लोकेषु worlds.

 There are eight syllables in 'Bhumi' (the earth), 'Antariksha' (sky) and 'Dyaus' (heaven) as well as the first foot of Gayatri¹ which reads 'Tat Savitur Varenyam.'² Hence the earth, sky and heaven constitute the first foot of the Gayatri.. He who knows the first foot of Gayatri consisting of the above three worlds conquers as much as there is to be conquered in earth, sky and heaven.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. Gayatri which is the chief of metres has three feet each of eight syllables. In this metre called Gaya- tri exists the verse Gayatri or Savitri--the most sacred verse of the Vedas. It appears in the Rig-Veda (III. LXII, 10) and reads as follows: 'Tat Savitur Varenyam, Bhargo Devasya Dhimahi, Dhiyo Yo nah Prachodayat,' i.e., we meditate on the adorable Light of the effulgent Deity. May he illumine our intellect. Vasistha Smriti (4. 3) glorifies Gayatri thus: 'The Brāhmans were created through Gayatri,' because Brahmanhood is possible by second birth through Gayatri alone.

2\. The syllable 'Ya' in this word is to be separated to supply the eighth syllable.\]

——————————————————————————————

** ऋचो यजूꣳषि सामानीत्यष्टावक्षराण्यष्टाक्षरꣳ ह वा एकं गायत्र्यै पदमेतदु हैवास्या एतत्स यावतीयं त्रयी विद्या तावद्ध जयति योऽस्या एतदेवं पदं वेद॥२॥ **



 ऋचः The Richah, यजूंषि Yajumshi सामानि (and) Sāmāni इति thus अष्टौ eight अक्षराणि syllables एकम् one पदम् foot (has) अष्टौ eight अक्षरं ह वै syllables. एतत् This (three Vedas) उ only ह एव certainly एतत् this (second foot), अस्याः of her (the Gayatri). सः He यः who एवम् as such वेद knows एतत् this पदम् foot एव only अस्याः of her (Gayatri) जयति conquers, obtains यावती as much विद्या knowledge तावत् ह as, इयम् this (three Vedas).

 There are eight syllables in 'Richah', 'Yajumsi' and 'Sāmāni' as well as in the second foot of Gayatri which reads, 'Bhargo Devasya Dhimahi'. Hence Rig Veda, Yajur Veda and Sama Veda constitute the second foot of the Gayatri. He who knows the second foot of the Gayatri consisting of the three Vedas obtains as much knowledge as can be obtained from the three Vedas.

** प्राणोऽपानो व्यान इत्यष्टावक्षराण्यष्टाक्षरꣳ ह वा एकं गायत्र्यै पदमेतदु हैवास्या एतत्स यावदिदं प्राणि तावद्ध जयति योऽस्या एतदेवं पदं वेदाथास्य एतदेव तुरीयं दर्शतं पदं परोरजा य एष तपति यद्वै चतुर्थं तत्तुरीयं दर्शतं पदमिति ददृश इव ह्येष परोरजा इति सर्वमु ह्येवैष रज उपर्युपरि तपत्येवꣳ हैव श्रिया यशसा तपति योऽस्या एतदेवं पदं वेद॥३॥**

 प्राणः Prāna, अपानः Apāna, व्यानः Vyāna, इति (make) thus, अष्टौ eight अक्षराणि syllables एकं वा One (third) पदं



 ह foot गायत्त्र्यै of Gayatri, अष्टाक्षरम् (has) eight syllables. एतत् उ ह वा this, above (three forms of the vital power) एतत् (is) that (foot) अस्याः of her (Gayatri). सः He, यः who, वेद knows एवम् thus एतत् this (foot) अस्याः of her (Gayatri) जयति conquers, wins यावत् as many, इदम् this प्राणि living beings, creatures, तावत् ह as (there are). अथ Now अस्याः her एतत् this एव indeed, तुरीयम् Turiya, fourth, दर्शतम् apparently seen, परोरजाः beyond Rajas (activity, sky) पदम् foot एषः That यः which, तपति shines ; तत् that, यत् which, वै verily (is) चतुर्थम् fourth, तुरीयम् (is) Turiya, दर्शतम् apparently seen, पदम् इति foot, हि because, एषः he, ददृशे (is) visible, इव as it were ; परोरजाः इति above the sky हि because, एषः एव he तपति shines सर्वम् on the entire, रजः Universe (created out of Rajas) उपरि above उपरि above, यः (he) who वेद knows, realises, एवम् thus, अस्याः her, एतत् this पदम् foot, एव indeed तपति shines, एवं ह in the same way, श्रिया with superiority, with splendour,यशसा with fame, एव indeed.

 There are eight syllables' in 'Prāna', 'Apāna' and 'Vyana' as well as in the third foot of Gayatri- 'Dhiyo yo nah Prachodayat.' So Prana, Apana and Vyana which are the three forms of the vital power constitute the third foot of Gayatri. He who knows the third foot of the Gayatri consisting of Prana, Apana and Vyana conquers all creatures that exist in the Universe. Now her Turiya foot, which is apparently seen high above the sky is indeed the sun that shines. 'Turiya' means what



is commonly understood as the fourth. The fourth foot of Gayatri i.e., the sun, is apparently seen, because the solar being is sun, as it were. he is high above the sky means that he shines on That the entire Universe created out of Rajas. He who realises the fourth foot of Gayatri as the solar being shines like the sun with splendour, and fame.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES —1. Two in Prana, three in Apana and three in Vyana make eight in all.\]

——————————————————————————————

** सैषा गायत्र्येतस्मिꣳ स्तुरीये दर्शते पदे परोरजसि प्रतिष्ठिता तद्वै तत्सत्ये प्रतिष्ठितं चक्षुर्वै सत्यं चक्षुर्हि वै सत्यं तस्माद्यदिदानीं द्वौ विवदमानावेयातामहमदर्शमहमश्रौषमिति य एवं ब्रूयादहमदर्शमिति तस्मा एव श्रद्दध्याम तद्वै तत्सत्यं बले प्रतिष्ठितं प्राणो वै बलं तत्प्राणे प्रतिष्ठितं तस्मादाहुर्बल‍ꣳ सत्यादोजीय इत्येवम्वेषा गायत्र्यध्यात्मं प्रतिष्ठिता सा हैषा गयाꣳस्तत्रे प्राणा वै गयास्तत्प्राणाꣳस्तत्रे तद्यद्गयाꣳस्तत्रे तस्माद्गायत्री नाम स यामेवामूꣳ सावित्रीमन्वाहैषैव सा स यस्मा अन्वाह तस्य प्राणाꣳस्त्रायते॥४॥**

 सा That (the three-footed) एषा this, गायत्री Gāyatri प्रतिष्ठिता rests एतस्मिन् on this, तुरीये fourth दर्शते apparently seen, परोरजसि celestial पदे foot (Sun). तत् That (Sun) वै again प्रतिष्ठितम् rests, तत् on that सत्ये truth. चक्षुः The eye वै verily (is) सत्यम् truth, हि for चक्षुः the eye, वै indeed (is)



 सत्यम् truth. तस्मात् Therefore यदि if इदानीम् even now द्वौ two विवदमानौ quarrelling, disputing, giving contradictory accounts एयाताम् come (one saying) अहम् I अदर्शम् saw (it), (another saying) अहम् I अश्रौषम् इति heard of (it) श्रद्दध्याम (we) believe, तस्मै him एव only यः who ब्रूयात् says एवम् thus. अहम् I अदर्शम् इति saw (it). तत् That वै verily तत् that सत्यम् truth प्रतिष्ठितम् rests बले on strength. प्राणः The vital power वै (is) verily बलम् strength. तत् That (truth) प्रतिष्ठितम् rests, प्राणे on the vital power तस्मात् Therefore आहुः (they) say, strength (is) ओजीयः mightier, more powerful सत्यात् इति than truth. एवम् उ Thus एषा this गायत्री Gāyatri प्रतिष्ठिता rests अध्यात्मम् on the vital power within the body. सा That ह एषा this गायत्री Gāyatri तत्रे saved, protected गयान् the Gayas. प्राणाः The organs वै indeed (are) गयाः the Gayas. तत् It तत्रे saves, protects, प्राणान् the organs. तत् Now, यत् because तत्रे (it) saved, protected गयान् the Gayas (the organs) तस्मात् therefore नाम (it is) called गायत्री Gayatri. अमुम् That सावित्रीम् Savitri याम् which सः he (the teacher) अन्वाह teaches (to the Pupil) एषा this एव only सा (is) she त्रायते (it) saves प्राणान् the organs तस्य of him सः he अन्वाह communicates, teaches.

 The three-footed Gayatri, consisting of the gross and subtle Universe, rests on the celestial foot the sun¹ which is apparently seen. That fourth foot, the sun, again rests on truth. It is well known that eye is indeed truth.² Therefore even now if two persons quarrel over a thing one saying,



 'I saw it ' and another contradicts him giving a different account as heard by him, we accept the account of the eye-witness as true and do not believe the other. Strength is the support of truth. The vital power is strength. Hence truth rests on the vital power. Therefore they say strength is mightier than truth. Thus the Gāyatri rests on the vital power that is within the body. That Gāyatri protected the Gayas³ which are the Therefore Gāyatri is the protector (saviour) of the organ. Gāyatri came to be so called because it protected the organs of the priests who recite them. The Savitri or hymn to the sun that the teacher teaches his pupil after investing him with the sacred thread, is this very Gāyatri which is no other than the vital power, and is the life of the whole Universe. Gāyatri protects the organs of the pupil to whom it is taught from falling into hell and other dire calamities.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. Because the sun is the life of the gross and subtle Universe. As wood when its pith is burnt or otherwise destroyed becomes dead, so things deprived of their essence become lifeless.

2\. As it has been said already in this Upanishad (3.9. 20) that the sun rests on the eye.

3\. Root-meaning of Gayas is that they produce sound. This is primarily true of the organ of speech. But here all the organs are called after it.—Anandagiri.\]

——————————————————————————————



** ताꣳ हैतामेके सावित्रीमनुष्टुभमन्वाहुर्वागनुष्टुबेतद्वाचमनुब्रूम इति न तथा कुर्याद्गायत्रीमेव सावित्रीमनुब्रूयाद्यदि ह वा अप्येवंविद्वह्विवि प्रतिगृह्णाति न हैव तद्गायत्र्या एकञ्चन पदं प्रति॥५॥**

 एके Some (the followers of some Sakha of the Vedas) अन्वाहुः communicate to, teach (their pupil) तां ह that एताम् this सावित्रीम् the Savitri अनुष्टुभम् (that is) in Anushtubh, (saying) वाक् speech (is) अनुष्टुब् Anushtubh. तत् That वाचम् speech अनुब्रूमः इति (we) shall impart. न Not कुर्यात् (one) should do तथा so, like that अनुब्रयात् (one) shall communicate to teach सावित्रीम् (that) Sāvitri एव (which is) indeed गायत्त्रीम् 'Gāyatri अपि ह Even यदि वा if एवंवित् such a knower प्रतिगृह्णाति accepts, receives बहु two much (gift) इव as it were न not हि एव much, enough प्रति for एकं च न one पदम् foot तत् गायत्र्याः of that Gāyatri.

 The followers of certain sākhās of the Vedas teach their initiated pupil the Savitri that is composed in the metre called Anushtubh saying, 'Speech is Anushtubh and it is also Saraswati in the body.' He shall communicate to the boy the speech (Saraswati). One should not do or know in that way, for what is taught by them is wholly wrong. Savitri which is verily Gayatri should be taught, because Gayatri is the vital power. If a sage with the above knowledge receives too much gift, it is nothing to him for he is identified with the



Universe. The total amount of gift he receives is not enough for even one foot of the Gāyatri.

 **स य इमाꣳस्त्रील्ँ लोकान्पूर्णान्प्रतिगृह्णीयात्सोऽस्या एतत्प्रथमं पदमाप्नुयादथ यावतीयं त्रयी विद्या यस्तावत्प्रतिगृह्णीयात्सोऽस्या एतद्द्वितीयं पदमाप्नुयादथ यावदिदं प्राणि यस्तावत्प्रतिगृह्णीयात्सोऽस्या एतत्तृतीयं पदमाप्नुयादथास्या एतदेव तुरीयं दर्शतं पदं परोरजा य एष तपति नैव केनचनाऽऽप्यं कुत उ एतावत्प्रतिगृह्णीयात्॥६॥**

 सः He (the knower of Gāyatri) यः who प्रतिगृह्णीयात् receives, accepts इमान् these त्रीन् three लोकान् worlds (earth, sky and heaven) पूर्णान् full, replete (with wealth) सः he (the knower), आप्नुयात् will receive, अस्याः her एतत् this प्रथमम् first पदम् foot. अथ Now सः he यः who प्रतिगृह्णीयात् receives, accepts तावत् as much विद्या knowledge यावती as इयम् this त्रयी the three (Vedas) आप्नुयात् will receive, will get, अस्याः her द्वितीयम् second पदम् foot. अथ Now सः he (the knower). यः who प्रतिगृह्णीयात् receives, accepts तावत् as much यावत् as इदम् this प्राणि creatures, living beings, आप्नुयात् will receive अस्या her एतत् this तृतीयम् third पदम् foot. अथ While. अस्याः her एव indeed एतत् this तुरीयम् fourth दर्शतम् apparently seen परोरजाः celestial पदम् foot, यः that एषः which तपति shines न not आप्यम् to be obtained एव indeed केन चन by anybody. कुतः How उ indeed प्रतिगृह्णीयात् (one) would receive एतावत् so much (wealth).



 The knower of the Gāyatri who receives the earth, sky and heaven full of wealth (such as cattle and horses) will receive as the result of his knowing only the first foot of the Gāyatri. The knower who receives all the knowledge that the three Vedas have to confer will receive as the result of his knowing only the second foot of Gāyatri. Similarly if the knower accepts as much wealth as is covered by all creatures, his acceptance will match the result of knowing only the third foot of Gāyatri. While her fourth, apparently sun, celestial foot which is the sun that shines high above the sky is not equivalent to any wealth accepted. It is indeed impossible for any body to receive so much wealth.¹

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. All this about wealth is simply imagined to extol the knowledge of Gayatri. By this the Upanishad emphasises the importance of meditation on the entire form of Gayatri.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **तस्या उपस्थानं गायत्र्यस्येकपदी द्विपदी त्रिपदी चतुष्पद्यपदसि न हि पद्यसे। नमस्ते तुरीयाय दर्शताय पदाय परोरजसेऽसावदो मा प्रापदिति यं द्विष्यादसावस्मै कामो मा समृद्धीति वा न हैवास्मै स कामः समृध्यते यस्मा एवमुपतिष्ठतेऽहमदः प्रापमिति वा॥७॥**



 तस्याः Her (of Gāyatri) उपस्थानम् going near and staying, salutation: गायत्त्रि O Gāyatri, असि (thou art एकपदी onefooted द्विपदी two-footed त्रिपदी three-footed, चतुष्पदी four-footed असि (and thou) art अपत् without foot, unattainable, हि for न not पद्यसे (thou) art comprehended, art attained. नमः Salutation ते to thee तुरीयाय the fourth दर्शताय apparently seen, परोरजसे celestial पदाय foot. असौ This अदः that (enemy, evil) मा not प्रापत् इति may attain, may obtain (his object); यम् to whom द्विप्यात् (he) has ill-feeling, curses वा or—असौ अस्मै such and such, so and so, naming कामः (his) object of desire मा not समृद्धी इति be abundant. सः That कामः desired object अस्मै ह एव of him यस्मै against whom उपतिष्टते (he) worships, salutes (the Gāyatri) एवम् thus न not समृध्यते abounds for, flourishes वा or अहम् I प्रापम् may attain अदः इति that (of his).

 Now follows the salutation of Gāyatri: Thou hast the three worlds as thy first foot; the three Vedas constitute thy second foot; the three forms of Vital power are thy third foot and the sun thy fourth foot. Beyond that thou art without feet in thy own unconditioned aspect. In that Supreme aspect thou being the Self described as 'Not this, not this' art not comprehended. I salute thy fourth, apparently sun, celestial foot which is the sun that shines above. May the evil that stands in my way of knowing thee never succeed in its attempt. If a knower of the Gāyatri wishes to curse



 his enemy, he should repeat this formula : ' May my enemy's (say, Devadatta's) object of desire never be abundant.' That desired object of the enemy against whom he salutes the Gāyatri never becomes abundant. He may also salute the Gāyatri saying: 'May I get the desired object of my enemy.'

 ** एतद्ध वै तज्जनको वैदेहो बुडिलमाश्वतराश्विमुवाच यन्नु हो तगायत्रीविदब्रूथा अथ कथꣳ हस्तीभूतो वहसीति मुख‍ꣳ ह्यस्याः सम्राण्न विदाञ्चकारेति होवाच तस्या अग्निरेव मुखं यदि ह वा अपि बह्विवाग्नावभ्यादधति सर्वमेव तत्सन्दहत्येव‍ꣳ हैवैवंविद्यद्यपि बह्विव पापं कुरुते सर्वमेव तत्सम्प्साय शुद्धः पूतोऽजरोऽमृतः सम्भवति॥८॥इति चतुर्दशं ब्राह्मणम्॥१४॥**

 एतत् ह On this (knowledge of Gāyatri) वै verily तत् that जनकः Janaka वैदेहः Emperor of Videha उवाच said बुडिलम् to Budila आश्वतराश्विम् the son of Āshwatarāshwi हो well, नु deliberately यत् as अब्रूथाः (you) said, called गायत्त्रीविद् (as) a knower of Gāyatri तत् then अथ now कथम् why वहसि (you) carry (me) हस्तीभूतः an elephant, a fool. उवाच ह (Budila) said—हि because सम्राट् 0 Emperor न not विदाञ्चकार (I) knew अस्याः her (of Gāyatri) मुखम् इति mouth. अग्निः Fire (is) एव indeed अस्याः her मुखम् mouth. अपि ह Even यदि वा if अभ्यादधति (common people) throws, puts, अग्नौ into the fire इव like बहु many, large quantity (of fuel) तत् it (that fuel) सन्दहति burns, consumes सर्वम् all एव indeed एवं ह एव



 similarly यदि if अपि even एवमूवित् a knower of this कुरुते commits बहु इव a great many पापम् sins सम्प्साय burning, consuming सर्वम् all एतत् this एव certainly सम्भवति becomes शुद्धः clean पूतः pure अजरः without decay अमृतः without death.

 Now follows an eulogistic story on the knowledge of the Gayatri. Emperor Janaka spoke to Budila, the son of Āshwatarashvi: 'Well, you called yourself a knower of the Gāyatri; how then that you afe acting to the contrary by carrying me as an elephant?' Budila said to the emperor in reply that it was due to his ignorance of the mouth of Gāyatri. The Emperor then said: Fire is the mouth of Gāyatri. Even if common people throw much fuel into the fire, that fuel is all consumed. Similarly one who knows that fire is the mouth of Gāyatri burns like fire all the sins committed by him due to acceptance of gifts, etc. That knowledge makes him clean, pure and free from decay as well as death.

**CHAPTER FIVE: SECTION FIFTEEN**

 **हिरण्मयेन पात्रेण सत्यस्यापिहितं मुखम्। तत्त्वं पूषन्नपावृणु सत्यधर्माय दृष्टये। पूषन्नकर्षे यम सूर्य प्राजापत्य व्यूह **



**रश्मीन्। समूह तेजो यत्ते रूपं कल्याणतमं तत्ते पश्यामि। योऽसावसौ पुरुषः सोऽहमस्मि। वायुरनिलममृतमथेदं भस्मान्त‍ꣳ शरीरम्। ॐ क्रतो स्मर कृतꣳ स्मर क्रतो स्मर कृतꣳ स्मर। अग्ने नय सुपथा राये अस्मान्विश्वानि देव वयुनानि विद्वान्। युयोध्यस्मज्जुहुराणमेनो भूयिष्ठां ते नमउक्तिं विधेम॥१॥ इति पश्चदशं ब्राह्मणम्॥१५॥ इति बृहदारण्यकोपनिषदि पञ्चमोऽध्यायः॥५॥**

 पात्रेण With vessel, disk हिरण्मयेन golden, shining मुखम् the face (real nature) सत्यस्य of satya (Brahman) अपिहितम् (is) covered, hidden पूषन् Pushan ( nourisher of the world) त्वम् you अपावृणु take away, remove तत् it, (the vessel) दृष्टये for the vision सत्यधर्माय (of me) whose nature is satya (Brahman). पूषन् O nourisher एकर्षे ( = एक + ऋषि) Osolitary sun (traveller) यम O controller (of the world) सूर्य O sun, (director of all beings) प्राजापत्य O son of Prajāpati (Hiranyagarbha) व्यूह withdraw रश्मीन् (thy) rays, समूह reduce, curb तेजः (thy) radiance पश्यामि (we) see तत् that रूपम् form ते of yours यत् which ते of yours ( is) कल्याणतमम् most auspicious. अहम् I अस्मि am सः that पुरुष : person (Satya Brahman) यः which (is) असौ this असौ this, अमृतम् (I am) immortal वायुः (may my) vital power (in the body) अनिलम् (go back) to the external air (cosmic force). अथ And इदम् this शरीरम् body भस्मान्तम् (be) reduced to ashes, go to the earth. क्रतो O Deity of deliberations ॐ (who art) Om स्मर remember कृतम् all, that done (by me) स्मर remember, क्रतो



O Deity of knowledge स्मर remember स्मर recollect कृतम् (my) deeds. अग्ने O Fire, नय lead, guide श्रस्मान् us सुपथा by the good way (Northern way) राये towards riches (the fruits of action) देव O Lord विद्वान् (you are) aware विश्वानि all वयुनानि mental conditions, works युयोधि remove, separateअस्मत् from us जुहराणम् tricky, crafty एनः sin, evil, विधेम (we) offer, repeat भूयिष्ठाम् good many नमउक्तिम् words of salutations ते to thee.

 The real nature of Satya-Brahman is covered¹ as it were, with the shining disk-the solar orb. O Sun, the nourisher of the world, take away the disk that serves as a cover, so that I, who am identical with Satya-Brahman (i.e., thee), may see the face. O, solitary² traveller, O controller of the world, O director of all beings, O son of Hiranyagarbha, withdraw thy rays, contract thy radiance. We wish to see thy most auspicious form. As I am identified with Satya-Brahman and immortal, when my body falls, may my vital power in the body go back to the cosmic force; and this body, too, return to the earth in the shape of ashes. O Fire, whose symbol is Om, O Deity of knowledge, remember all my deeds. O Deity of knowledge, recollect all my actions. O Fire, guide us along the northern way towards the fruits of actions. O Lord, thou art aware of our actions and mental conditions. Free us from the tricky evil. We offer repeated salutations to thee.



——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Because without concentration of mind it cannot be seen.

2\. As Taittirya Samhita (7. 4. 18. 1) says, 'The sun roams alone.'\]

——————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER SIX: SECTION ONE**

 **ॐ यो ह वै ज्येष्ठं च श्रेष्ठं च वेद ज्येष्ठश्च श्रेष्ठश्व स्वानां भवति प्राणो वै ज्येष्ठश्च श्रेष्ठश्च ज्येष्ठश्च श्रेष्ठश्च स्वानां भवत्यपि च येषां बुभूषति य एवं वेद॥१॥**

ॐ Om, a word of auspiciousness.यः (He) who वै ह emphatically, surely वेद knows ज्येष्टं च the oldest, the first श्रेष्ठं च and the greatest भवति becomes ज्येष्ठः च the oldest च and श्रेष्टः the greatest, the best स्वानाम् among (his) relatives, people. वै Verily, legitimately प्राणः the vital power ज्येष्ठः च (is) the oldest च and श्रेष्टः the greatest, the best यः (he) who वदे knows, meditates एवम् (as) such भवति becomes ज्येष्ठः च the oldest च and श्रेष्ठः best स्वानाम् among relatives, among peers अपि च as well as येषां among whom बुभूषति (he) desires to be (such).

 Om. One who knows that vital power is prior to all the organs in years and attributes, surely becomes the first and best among his own people. The vital power is legitimately the oldest¹ and greatest of all the organs. He who meditates



 upon the vital power as such emphatically becomes by virtue of that meditation the first and best among his own people as well as others whom he desires to beat in seniority and superiority.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. Because the vital power is the first of all organs to begin functioning. The embryo is fostered by it from the very time of its conception. Other organs start to function only after the vital power does so.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** यो ह वै वसिष्ठां वेद वसिष्ठः स्वानां भवति वाग्वै वसिष्ठा वसिष्ठः स्वानां भवत्यपि च येषां बुभूषति य एवं वेद॥२॥**

 यः (He) who वै ह verily, surely वेद knows वसिष्ठाम् Vasistha भवति becomes वसिष्ठः the Vasistha स्वानाम् among (his) people. वाक् speech वै indeed वसिष्टा (is) the Vasistha यः (He) who वेद knows एवम् thus भवति becomes वसिष्ठः Vasistha स्वानाम् among (his) relatives अपि च as well as येषां ((among those) of whom बुभुषति (he) desires to be.

 \[The ensuing conversation shows how the vital power is also the greatest of all organs. For, in a family the oldest member may not be the greatest for want of good qualities; sometimes the youngest member is the best on account of superior qualities.\]

He who knows the Vasistha¹ surely becomes the Vasistha among his people. The speech is indeed the Vasistha. He who Knows speech as



such verily becomes the Vasistha among his people as well as others whom he desires to overcome in wealth and eloquence.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. The literal meaning of the word is 'That which enables one to live in splendour or that which covers. one with splendour '.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** यो ह वै प्रतिष्ठां वेद प्रतितिष्ठति समे प्रतितिष्ठति दुर्गे चक्षुर्वै प्रतिष्ठा चक्षुषा हि समे च दुर्गे च प्रतितिष्ठति प्रतितिष्ठति समे प्रतितिष्ठति दुर्गे य एवं वेद॥३॥**

 यः (He) who वै ह verily, surely वेद knows प्रतिष्ठाम् Pratistha प्रतितिष्ठति lives steadily समे in smooth (places and times), प्रतितिष्ठति stands firm दुर्गे in difficult (places and times). वै Verily चक्षुः the eye (is) प्रतिष्ठा the Pratistha ; हि for चक्षुषा through the eye प्रतितिष्ठति (one) lives steadily समे च in smooth दुर्गे च as well as in difficult (places and times). यः (He) who एवम् thus वेद knows प्रतितिष्ठति lives steadily समे in smooth (places and times) प्रतितिष्ठति lives. steadily दुर्गे in difficult (places and times).

 He who knows Pratistha¹ surely stands firm in smooth places and times as well as in inaccessible places and hard times such as those of famine. The eye is indeed the Pratistha, because by seeing them through the eye one stands firm in favourable as well as in adverse places and times. He who



knows the speech as such stands firm in good as well as bad situations and circumstances.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES 1. Literally it means that which has steadiness or that by which one becomes steady in life.\]

——————————————————————————————

** यो ह वै सम्पदं वेद सꣳ हास्मै पद्यते यं कामं कामयते श्रोत्रं वै सम्पच्छ्रोत्रे हीमे सर्वे वेदा अभिसम्पन्नाः सꣳ हास्मै पद्यते यं कामं कामयते य एवं वेद॥४॥**

 अस्मै To him यः who वै ह verily वेद knows सम्पदम् Sampad, prosperity सम्पद्यते comes ह surely यः whatever कामम् desire, object कामयते (he) desires. श्रोत्रम् The ear (is) वै verily सम्पत् Sampad, prosperity, हि for श्रोत्रे through the ears सर्वे all इमे these वेदाः Vedas अभिसम्पन्नाः (are) treasured, known. अस्मै To him यः who एवम् thus वेद knows सम्पद्यते ह comes यम् whatever कामम् desire, object कामयते (one ) desires.

 To him who knows that which is possessed of prosperity comes whatever object he desires. The ear indeed is endowed with the attribute of prosperity; because when the organ of hearing remains intact, the Vedas are known and the sacrifices enjoined by them are performed for the attainment of desired objects. To him who knows the ear as such verily comes his desired object.



** यो ह वा आयतनं वेदाऽऽयतनꣳ स्वानां भवत्यायतनं जनानां मनो वा आयतनमायतन‍ꣳ स्वानां भवत्यायतनं जनानां य एवं वेद ॥५॥**

 यः (He) who वै ह verily वेद knows आयतनम् the abode भवति becomes आयतनम् the abode, the refuge स्वानाम् of his people, आयतनम् the abode जनानाम् of the other people. मनः The mind वै indeed आयतनम् (is) the abode, the refuge. यः (He) who वेद knows एवम् thus भवति becomes आयतनम् the abode, the refuge स्वानाम् of his people, आयतनम् the abode जनानाम् of other people.

 He who knows the refuge verily becomes the refuge of his own people as well as others. The mind indeed is the refuge of the organs and their objects; because the mind directs the organs, and harbours the objects that are enjoyed by the Self. He who knows the mind as such verily becomes the refuge of his own people as well as others.

** यो ह वै प्रजापतिं वेद प्रजायते ह प्रजया पशुभी रेतो वै प्रजातिः प्रजायते ह प्रजया पशुभिर्य एवं वेद॥६॥**

 यः (He) who वै ह verily वेद knows प्रजातिम् Prajāti, that which is endowed with the attribute of generation प्रजायते ह becomes rich प्रजया with offspring पशुभिः with animals. रेतः Semen, the organ of generation वै (is) verily प्रजातिः Prajāti.



यः (He) who वेद knows एवम् thus प्रजायते ह becomes rich प्रजया with offspring पशुभिः with animals.

 He who knows that which is endowed with the attribute of generation becomes rich with offsprings and animals. The generative organ is indeed possessed of the attribute of generation. He who knows it to be such becomes rich with offsprings and animals.

 **ते हेमे प्राणा अहꣳ श्रेयसे विवदमाना ब्रह्म जग्मुस्तद्धोचुः को नो वसिष्ठ इति तद्धोवाच यस्मिन्व उत्क्रान्त इदꣳशरीरं पापीयो मन्यते स वो वसिष्ठ इति॥७॥**

 ते ह Those इमे these प्राणाः sense-organs विवदमानाः quarrelling over, disputing over (their greatness)अहं श्रेयसे (each) for his superiority जग्मु went to, approached ब्रह्म Brahman, Prajāpati ऊचुः said इति this तत् ह to him कः which नः of us वसिष्ठः the Vasistha, superior तत् ह He (Prajapati) उवाच said, replied सः he, that one वः of you वसिष्ठः इति (is) superior यस्मिन् in which वः of you उत्क्रान्ते in going out (of the body), in departing मन्यते think, regards इदम् this शरीरम् body पापीयः more sinful, more wretched.

 Once these organs quarrelled over their respective superiority, approached Prajapati and asked him which of them was the superior. Prajapati replied,¹ 'He who among yourselves going out of



this body regards it much more sinful than before² is superior.'

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES —1. Prajapati said this for creating disgust in. us for the body.

2\. Body being composed of impure matters is wretched. even while alive.\]

——————————————————————————————

** वाग्घोच्चक्राम सा संवत्सरं प्रोष्याऽऽगत्योवाच कथमशकत मदृते जीवितुमिति ते होचुर्यथाऽकला अवदन्तो वाचा प्राणन्तः प्राणेन पश्यन्तश्चक्षुषा शृण्वन्तः श्रोत्रेण विद्वाꣳसो मनसा प्रजायमाना रेतसैवमजीविष्मेति प्रविवेश ह वाक्॥८॥**

 वाक् The speech ह a particle उच्चक्राम went out, got out. सा She, It प्रोष्य spending, having sojourned संवत्सरं a whole year आगत्य coming back उवाच said इति this कथम् how अशकत (you) are able जीवितुम् to live ऋते without मत् me. ते They (other organs) ह ऊचुः said यथा as अकलाः the dumb, the mute अवदन्तः without speaking वाचा through the organ of speech, प्राणन्तः living, doing the vital function प्राणेन through the vital power, पश्यन्तः seeing, doing the function of vision चक्षुषा through the eyes, श्रृण्वन्तः hearing श्रोत्रेण through. the ear, विद्वांसः knowing, considering what ought or ought not to be done मनसा through the mind, प्रजायमानाः procreating, generating रेतसा through the semen, through the organ of generation एवम् thus अजीविष्म इति (we) have lived. वाक् The speech प्रविवेश ह entered.



 Thus addressed by Prajapati the speech first got out of the body to try his power. Having spent one whole year outside the body it returned and said, "How were you able to live without me?" Other organs replied that they lived just as in the world the mute men live without the power of speech doing the vital function through the vital power, doing the function of vision through the eyes, hearing through the ears, considering what ought or ought not to be done through the mind and procreating through the organ of generation. Thus answered by the organs the speech realised that it was not the chief in the body and got back. into the same.

 **चक्षुर्होच्चक्राम तत्संवत्सरं प्रोष्याऽऽगत्योवाच कथमशकत मदृते जीवितुमिति ते होचुर्यथाऽन्धा अपश्यन्तश्चक्षुषा प्राणन्तः प्राणेन वदन्तो वाचा शृण्वन्तः श्रोत्रेण विद्वाꣳसो मनसा प्रजायमाना रेतसैवमजीविष्मेति प्रविवेश ह चक्षुः॥९॥**

 चक्षुः ह The eye उच्चक्राम went out, got out. तत् It प्रोष्य spending out संवत्सरम् a whole year आगत्य returning उवाच said इति this कथम् how अशकत (you) were able जीवितुम् to live ऋते without मत् me. तेह They (other organs) ऊचुः said यथा as अन्धाः the blind अपश्यन्तः without seeing चतुषा through the eyes, प्राणन्तः living प्राणेन through the vital: power, वदन्तः speaking वाचा through the organ of speech,



शृण्वन्तः hearing श्रोत्रेण through the ears, विद्वांसः knowing मनसा through the mind, प्रजायमानाः procreating रेतसा through the semen, through the organ of generation एवम् thus श्रजीविष्म इति (we) have lived प्रविवेश ह Entered चक्षुः the eye.

 Then the eye got out of the body to try its power. Having sojourned one whole year outside the body it returned and said, "How were you able to live without me?" Other organs replied that they lived just as in the world the blind men live without sight, doing the vital function through the vital power, speaking through the organ of speech, hearing through the ears, considering through the mind what should or should not be done as well as procreating through the organ of generation. Thus answered, the eye realised that it was not the chief in the body and got back into the same.

** श्रोत्रꣳ होच्चक्राम तत्संवत्सरं प्रोष्याऽऽगत्योवाच कथमशकत महते जीवितुमिति ते होचुर्यथा बधिरा अशृण्वन्तः श्रोत्रेण प्राणन्तः प्राणेन वदन्तो वाचा पश्यन्तश्चक्षुषा विद्वाꣳसो मनसा प्रजायमाना रेतसैवमजीविष्मेति प्रविवेश ह श्रोत्रम्॥१०॥**

 श्रोत्रं ह The ear, the organ of hearing उच्चक्राम got out.तत् It प्रोष्य spending out संवत्सरम् whole year आगत्य returning उवाच said इति this कथम् how अशकत were (you) able जीवितुम्



to live ऋते without मत् me. ते ह They (other organs) ऊचुः said यथा as बधिराः the deaf अशृण्वन्तः without hearing श्रोत्रेण through the ears, प्राणन्तः living, doing the vital function प्राणेन through the vital power, वदन्तः speaking वाचा through the organ of speech, पश्यन्तः seeing, doing the function of vision चक्षुषा through the eyes, विद्वांसः knowing मनसा through the mind प्रजायमानाः procreating रेतसा through the semen, . through the organ of generation एवम् thus अजीविष्म इति (we) have lived. प्रविवेश ह Entered श्रोत्रम् the ear, the organ of hearing.

 Then the organ of hearing got out of the body to try its power. Having spent one whole year outside the body it returned and said, "How were you able to live without me?" Other organs replied that they lived just as in the world the deaf men live, without the power of hearing but doing the vital function through the vital power, speaking through the organ of speech, doing the function of vision through the eyes, considering through the mind what should or should not be done as well as. procreating through the organ of generation. Thus answered, the organ of hearing realised that it is not the chief in the body and got back into the same.

** मनो होच्चक्राम तत्संवत्सरं प्रोष्याऽऽगत्योवाच कथमशकत मदृते जीवितुमिति ते होचुर्यथा मुग्धा अविद्वाꣳसो मनसाः**



**प्राणन्तः प्राणेन वदन्तो वाचा पश्यन्तश्चक्षुषा शृण्वन्तः श्रोत्रेण प्रजायमाना रेतसैवमजीविष्मेति प्रविवेश ह मनः॥११॥**

 मनः ह The mind उच्चक्राम got out. तत् It प्रोष्य spending out संवत्सरम् a whole year out आगत्य returning उवाच said इति this कथम् how अशकत were (you) able जीवितुम् to live ऋते without मत् me. ते ह They (other organs) ऊचुः said यथा as मुग्धाः idiots अविद्वांसः without knowing मनसा through the mind, प्राणन्तः living, doing the vital function प्राणेन through the vital power, वदन्तः speaking वाचा through the organs of speech, पश्यन्तः seeing चक्षुषा through the eye, शृण्वन्तः hearing श्रोत्रेण through the ear, प्रजायमानाः procreating रेतसा through the semen, through the generative organ, एवम् thus अजीविष्म इति (we) have lived. मनः The mind प्रविवेश ह entered.

 Then the mind got out of the body to try his eminence. Having stayed out for the space of a year it returned and said, "How were you able to live without me?" Other organs replied that they lived just as in the world idiots live, without considering what should or should not be done through the mind, but doing the vital function through the vital power, speaking through the organ of speech, seeing through the eyes, hearing through the ear, and procreating through the generative organ. Thus answered, the mind understood that it was not the chief in the body and got back into the same.



 ** रेतो होच्चक्राम तत्संवत्सरं प्रोष्याऽऽगत्योवाच कथमशकत मदृते जीवितुमिति ते होचुर्यथा क्लीवा अप्रजायमाना रेतसा प्राणन्तः प्राणेन वदन्तो वाचा पश्यन्तश्चक्षुषा शृण्वन्तः श्रोत्रेण विद्वाꣳसो मनसैवमजीविष्मेति प्रविवेश ह रेतः॥१२॥**

 रेतः ह Semen (generative organ) उच्चक्राम went out. तत् It प्रोष्य spending out संवत्सरम् a whole year आगत्य returning उवाच said इति this, कथम् how अशकत were (you) able जीवितुम् to live ऋते without मत् me? ते ह They (other organs) ऊचुः said यथा as क्लीबाः eunuchs, the impotent अप्रजायमानाः procreating रेतसा through semen (organ of generation), प्राणन्तः living प्राणेन through the vital power, वदन्तः speaking वाचा through the organs of speech, पश्यन्तः seeing चक्षुषा through the eye, शृण्वन्तः hearing श्रोत्रेण through the ear, विद्वांसः knowing मनसा through the mind. एवम् Thus अजीविष्म इति (we) have lived प्रविवेश ह Entered रेतः generative organ.

 The generative organ got out of the body to try its eminence. Having been away from the body for the space of a year it returned and said, "How were you able to live without me?" Other Organs replied that they lived just as in the world the impotent live without the power of procreation but doing the vital function through the vital power, speaking through the organ of speech, seeing through the eyes, hearing through the ears, and



considering what should or should not be done. through the mind. Thus answered, the generative organ understood that it was not eminent in the body and got back into the same.

 **अथ ह प्राण उत्क्रमिष्यन्यथा महासुहयः सैन्धवः पड्वीशशङ्कून्संवृहेदेवꣳ हैवेमान्प्राणान्संववर्ह ते होचुर्मा भगव उत्क्रमीर्न वै शक्ष्यामस्त्वदृते जीवितुमिति तस्यो मे बलिं कुरुतेति तथेति॥१३॥**

 अथ ह Then यथा as, when प्राणः the vital power उत्क्रमिष्यन् about to go out संववर्ह (it) shook off इमान् those प्राणान् organs इव as it were एवं ह just as महासुहयः a great fine horse सैन्धवः born in Sind संवृहेत shakes out षड्वीशशङ्कून् the tether-pegs they (other organs) उचुः said इति thus: भगवः Sir मा not उत्क्रमीः depart. वै Verily न not शक्ष्यामः (we) are able जीवितुम् to live ऋते without त्वत् you ; तस्य to that, to such मे myself कुरुत do, give बलिम् इति offering, tribute, तथा इति so ( let it be).

 Then when the vital power was about to leave the body it shook off those organs from their places, just as a large-sized, noble-featured horse born in Sind simultaneously shakes off the tether pegs. They requested him not to leave, for they could not live without him. The vital power said, If you have realised my eminence, do offerings to



me, who is your chief. " The organs, when demand-ed tribute agreed, and said ' let it be so. '

 \[This conversation is an imaginary device to show how a wise man reasons, when he wants to find out for the purposes of meditation the greatest of organs.\]

 **सा ह वागुवाच यद्वा अहं वसिष्ठाऽस्मि त्वं तद्वसिष्ठोऽसीति यद्वा अहं प्रतिष्ठाऽस्मि त्वं तत्प्रतिष्ठोऽसीति चक्षुर्यद्वा अहꣳ सम्पदस्मि त्वं तत्सम्पदसीति श्रोत्रं यद्वा अहमायतनमस्मि त्वं तदायतनमसीति मनो यद्वा अहं प्रजातिरस्मि त्वं तत्प्रजातिरसीति रेतस्तस्यो मे किमन्नं किं वास इति यदिदं किञ्चाऽऽश्वभ्य आ कृमिभ्य आ कीटपतङ्गेभ्यस्तत्तेऽन्नमापो वास इति न ह वा अस्यानन्नं जग्धं भवति नानन्नं प्रतिगृहीतं य एवमेतदनस्यान्नं वेद तद्विद्वाꣳसः श्रोत्रिया अशिष्यन्त आचामन्त्यशित्वाऽऽचामन्त्येतमेव तदन्नमनग्नं कुर्वन्तो मन्यन्ते॥१४॥ इति प्रथमं ब्राह्मणम्॥१॥**

 सा ह She वाक् the speech उवाच said इति this तत् that वसिष्ठः Vasistha, eminent, chief वै verily असि are त्वम् you यत् which वसिष्ठः Vasistha, attribute of eminence अस्मि am अहम् I. चक्षुः The eye इति (said) this तत् that प्रतिष्ठा steadiness असि are त्वम् you यत् which प्रतिष्ठा steadiness वै verily अहम् I अस्मि am. श्रोत्रम् The ear इति (said) this तत् that सम्पत् prosperity असि are त्वम् you यत् which सम्पत् prosperity, वै verily अहम् I अस्मि am. मनः The mind इति (said) this



तत् that आयतनम् abode असि are त्वम् you यत् which आयतनम् abode वै verily अहम् I अस्मि am. रेतः Semen (generative organ) इति (said) this तत् that प्रजातिः procreation, generation असि are त्वम् you यत् which प्रजातिः procreation वै verily अहम् I अस्मि am. इति (Vital force said) this उ oh किम् what अन्नम् food, किम् what वासः dress, तस्य of that मे myself यत् इदं किं च whatever there (is) आ+श्वभ्यः upto dogs आ+कृमिभ्यः upto worms आ+कीटपतङ्गेभ्यः upto insects and moths तत् that (is) ते your अन्नम् food इति (and) this आपः water वासः dress अस्य of him यः who वेद knows एवम् thus एतत् this अन्नम् food अनस्य of the vital power वै ह indeed न not भवति is जग्धम् eaten अनन्नम् (न+अन्नम्) improper food; न not परिगृहीतम् (is) received अनन्नम् forbidden food. तत् That विद्वांसः the knowers, Brahmanas श्रोत्रियाः the Vedic scholars आचामन्ति sip water अशिष्यन्तः about to eat, before eating अशित्वा after eating आचामन्ति drink water; मन्यन्ते (they) think एतम् एव that कुर्वन्तः making अनन्नम् (न+नग्नम्) dressed, clothed तत् that अन्नम् vital power.

 The speech first came forward to make his offering to the vital power and said, "The attribute of eminence with which I am endowed belongs to you. You are eminent with that." Then the eye offered his tribute saying, "The attribute of steadiness of which I am possessed belongs to you; for you are that steadiness." The ear paid its tribute saying, "The attribute of prosperity which is mine is yours." The mind then gave its



attribute of abode to this chief. Similarly the generative organ offered its attribute of procreation to him. When handsome tributes were thus paid to the vital power, it wanted to know what would be its food and dress. The organs replied that whatever is known in the world as food for dogs, worms, insects and moths as well as other creatures is all your food¹ and water that is drunk will stand for your dress.² He who knows that every thing is the food of the vital power does never accept or eat any forbidden food.³ Therefore Brahmanas who are vedic scholars drink a little water before and after taking food. They think that this act of sipping gives dress to the vital power.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. It is an injunction to meditation upon everything as the food of the vital force.

2\. Another injunction for meditation on water as the dress of the vital force.

3\. It is an eulogy of the meditation on everything as the food of the vital power. The vital power in general is meant here, not any of its particular form that is associated with the body of an individual. Although everything may be food for the cosmic vital power, it cannot be so for its particular form. Some kind of food may sustain the life of some creatures as poison sustains the worm born in it, but it will mean death to an animal or man. Hence it does not mean that the eating of prohibited food is harmless.\]

——————————————————————————————



** श्वेतकेतुर्ह वा आरुणेयः पञ्चालानां परिषदमाजगाम स आजगाम जैविलिं प्रवाहणं परिचारयमाणं तमुदीक्ष्याभ्युवाद कुमारा३ इति स भो३ इति प्रतिशुश्रावानुशिष्टोऽन्वसि पित्रेत्योमिति होवाच॥१॥**

 श्वेतकेतुः ह Svetaketu आरुणेयः the son of Āruni वै certainly आजगाम went परिषदम् to the assembly पञ्चालानाम् of the Panchalas. सः He आजगाम came प्रवाहणम् to Pra-vahana जैबलिम् the son of Jivala परिचारयमाणम् having (his servants) to wait upon him. उदीच्य Seeing तम् him अभ्युवाद (the king) said, addressed (him) इति thus कुमारा ३\* oh youth. सः He (Svetaketu) प्रतिशुश्राव replied इति thus भो ३ yes, Sir अन्वासि have (you) been अनुशिष्टः taught पित्रा इति by father. ह उवाच (He) said ओम् इति yes.

 Taught by his father Āruni, Svetaketu went to the learned assembly of the Panchālas to display his learning. With a mind to conquer the as-sembly and the royal court he approached Pravāhana, the son of Jivala, and the King of Panchāla, who was having his servants to attend on him. As soon as he arrived, the King addressed him ' Oh youth.'¹ Thus addressed, Svetaketu said, " Yes, Sir. " The King then asked him whether

——————————————————————————————

\* The prolonged accent expresses censure.

——————————————————————————————



he was taught by his father. The other replied in the affirmative.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. This form of address is used in anger; for a King being a Khsatriya is not entitled to address a Brahmana in this way.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **वेत्थ यथेमाः प्रजाः प्रयत्यो विप्रतिपद्यन्ता ३ इति नेति होवाच वेत्थो यथेमं लोकं पुनरापद्यन्ता ३ इति नेति हैवोवाच वेत्थो यथाऽसौ लोक एवं बहुभिः पुनः पुनः प्रयद्भिर्न सम्पूर्यता ३ इति नेति हैवोवाच वेत्थो यतिथ्यामाहुत्याꣳ हुतायामापः पुरुषवाचो भूत्वा समुत्थाय वदन्ती ३ इति नेति हैवोवाच वेत्थो देवयानस्य वा पथः प्रतिपदं पितृयाणस्य वा यत्कृत्वा देवयानं वा पन्थानं प्रतिपद्यन्ते पितृयाणं वाऽपि हि न ऋषेर्वचः श्रुतं द्वे सृती अश्रृणवं पितॄणामहं देवानामुत मर्त्यानां ताभ्यामिदं विश्वमेजत्समेति यदन्तरा पितरं मातरं चेति नाहमत एकञ्चन वेदेति होवाच॥२॥**

 वेत्थ Do (you) know यथा how, by which way इमाः these प्रजाः people प्रयत्यः when departing, when dying विप्रतिपद्यन्ते इति go to particular places? उवाच ह (He) said न इति no. वेत्थ उ Do (you) know यथा how, by which way आपद्यन्ते (they) come, return पुनः again इमम् to this लोकम् world? न इति ह no उवाच एव (he) said. वेत्थ उ Do (you) know यथा how, why असौ that, the other, the next लोकः world न not सम्पूर्यते is filled बहुभिः by so many प्रयद्भिः departing (dying) ones



एवम् thus, in the familiar way पुनः again पुनः इति again. न No उवाच एव said (he). वेत्थ Do (you) know यतिथ्याम् how many आहुत्याम् oblations, libations हुतायाम् being offered आपः water, the liquid offerings, समुत्थाय rising up भूत्वा becoming, being passed of पुरुषवाचः a human voice वदन्ती इति speaks ? न इति ह No उवाच एव said (he) वेत्थ उ do (you) know प्रतिपदम् the means of access, the rites पथः to the path देवयानस्य the way of the gods वा or पितृयानस्य of the way of the manes कृत्वा doing, adopting यत् which प्रतिपद्यन्ते (people) attain, get पन्थानम् to the path देवयानस्य of the way of the gods वा or पितृयानस्य of the way of the Manes. अपि हि Moreover न not श्रुतम् heard वचः words ऋषेः of the Rishi— अहम् I अशृणवम् have heard द्वे two सृती routes, paths मर्त्यानाम् of mortals, of men पितॄणाम् of the fathers, of the Manes उत and देवानाम् of the gods एजत् going ताभ्याम् along these two (paths) इदम् this विश्वम् universe समेति is united यत् which (lies) अन्तरा between पितरम् the father (earth) च and मातरम् इति the mother (heaven) उवाच ह said (he) अहम् I न not वेद् know एकं चन one अतः इति of them.

 The King asked him, "Do you know how these people are divided ¹ after death?" Svetaketu replied in the negative. The King asked him again "Do you know how do these people come back to this world?" The other gave a negative reply. The King then asked him if he knows why the next world never becomes full, although so many people are leaving this world in the



familiar way for it? 'No' replied Svetaketu. "Do you know after how many libations are offered, the liquid offerings take a human form and become endowed with a human voice and speaks"? 'No', replied the other. "Do you know the ways of entrance to the way of the gods or the way of the fathers, in other words, the kind of rites by whose performance people gain access to either way?" Moreover have you not heard the following words of the Rishi ²: 'I have heard of the two paths for transmigration relating to men. Going along these two paths this universe ³ is united.' They lie between the earth and heaven. Svetaketu replied, "I know not a single of this set of questions."

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The departed spirits travel along the same route and then come to a point where the roads diverge into different directions. Some take the one and some the other.

2\. This Mantra appears in the Rig-Veda (10. 88. 15.) In Shatapath Brahman (13. 2. 9. 7) and Taittiriya Brahman (3. 8. 9. 1) it is also said: 'This earth is the mother and heaven is the father.'

3\. The universe consisting of means and ends. This world is connected with the next by these two paths. The departed spirits go to their destinations, travelling on these two paths that are within the two halves of the Universe, and therefore belong to the relative world. They are unable to lead one to Absolute Goal.—Anandagiri.\]

——————————————————————————————



** अथैनं वसत्योपमन्त्रयाञ्चक्रेऽनादृत्य वसतिं कुमारः प्रदुद्राव स आजगाम पितरं तꣳ होवाचेति वाव किल नो भवान्पुराऽनुशिष्टानवोच इति कथꣳ सुमेध इति पञ्च मा प्रश्नान्राजन्यबन्धुरप्राक्षीत्ततो नैकञ्चन वेदेति कतमे त इतीम इति ह प्रतीकान्युदाजहार॥३॥**

 अथ Then उपमन्त्रयाञ्चक्रे (the King) invited, told एनम् him (Swetaketu) वसत्या for a stay, to live as student कुमारः the boy प्रदुद्राव went away, hurried away अनादृत्य disregarding वसतिम् (the invitation) for a stay, to live as student. सः He (Swetaketu) आजगाम came पितरम् to father उवाच ह (and) said तम् to him इति this वाव well भवान् you किल indeed अवोचः told नः us, me पुरा before, at the time of finishing study अनुशिष्टान् इति instructed. कथम् Why सुमेधः इति (my) intelligent son? राजन्यबन्धुः an associate of the Kshatriyas, the fellow of a Rajanya, अप्राक्षीत् asked मा me पञ्च five प्रश्नान् questions. वेद् (I) know न not एकं चन one ततः इति of them, कतमे which (are) ते इति they इमे इति these उदाजहार (he) reproduced, repeated प्रतीकानि the sentences, the words.

 After removing his pride of learning the King invited Svetaketu for a stay. But Svetaketu did not care for the invitation to live as a student and hastened away to his father. He came to his father and asked him, "Well, you told me at the time of finishing study that you had instructed me in every branch of learning." The father said,



"What has caused your grief, my intelligent son?" "That wretched King asked me five questions none of which I could answer," replied the son. The father inquired those questions asked by the King. The son reproduced the very words of those questions to his father.

 **स होवाच तथा नस्त्वं तात जानीथा यथा यदहं किञ्च वेद सर्वमहं तत्तुभ्यमवोचं प्रेहि तु तत्र प्रतीत्य ब्रह्मचर्यं वत्स्याव इति भवानेव गच्छत्विति स आजगाम गौतमो यत्र प्रवाहणस्य जैवलेरास तस्मा आसनमाहृत्योदकमाहारयाञ्चकारथ हास्मा अर्घ्यं चकार तꣳ होवाच वरं भगवते गौतमाय दद्म इति॥४॥**

 सः ह He (Āruni) उवाच said तात my son त्वम् you जानीथाः should know, should believe नः from us, from me यथा as यत् किञ्चन whatever अहम् I वेद knew तथा so सर्वम् all तत् that अहम् I अवोचम् told, taught तुभ्यम् you. तु But प्रेहि come प्रतीत्य going तत्र there वत्स्यावः (we both) shall live ब्रह्मचर्यम् इति life of a student, भवान् you एव alone गच्छतु इति go please. सः That गौतमः Gautama, (Āruni) descended from Gautama आजगाम came यत्र to where प्रवाहणस्य (the house) of Pravahana जैवलेः the son of Jivala आस was. आहृत्य Bringing तस्मै for him (for Āruni) आसनम् a seat उदकम् water आहारयाञ्चकार caused to be brought. अथ ह Then चकार (the King) made अस्मै for him अर्घ्यम् reverential offering उवाच ह said तम् to him दद्मः (we) shall give, shall offer, वरम् a boon भगवते to revered गौतम Gautama इति.



 Āruni in order to soothe his angry son said, "My son, believe me, whatever of meditations I knew I taught you all that. I too do not know what the King asked about. Therefore, let us go there and live as students with the King to learn it. The son refused to go to the King. At this, Āruni, descended from Gautama, went to where King Pravāhaṇa, son of Jivala, was holding an assembly. The King offered a respectable seat to Āruni, got water for him through servants and gave him the reverential offering. Then the King said to Āruni, "Revered Sir, we will offer you a boon consisting of cows, horses, etc."

** स होवाच प्रतिज्ञातो म एष वरो यां तु कुमारस्यान्ते वाचमभाषथास्तां मे ब्रूहीति॥५॥**

 सः He (Āruni) उवाच ह said एषः this वरः boon प्रतिज्ञातः is promised मे to me; तु but ब्रूहि tell मे me ताम् that वाचम् speech याम् which अभाषथाः (you) spoke अन्ते near, in the presence कुमारस्य इति of (my) boy, son.

 Āruni said, "You have promised me this boon. Please tell me what you spoke to my son about those questions. This is my boon."

 ** स होवाच दैवेषु वै गौतम तद्वरेषु मानुषाणां ब्रूहीति॥६॥**



 सः He (the King) उवाच ह said गौतम Gautama (Āruni) वै verily तत् that (is) वरेषु among the boons दैवेषु belonging to gods, divine, heavenly ब्रूहि ask, name मानुषाणाम् इति (boon) regarding men, human, among worldly things.

 The King said to Āruni, “ That belongs to divine boons. Please name some human boon.”

 **स होवाच विज्ञायते हास्ति हिरण्यस्यापात्तं गोअश्वानां दासीनां प्रवाराणां परिधानस्य मा नो भवान्बहोरनन्तस्यापर्यन्तस्याभ्यवदान्योऽभूदिति वै स गौतम तीर्थेनेच्छासा इत्युपैम्यहं भवन्तमिति वाचा ह स्मैव पूर्व उपयन्ति स होपायनकीर्त्योवास॥७॥**

 सः He (Āruni) उवाच ह said विज्ञायते (it) is known अस्ति there is अपात्तम् attainment, plenty हिरण्यस्य of gold गोअश्वानाम् of cattle and horses दासीनाम् of maid-servants प्रवाराणाम् of retinue, of attendants परिधानस्य of dress, भवान् you मा not अभूत् be नः (=माम्) towards me अभ्यवदान्यः ungenerous, stingy बहोः possessed of good qualities, plentiful अनन्तस्य everlasting, producing infinite results अपर्यन्तस्य इति inexhaustible (boon) reaching down to descendants. सः He (said) वै verily गौतम Gautama, Āruni इच्छासै wish, seek तीर्थेन इति according to the scriptures, in the proper way अहम् I उपैमि approach भवन्तम् इति you पूर्वे the ancients उपयन्ति स्म used to approach (a teacher), came as students वाचा ह through words एव only. सः ह He उवास lived, became (a



student) उपायन-कीर्त्या by mere announcement, by simple declaration.

 Āruni said, " It is known to you that I already have got plenty of gold, cattle, and horses, maid-servants, attendants and apparel. Having been generous every where, be not stingy towards me alone as regards this boon which is plentiful, produces infinite results and reaches down to descendants. " Thus addressed the King said, " Then you must wish to have this learning in the way prescribed by scriptures. " At this Āruni said, " I come to you as a student. " The ancients seeking instructions became students of a teacher by mere announcement, not by actually approaching his feet or serving him. Hence Āruni became a student simply by declaring that he was at his service without actually approaching the King’s feet according to the custom.

 ** स होवाच यथा नस्त्वं गौतम माऽपराधास्तव च पितामहा यथेयं विद्येतः पूर्वं न कस्मिꣳश्चन ब्राह्मण उवास तां त्वहं तुभ्यं वक्ष्यामि को हि त्वैवं ब्रुवन्तमर्हति प्रत्याख्यातुमिति॥८॥**

 सः ह He (the King) उवाच said गौतम Gautama, Āruni यथा as तव च your पितामहाः paternal grand-fathers तथा so त्वम् you मा (do) not (take) अपराधाः offence (with us). इतः Before पूर्वम् this इयम् this विद्या learning, knowledge न never



उवास lived, rested कस्मिन् चन in any ब्राह्मणे Brāhmaṇa तु but अहम् I वक्ष्यामि shall speak, shall instruct ताम् it तुभ्यम् to you ; हि तु for कः who अर्हति is able प्रत्याख्यातुम् to refuse, to withhold ब्रुवन्तम् one speaking एवम् thus.

 Thinking that Āruni was hurt, the King begged his pardon and said, "Please do not be offended with us. Be good to observe the attitude of your paternal grand-fathers who did not take offence with us. Before this transmission to you the knowledge that you have asked for never lived with a Bṛāhmana. It has been handed down through a line of Kshatriya teachers. That tradition cannot be maintained any more. I shall instruct even this knowledge to you ; because who can withhold this knowledge from you after you speak in this way.

 ** असौ वै लोकोऽग्निर्गौतम तस्याऽऽदित्य एव समिद्रश्मयो धूमोऽहर्चिर्दिशोऽङ्गारा अवान्तरदिशो विस्फुलिङ्गास्तस्मिन्नेतस्मिन्नग्नौ देवाः श्रद्धां जुह्वति तस्या आहुत्यै सोमो राजा सम्भवति॥९॥**

 वै Verily असौ that लोकः world, the heaven, गौतम O Gautama, O Āruni अग्निः (is) fire. आदित्यः The sun एव only (is) तस्य its समित् fuel, रश्मयः the rays धूमः (its) smoke, अहः the day अर्चिः (its) flame, दिशः the (four) directions, quarters, अङ्गाराः (its) cinder, embers, अवान्तरदिशः the inter-



mediate quarters विस्फुलिङ्गाः (its) sparks. तस्मिन् In that एतस्मिन् in this अग्नौ in fire देवाः the gods जुह्वति offer श्रद्धाम् faith. तस्याः Out of that आहुतेः offering राजा King सोमः moon सम्भवति is born, comes forth.

 The King spoke to Āruni: Heaven is to be looked upon verily as fire.¹ The sun is its fuel, because as the sun illumines heaven, so fuel is kindled. The rays are its smoke; for as the former emanate from the sun, so the latter rises from fuel. The day is its flame because both are bright. The four directions are its cinder, because they represent a calm condition. The intermediate directions are its sparks, because the former are scattered like sparks. In this fire of heaven Indra and other gods offer faith as an oblation. Out of that offer-ing is born Moon² who is the King of the Manes and the Brāhmanas.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The fourth question is first answered, be-cause when this question is solved, others will be easily solved. The order of question is broken on account of the importance of the first one.—Anandagiri.

2\. In the Shatapath Brahmana (11. 6. 2. 6-7) is described the departure of the two oblations of the Agnihotra sacrifice, thus: They enter the sky of which they make an Āhavanīya fire, with fire as its fuel and Sun’s rays as its white oblation. After offering libations to the sky they enter heaven of which also they make an Āhavanīya fire with Sun as its fuel and so\]

——————————————————————————————



on. This Āhavanīya fire is the chief of the three Vedic sacri-ficial fires which the people of the higher three castes are enjoined to tend regularly. The aforesaid oblations of the Agnihotra take along with them their accessories such as Āhavanīya fire, fuel, spark, cinder, smoke and the articles of oblation, for example, milk. These accessories retain their separate existence in an extremely subtle form in heaven. That subtle form of the oblations with their accessories which never cease to exist even during the dissolution of the world is called Apurba which literally means new. According to Mīmānsā Philosophy this Apurba, which has the peculiar indestructible power of materialisation at a subsequent period, reappear in its old form at the time of manifestation. The whole universe is described as being the development of the Apurba of these two oblations. When these subtle liquid substances form a part of the Agnihotra and are known as ' faith ' enter heaven with the sacrificer to make a new body for him in the lunar world, they are said to be offered as oblations.—Sankar and Anandagiri.

 ** पर्जन्यो वा अग्निर्गौतम तस्य संवत्सर एव समिदभ्राणि धूमो विद्युदर्चिरशनिरङ्गारा ह्रादुनयो विस्फुलिङ्गास्तस्मिन्नेतस्मिन्नग्नौ देवाः सोमꣳ राजानं जुह्वति तस्या आहुत्यै वृष्टिः सम्भवति॥१०॥**

 वै Verily गौतम O Gautama पर्जन्यः Parjanya (the god of rain) अग्निः (is) fire. संवत्सरः The year (is) तस्य its समित् fuel, अभ्राणि the clouds धूमः (its) smoke, विद्युत् lightning अर्चिः (its) flame, अशनिः thunderbolt अङ्गाराः (its) cinder,



embers, हादुनयः the rumblings, the rollings विस्फुलिङ्गाः (its) sparks. तस्मिन् In that एतस्मिन् in this अग्नौ in fire देवाः gods, the priests जुह्वति make offerings सोमराजानम् to King moon ; तस्याः out of that आहुत्यै offering वृष्टिः rain सम्भवति is produced, springs forth.

 O Gautama, Parjanya, the rain-god is to be looked upon verily as second fire, the second receptacle of the two oblations (in the order of their return). The year is its fuel, because the fire of Parjanya is kindled by the year as it revolves with its parts beginning from autumn and ending in summer. The clouds are its smoke because of its cloudy appearance. Lightning as its flame, since both are luminous. The thunderbolt is its cinder because both are hard. The rumblings of the clouds are its sparks, for both scatter and are numerous. In this receptacle of the two oblations the priests mentioned above make offering to King Moon, who was made out of the offering of heaven. He is offered in the fire of Parjanya and out of that offering of Moon rain is produced.

 **अयं वै लोकोऽग्निर्गौतम तस्य पृथिव्येव समिदग्निर्धूमो रात्रिरर्चिश्चन्द्रमा अङ्गारा नक्षत्राणि विस्फुलिङ्गास्तस्मिन्नेतस्मिन्नग्नौ देवा वृष्टिं जुह्वति तस्या आहुत्या अन्नꣳ सम्भवति॥११॥**

 वै Verily अयम् this लोकः world अग्निः (is) fire गौतम O Gautama. पृथिवी The earth एव only तस्य (is) its समित्



fuel, अग्निः fire धूमः (its) smoke, रात्रिः the night अर्चिः (its) flame, चन्द्रमाः the moon अङ्गाराः (its) cinders, नक्षत्राणि the stars विस्फुलिङ्गाः (its) sparks. तस्मिन् In that एतस्मिन् in this अग्नौ in fire देवाः the gods जुह्वति offer वृष्टिम् rain, तस्याः out of that आहुत्याः offering अन्नम् food सम्भवति is produced.

This world,¹ O Gautama, is verily to be looked upon as the third fire. The earth is the fuel of that fire, because this world² is kindled by the earth.³ Fire is its smoke because both rise from their abode, the earth. The night is its flame, because both originate from the contact of fuel.⁴ The moon is its cinder, because as the cinder is produced from flames, so is the moon in the night. The stars are its sparks because both scatter. In this fire of the world the gods offer rain. Out of that offering of rain food such as rice and barley is produced.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. This world is the place where all creatures are born and experience the results of their previous works. It consists of works, factors and their results.

2\. This world is related to the earth as a person is to his body.—Anandagiri.

3\. Fuel which abounds in earth produces fire and also gives rise to smoke.

4\. As the contact of fuel with fire produces flame, so the darkness of night is caused by a part of the earth shadowing the solar rays.—Anandagiri.\]

——————————————————————————————



** पुरुषो वा अग्निर्गौतम तस्य व्यात्तमेव समित्प्राणो धूमो वागर्चिश्चक्षुरङ्गाराः श्रोत्रं विस्फुलिङ्गास्तस्मिन्नेतस्मिन्नग्नौ देवा अन्नं जुह्वति तस्या आहुत्यै रेतः सम्भवति॥१२॥**

 वै Verily पुरुषः man, familiar human being गौतमः O Gautama अग्निः (is) fire, व्यात्तम् the open mouth तस्य (is) its समित् fuel, प्राणः the vital power (its) धूमः smoke, वाक् speech, the word (its) अर्चिः flame, चक्षुः the eye (its) अङ्गाराः cinders, श्रोत्रम् the ear विस्फुलिङ्गाः (its) sparks. तस्मिन् In that एतस्मिन् in this अग्नौ in fire देवाः the gods जुह्वति offer अन्नम् food. तस्याः out of that आहुत्यै offering रेतः semen सम्भवति is produced.

 The familiar human being with head, hands etc. O Gautama, is to be looked upon verily as the fourth fire. The open mouth is its fuel, because through mouth a man shines with speech, Vedic study etc., as the fire is kindled with fuel. The vital power is its smoke, because both rise from the mouth. The word is its flame, because as a flame reveals things, so the word signifies its objects. The eye is its cinder, because both are sources of light. The ear is its sparks owing to the similarity of scattering. In this fire of man the gods ¹ offer food. Out of that offering of food semen is produced.



——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The forms of vital power are taken here as gods, for the same are the forms of the vital power in the body and they put food into a man.\]

——————————————————————————————

 ** योषा वा अग्निर्गौतम तस्या उपस्थ एव समिल्लोमानि धूमो योनिरर्चिर्यदन्तः करोति तेऽङ्गारा अभिनन्दा विस्फुलिङ्गास्तस्मिन्नेतस्मिन्नग्नौ देवा रेतो जुह्वति तस्या आहुत्यै पुरुषः सम्भवति स जीवति यावज्जीवत्यथ यदा म्रियते॥१३॥**

 योषा Woman वै verily अग्निः (is) fire गौतम O Gautama, उपस्थः the haunch एव only तस्याः her समित् fuel, लोमानि hairs धूमः (its) smoke, योनिः organ अर्चिः (is) flame, यत् अन्तः करोति cohabitation ते they अङ्गाराः (its) cinder, अभिनन्दाः the fits of enjoyments विस्फुलिङ्गाः (its) sparks. तस्मिन् In that एतस्मिन् in this अग्नौ in the sacrificial fire देवाः the gods जुह्वति offer रेतः semen. तस्याः Out of that आहुत्यै offering पुरुषः a man सम्भवति is born, is produced. सः He जीवति lives यावत् as long as जीवति (he) is destined to live. अथ Then यदा when म्रियते (he) dies.

 Woman, O Gautama is to be imagined as the fifth receptacle of sacrificial fire . . . . . its fuel, hairs its smoke, . . . . . its flame, . . . . . its cinder, fits of enjoyment its sparks. In this sacrificial fire the gods offer semen. Out of that offering a man is produced.¹ He lives as long as the resultant of his past actions, which causes him live in this body, lasts. Then, when he becomes dead.



——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Man is born by the successive offering of the liquid substances in the fires of heaven, Parjanya, this world, man and woman in the increasingly grosser forms of faith, moon, rain, food and seed respectively. Therefore the answer of the fourth question is that when the offering of the fifth oblation is made in the fire of woman, the liquid substances get transformed into semen and endowed with a human voice.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **अथैनमग्नये हरन्ति तस्याग्निरेवाग्निर्भवति समित्समिद्धूमो धूमोऽर्चिरर्चिरङ्गारा अङ्गाराविस्फुलिङ्गा विस्फुलिङ्गास्तस्मिन्नेतस्मिन्नग्नौ देवाः** **पुरुषं जुह्वति तस्या आहुत्यै पुरुषो भास्वरवर्णः सम्भवति॥१४॥**

 अथ Then हरन्ति (the priests) carry एनम् him (the dead man) अग्नये for the (funeral) fire. अग्निः The fire एव only भवति is तस्य his अग्निः fire, समित् the fuel समित् (his) fuel, धूमः the smoke धूमः (its) smoke, अर्चिः the flame अर्चिः (his) flame, अङ्गाराः the cinder अङ्गाराः (his) cinder, विस्फुलिङ्गाः the sparks विस्फुलिङ्गाः (his) sparks. तस्मिन् In that एतस्मिन् in this अग्नौ fire देवाः the gods जुह्वति offer पुरुषम् the man तस्याः out of that आहुत्यै offering पुरुषः the man सम्भवति emerges भास्वरवर्णः radiant.

 The priests carry the dead man to be put in the funeral fire, the last receptacle for the sacrifice in which he himself becomes the oblation. The well-known fire becomes his fire, the familiar fuel



his fuel, the smoke his smoke, the flame his flame, the cinder his cinder and the sparks his sparks. In this funeral fire the gods offer the man as the last oblation. Out of that offering the man comes out exceedingly bright.¹

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. Brightness is due to purification by rites performed from conception to funeral ceremony.\]

——————————————————————————————

 **ते य एवमेतद्विदुर्यो चामी अरण्ये श्रद्धाꣳ सत्यमुपासते तेऽर्चिरभिसम्भवन्त्यर्चिषोऽहरह्न आपूर्यमाणपक्षणमापूर्यमाणपक्षाद्यान्षण्मासानुदङ्ङादित्य एति मासेभ्यो देवलोकं देवलोकादादित्यमादित्याद्वैद्युतं तान् वैद्युतान्पुरुषो मानस एत्य ब्रह्मलोकान्गमयति ते तेषु ब्रह्मलोकेषु पराः परावतो वसन्ति तेषां न पुनरावृत्तिः॥१५॥**

 ते Those ये who विदुः know एतत् this एवम् as such च and ते those अमी others (the hermits and monks) ये who उपासते meditate सत्यम् upon\* Satya (Brahman) (Hiraṇyagarbha) श्रद्धाम् with, faith अरण्ये in the forest अभि सम्भवन्ति reach अर्चिः the flame, the deity identified with the flame, अर्चिषः from the flame, from the deity of the flame अहः to the day, to the deity of the day अहः from day, from the deity of the day आपूर्यमाण-पक्षम् to the bright fortnight, the deity, to the deity of the bright fortnight आपूर्यमाणपक्षात् from the bright fortnight, from the deity of the bright fortnight षट्

——————————————————————————————

\*Refer to 5. 1. 1 passage.

——————————————————————————————



मासान् to the six months, to the deities of the six months यान् in which आदित्यः the sun एति goes, travels उदङ् north-ward मासेभ्यः from the months, from the deities of the months देवलोकम् to the world of the gods, to the deity identified with the world of the gods, देवलोकात् from the world of the gods, from the deity identified with the world of the gods आदित्यम् to the sun, आदित्यात् from the sun वैद्युतम् to the lightning, to the deity of the lightning ; पुरुषः a being मानसः mind-born, created from the mind (of the Hiraṇyagarbha), a denizen of the world of Hiraṇyagarbha एत्य coming गमयति causes to go, takes तान् those वैद्युतान् the lightnings, deities of the lightning ब्रह्मलोकान् to the worlds of Hiraṇyagarbha. ते Those पराः perfect ones वसन्ति live, dwell परावतः for a great many superfine years, many human cycles तेषु in those ब्रह्मलोकेषु in the worlds of Brahman (Hiraṇyagarbha), न no पुनरावृत्तिः return तेषाम् of them इह\* here, to this world.

 \[The first question is answered in this passage.\]

 Those¹ who know this meditation on five fires in terms of fuel, smoke, cinder, sparks, etc. as described above as well as the hermits and monks who constantly live in the forest and meditate with faith upon Hiraṇyagarbha all reach the deity identified with the flame who is stationed in the northern way. Being conducted by this deity, they reach the deity of the bright fortnight. Led by

——————————————————————————————

\*The word occurs in the Madhyandin Śākha.

——————————————————————————————



him they reach a group of the six deities (of six months) identified with the northern march of the sun. Being conducted by these deities, they reach the deity identified with the world of the gods. From him they go to the sun, and from the sun they go to the deity identified with lightning. Then a denizen of the world of Hiraṇyagarbha meets and takes them to the world of Hiraṇyagarbha. They become perfect and dwell in the worlds of Hiraṇyagarbha for many human cycles which constitute the life time of Hiraṇyagarbha. From there they do not return any more to this world.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The householders qualified for these rites who realise that they are born of fire, are children of fire, are but another form of fire, are meant here. That they enter the northern way is known from the Vishnu Puran (2. 8. 92-94) which says : “Eighty-eight thousand sages led a life of continence, entered the northern way of the sun and attained relative immortality. As long as they do not know this meditation on the five fires or Hiraṇyagarbha they are born of the fire of woman again and again and rotate constantly like the Persian wheel by their comings and goings between this world and the next. But the knowledge of this meditation frees them from ceaseless rotation of births and deaths.

2.The plural number indicates the higher and lower planes in the world of Hiraṇyagarbha attained according to the different grades in meditations.\]

——————————————————————————————



** अथ ये यज्ञेन दानेन तपसा लोकाञ्जयन्ति ते धूममभिसम्भवन्ति धूमाद्रात्रिꣳ रात्रेरपक्षीयमाणपक्षमपक्षीयमाणपक्षाद्यान्षण्मासान्दक्षिणादित्य एति मासेभ्यः पितृलोकं पितृलोकाच्चन्द्रं ते चन्द्रं प्राप्यान्नं भवन्ति ताꣳस्तत्र देवा यथा सोमꣳ राजानमाप्यायस्वापक्षीयस्वेत्येवमेनाꣳस्तत्र भक्षयन्ति तेषां यदा तत्पर्यवैत्यथेममेवाऽऽकाशमभिनिष्पद्यन्त आकाशाद्वायुं वायोर्वृष्टिं वृष्टेः पृथिवीं ते पृथिवीं प्राप्यान्नं भवन्ति ते पुनः पुरुषाग्नौ हूयन्ते ततो योषाग्नौ जायन्ते लोकान्प्रत्युत्थायिनस्त एवमेवानुपरिवर्तन्तेऽथ य एतौ पन्थानौ न विदुस्ते कीटाः पतङ्गा यदिदं दन्दशूकम्॥१६॥ इति द्वितीयं ब्राह्मणम्॥२॥**

 अथ While ते those (the ritualists) ये who जयन्ति conquer लोकान् the worlds यज्ञेन by sacrifices, दानेन by charity, by distribution of gifts, तपसा by austerity, by penance अभिसम्भवन्ति reach, get to: धूमम् smoke, deity of smoke धूमात् from smoke, from the deity of smoke रात्रिम् to night, to the deity of the night, रात्रेः from night, from the deity of the night अपक्षीयमाण-पक्षम् to the dark fortnight, to the deity of the dark fortnight, अपक्षीयमाणपक्षात् from the dark fortnight, from the deity of the dark fortnight यान् to those षण्मासान् six months, the deities of six months (in which) आदित्यः the sun दक्षिणा towards the south, southward एति goes. मासेभ्यः From the months, from the deities of the six months पितृलोकम् to the world of the Manes, to the deity of the world of the Manes, पितृलोकात् from the world of the Manes, from



the deity of the world of the Manes चन्द्रम् to the moon. ते They प्राप्य getting, reaching चन्द्रम् the moon भवन्ति become अन्नम् food, a new watery body. तत्र There देवाः the gods भक्षयन्ति eat, enjoy तान् those एनान् these तत्र there एवम् thus यथा as (the priests drink) राजानम् the King, the resplendent सोमम् Soma juice (saying as it were) आप्यायस्व do flourish, do increase अपक्षीयस्व इति do dwindle, do decrease यदा when तेषाम् their तत् that (the momentum of past works) पर्यवैति expire, is exhausted अथ then अभिनिष्पद्यन्ते (they) go इमम् to this आकाशम् sky एव indeed, आकाशात् from the sky वायुम् to air, वायोः from air वृष्टिम् to rain, वृष्टेः from rain पृथिवीम् to the earth. ते They प्राप्य getting, पृथिवीम् to the earth भवन्ति become अन्नम् the food. ते They पुनः again हूयन्ते are offered पुरुषाग्नौ in the fire of man (adult). ततः Thence योषाग्नौ in the fire of woman (whence) जायन्ते (they) are born प्रत्युत्थायिनः those who desire to go लोकान् to (other) worlds. ते They एवम् एव thus अनुपरिवर्त्तन्ते rotate, अथ while ते those ये who विदुः know, practise meditation or rites न not एतौ these पन्थानौ two ways (become) कीटाः worms, insects पतङ्गाः moths, flies इदम् this यत् that दन्दशूकम् having the nature of biting others.

 While the ritualists who do not know as above but possess the knowledge of the six things such as the departure of the two oblations connected with the Agnihotra sacrifice conquer the worlds¹ by sacrifices such as Agnihotra, distribution of gifts outside the altar, and penance such as Krichchra



and Chāndrayana fasts reach the deity of smoke. Conducted by that deity they go to the deity of the night. Led by him they reach the deity of the dark fort-night. From him they go to the deities of the six months in which the sun turns towards the south. From them they get to the deity of the world of the fathers and from him they reach the moon. In the moon the ritualists get a new watery body and are enjoyed by the gods like the servants by their Masters as the local priests cheer up the resplendent Soma juice saying, 'do increase, do increase,' and thus drink it in the sacrifices. And when the momentum of their past works—such as sacrifices, charity, etc. that led them to the moon—expire,² they become fine and come down to this sky. From the sky they go to air.³ From air they fall on the earth as rain; on the earth they turn into food like rice and barley. Then they are offered as food in the fire of an adult. There they are converted into semen and are poured in the fire of women, whence they are born and perform the Agnihotra and other sacrifices for going to other worlds. Thus these ritualists continuously rotate in a circle like the Persian wheel till they realise Brahman for the attainment of the northern way or immediate liberation. While those who do not practise meditation or perform sacrifices



to attain the northern or the southern way respec- tively are born¹ as worms and flies and other tiny biting creatures like gnats and mosquitoes.

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. The plural number indicates the varieties of results.

2\. The new watery body built for the ritualists in the moon for their enjoyment melts on the exhaustion of their past works like a lump of ice in contact with sunshine.

3\. Those ritualists who live with an ether-like fine body in the sky are blown hither and thither by the wind etc.

4\. Such existence is very painful and difficult to get rid of. The Shruti, therefore, warns us to try our utmost to give up our natural pursuit of work and knowledge, perform those sacrifices and meditations enjoined by the scriptures and attain the southern or northern way.\]

——————————————————————————————

**CHAPTER SIX : SECTION THREE**

 **स यः कामयेत महत्प्राप्नुयामित्युदगयन आपूर्यमाणपक्षस्य पुण्याहे द्वादशाहमुपसद्व्रती भूत्वौदुम्बरे कꣳसे चमसे वा सर्वौषधं फलानीति सम्भृत्य परिसमूह्य परिलिप्याग्निमुपसमाधाय परस्तीर्याऽऽवृताज्यꣳ सꣳस्कृत्य पुꣳसा नक्षत्रेण मन्थꣳ सन्नीय जुहोति। यावन्तो देवास्त्वयि जातवेदस्तिर्यञ्चो घ्नन्ति पुरुषस्य कामान्। तेभ्योऽहं भागधेयं जुहोमि ते मा तृप्ताः सर्वैः कामै-**



**स्तर्पयन्तु स्वाहा। या तिरश्ची निपद्यतेऽहं विधरणी इति तां त्वा घृतस्य धारया यजे सꣳराधनीमहꣳ स्वाहा॥१॥**

 सः He यः who कामयेत desires प्राप्नुयाम् (I) shall attain महत् इति great, greatness जुहोति offers oblations पुण्येऽहे on an auspicious day, on a favourable day आपूर्यमाणपक्षस्य of the fortnight in which moon waxes पुंसा under a male नक्षत्रेण star उदगयने during the north-ward march of the sun भूत्वा being उपसद्-व्रती under a vow of the Upasads द्वादशाहम् for twelve days सम्भृत्य collecting चमसे in a cup वा or कंसे in bowl औदुम्बरे of Udumba wood सर्वौषधम् all herbs फलानि इति grains परिसमूह्य sweeping (the ground) परिलिप्य plastering (the ground) उपसमाधाय collecting, gathering अग्निम् the fire परिस्तीर्य spreading (the Kusha grass) संस्कृत्य purifying आवृता- ज्यम् ghee covered (in a vessel) सन्नीय interposing, placing near मन्थम् Mantha (paste made of those things). जातवेद O Fire तेभ्यः to those देवाः gods त्वयि under you यावन्तः who घ्नन्ति destroy, frustrate तिर्यञ्चः adversely, spitefully पुरुषस्य people's कामान् desires अहम् I जुहोमि offer भागधेयम् (their) share, portion. ते They तृप्ताः being satisfied, being pleased तर्पयन्तु may satisfy, may fulfil मा me सर्वैः with all कामैः desires. स्वाहा Svāhā! ताम् to that संराधनीम् the all accomplishing deity, all producing goddess या who निपद्यते turns out, becomes तिरश्ची adverse, spiteful त्वा under you (considering) अहम् I (am) विधरणी इति the support (of all) अहम् I यजे offer धारया with (this) stream, current घृतस्य of ghee, स्वाहा Svāhā.



 \[Of meditation and rites the former is independent whereas the latter are dependent on divine and human wealth. For the purpose of acquiring in a harmless way wealth necessary for the rites, the ceremony of Manth (paste) is being described as a means of achieving greatness which is followed by wealth as a matter of course.\]

 Those who want to be great should perform sacrifices as follows on a favourable day under a star having a masculine name during the northward move of the sun : The sacrificer should undertake for twelve days a vow of the upasads ¹ in which he has to drink cow's milk. He should gather in a vessel of udumber wood shaped like a cup or bowl all herbs and their grains ² as far as available and within his means, clean the ground, prepare the Avasathya fire, spread the kusha grass, purify the ghee covered in a vessel according to the Sthalipāka ³ ceremony, place between himself and the fire the paste made of the collected herbs and grains and offer oblations with a ladle of udumber wood saying these mantras : ‘O Fire, I offer this portion to those gods under you who adversely stand in the way of peoples' desires. May they be pleased and fulfil my desire ! Swāhā : To that all-accomplishing goddess who becomes adverse under you, considering herself



the support of all, I offer this current of ghee. Swāhā.’

——————————————————————————————

\[NOTES—1. These rites are connected with the Jyotishtoma sacrifice in which the sacrificer has to live on cow’s milk according to the yield of an increasing and decreasing number of teats of the cow.

2\. Ten kinds of village-grown grains enumerated in 6. 3. 13. are to be included.

3\. It is a religious ceremony performed by the householders. The word literally means ‘cooking in a pot.’\]

——————————————————————————————

** ज्येष्ठाय स्वाहा श्रेष्ठाय स्वाहेत्यग्नौ हुत्वा मन्थे सꣳस्रवमवनयति प्राणाय स्वाहा वसिष्ठायै स्वाहेत्यग्नौ हुत्वा मन्थे सꣳस्रवमवनयति वाचे स्वाहा प्रतिष्ठायै स्वाहेत्यग्नौ हुत्वा मन्थे सꣳस्रवमवनयति चक्षुषे स्वाहा सम्पदे स्वाहेत्यग्नौ हुत्वा मन्थे सꣳस्रवमवनयति श्रोत्राय स्वाहाऽऽयतनाय स्वाहेत्यग्नौ हुत्वा मन्थे सꣳस्रवमवनयति मनसे स्वाहा प्रजात्यै स्वाहेत्यग्नौ हुत्वा मन्थे सꣳस्रवमवनयति रेतसे स्वाहेत्यग्नौ हुत्वा मन्थे सꣳस्रवमवनयति॥२॥**

 हुत्वा Offering oblations अग्नौ इति in the fire (saying) स्वाहा Swāhā ज्येष्ठाय to the eldest स्वाहा Swāhā श्रेष्ठाय to the greatest, to the best अवनयति (he) drips, pours संस्रवम् the remnant adhering to the ladle मन्थे in the paste, हुत्वा इति offering oblations अग्नौ in the fire (saying) स्वाहा Swāhā प्राणाय to the vital power, स्वाहा Swāhā to the Vasishtha
